## Behavioral

### Q801: Tell me about yourself.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Structure: Present (current role) -> Past (relevant experience) -> Future (why this role). STAR approach: Situation, Task, Action, Result. Keep to 2 minutes. Highlight achievements, not responsibilities. Use numbers (improved performance by 30%). Tailor to role requirements. Focus on recent experience. Practice: record yourself. Common structure: "I'm a [role] with [X years] experience in [technology]. Currently at [company], I [key achievement]. Previously at [past company], I [another achievement]. I'm excited about this role because [specific reason]."

---

### Q802: Why do you want to work here?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Research company: products, culture, tech stack, recent news, mission. Connect their work to your interests. Show enthusiasm, not desperation. Avoid: "I need a job", "good salary", "close to home". Structure: "I admire [company's] work in [specific area]. My experience in [skill] aligns with your [project/product]. I'm excited about [specific reason]." Example: "Your focus on AI-powered developer tools is exactly what I want to build. My background in LLM fine-tuning and developer tooling makes this a great fit."

---

### Q803: Describe a challenging project.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
STAR method. S: complex project with tight deadline, unclear requirements, technical challenges. T: your specific role and responsibility. A: steps taken - research, architecture, collaboration, trade-offs. R: successful delivery, lessons learned. Show: problem-solving, ownership, resilience, teamwork. Example: migrating monolithic app to microservices. Challenge: data consistency, no downtime. Actions: incremental migration (Strangler Fig), event-driven architecture, phased rollout. Result: zero downtime migration, 2x deployment frequency.

---

### Q804: Tell me about a time you failed.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Show self-awareness, accountability, learning. Avoid blaming others or trivial failures. Structure: what happened, why it failed, what you learned, what changed afterward. Keep professional (not personal failures). Example: launched feature without enough load testing -> crashed in production. Lesson: implement load testing in CI, timeouts, circuit breakers. Took ownership, fixed, documented. Key: what you learned and how you improved. Interviewers want to see growth mindset, not perfection.

---

### Q805: How do you handle conflicts?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Focus on collaboration, respect, and solution-orientation. Listen first, understand perspective, find common ground. If technical disagreement: data-driven decisions (benchmarks, A/B tests). If interpersonal: focus on problem not person, involve mediator if needed. Example: disagreed on architecture (monolith vs microservices). Actions: researched both options, presented pros/cons with data, compromise: modular monolith with future migration path. Result: moved forward, team aligned. Show emotional intelligence, respect for differing opinions.

---

### Q806: Describe a time you showed leadership.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Leadership without authority: mentoring junior, organizing project, influencing decisions, owning outcome. Example: junior dev struggled with testing. I paired with them, set up testing standards, created templates. Result: their test coverage improved, confidence grew. Or: led migration of critical service, coordinated across 3 teams, managed timeline, resolved blockers. Key: highlight initiative, ownership, impact on others. Not necessarily about title - about making things better for the team.

---

### Q807: How do you stay updated?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Show continuous learning habit. Sources: newsletters (TLDR, The Algorithm), blogs (company engineering blogs, Martin Fowler, Julia Evans), podcasts (Software Engineering Daily, Lex Fridman), conferences (recorded talks), books (DDIA, Clean Code), courses (Fast.ai, Coursera), side projects, open source contributions. Specific: "I follow [blog/newsletter], built [side project] using [new technology], took [course] on [topic]." Show genuine curiosity, not checkbox ticking. Mention how you applied what you learned.

---

### Q808: Why did you leave your last job?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stay positive, professional, forward-looking. Focus on growth opportunities, not grievances. Acceptable: wanted more responsibility, different tech stack, better product impact, career growth. Avoid: bad manager, toxic culture, boring work, salary complaints. Example: "I'm looking for more challenging problems in my domain" or "I want to work on AI applications at scale." Be honest but diplomatic. If laid off: state factually without negativity ("company restructuring").
---

### Q809: Where do you see yourself in 5 years?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Show ambition aligned with company growth. Balance: concrete enough to show thought, flexible enough to adapt. Technical: "I want to be a technical leader in AI/ML, designing systems that impact millions." Management vs IC. Show interest in growing with the company: "I want to deepen my expertise in [area] while taking ownership of larger projects that impact company goals." Avoid: "Your job", "C-level position" (unrealistic), "I don't know."

---

### Q810: Tell me about a time you disagreed with your manager.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Show respectful disagreement, data-driven argument, acceptance of final decision. Example: manager wanted aggressive deadline that would compromise quality. Actions: presented risk assessment, proposed alternative (scope reduction, timeline extension). Manager explained business constraints, compromise: ship MVP on time with documented tech debt for later. Result: product shipped, debt tracked, delivered next quarter. Key: respect authority, advocate for what's right, be flexible, no ego.

---

### Q811: Describe your ideal work environment.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Honest but align with company culture. Elements: collaborative team, blameless culture, technical excellence, autonomy, clear goals, growth opportunities, good work-life balance. Example: "I thrive in an environment with smart, collaborative teammates where I can own problems end-to-end. I value clear communication, technical mentorship, and the freedom to make technical decisions." Avoid: impossible demands (no meetings, complete isolation), negative framing (I hate open offices). Show flexibility.

---

### Q812: How do you handle tight deadlines?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prioritize, communicate, trade-off. Scenario: project deadline unrealistic. Steps: identify critical path, estimate effort, communicate risks early, negotiate scope (what can be cut), focus on highest impact work, work efficiently (no multitasking). Example: feature needed in 2 weeks, estimated 3. Proposed: reduce scope (ship core functionality, defer edge cases). Communicated daily progress. Worked efficiently (no overtime as norm). Result: shipped on time with clear plan for follow-up. Key: proactive communication, prioritization, no heroics.

---

### Q813: Describe a time you mentored someone.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Focus on impact on mentee, not just what you did. Example: onboarded new grad to team. Actions: pair programming sessions, code review with explanations, weekly 1:1s, documentation improvements. Result: they became productive in 2 months (vs typical 3), later mentoring others. Or: mentored intern: structured learning plan, real tasks, feedback loops. Result: successful project, full-time offer. Show teaching ability, patience, and genuine interest in helping others grow.

---

### Q814: What's your biggest achievement?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Choose relevant, quantifiable, impactful. Use STAR. Example: "Redesigned recommendation system at my last company, improving click-through rate by 25% while reducing latency by 40%. This impacted 10M users monthly and contributed to $5M additional revenue." Key: specific numbers, technical depth, business impact. Not just what you did but why it was hard and what it achieved. Pick 2-3 achievements you can talk about in depth.

---

### Q815: How do you approach learning a new technology?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Structured approach: 1. Understand the problem it solves (high-level context). 2. Official docs + tutorials (hands-on). 3. Build a small project (learn by doing). 4. Read best practices (books, blogs, codebases). 5. Teach someone (solidifies learning). Resources: documentation, REPL/notebooks, GitHub, Stack Overflow, community. Example: learning Go: read "Effective Go", built CLI tool, contributed to open source project. Show learning strategy, not just resource list. Emphasis on building practical projects to learn.

---

### Q816: Tell me about a time you improved a process.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Identify inefficiency, propose solution, implement, measure impact. Example: CI pipeline took 45 minutes. Actions: parallelized test execution, optimized Docker layers, split into stages. Result: 15 minutes build time (3x faster), developer productivity improved. Or: manual deployment process. Automated with CI/CD pipeline. Reduced deployment time from 2 hours to 10 minutes. Zero deployment errors. Key: identify pain point, metric before/after, benefited the team.

---

### Q817: How do you handle multiple priorities?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prioritization frameworks: Eisenhower Matrix (urgent/important), Impact/Effort matrix, MoSCoW (Must/Should/Could/Won't). Communication: get clarity from stakeholders on priority, push back when needed, communicate impact of trade-offs. Tools: Kanban boards, task tracking (Jira, Linear), daily prioritization. Example: three urgent features from different stakeholders. Steps: clarified business priorities with product manager, negotiated deadlines, communicated timeline, delivered highest priority first, deferred lower impact work. Key: systematic approach, proactive communication.

---

### Q818: What do you do when you don't know something?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
First attempt: research (docs, Google, Stack Overflow). If still stuck: ask well-formed question (show what you tried, where you're stuck). Know when to ask (don't spend hours if someone knows answer in 2 minutes). Ask specific person if relevant (SME). Document findings for future. Example: debugging memory leak. Steps: used profiler, narrowed to cache, researched GC tuning, asked senior for code review of my fix. Result: resolved, wrote internal guide. Shows: resourcefulness, knowing limits, effective communication.

---

### Q819: Describe your perfect team.
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Collaboration: blameless culture (postmortems, not witch hunts). Communication: clear, async-friendly (Slack, docs), transparent. Technical: code review culture, high testing standards, good documentation, CI/CD. Process: agile without bureaucracy, appropriate meetings (standups, retros), autonomy. Growth: mentorship, learning time (hackathons, brown bags). Diversity: different perspectives, respectful debate. Example: "A team with psychological safety where people can disagree openly, learn from failures, and support each other's growth. Good engineering practices and reasonable deadlines."

---

### Q820: Why should we hire you?
**Topic:** Behavioral
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tailored to job requirements. Match your skills to their needs. Structure: "I have [skill] in [area], demonstrated by [achievement]. I'm excited about [company's work] in [specific]. I can contribute [specific value] from day one." Example: "With 5 years of full-stack experience and strong AI/ML knowledge, I can bridge the gap between production systems and model deployment. I've built and deployed ML pipelines serving 1M+ requests/day. Your AI platform team aligns with my expertise and interests." Provide crisp, impactful reasons.

## DevOps & Cloud

### Q561: What is Docker?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Docker
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Containerization platform packaging applications with dependencies into portable containers. Container shares host OS kernel (no guest OS), starts faster than VM. Dockerfile: FROM, RUN, COPY, CMD, EXPOSE. Images are read-only templates. Containers are running instances. docker build, docker run, docker push, docker pull. Layers cached for faster rebuilds. Docker Compose defines multi-container apps. Kubernetes for production container orchestration.

---

### Q562: Docker Compose?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Docker
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
docker-compose.yml defines services, networks, volumes. docker-compose up/down. Each service is a container with environment, ports, dependencies. For single-host development. docker-compose scale (legacy), docker stack deploy (Swarm). Not for production multi-host (use Kubernetes).

---

### Q563: Kubernetes architecture?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Control Plane: API Server (REST API), etcd (key-value store), Scheduler (assign Pods to Nodes), Controller Manager (node/replication). Worker Nodes: kubelet (Pod agent), kube-proxy (networking), container runtime (containerd). Pod: smallest unit (one+ containers). Service: stable endpoint (ClusterIP/NodePort/LoadBalancer). Deployment: declarative updates, rolling updates, rollbacks. ConfigMap/Secret for configuration. Namespace for isolation.

---

### Q564: Pods vs Deployments?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pod: ephemeral, basic unit, no self-healing. Deployment: manages ReplicaSet, desired count, rolling updates (maxSurge/maxUnavailable), rollbacks. StatefulSet: stable identity, persistent storage, ordered scaling for stateful apps. DaemonSet: runs on all nodes (logging). Job/CronJob: batch tasks.

---

### Q565: CI/CD Pipeline?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - CI/CD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Source -> Build -> Test -> Package -> Deploy -> Monitor. CI: frequent integration with automated build/test. CD: auto-deploy after CI passes. Tools: Jenkins, GitLab CI, GitHub Actions, CircleCI. Stages: checkout, compile, unit test, integration test, static analysis, build image, push registry, deploy staging, e2e test, deploy production. Branch strategies: GitFlow, trunk-based, GitHub Flow.

---

### Q566: Infrastructure as Code (IaC)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Terraform
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Managing infrastructure through code. Terraform: declarative HCL, state file, multi-cloud. plan (preview), apply (execute), destroy. Remote state (S3) for teams. Ansible: agentless config management (YAML playbooks). CloudFormation: AWS-native. Pulumi: general-purpose languages.

---

### Q567: What is Helm?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Kubernetes package manager. Charts: packaged K8s resources with templates and values.yaml. helm install/upgrade/rollback. Dependencies. Kustomize: native K8s customization, no templating. Helmfile: declare desired releases.

---

### Q568: AWS core services?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - AWS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compute: EC2 (VMs), Lambda (serverless), ECS/EKS (containers). Storage: S3 (object), EBS (block), EFS (file). Database: RDS (relational), DynamoDB (NoSQL), ElastiCache (Redis). Networking: VPC, Route53, CloudFront, ALB/NLB. Security: IAM, KMS, WAF, Shield. Monitoring: CloudWatch, X-Ray. CI/CD: CodePipeline, CodeBuild, CodeDeploy.

---

### Q569: What is Serverless?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Serverless
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Cloud provider manages servers. Pay per execution (not idle). AWS Lambda: function as a service (FaaS). Event-driven (S3, API Gateway, SQS, DynamoDB Streams). Cold start: latency on first invocation after idle. Mitigations: provisioned concurrency, keep-warm via periodic pings, Lambda SnapStart (Java). Limitations: max 15min timeout, 10GB memory, deployment package size. Best for: event processing, webhooks, CRUD APIs, data transformation.

---

### Q570: Kubernetes Services types?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ClusterIP: internal IP only (default). NodePort: exposes on each node's IP at static port (30000-32767). LoadBalancer: provisions cloud load balancer (external IP). ExternalName: DNS CNAME record. Ingress: HTTP/HTTPS routing to Services (not a Service type, but Ingress resource). Service Mesh (Istio/Linkerd): advanced traffic management beyond Ingress.

---

### Q571: Kubernetes ConfigMap vs Secret?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ConfigMap: non-confidential config data (key-value or file). Secret: for sensitive data (base64 encoded, encrypted at rest via KMS). Both injected as environment variables or mounted as volumes. Secrets not encrypted by default (just base64). Use external secret management: HashiCorp Vault, Sealed Secrets, External Secrets Operator, AWS Secrets Manager CSI driver.

---

### Q572: Docker multi-stage builds?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Docker
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
FROM golang:alpine AS builder -> compile -> FROM alpine:latest -> COPY --from=builder /app . Reduced final image (no build tools). Keeps images small and secure. Python example: builder installs all dev deps, final image only has runtime deps.

---

### Q573: What is Terraform state?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Terraform
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
JSON file mapping real-world resources to config. Enables: diff detection, dependency ordering, destroy tracking. Local state: terraform.tfstate. Remote state: S3/DynamoDB (locking) for team use. State locking prevents concurrent modifications. terraform import to add existing resources. Workspaces: separate state per environment (dev/staging/prod). No state sharing between workspaces.

---

### Q574: Kubernetes probes?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
livenessProbe: if fails, restart container (check if alive). readinessProbe: if fails, remove from Service endpoints (check if ready for traffic). startupProbe: for slow-starting containers (delays liveness/readiness). Types: HTTP GET (HTTP status), TCP Socket (port open), Exec (command exit code). Configure: initialDelaySeconds, periodSeconds, timeoutSeconds, failureThreshold. Avoid heavy probes (resource waste).

---

### Q575: What is a Service Mesh (Istio)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Service Mesh
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Infrastructure layer for service communication. Sidecar proxy (Envoy) alongside each pod. Features: traffic management (weighted routing, circuit breakers, retries), security (mTLS, RBAC), observability (metrics, tracing, access logs). Control plane (istiod): pilot (traffic), citadel (certificates), galley (config). Bookinfo demo. Alternatives: Linkerd (lightweight, Rust-based), Consul Connect, Kuma.

---

### Q576: Horizontal vs Vertical Pod Autoscaling?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HPA (Horizontal Pod Autoscaler): scales Pod count based on CPU/memory utilization or custom metrics. targetAverageUtilization. VPA (Vertical Pod Autoscaler): adjusts resource requests/limits. Recommender mode (recommends), Auto mode (applies). Cluster Autoscaler: adds/removes nodes when Pods are pending (can't fit). Karpenter (AWS): faster node scaling. Custom metrics: Prometheus adapter, KEDA (event-driven scaling based on Kafka/SQS lengths).

---

### Q577: Cloud Design Patterns?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Circuit Breaker (Resilience4j): fail fast, prevent cascading. Retry with exponential backoff + jitter. Bulkhead: isolate failures per resource pool. Saga: distributed transactions with compensating actions. Strangler Fig: gradually migrate from monolith to microservices. Sidecar: co-locate helper container. Ambassador: proxy for external services. CQRS: separate read/write models. Event Sourcing: store changes as events. Cache-Aside: cache misses load from DB. Throttling: rate limiting.

---

### Q578: Monitoring and Observability?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Monitoring
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Logs (why): ELK (Elasticsearch/Logstash/Kibana), Loki (Grafana), structured JSON logging. Metrics (what): Prometheus (pull model, time-series DB), Grafana (dashboards), rate/errors/duration. Traces (where): OpenTelemetry + Jaeger/Zipkin, distributed tracing. USE method (Utilization, Saturation, Errors) for resource monitoring. RED method (Rate, Errors, Duration) for service monitoring. SLAs/SLOs/SLIs. Error budgets. Alerting: Alertmanager, PagerDuty. On-call rotation.

---

### Q579: Git branching strategies?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Git
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
GitFlow: develop + feature branches -> release -> main + hotfix. Structured, complex. GitHub Flow: feature branch -> PR -> main. Simple, continuous deployment. Trunk-Based Development: short-lived feature branches (hours), frequent merge to main. Release branches for stable. GitLab Flow: environment branches (staging, production). Feature flags: decouple deployment from release. Monorepo vs multi-repo. Conventional commits (<type>: <description>) for automatic versioning.

---

### Q580: What is SRE (Site Reliability Engineering)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Applying software engineering practices to operations. Google's approach: reliability as feature. Error budgets: 100% - SLO. Burn rate: how fast budget consumed. Toil elimination: automate manual ops (<50% ops work). Service Level Objectives (SLOs): target metrics. Service Level Indicators (SLIs): measured metrics. SLAs: contractual guarantees. Incident response: severity levels, escalation, postmortems (blameless). Chaos engineering: proactive reliability testing.

---

### Q581: Container Security?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Image scanning (Trivy, Snyk, Clair) for vulnerabilities. Minimal base images (distroless, Alpine). No root user (USER nonroot). Immutable containers (no runtime patching). Secret management (not in images). Network policies (zero trust). Pod Security Standards (privileged/baseline/restricted). Admission controllers: OPA/Gatekeeper, Kyverno for policy enforcement. Signing: cosign (Sigstore) for image verification. Runtime security: Falco (syscall monitoring), AppArmor/Seccomp profiles. SBOM (Software Bill of Materials).

---

### Q582: CI/CD tools comparison?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - CI/CD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Jenkins: most flexible, plugin ecosystem, Groovy DSL, master/agent, high maintenance. GitLab CI: integrated, .gitlab-ci.yml, runners, Docker/Kubernetes executor, auto DevOps. GitHub Actions: integrated, YAML, hosted runners, marketplace actions, matrix builds. CircleCI: config.yml, parallelism, orbs, fast. ArgoCD: GitOps CD tool, syncs Kubernetes to Git state. Flux: continuous delivery for K8s, Git as source of truth. Spinnaker: multi-cloud CD, complex.

---

### Q583: Cloud Cost Optimization?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - AWS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Right-sizing: match resource size to actual usage (no over-provisioning). Reserved Instances: 1-3 year commitment for discount. Spot Instances: unused capacity (up to 90% off), preemptible. Auto-scaling: scale down during low traffic. Storage tiering: S3 Standard -> Infrequent Access -> Glacier. Data transfer costs: keep within region. Serverless: pay per execution (Lambda, Fargate). Tools: AWS Cost Explorer, Trusted Advisor, third-party (CloudHealth, Vantage). Tag resources for cost allocation.

---

### Q584: What is GitOps?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - GitOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Git as single source of truth for declarative infrastructure and application configuration. Desired state in Git, operator syncs to achieve state. ArgoCD / Flux: pull-based (operator watches Git, syncs K8s). Benefits: versioned history, audit trail, easy rollback, review via PRs, single pane of glass. Principles: declarative config, Git as source of truth, automated sync, drift correction. Compared to CI/CD push-based: GitOps operator runs in cluster, doesn't need external access.

---

### Q585: What is a Sidecar Container?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Additional container in same Pod providing supporting functionality. Shares same network namespace and volumes. Examples: Envoy proxy (service mesh), log shipper (Filebeat), config reloader, secrets provider. Benefits: encapsulated and reusable, independent lifecycle, language-agnostic. Sidecar vs Init container: init runs to completion (startup), sidecar runs alongside (runtime).

---

### Q586: What is Kubernetes RBAC?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Role-Based Access Control. Role (namespace-level) / ClusterRole (cluster-wide): permissions (verbs on resources). RoleBinding / ClusterRoleBinding: binds Role to subjects (User, Group, ServiceAccount). Default: deny all. ServiceAccount: for Pod identity (not human). Best practices: least privilege, specific ServiceAccounts per app, namespaces for isolation. Tools: kubectl auth can-i (check permission). OIDC integration for SSO.

---

### Q587: Cloud Networking (VPC)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - AWS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
VPC (Virtual Private Cloud): isolated virtual network. Subnets: public (route to Internet Gateway), private (no direct internet), isolated (no NAT). Security Groups: stateful instance-level firewall (allow rules only). Network ACLs: stateless subnet-level firewall (allow/deny rules). NAT Gateway/Instance: private subnet outbound internet. VPC Peering: connect VPCs. Transit Gateway: hub-and-spoke VPC connectivity. VPN: site-to-site IPsec. Direct Connect: dedicated physical connection. PrivateLink: access services privately within AWS. VPC Endpoints: S3/DynamoDB without internet.

---

### Q588: Container Orchestration comparison?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Kubernetes: industry standard, complex, massive ecosystem, steep learning curve. Docker Swarm: simpler, Docker-native, less features, limited scaling. Nomad (HashiCorp): simpler, single binary, supports containers + non-containers, integrates with Consul/Vault. Mesos/Marathon: Apache, older, less popular. AWS ECS: AWS-native, simpler than K8s, Fargate (serverless). AWS EKS: managed K8s. Azure AKS, GCP GKE.

---

### Q589: What is CircleCI vs Jenkins?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - CI/CD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CircleCI: SaaS, YAML config, parallelism, orbs, caching, fast setup, less maintenance. Jenkins: self-hosted, most extensible (plugins), Groovy DSL, master/agent architecture, mature. CircleCI better for: quick setup, cloud-native. Jenkins better for: complex pipelines, on-premise, deep customization. Both support Docker, K8s, artifact management.

---

### Q590: Cloud Security best practices?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
IAM: least privilege, roles (not users), no root keys. Network: private subnets, security groups (allow only needed), VPC flow logs. Data: encryption at rest (KMS) and in transit (TLS). Key rotation. Monitoring: CloudTrail (API logging), GuardDuty (threat detection), AWS Config (compliance). Secrets: Secrets Manager (rotation), Parameter Store. Infrastructure: IaC scanning (Checkov, tfsec), CIS benchmarks. Incident response: playbooks, automated containment. Shared Responsibility Model: AWS secures cloud, customer secures IN cloud.

---

### Q591: Python in DevOps?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Python
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Python widely used in DevOps: Ansible (config mgmt YAML/JSON -> Python modules), Boto3 (AWS SDK), CDK (AWS Cloud Development Kit - define cloud resources in Python), Fabric (remote execution), Invoke (task runner), Pyinfra (automation), SaltStack. Use for: custom automation, API wrappers, CLI tools, data processing (log parsing), infrastructure scripting. Lambda functions (Python is first-class).

---

### Q592: What is Virtualization?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Running multiple virtual machines on single physical hardware via hypervisor. Type 1 (Bare metal): Hyper-V, ESXi, KVM - directly on hardware. Type 2 (Hosted): VirtualBox, VMware Workstation - on host OS. Each VM has full OS, kernel, apps. Overhead: full OS per VM. Containerization is lighter (share host kernel). Snapshot and migration features.

---

### Q593: What is a Reverse Proxy (Nginx)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Nginx: high-performance HTTP server and reverse proxy. Use: load balancing (upstream), static file serving, SSL termination, rate limiting (limit_req), caching, compression, URL rewriting, authentication (basic auth, OAuth proxy). Config: location blocks, try_files, proxy_pass. Event-driven, async architecture (handles many connections with few threads). Competition: Apache (process-based), Caddy (auto HTTPS, simpler).

---

### Q594: What is Vault (HashiCorp)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Secret management: dynamic secrets, encryption as a service, leasing/renewal, revocation. Storage backend: integrated storage (Raft), Consul, file. Secrets engines: KV, database (dynamic DB creds), AWS (dynamic IAM), PKI (dynamic certs), Transit (encryption). Auth methods: token, LDAP, Kubernetes, AWS IAM, OIDC. Audit log: all operations logged. Vault Agent for sidecar secret injection.

---

### Q595: Database in container (stateful)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Running databases in containers is debated. Pros: portability, same infra as apps, CI/CD for schema. Cons: state management complexity, data loss risk (ephemeral disks), performance overhead (network, storage), backup complexity. Run DB on: dedicated nodes (taints/tolerations), local SSDs (not network storage), StatefulSet with stable storage. Alternatives: managed DB services (RDS, Cloud SQL, Azure SQL Database) for production.

---

### Q596: Prometheus architecture?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Monitoring
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pull-based monitoring: Prometheus server scrapes metrics from targets at configured intervals. Exporters: node_exporter (system metrics), kube-state-metrics (K8s objects), cAdvisor (container metrics), application-specific (/metrics endpoint). Alertmanager: deduplicates, groups, routes alerts. Pushgateway: for ephemeral/batch jobs (push metrics). Service discovery: K8s, Consul, file-based. Storage: local TSDB (time-series DB), remote write to long-term storage (Thanos, Cortex, VictoriaMetrics). PromQL query language.

---

### Q597: What is Jaeger/Zipkin (Tracing)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Monitoring
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Distributed tracing: trace request across microservices. Trace = tree of spans. Span: unit of work with name, duration, tags, logs. Context propagation: traceId, spanId via HTTP headers (traceparent, x-request-id). Sampling: head-based (pre-decide which traces to sample), tail-based (decide after trace complete). Jaeger: CNCF, HotROD demo, Jaeger Query UI. Zipkin: older, simpler. OpenTelemetry: unified standard for traces, metrics, logs. Instrument client libraries.

---

### Q598: Chaos Engineering (Chaos Monkey)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Netflix Chaos Monkey: randomly terminate EC2 instances in production to test resilience. Part of Simian Army. Tools: Chaos Mesh (K8s-native), Litmus (K8s), Gremlin (SaaS), Chaos Toolkit. Experiment types: pod kill, network latency, CPU stress, disk failure, DNS failure. Principles: blast radius limited, hypothesis-driven, automated experiments, production (but careful). GameDays: scheduled resilience testing.

---

### Q599: What is S3 storage classes?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - AWS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
S3 Standard: frequent access, 99.99% availability, 99.999999999% durability. S3 Intelligent-Tiering: auto-move between tiers (monitoring fee). S3 Standard-IA: infrequent access (but rapid when needed), lower storage fee + retrieval cost. S3 One Zone-IA: less available (single AZ), lower cost. S3 Glacier Instant Retrieval: archive with ms retrieval. S3 Glacier Flexible Retrieval: minutes to hours. S3 Glacier Deep Archive: 12h retrieval, lowest cost. Lifecycle policies auto-transition between classes.

---

### Q600: What is SQS vs SNS vs EventBridge?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - AWS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SQS (Simple Queue Service): message queue, pull-based (consumer polls). Standard (at-least-once, best-effort ordering) vs FIFO (exactly-once, strict ordering). Dead-letter queue for failed messages. Visibility timeout (message hidden while processing). SNS (Simple Notification Service): pub-sub, push-based. Topics -> subscribers (SQS, Lambda, Email, HTTP). Fan-out: single SNS message -> multiple SQS queues. EventBridge: event bus for SaaS integrations. More features: schema registry, filtering, replay, cross-account.

---

### Q601: Kubernetes Namespaces?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Virtual clusters within a physical cluster. Resource isolation: quotas (ResourceQuota), limits (LimitRange). Network policies per namespace. RBAC per namespace. Default namespaces: default, kube-system, kube-public, kube-node-lease. Use: separate environments (dev/staging/prod), multi-tenancy, team isolation. DNS: service.namespace.svc.cluster.local. Context: kubectl config set-context --namespace=my-ns.

---

### Q602: What is Terraform Modules?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Terraform
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Reusable infrastructure components. Source: local paths, Terraform Registry, GitHub, S3. module "vpc" { source = "terraform-aws-modules/vpc/aws" version = "5.0.0" }. Input variables, output values. Benefits: standardization, reuse across teams/projects, versioning. Module composition: combine modules to build complete infrastructure. Private registry: Terraform Cloud/Enterprise.

---

### Q603: What is Cloudflare?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - CDN
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CDN + security + DNS + more. Reverse proxy: terminates connection, forwards to origin. Features: CDN (caching static/dynamic), DDoS protection (anycast network absorbs attacks), WAF (OWASP rules), SSL/TLS (Flexible/Full/Full Strict), Argo Smart Routing, Workers (edge compute), Pages (static hosting), Load Balancing, Rate Limiting, Bot Management. Global anycast network. Free tier generous. DNS: fastest propagation (global network).

---

### Q604: What is a CD Pipeline (Continuous Delivery vs Continuous Deployment)?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - CI/CD
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Continuous Delivery: code changes automatically built, tested, and prepared for release. Manual approval to deploy to production. Continuous Deployment: every change that passes pipeline auto-deploys to production. CD builds on CI. Benefits for CD: faster time to market, reduced manual error, frequent releases (smaller changes). Requires: good test coverage, feature flags, monitoring, rollback capability.

---

### Q605: What is Azure DevOps?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Azure
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Microsoft DevOps platform: Azure Repos (Git repos), Azure Pipelines (CI/CD, multi-platform), Azure Boards (work items, kanban), Azure Test Plans (manual/exploratory testing), Azure Artifacts (package feeds - NuGet, npm, Maven). YAML pipelines: multi-stage, jobs/steps, variables, templates. Supports: .NET, Java, Python, Node.js, Docker, K8s. Self-hosted agents or Microsoft-hosted.

---

### Q606: What is a Blue-Green Deployment?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two identical environments: Blue (current), Green (new). Route all traffic to Blue. Deploy new version to Green. Test Green. Switch traffic to Green (load balancer/router). Rollback: switch back to Blue. Reduces downtime (instant switch). Requires double infrastructure (temporarily). Canary deployment: gradually shift small % of traffic to new version. A/B testing: different versions for different user segments.

---

### Q607: What is ELK Stack?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Monitoring
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Elasticsearch (search/analytics engine), Logstash (data processing pipeline), Kibana (visualization). Beats (lightweight data shippers): Filebeat (log files), Metricbeat (system metrics), Heartbeat (uptime). Alternative: Elastic Agent (unified). Cloud: Elastic Cloud. Competitors: Loki (Grafana - log aggregation), Splunk (commercial). Use: centralized logging, application debugging, security analytics (SIEM), infrastructure monitoring.

---

### Q608: Kubernetes Resource Limits?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
requests: minimum guaranteed resources (scheduling decision). limits: maximum allowed (throttled/dropped). CPU: compressible (throttled if exceeded). Memory: incompressible (OOM killed if exceeded). Service QoS classes: Guaranteed (limits=requests), Burstable (requests < limits), BestEffort (no requests/limits). Overcommit ratio: total requests > node capacity (allows more Pods). LimitRange enforces default per namespace. ResourceQuota limits total per namespace.

---

### Q609: What is Azure/AWS/GCP comparison?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
AWS: largest market share, broadest services, oldest, most mature. Azure: best for Microsoft stack (.NET, SQL Server, Active Directory integration), hybrid cloud (Azure Arc). GCP: strong in data/ML (BigQuery, Vertex AI), Kubernetes (GKE originated), networking (global fiber). All provide: compute, storage, database, networking, serverless, ML/AI, IoT. Pricing complexity varies. Multi-cloud strategy for avoiding vendor lock-in.

---

### Q610: What is a CronJob?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Runs Jobs on schedule (cron format). spec.schedule: "*/5 * * * *" (every 5 min). spec.jobTemplate: defines Job spec. Starting deadline, concurrency policy (Allow/Forbid/Replace), successful jobs history limit. suspend field to pause. Use: database backups, report generation, log rotation, data cleanup.

---

### Q611: Service Discovery patterns?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Client-side: consumer queries registry (Eureka, Consul) for available instances, load balances itself. Server-side: load balancer (ELB/K8s Service) handles discovery. DNS-based: BIND, route53, K8s DNS (CoreDNS). Consul: service mesh (connect), KV store, health checks. K8s: Services resolved via DNS (SRV records). etcd: used by K8s and Cloud Foundry.

---

### Q612: What is SBOM?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Software Bill of Materials: inventory of all components (libraries, packages, licenses) in software. Formats: SPDX, CycloneDX. Generation: syft, trivy, gradle/maven plugins. Use: vulnerability management (cross-reference CVEs), license compliance, supply chain security. Executive Order (US) mandates SBOM for government software.

---

### Q613: What is DaemonSet?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensures all (or some) nodes run a copy of Pod. As nodes added/removed, DaemonSet adds/removes Pods. Use: log collectors (Fluentd, Filebeat), monitoring agents (Prometheus node_exporter, Datadog agent), kube-proxy, networking (Calico, Cilium). nodeSelector/affinity for subset of nodes. Rolling update strategy.

---

### Q614: What is Terraform Workspace?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Terraform
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Multiple state files for same configuration. terraform workspace new dev, terraform workspace select prod. Separate state per workspace (default, dev, prod). Remote backend: terraform.workspace interpolation. Better approach: separate directories per environment (avoid accidental production changes). Terragrunt: keep configurations DRY, manage multiple environments.

---

### Q615: Deployment strategies?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Recreate: terminate old version, deploy new. Simple, downtime. Rolling Update: gradually replace Pods (K8s Deployment default). Blue-Green: two environments, switch traffic. Canary: small % traffic -> new version, monitor, gradually increase. A/B testing: different versions for different users. Shadow/Mirroring: new version receives copy of real traffic (no impact on response). Feature flags: deploy code inactive, toggle on.

---

### Q616: What is a ConfigMap hot reload?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ConfigMap changes NOT automatically reloaded in running containers. Need to: restart Pod (kubectl rollout restart), use sidecar reloader (ConfigMap Reload, Reloader), or watch K8s API for changes. Environment variables: cannot hot reload (only on Pod creation). Volume mounts: can detect changes (application must watch file). Better approach: external config service (Spring Cloud Config, Consul) for dynamic config.

---

### Q617: What is Knative?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Serverless
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Kubernetes-based serverless platform. Serving: auto-scaling (including zero), request-driven, revisioning, traffic splitting. Eventing: event-driven architecture, triggers, brokers, channels. Scale to zero when idle (scale up on request). Builds on K8s (Istio/Contour for ingress). Use: event-driven apps, serverless on K8s (alternative to Lambda on-premises). Operators: knative-serving, knative-eventing.

---

### Q618: What is Docker Networking?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Docker
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Bridge (default): isolated network per host, port mapping. Host: share host network (no isolation). Overlay: multi-host networking (Docker Swarm/K8s). None: no networking. Macvlan: assign MAC addresses to containers (appear as physical devices). Docker Compose creates bridge network. docker network create. DNS resolution via container name (Compose) or links (legacy).

---

### Q619: What is Ansible?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Config Management
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Agentless configuration management tool (SSH-based). YAML playbooks: plays -> tasks -> modules. Inventory: list of hosts (static or dynamic from cloud). idempotent: runs same result regardless of state. Modules: apt, yum, copy, template, service, command, docker, kubernetes. Roles: reusable playbook components (tasks, handlers, templates, defaults, vars). ansible-galaxy: role repository. Tower/AWX: web UI. Good for: server setup, app deployment, config management. Not as good as Terraform for provisioning.

---

### Q620: Observability with OpenTelemetry?
**Topic:** DevOps & Cloud - Monitoring
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
OpenTelemetry (OTel): unified standard for telemetry data (traces, metrics, logs). Collector: vendor-agnostic processing pipeline (receivers -> processors -> exporters). Auto-instrumentation for popular frameworks. Manual instrumentation via SDK. Semantic conventions for standard attributes. Exports to: Jaeger, Zipkin, Prometheus, Datadog, New Relic, AWS X-Ray, Azure Monitor. OTLP protocol. Replaces OpenTracing and OpenCensus.

## Deep Learning

### Q691: Neural network basics?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Artificial Neural Network: input layer -> hidden layers -> output layer. Each neuron: weighted sum of inputs + bias -> activation function. w1*x1 + w2*x2 + ... + b. Feedforward: input propagates through layers. Backpropagation: compute gradient of loss w.r.t. weights (chain rule), update weights via gradient descent. Activation functions: ReLU (most common), Sigmoid (output 0-1), Tanh (-1 to 1), Leaky ReLU, Swish. Loss functions: MSE (regression), Cross-Entropy (classification). Optimizers: SGD, Adam (adaptive learning rate), RMSprop.

---

### Q692: Activation functions comparison?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Sigmoid: 0 to 1, smooth, for binary classification output. Problem: vanishing gradient (saturated neurons have near-zero gradient), not zero-centered. Tanh: -1 to 1, zero-centered (helps convergence). Still vanishing gradient. ReLU: max(0,x), fast, no vanishing gradient for positive values. Problem: dead neurons (dying ReLU - never activate). Leaky ReLU: small positive slope for negative (0.01x). Parametric ReLU: learnable alpha. ELU: negative values, smooth. Swish: x * sigmoid(x), found via NAS. GELU: used in Transformers (GPT, BERT). Softmax: multi-class output (probabilities sum to 1). Modern: ReLU in hidden, Softmax/Sigmoid in output.

---

### Q693: What is Backpropagation?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Algorithm to train neural networks: compute gradient of loss w.r.t. each weight by chain rule from output to input. 1. Forward pass: compute predictions. 2. Compute loss. 3. Backward pass: compute dL/dW for each layer (gradient). 4. Update weights: W = W - lr * dL/dW. Chain rule: dL/dW1 = dL/dOut * dOut/dZ * dZ/dW1. Computational graph: nodes = operations, edges = tensors. Automatic differentiation: PyTorch (autograd), TensorFlow (GradientTape). Vanishing gradient: gradients become very small in deep networks. Exploding gradient: gradients become very large. Solutions: proper initialization (Xavier/He), batch norm, ReLU, residual connections.

---

### Q694: CNN (Convolutional Neural Network)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning - CNN
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
For grid-like data (images, time series). Convolution layer: learnable filters slide over input, producing feature maps. Key properties: translation equivariance, parameter sharing, local connectivity. Pooling layer (MaxPool, AvgPool): reduce spatial dimensions. Fully Connected layer at end for classification. Architectures: LeNet (1998), AlexNet (2012 - ImageNet breakthrough), VGG (small 3x3 filters, deep), ResNet (skip connections - solved vanishing gradient), Inception/GoogLeNet (parallel convs 1x1, 3x3, 5x5), DenseNet (dense connections), EfficientNet (compound scaling). Transfer learning: use pretrained ImageNet weights, fine-tune on custom dataset.

---

### Q695: RNN and LSTM?
**Topic:** Deep Learning - RNN
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
RNN (Recurrent Neural Network): processes sequences (text, time series, audio). Hidden state passed between time steps. Problems: vanishing gradient (long sequences), difficulty capturing long-range dependencies. LSTM (Long Short-Term Memory): designed to avoid vanishing gradient. Cell state (long-term memory) + hidden state. Gates: forget gate (what to discard), input gate (what to store), output gate (what to output). GRU (Gated Recurrent Unit): simplified LSTM (reset + update gates). LSTM/GRU handle sequences up to ~100-200 steps. Bidirectional LSTM: processes sequence forward + backward. Stacked LSTM: multiple layers.

---

### Q696: Transformers architecture?
**Topic:** Deep Learning - Transformers
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
"Attention is All You Need" (Vaswani et al., 2017). Encoder-Decoder structure. Key innovation: Self-Attention mechanism. No recurrence (fully parallelizable). Components: Input Embedding + Positional Encoding (since no RNN). Self-Attention: Q (query), K (key), V (value). Attention(Q,K,V) = softmax(Q*K^T / sqrt(d_k)) * V. Multi-Head Attention: multiple attention heads in parallel (capture different relationships). Feed-Forward Network (FFN): two linear layers with ReLU. Add & Norm: residual connection + layer normalization. Encoder: N layers of Multi-Head Attn + FFN. Decoder: same + Masked Self-Attn (prevent looking ahead) + Cross-Attention (attends to encoder). Used by: BERT (encoder-only), GPT (decoder-only), T5 (encoder-decoder).

---

### Q697: Attention mechanism?
**Topic:** Deep Learning - Transformers
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compute weighted sum of values based on similarity between query and keys. Scaled Dot-Product Attention: Attention(Q,K,V) = softmax(Q*K^T / sqrt(d_k)) * V. Softmax gives attention weights (how much each position attends to others). sqrt(d_k) scaling prevents large dot products pushing softmax to extreme gradients. Multi-Head: h parallel attention heads (concatenated then projected). Allows model to attend to different positions for different reasons. Self-attention: Q, K, V from same sequence. Cross-attention: Q from decoder, K,V from encoder. Masked attention: prevents attending to future positions (autoregressive). Quadratic complexity O(n^2) - limitation for long sequences.

---

### Q698: PyTorch basics?
**Topic:** Deep Learning - PyTorch
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Dynamic computation graph (define-by-run). Tensor: GPU-capable array (like NumPy). torch.tensor([1,2,3]). autograd: automatic differentiation. tensor.requires_grad=True, tensor.backward(), tensor.grad. Model: torch.nn.Module (define layers in init, forward method). Loss: torch.nn.L1Loss, MSELoss, CrossEntropyLoss. Optimizer: torch.optim.SGD, Adam. Data: Dataset and DataLoader (iterable, batching, shuffling). Training loop: for epoch in range(n): for batch in dataloader: optimizer.zero_grad(); loss = model(batch); loss.backward(); optimizer.step(). Device: model.to('cuda'), tensor.to('cuda'). DataParallel/DistributedDataParallel for multi-GPU. TorchScript for production. torch.compile (PT2) for JIT optimization.

---

### Q699: TensorFlow vs PyTorch?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
PyTorch: dynamic graphs (easier debugging, Pythonic), eager execution, stronger in research, more intuitive. TensorFlow: static graphs (TF1) or eager (TF2 via Keras), production deployment (TF Serving, TFLite, TensorFlow.js), TFX for end-to-end ML pipelines. Currently: PyTorch dominates research (95%+ papers), TF still strong in production. Choosing: research -> PyTorch, production (TPU, mobile, web) -> TensorFlow. Both excellent. JAX for high-performance research (functional, XLA compilation).

---

### Q700: Transfer Learning?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Use pretrained model (trained on large dataset like ImageNet) as starting point for new task. Freeze early layers (general features: edges, textures). Fine-tune later layers (task-specific features). Benefits: less data needed, faster training, better performance. Types: feature extraction (freeze entire backbone, train new classifier), fine-tune (unfreeze some/all layers, continue training). Progressive unfreezing: gradually unfreeze layers from top. Domain adaptation: pretrained on source domain, fine-tune on target. Common pretrained: ResNet, EfficientNet, BERT, GPT.

---

### Q701: Batch Normalization?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Normalize layer inputs: subtract batch mean, divide by batch std. Learnable scale (gamma) and shift (beta). Benefits: reduces internal covariate shift, allows higher learning rate, reduces gradient dependence on initialization, acts as regularizer (noise from batch statistics). Training: per-batch statistics. Inference: running average of mean/std. Implementation: BatchNorm1d (linear), BatchNorm2d (conv). LayerNorm: normalizes across features (used in Transformers). InstanceNorm: per-channel per-sample. GroupNorm: intermediate between LayerNorm and InstanceNorm.

---

### Q702: Dropout?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Regularization: randomly drop p% of neurons during training (set to 0). Forces network to learn redundant representations, prevents co-adaptation. Efficient approximation of bagging (training many subnetworks). p = 0.2-0.5 (higher for larger layers). During inference: all neurons active, outputs scaled by (1-p) (inverted dropout: training output divided by (1-p)). ReLU + Dropout common combination. Variants: Spatial Dropout (drop entire channels), Alpha Dropout (for SELU activation), Monte Carlo Dropout (dropout at inference for uncertainty estimation).

---

### Q703: Gradient Descent variants?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Batch GD: compute gradient over entire dataset (accurate, slow, can't handle large data). SGD: compute gradient per sample (fast, noisy updates, escapes local minima). Mini-batch GD: compromise (batch of 32-256). Momentum: accumulate past gradients (smooth updates, escape local minima). v = beta*v - lr*grad; params += v. Nesterov: look ahead before stepping (faster convergence). Adagrad: per-parameter learning rate (divides by sqrt(sum of squared gradients)). RMSprop: moving average of squared gradients. Adam: Momentum + RMSprop + bias correction (most popular). AdamW: Adam with decoupled weight decay (better than L2 regularization). Learning rate schedules: step decay, cosine annealing, warmup, cyclic.

---

### Q704: Loss functions?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Regression: MSE (L2 - penalizes large errors), MAE (L1 - robust to outliers), Huber Loss (smooth MAE/MSE combination). Binary Classification: Binary Cross-Entropy (BCE), Hinge Loss (SVM), Focal Loss (for imbalanced). Multi-class Classification: Categorical Cross-Entropy, Sparse CCE (when labels are integers). Contrastive: Triplet Loss (face recognition), Contrastive Loss (Siamese networks), NT-Xent (SimCLR - self-supervised). Generative: KL Divergence, Wasserstein Loss (GANs). Segmentation: Dice Loss, IoU Loss. Object Detection: YOLO loss, Focal Loss (RetinaNet).

---

### Q705: Overfitting in deep learning?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Deep networks prone to overfitting (millions of parameters). Prevention: more data (augmentation, synthetic). Regularization: L1/L2 weight decay, dropout, early stopping. Data augmentation: rotation, flip, crop, color jitter (images), back-translation (text). Transfer learning: start from pretrained, fine-tune with small learning rate. Batch normalization: slight regularization effect. Reduce model size: fewer layers/neurons, bottleneck layers. Label smoothing: soften one-hot targets (prevents overconfidence). Mixup: linear interpolation between training samples. Stochastic Depth (ResNets): randomly drop layers. Weight Decay separate from Adam (AdamW).

---

### Q706: GANs (Generative Adversarial Networks)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two networks competing: Generator (G) creates fake data, Discriminator (D) distinguishes real vs fake. Min-max game: G tries to fool D, D tries to detect G. Loss: D maximizes log(D(x)) + log(1-D(G(z))). G minimizes log(1-D(G(z))). After training: G can generate realistic data from random noise. Challenges: mode collapse (G generates limited variety), training instability (balancing G and D). Variants: DCGAN (convolutional), WGAN (Wasserstein loss - stable), CycleGAN (unpaired image translation), StyleGAN (high-quality faces), BigGAN. Use: image generation, super-resolution, style transfer, data augmentation.

---

### Q707: VAEs (Variational Autoencoders)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Generative model. Encoder outputs mean and log-variance of latent distribution. Reparameterization trick: sample = mean + std * epsilon (epsilon ~ N(0,1)). Allows gradient flow through sampling. Decoder reconstructs from latent sample. Loss: reconstruction loss (input vs output) + KL divergence (regularizes latent to follow prior N(0,1)). Beta-VAE: weighted KL term for disentangled representations. Applications: anomaly detection (high reconstruction error), image generation, representation learning. Not as sharp images as GANs but more stable training and better latent space structure.

---

### Q708: Encoder-Decoder models?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Sequence-to-sequence: encoder maps input to context vector, decoder generates output from context. Used for: machine translation, summarization, image captioning. LSTM Encoder-Decoder: encoder last hidden state -> decoder initial state. Problems: context bottleneck (fixed-size vector for long sequences). Attention mechanism: decoder computes weighted context from all encoder hidden states. Transformer: eliminates recurrence entirely, parallelizable, handles long sequences with self-attention.

---

### Q709: Word Embeddings (Word2Vec, GloVe)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Dense vector representation of words (learned from large corpus). Properties: similar words close together, analogies (king - man + woman = queen). Word2Vec: CBOW (predict target from context) or Skip-gram (predict context from target). Training: large corpus, negative sampling for efficiency. GloVe: count-based (co-occurrence matrix factorization). FastText: subword information (handles OOV, morphology). Contextual embeddings (ELMo, BERT, GPT): different embedding per context ("bank" in river vs money). Modern NLP uses contextual embeddings exclusively.

---

### Q710: Sequence-to-Sequence with Attention?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Encoder reads input sequence, produces hidden states. Decoder generates output, with attention mechanism allowing decoder to focus on relevant input parts. Attention weights: decoder hidden state vs each encoder hidden state -> softmax -> weighted sum. Luong attention (dot product, general, concat). Bahdanau attention (additive). Benefits: handles long sequences, better performance, interpretability (visualize attention weights). Used in: Neural Machine Translation (NMT), text summarization, speech recognition, image captioning. Replaced by Transformer (self-attention).

---

### Q711: ResNet and Skip Connections?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Residual Network (ResNet, 2015): introduces skip connections (identity shortcut). F(x) = H(x) - x. Layer learns residual (F(x)), output = F(x) + x. Solves vanishing gradient in very deep networks (gradient flows directly through skip connection). Allows training 100+ layers (152-layer ResNet won ILSVRC 2015). Variants: ResNeXt (grouped convolutions), Wide ResNet (wider, shallower), DenseNet (dense connections: each layer receives all previous feature maps - feature reuse). EfficientNet: neural architecture search (NAS) for optimal depth/width/resolution scaling.

---

### Q712: Data Augmentation techniques?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Images: rotation, flip (horizontal), crop/resize, color jitter (brightness, contrast, saturation, hue), noise addition, cutout/random erasing (mask random region), mixup (blend images), CutMix (cut and paste patches), AutoAugment (learned augmentation policy), RandAugment (random magnitude), AugMix (diverse augmentations). Text: synonym replacement, back-translation, random insertion/deletion/swap, EDA (Easy Data Augmentation), MixText. Audio: noise injection, time stretching, pitch shifting, SpecAugment (mask spectrogram regions). Data augmentation is crucial for generalization when limited data.

---

### Q713: Explainable AI (XAI)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Methods to explain ML/DL predictions. LIME: local surrogate model (perturb input, see how predictions change). SHAP: Shapley values from game theory (feature contribution to prediction). Grad-CAM: visualize CNN attention regions (heatmap over image). Integrated Gradients: path integral of gradients. Attention visualization: for Transformer models. Feature importance (tree-based). Partial Dependence Plots (PDP). ICE plots. Model-specific: coefficients (linear), decision tree structure. Trade-off: accuracy vs interpretability. Increasingly important for regulated industries (healthcare, finance).

---

### Q714: Self-Supervised Learning?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Learning from unlabeled data by creating pretext tasks. Model learns useful representations without manual labels. Contrastive learning: pull positive pairs together, push negatives apart. SimCLR (image augmentations -> maximiye agreement between augmented views). BYOL: no negative pairs (predicts online from target network). MoCo: momentum contrast (dynamic dictionary). MAE (Masked Autoencoder): mask random patches, reconstruct. NLP: BERT (mask tokens, predict). Self-supervised pretraining + supervised fine-tuning = dominant paradigm.

---

### Q715: Graph Neural Networks (GNN)?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Neural networks for graph data (nodes + edges). Message passing: each node aggregates features from neighbors, updates own representation. Layers: Graph Convolutional Network (GCN) - mean aggregation, GraphSAGE - sample + aggregate, GAT - attention-based aggregation. Readout: combine all node features for graph-level prediction. Use: molecular property prediction (drug discovery), social network analysis, recommendation (bipartite graphs), knowledge graph completion, physics simulation. Challenges: oversmoothing (many layers), scalability (large graphs), inductive vs transductive.

---

### Q716: Training tricks in Deep Learning?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Learning rate scheduling: warmup (linear increase), cosine annealing, ReduceLROnPlateau. Gradient clipping: prevent exploding gradients (max_norm). Weight initialization: Xavier (sigmoid/tanh), He/Kaiming (ReLU). Batch normalization after conv/linear layers. Layer normalization for Transformers. Gradient accumulation: simulate larger batch size. EMA (Exponential Moving Average) of model weights for inference. Label smoothing. Mixed precision training (float16). Gradient checkpointing: trade compute for memory. Cyclic LR (SLR). Progressive resizing (training with increasing image size). Swish/SiLU activation.

---

### Q717: Hyperparameter tuning in DL?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Key hyperparameters: learning rate (most important), batch size, optimizer (Adam/SGD), number of layers, hidden size, dropout rate, weight decay, activation function. Learning rate: typically 1e-5 to 1e-3 (smaller for fine-tuning). Batch size: 32-512 (smaller batches -> more regularization). Grid/random search expensive. Bayesian optimization: Optuna, Hyperopt, Ray Tune. Population-based training (PBT): training with hyperparameter mutations. Learning rate range test (LR finder): increase LR exponentially, find steepest descent region.

---

### Q718: Reinforcement Learning basics?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Agent learns through interaction with environment. States (observation) -> actions -> reward. Policy: agent's behavior function (map state -> action). Value function: expected cumulative reward from state. Q-function: expected reward from state-action. Exploration vs exploitation: epsilon-greedy (random actions with probability), UCB, Thompson sampling. Deep RL: DQN (Deep Q-Network - Q-learning with neural net), Policy Gradients (REINFORCE), Actor-Critic (A2C, A3C), PPO (stable, simple), SAC (soft actor-critic), DDPG (continuous control). Use: games (AlphaGo), robotics, autonomous driving, recommendation.

---

### Q719: Autoencoders?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Unsupervised neural network: input -> encoder -> bottleneck (latent) -> decoder -> reconstruction. Loss: reconstruction error (input vs output). Bottleneck forces efficient representation. Undercomplete: bottleneck smaller than input (compression). Denoising Autoencoder: input corrupted, train to recover clean. Sparse Autoencoder: sparsity constraint on latent. Variational Autoencoder (VAE): probabilistic latent. Use: dimensionality reduction, anomaly detection (high reconstruction error), denoising, feature extraction, generative modeling.

---

### Q720: Diffusion Models?
**Topic:** Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Generative model. Forward process: gradually add noise to data (T steps). Reverse process: learn to denoise (predict noise added). Loss: simple MSE on predicted noise. Training: sample t, add noise, predict noise. Sampling: start with pure noise, iteratively denoise. DDPM (Denoising Diffusion Probabilistic Models): equal weight to all timesteps. DDIM: deterministic sampling (faster). Latent Diffusion (Stable Diffusion): diffusion in latent space (VAE encoder/decoder). Text conditioning via cross-attention (CLIP text encoder). Classifier-free guidance: balance diversity vs quality. State-of-the-art in image generation (DALL-E 2/3, Stable Diffusion, Midjourney, Imagen). Better than GANs: stable training, mode coverage.

## Data Structures & Algorithms

### Q251: Array vs Linked List?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Array: contiguous memory, O(1) access by index, O(n) insert/delete (shift), cache-friendly, fixed size. Linked List: scattered memory (nodes with pointers), O(n) access by index, O(1) insert/delete given node reference, dynamic size. Singly linked list: next pointers only. Doubly linked list: prev + next pointers. Circular: tail points to head.

---

### Q252: Reverse a linked list?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Iterative: maintain prev, current, next pointers. While loop: save next, point current.next to prev, move prev and current forward. Time: O(n), Space: O(1). Recursive: reverse rest, point head.next.next = head, head.next = null. Return new head. Time: O(n), Space: O(n) for recursion stack.

---

### Q253: Detect cycle in linked list?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Floyd's Tortoise and Hare: slow moves 1 step, fast moves 2 steps. If cycle exists, they meet within the cycle. To find cycle start: after meeting, reset one pointer to head, both move 1 step until they meet at cycle start. Time: O(n), Space: O(1).

---

### Q254: Find middle of linked list?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Tortoise and Hare: slow +1, fast +2. When fast reaches end, slow is at middle. For even length, return second middle (or first depending on implementation).

---

### Q255: Merge two sorted linked lists?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Dummy head + two-pointer comparison. while both not null: take smaller, advance pointer. Append remaining. Time: O(n+m), Space: O(1). Recursive also possible.

---

### Q256: Stack vs Queue?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Stack: LIFO (Last In First Out). Operations: push (top), pop, peek. Queue: FIFO (First In First Out). Operations: enqueue (rear), dequeue (front), peek. Stack uses: recursion (call stack), undo/redo, expression evaluation, DFS. Queue uses: BFS, task scheduling, print spooling, request queuing.

---

### Q257: Implement Queue using Stacks?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two stacks: input stack for enqueue, output stack for dequeue. Enqueue: push to input. Dequeue: if output empty, pop all from input to output. Peek from output. Amortized O(1) per operation.

---

### Q258: Valid Parentheses?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Stack approach: iterate string, push opening brackets ({[), when closing bracket encountered, pop and check if matching. If mismatch or stack not empty at end, invalid. Time: O(n), Space: O(n).

---

### Q259: Binary Tree vs Binary Search Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Binary Tree: each node has at most 2 children. BST: left child < parent < right child (for all nodes). BST provides O(log n) average search/insert/delete (balanced) or O(n) worst (skewed). Tree traversals: Preorder (root-left-right), Inorder (left-root-right -> sorted for BST), Postorder (left-right-root), Level-order (BFS).

---

### Q260: Binary Tree Level Order Traversal?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
BFS using Queue. Enqueue root. While queue not empty: process size nodes (current level), enqueue children. Return List<List<Integer>>. Time: O(n), Space: O(n).

---

### Q261: Validate Binary Search Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Inorder traversal (should be sorted) or recursive range check: each node value must be within (min, max) where min/max are ancestor constraints. Use Long.MIN_VALUE/MAX_VALUE for edge cases with Integer.MIN/MAX.

---

### Q262: Lowest Common Ancestor of BST?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
BST property: if p < root < q, root is LCA. If both smaller, go left. If both larger, go right. Iterative or recursive. Time: O(h), Space: O(1). For binary tree (non-BST): recursive search in left/right, if both return non-null, current is LCA.

---

### Q263: Binary Tree Maximum Depth?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Recursive: 1 + max(maxDepth(left), maxDepth(right)). Base case: null node returns 0. Time: O(n). Iterative: BFS with level counter.

---

### Q264: Balanced Binary Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Height-balanced: depth difference between left and right subtrees <= 1 for ALL nodes. Recursive: compute height (or use -1 for unbalanced). If left or right unbalanced -> return -1. If abs(leftHeight - rightHeight) > 1 -> return -1. Else return 1 + max(left, right).

---

### Q265: Heap data structure?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Complete binary tree stored as array. Max-heap: parent >= children (root is max). Min-heap: parent <= children (root is min). Array representation: root at index 0, left child = 2i+1, right child = 2i+2, parent = (i-1)/2. Heapify: O(log n). Build heap: O(n). Insert (push): add at end, bubble up O(log n). Extract (pop): swap root with last, bubble down O(log n). PriorityQueue in Java.

---

### Q266: Top K Frequent Elements?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Frequency map -> Min-heap of size K (or QuickSelect). Insert (num, frequency) into heap, keep K largest. O(n log k). Bucket sort approach for O(n): array of lists indexed by frequency.

---

### Q267: Graph representations?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Adjacency Matrix: n x n boolean/int matrix. O(1) edge check, O(V^2) space. Dense graphs. Adjacency List: array of lists (neighbors per vertex). O(V+E) space, O(degree) edge check. Sparse graphs. Edge List: list of (u, v, weight). For Kruskal's algorithm.

---

### Q268: BFS vs DFS?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
BFS: Queue-based, level by level, shortest path in unweighted graph, O(V+E). DFS: Stack/recursion-based, explore deeply first, O(V+E). BFS uses more memory (queue). DFS uses less (recursion stack). BFS -> shortest path. DFS -> cycle detection, topological sort, maze solving, connected components.

---

### Q269: Detect cycle in directed graph?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DFS with three colors: WHITE (unvisited), GRAY (visiting), BLACK (visited). If we encounter GRAY node, cycle exists. Kahn's algorithm (topological sort using indegree): if all nodes can be processed (no remaining edges), no cycle. Time: O(V+E).

---

### Q270: Topological Sort?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Linear ordering of DAG where for every edge u->v, u comes before v. Kahn's algorithm (BFS): compute indegrees, push 0-indegree nodes to queue, process (decrement neighbor indegrees, push if 0). DFS-based: postorder stack. Applications: build systems, course prerequisites, task scheduling.

---

### Q271: Dijkstra's Algorithm?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Shortest path in weighted graph (non-negative edges). PriorityQueue (min-heap) of (distance, node). Start: distance[source]=0, all others = INF. Extract min node, relax neighbors (if new distance < old, update and push). O((V+E) log V) with heap. Bellman-Ford handles negative edges, O(VE). Floyd-Warshall: all-pairs shortest paths, O(V^3).

---

### Q272: Bubble Sort?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Repeatedly swap adjacent elements if out of order. After each pass, largest element bubbles to end. Optimized: stop if no swaps in a pass. Time: O(n^2) avg/worst, O(n) best (already sorted). Space: O(1). Stable. Not practical for large data. Use for educational purposes only.

---

### Q273: Merge Sort?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Divide and conquer: split array in half, recursively sort halves, merge. Merge: two-pointer comparison into temp array, copy back. Time: O(n log n) all cases. Space: O(n) auxiliary. Stable. Good for linked lists (O(1) auxiliary space). Parallelizable. External sorting.

---

### Q274: Quick Sort?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Divide and conquer: choose pivot, partition array (elements < pivot, pivot, elements > pivot), recursively sort partitions. Partition: Lomuto (single scan) / Hoare (two pointers, more efficient). Time: O(n log n) avg, O(n^2) worst (bad pivot). Random pivot/median-of-three mitigates worst case. Space: O(log n) in-place. NOT stable. Unstable, but fastest in practice.

---

### Q275: Binary Search?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Search sorted array by repeatedly dividing search interval in half. Compare target with middle element, eliminate half. Time: O(log n). Space: O(1) iterative, O(log n) recursive. Variants: find first/last occurrence (lower bound/upper bound), find insertion position.

---

### Q276: Two Sum problem?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Find indices of two numbers that sum to target. Hash Map approach: iterate array, for each num check if (target - num) exists in map, else add num to map. O(n) time, O(n) space. Sort + two-pointer for O(n log n). Two Sum II (sorted): two pointers from ends.

---

### Q277: Three Sum?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Find all triplets summing to zero. Sort array. For each num[i], two-pointer search in remaining (i+1, n-1). Skip duplicates. O(n^2) time, O(1) extra space (excluding output). Careful: avoid duplicate triplets via early skip.

---

### Q278: Maximum Subarray (Kadane's Algorithm)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
maxEndingHere and maxSoFar. Iterate: maxEndingHere = max(num, maxEndingHere + num). maxSoFar = max(maxSoFar, maxEndingHere). O(n) time, O(1) space. Also tracks start/end indices.

---

### Q279: Longest Substring Without Repeating Characters?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Sliding window with HashMap/Set. Window [left, right). Expand right, add char to set. If duplicate (char in set), shrink left (remove left char from set). Track max window length. O(n) time, O(min(n, m)) space for charset. For ASCII: boolean[256] array.

---

### Q280: Best Time to Buy and Sell Stock?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Single pass: track minPriceSoFar. At each price, calculate profit = price - minPriceSoFar, update maxProfit. O(n). Multiple transactions: sum all positive differences between consecutive days. With cooldown: DP with state machine.

---

### Q281: Clone a Graph?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DFS/BFS with HashMap to track cloned nodes. For each neighbor: if not cloned, recursively clone (DFS) or queue (BFS). Connect neighbors. Avoid infinite loop for cycles.

---

### Q282: Number of Islands?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DFS/BFS on grid. For each '1' not visited, start DFS (mark visited 0s), increment island count. DFS: check bounds, mark '0', recurse in 4 directions. Time: O(m*n). Union-Find also possible.

---

### Q283: Longest Palindromic Substring?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Expand Around Center: for each position (and between positions), expand outward while palindrome. Track longest. O(n^2). Manacher's algorithm: O(n) (linear). DP: boolean dp[i][j] for substring i..j, O(n^2).

---

### Q284: Coin Change (Minimum Coins)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP: dp[amount] = min coins needed. dp[i] = min(dp[i], dp[i - coin] + 1). Initialize dp[0]=0, others = INF. Iterate amounts 1..amount, try each coin. O(amount * coins). Recursive with memoization also works.

---

### Q285: Edit Distance (Levenshtein Distance)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
DP[i][j] = min operations to convert word1[0..i) to word2[0..j). if chars equal: dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j-1]. else: min(insert=dp[i][j-1], delete=dp[i-1][j], replace=dp[i-1][j-1]) + 1. O(m*n). Space optimized: 1D array.

---

### Q286: Knapsack Problem (0/1)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP[i][w] = max value using first i items with weight <= w. Either include item i (if weight[i] <= w): value[i] + dp[i-1][w-weight[i]], or exclude: dp[i-1][w]. Take max. O(n*W). Space optimized: 1D array iterate backwards. Unbounded knapsack: same item multiple times, iterate forward.

---

### Q287: Longest Common Subsequence?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
dp[i][j] = LCS of text1[0..i) and text2[0..j). If chars match: 1 + dp[i-1][j-1]. Else: max(dp[i-1][j], dp[i][j-1]). O(m*n). Reconstruct by backtracking dp table. Space optimized: 2 rows.

---

### Q288: Find Median of Two Sorted Arrays?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Binary search on smaller array. Partition both arrays such that left half contains (m+n+1)/2 elements. Check maxLeft <= minRight. Adjust partition via binary search. O(log(min(m,n))). Handle edge cases (empty arrays).

---

### Q289: Sliding Window Maximum?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Deque (decreasing order). Iterate array, maintain window positions. Remove indices out of window (from front). Remove smaller values (from back). Front is max for current window. O(n) time. Alternative: max-heap (O(n log k)).

---

### Q290: Trie (Prefix Tree)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tree structure for string operations. Each node: children array (size 26 for lowercase) or map, boolean isEnd. Operations: insert (O(L)), search (O(L)), startsWith (O(L)). Applications: autocomplete, spell checker, IP routing (longest prefix matching), word search.

---

### Q291: LRU Cache?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
