HashMap + Doubly Linked List. Map: key -> Node. Linked List: most recently used at head, least recently used at tail. get(): remove node -> move to head. put(): if exists, update+move to head. If full, remove tail + map entry. All O(1). Java: LinkedHashMap with accessOrder=true overrides removeEldestEntry.

---

### Q292: Invert Binary Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Recursive: swap left and right children, recurse on children. Base case: null node returns null. Iterative: BFS/DFS queue. Time: O(n).

---

### Q293: Search in Rotated Sorted Array?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Modified binary search. Find mid. Check which half is sorted (left half sorted if nums[low] <= nums[mid]). If target in sorted half, search there, else search other half. O(log n). Handles duplicates (O(n) worst case when many duplicates).

---

### Q294: Permutations of Array?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Backtracking: track used boolean array, build current permutation. For each position, try each unused element. Recurse, backtrack (mark unused). Time: O(n * n!) total permutations. Unique permutations: sort + skip duplicates.

---

### Q295: Combination Sum?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Backtracking: candidates sorted (optional). At each step, try candidate (can reuse same element). Recurse with updated target. Backtrack (remove last). Prune: skip if candidate > remaining target. Time: O(2^(target/min_candidate)).

---

### Q296: Word Search (Board)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DFS + backtracking on 2D board. For each cell matching word[0], start DFS. In DFS: check bounds, visited, char match. Mark cell visited (temporary char change), recurse in 4 directions. Restore char. Return true if word found. O(m*n*4^L) where L = word length. Prune with early termination.

---

### Q297: Longest Increasing Subsequence?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP: dp[i] = LIS ending at i. dp[i] = 1 + max(dp[j]) for j < i and nums[j] < nums[i]. O(n^2). Patience sorting (binary search): maintain piles (tails array), for each num binary search for position. O(n log n). Not exact sequence, only length.

---

### Q298: Max Area of Island?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DFS from each unvisited '1'. Count cells in island. Track max. DFS: check bounds, if 0/visited return 0. Mark visited (set to 0), return 1 + sum of 4-direction DFS. O(m*n).

---

### Q299: Flatten Binary Tree to Linked List?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Recursive (postorder): flatten left, flatten right. Store temp = root.right. root.right = root.left. root.left = null. Traverse to end of new right (original left), attach temp. Morris traversal O(1) space.

---

### Q300: Merge K Sorted Lists?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Min-Heap of size K. Add heads of all lists. Extract min from heap, add to result, push next node of extracted list. O(N log K) where N = total nodes. Divide and conquer: merge pairs recursively (merge 2 lists at a time). O(N log K).

---

### Q301: Subtree of Another Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Check if root matches subRoot (same tree check), or recurse on left/right. Same tree check: both null -> true. One null -> false. Values equal -> recurse left and right.

---

### Q302: Kth Smallest Element in BST?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Inorder traversal (sorted). Recursive: pass k counter by reference/array. Decrement count at each node, if count becomes 0 return value. Iterative: stack-based inorder. Time: O(H + k). Space: O(H).

---

### Q303: Serialize and Deserialize Binary Tree?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Preorder traversal with null markers. Level order (BFS). String format: "1,2,3,null,null,4,5". Serialize: recursive preorder, append "null" for null children, comma-separated. Deserialize: split string, queue/iterator, recursive build. Time: O(n).

---

### Q304: Rotate Image (Matrix)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Transpose (swap matrix[i][j] with matrix[j][i]) then reverse each row. Or rotate layers: for each layer, rotate four-corner cells. In-place O(n^2). 90 degrees clockwise.

---

### Q305: Spiral Matrix?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Four pointers: top, bottom, left, right. Traverse right (top row, top++), down (right col, right--), left (bottom row, bottom--), up (left col, left++). Repeat until pointers cross. O(m*n). Edge cases: single row/column.

---

### Q306: Set Matrix Zeroes?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
O(m+n) space: rowSet, colSet, iterate mark rows/cols with zero. Second pass: set zeroes. O(1) space: use first row and first column as markers. Handle first row/col separately (store if they need zeroing).

---

### Q307: Word Ladder?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
BFS on word graph. Use queue, visited set. For each word, change each char to 'a'-'z', check if in wordSet and not visited. Track level/step. Return steps when reaching endWord. Build adjacency lazily (no pre-built graph). Time: O(M^2 * N) where M = word length, N = words. Bidirectional BFS optimizes.

---

### Q308: Decode String ("3[a2[c]]" -> "accaccacc")?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two stacks: count stack (for integers), result stack (for previous strings). Iterate: digit -> accumulate to count. '[' -> push current count and result, reset. ']' -> pop count and prev string, repeat prev + current result. Letter -> append to current result. Time: O(n).

---

### Q309: Trapping Rain Water?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Two pointers: left, right, track maxLeft, maxRight. At each step, process the smaller side. Water at position = min(maxLeft, maxRight) - height. Move pointer inward. O(n) time, O(1) space. Other approaches: prefix/suffix max arrays, stack (monotonic decreasing heights).

---

### Q310: LCA in Binary Tree (not BST)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Recursive: if root is null or root matches p/q, return root. Search left and right. If both return non-null, current is LCA. If only one non-null, that's LCA. Time: O(n). Space: O(h) recursion stack.

---

### Q311: Container With Most Water?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two pointers: left (0), right (n-1). area = min(height[left], height[right]) * (right-left). Move the pointer with smaller height inward (since reducing width, need taller height). Track max area. O(n).

---

### Q312: House Robber?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP: at each house i, max = max(rob[i-2] + nums[i], rob[i-1]). O(n). Space optimized: two variables. Circular version: run DP on [0,n-2] and [1,n-1], take max.

---

### Q313: Jump Game?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Greedy: track maxReach (farthest index reachable). Iterate, if i > maxReach return false. Update maxReach = max(maxReach, i + nums[i]). Return true if reachable. Jump Game II (min jumps): BFS-like greedy, track currentEnd and farthest. Time: O(n).

---

### Q314: Product of Array Except Self?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Left prefix products array, right prefix products array. result[i] = left[i-1] * right[i+1]. O(n) time, O(n) space. O(1) space: compute result as left pass (result[i] = prefix product of left), then right pass multiply (suffix product). No division allowed.

---

### Q315: Unique Paths (Grid)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
dp[i][j] = dp[i-1][j] + dp[i][j-1] (only down/right). dp[0][0] = 1. O(m*n). Space optimized: 1D array (dp[j] += dp[j-1]). Combinatorics: C(m+n-2, m-1) = (m+n-2)!/((m-1)!(n-1)!).

---

### Q316: Climbing Stairs?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Fibonacci: dp[n] = dp[n-1] + dp[n-2] (1 step or 2 steps). dp[1]=1, dp[2]=2. O(n). Space: two variables. Closed form: Binet's formula O(log n).

---

### Q317: Palindrome Linked List?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Find middle (slow/fast). Reverse second half. Compare first and reversed second half. Restore if needed. Time: O(n), Space: O(1). Alternatively: copy to array (O(n) space).

---

### Q318: Remove Nth Node From End of List?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two-pointer: fast moves n steps ahead, then slow and fast move together until fast reaches end. slow is at nth-1 from end. Remove slow.next. Dummy head handles edge case (removing head). O(n).

---

### Q319: Meeting Rooms II?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Minimum meeting rooms needed. Separated start/end times, sort both. Two-pointer: if start < end -> increment needed rooms (start pointer++). Else decrement (end pointer++). Track max needed. O(n log n). Alternatively: min-heap of end times.

---

### Q320: Alien Dictionary?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Build adjacency graph from adjacent word pairs (first differing character). Find topological sort. Detect cycle (invalid order). Handle edge cases: identical words (ok), prefix issue (shorter before longer - invalid). Topological sort via DFS or Kahn's algorithm.

---

### Q321: Sudoku Solver?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Backtracking: find empty cell, try '1'-'9'. Validate row, column, 3x3 box. If valid, recurse. If solved, return. Backtrack (reset cell). Time: O(9^(n)). Pruning: validate before recursion.

---

### Q322: N-Queens?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Backtracking: place queens row by row. Track columns, diagonals (row-col), anti-diagonals (row+col) via sets. For each row, try columns. If no conflict, place queen and recurse. Time: O(n!).

---

### Q323: Regular Expression Matching?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
DP[i][j] = match text[0..i) with pattern[0..j). Handle '*' (matches zero or more of preceding char). Initialize dp[0][0]=true, dp[0][j] for patterns like a*b*c*. DP transitions based on pattern char and '*'. O(m*n).

---

### Q324: Find Missing Number (0 to n)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
XOR all numbers from 0 to n with array elements. Missing = XOR result. O(n) time, O(1) space. Alternative: sum formula n*(n+1)/2 - sum(array). Watch for overflow.

---

### Q325: First Missing Positive?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Cyclic sort / index placement: place nums[i] at index nums[i]-1 if in range [1, n]. First index where nums[i] != i+1 is answer. O(n) time, O(1) space.

---

### Q326: Sort Colors (Dutch National Flag)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Three pointers: low (end of 0s), mid (current), high (start of 2s). If nums[mid]==0: swap(low, mid), low++, mid++. If 1: mid++. If 2: swap(mid, high), high--. O(n), O(1). One pass.

---

### Q327: Find All Duplicates in Array?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Mark visited by negating value at index (nums[abs(val)-1] = -abs(nums[abs(val)-1])). If already negative, val is duplicate. O(n), O(1) space assuming values in [1,n].

---

### Q328: Subarray Sum Equals K?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HashMap of prefix sum -> count. For each position, prefixSum - k exists in map -> add count. Update map[prefixSum]++. Handle prefixSum == k case. O(n) time, O(n) space.

---

### Q329: Task Scheduler?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Greedy: most frequent task determines idle slots. maxFreq = max count. maxCount = number tasks with maxFreq. totalIdle = (maxFreq - 1) * (n + 1). Fill remaining tasks in idle slots. Answer = max(tasks.length, (maxFreq-1)*(n+1) + maxCount). O(n).

---

### Q330: K Closest Points to Origin?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Min-heap: insert all points, extract K. O(n log n). Max-heap of size K: keep K closest. O(n log k). QuickSelect: partition by distance, choose Kth smallest. O(n) avg. No sorting needed.

---

### Q331: Design Tic-Tac-Toe?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Track rows[n], cols[n], diagonal, anti-diagonal. Move: increment player's row/col/diag. If any reaches n -> win. O(1) per move. No board storage needed.

---

### Q332: Bulls and Cows?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Bulls: exact matches (same position, same digit). Cows: correct digit wrong position. Count bulls in first pass. For cows: use two count arrays (size 10), increment for secret, decrement for guess, sum of positive = cows (after removing bulls).

---

### Q333: Count Primes (Sieve of Eratosthenes)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
boolean[] isPrime initialized true. Mark 0,1 false. For i = 2 to sqrt(n): if isPrime[i], mark multiples (2*i, 3*i, ...) as false. Count true entries. O(n log log n). Space: O(n).

---

### Q334: Power of Three / Power of Two?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Power of Two: n > 0 && (n & (n-1)) == 0. Power of Three: max power of 3 within int range mod n == 0 (1162261467 % n == 0). Or loop: while n > 1 and n % 3 == 0: n /= 3. Return n == 1.

---

### Q335: Happy Number?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Floyd's cycle detection: slow (sum of squares) and fast (sum twice). If they meet at 1 -> happy. If cycle detected (slow == fast != 1) -> not happy. Or HashSet to detect cycles.

---

### Q336: Excel Sheet Column Title/Number?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Number to Title: while n > 0: n-- (1-indexed), result = char('A' + n % 26) + result, n /= 26. Title to Number: result = 0, for each char: result = result * 26 + (char - 'A' + 1).

---

### Q337: Fraction to Recurring Decimal?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Sign, numerator = abs(n), denominator = abs(d). result = string(numerator/denominator) + ".". HashMap<Long, Integer> remainder to position. While remainder != 0: remainder *= 10, result += remainder/denominator. If remainder repeats -> insert parentheses at stored position.

---

### Q338: Evaluate Reverse Polish Notation?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stack<Integer>. For each token: if operator ("+","-","*","/"): pop two operands (order matters for - and /), apply, push result. Else: push Integer.parseInt(token). Return stack pop. O(n). Handle division truncation toward zero.

---

### Q339: Course Schedule II?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Topological sort via Kahn's algorithm. Build adjacency list and indegree array from prerequisites. Queue courses with indegree 0. Process: add to result, decrement neighbor indegrees, enqueue if 0. If result size != numCourses -> cycle (impossible). Return result.

---

### Q340: Design HashMap?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Array of LinkedList/BST buckets. Load factor threshold. Hash function: key % capacity. Chaining for collisions. get/put/remove: compute hash, traverse bucket, find key.

---

### Q341: Longest Palindromic Subsequence?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP[i][j] = LPS from i to j. If s[i]==s[j]: 2 + dp[i+1][j-1]. Else: max(dp[i+1][j], dp[i][j-1]). Fill diagonally (length increasing). O(n^2). Unlike substring, subsequence doesn't require contiguous characters.

---

### Q342: Minimum Window Substring?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Sliding window with frequency maps (required vs window). Expand right until all chars covered. Then shrink left while still covering, track min window. O(n) time, O(k) space (k = charset). Two pointer technique.

---

### Q343: Word Break?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DP: dp[i] = wordBreak(s[0..i)). dp[0]=true. For i=1..n: for j=0..i: if dp[j] and s[j..i) in dict -> dp[i]=true. O(n^2 * m) for substring. Optimize: BFS/DFS with memoization, Trie for prefix matching.

---

### Q344: Gas Station (Circular Tour)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
If total gas < total cost -> impossible. Greedy: track current tank, start station. Iterate: if tank < 0 (cannot reach next), set start = i+1, reset tank. O(n). Proof: if car starts at A and fails at B, any start between A and B also fails.

---

### Q345: Partition Equal Subset Sum?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
If total sum odd -> false. target = sum/2. DP boolean[n+1][target+1]. dp[i][sum] = dp[i-1][sum] || dp[i-1][sum - nums[i-1]]. Space optimized: 1D array iterate backwards. Or memoized DFS.

---

### Q346: Maximum Product Subarray?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Track maxEndingHere AND minEndingHere (negative * negative = positive). At each step: candidates = (num, num*maxEnding, num*minEnding). maxEnding = max(candidates), minEnding = min(candidates). maxSoFar = max(maxSoFar, maxEnding). O(n).

---

### Q347: Find Peak Element?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Binary search (array not sorted but guarantees peak exists). Compare nums[mid] with nums[mid+1]. If nums[mid] > nums[mid+1]: peak in left half (including mid). Else: peak in right half. O(log n). Multiple peaks, return any.

---

### Q348: Longest Consecutive Sequence?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HashSet of all numbers. For each num, check if num-1 exists (if yes, num is not start of sequence). If not start, skip. If start, count consecutive numbers (num, num+1, num+2...) in set. Track longest. O(n) time, O(n) space.

---

### Q349: Distribute Candies?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Max different types Alice can get = min(unique candy types, n/2). If sister must eat half, she can eat at most half or all unique types.

---

### Q350: Reverse Words in a String?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Trim, split by spaces, reverse array, join. O(n). In-place: reverse entire string, then reverse each word. Handle multiple spaces.

---

### Q351: String Compression?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two pointers: read and write. Count consecutive chars. Write char, write count (if >1). O(n). In-place modification of char array. Handle single char (no count needed).

---

### Q352: Island Perimeter?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
For each land cell, add 4. If neighbor is also land, subtract 2 for each shared edge (overcounted both cells). O(m*n). Or count edges water/boundary.

---

### Q353: First Unique Character in String?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Frequency array/count of 26 or 256. First pass: count. Second pass: return first index with count 1. O(n).

---

### Q354: Ransom Note (Magazine)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Count magazine letters. Decrement for ransom note letters. If any count < 0 -> false. O(n+m). 26-int array for lowercase.

---

### Q355: Intersection of Two Arrays?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
HashSet of first array. Check second array. Return result. For sorted arrays: two-pointer. For duplicates: count frequencies.

---

### Q356: Majority Element (> n/2 times)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Boyer-Moore Voting: candidate = first, count = 1. For each num: if count==0, candidate=num, count=1. If num==candidate, count++ else count--. Verify candidate appears > n/2. O(n) time, O(1) space.

---

### Q357: Find Duplicate Number (no extra space)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Floyd's cycle detection on array as linked list (index -> value). nums[i] contains link to index nums[i]. Slow/fast pointers find cycle. O(n) time, O(1) space. Array values [1, n] guarantee cycle.

---

### Q358: Rotate Array by K?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Reverse all, reverse first k, reverse last n-k. Handle k > n: k %= n. O(n) time, O(1) space.

---

### Q359: Remove Duplicates from Sorted Array?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Two pointers: i (slow - last unique), j (fast - iterate). If nums[j] != nums[i]: nums[++i] = nums[j]. Return i+1. O(n), O(1). In-place.

---

### Q360: Move Zeroes?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Two pointers: lastNonZeroIndex = 0. Iterate, if non-zero: swap(nums[i], nums[lastNonZeroIndex]), lastNonZeroIndex++. All zeroes bubble to end. O(n).

---

### Q361: Find All Numbers Disappeared in Array?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Mark visited: negate nums[abs(nums[i]) - 1]. Iterate: if nums[i] > 0, i+1 is missing. O(n) time, O(1) space.

---

### Q362: Third Maximum Number?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Track first, second, third maximums (Long.MIN_VALUE). Iterate: skip if duplicate. Update comparisons in order. Return third if not MIN_VALUE else first.

---

### Q363: Add Two Numbers (Linked List)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Simulate addition with carry. Dummy head. While list1 or list2 or carry: sum = v1 + v2 + carry, node = sum % 10, carry = sum / 10, advance pointers. O(max(n,m)).

---

### Q364: Odd Even Linked List?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
odd = head, even = head.next, evenHead = even. While even and even.next: odd.next = even.next (next odd), odd = odd.next, even.next = odd.next (next even), even = even.next. odd.next = evenHead. O(n).

---

### Q365: Intersection of Two Linked Lists?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Two pointers: pA = headA, pB = headB. When one reaches end, redirect to other list's head. They meet at intersection (or both null). O(n+m) time, O(1) space. Proof: they travel same total distance.

---

### Q366: Linked List Cycle II (Find Cycle Start)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Floyd: slow/fast meet. Reset slow to head. Both move 1 step until they meet again at cycle start. Proof: distance from head to cycle start = distance from meeting point to cycle start.

---

### Q367: Copy List with Random Pointer?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Interweave: insert cloned node after each original. Assign random pointers: cloned.random = original.random.next. Separate lists. O(n) time, O(1) extra space. Or HashMap for O(n) space.

---

### Q368: Sort List (Merge Sort on Linked List)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Find middle (slow/fast), recursively sort halves, merge (sorted merge). O(n log n) time, O(log n) space (recursion). Mergesort is natural for linked lists (no random access needed).

---

### Q369: Reorder List (L0->Ln->L1->Ln-1->...)?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Find middle. Reverse second half. Merge first half and reversed second half (alternating). O(n).

---

### Q370: Palindrome Number?
**Topic:** Data Structures & Algorithms
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Reverse half: revert = 0. While x > revert: revert = revert * 10 + x % 10. x /= 10. Return x == revert || x == revert/10 (odd digits). Handle negative. O(log n). No string conversion.

## Frontend

### Q511: HTML5 semantic elements?
**Topic:** Frontend - HTML
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Semantic elements clearly describe their meaning to browser and developer. <header>, <nav>, <main>, <article>, <section>, <aside>, <footer>, <figure>, <figcaption>, <mark>, <time>, <details>, <summary>. Benefits: accessibility (screen readers), SEO, readability, maintainability. Avoid: <div> for everything. Use <article> for self-contained content, <section> for thematic grouping, <nav> for navigation links.

---

### Q512: CSS Box Model?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Every element has: Content (text/image), Padding (inner space), Border (outline), Margin (outer space). box-sizing: content-box (default - width includes only content), border-box (width includes content + padding + border - recommended). Total width = margin-left + border-left + padding-left + content + padding-right + border-right + margin-right.

---

### Q513: Flexbox vs Grid?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Flexbox: 1-dimensional (row OR column). Distributing items along main axis, alignment on cross axis. Good for: nav bars, centering, small components. Grid: 2-dimensional (rows AND columns). Explicit grid lines. Good for: page layout, complex arrangements, overlapping items. Both: gap, alignment (justify-content, align-items). Flexbox: flex-grow/shrink, order. Grid: grid-template-areas, grid-column/row.

---

### Q514: CSS specificity and inheritance?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Specificity determines which CSS rule applies. Hierarchy: !important > inline styles > IDs > classes/attributes/pseudo-classes > elements/pseudo-elements. Calculated: (a, b, c, d) - count of inline, IDs, classes, elements. Higher wins. Inherited properties: color, font-family (not: margin, padding, border, background). initial: set to default. inherit: force inheritance. unset: inherit if natural, else initial. !important overrides all (avoid if possible).

---

### Q515: JavaScript event loop and async?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
JavaScript is single-threaded (one call stack). Event loop: executes call stack, processes microtask queue (Promise.then, MutationObserver, queueMicrotask), then macrotask queue (setTimeout, setInterval, I/O, UI rendering). Microtasks before macrotasks. Async/await: syntactic sugar over Promises. async function returns Promise. await pauses until Promise resolves. Callback queue: FIFO. Event loop continuously checks: call stack empty? -> microtask -> macrotask tick.

---

### Q516: JavaScript closures?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Function that retains access to its lexical scope even when executed outside that scope. Inner function "closes over" variables from outer function. function outer(x) { return function inner(y) { return x + y; } }. const add5 = outer(5); add5(3) -> 8. x is preserved. Use: data privacy (private variables), partial application, module pattern, event handlers with preserved state. Memory: closed-over variables not GC'd while closure exists.

---

### Q517: JavaScript Prototypal Inheritance?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Objects inherit from other objects via [[Prototype]] chain. __proto__ (legacy), Object.getPrototypeOf() (modern). Object.create(parent) sets prototype. Constructor functions: new creates instance with prototype set to Constructor.prototype. ES6 classes: syntactic sugar over prototype chain. class Dog extends Animal { }. instanceof checks prototype chain. Property lookup: own property -> prototype -> ... -> Object.prototype -> null.

---

### Q518: React Virtual DOM?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Lightweight JavaScript object representation of real DOM. On state/props change: new VDOM tree created. Diffing algorithm compares old and new VDOM (reconciliation). Minimal set of changes applied to real DOM (batched updates). Optimization: keys on lists (stable identity), shouldComponentUpdate/PureComponent/React.memo. Fiber: React 16+ rewrite for incremental rendering, priority scheduling, pause/resume work.

---

### Q519: React hooks: useState, useEffect, useContext?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
useState(name): stateful value + setter. Component re-renders on set. Lazy initial state (function). useEffect(() => { }, [deps]): side effects (API calls, subscriptions, DOM updates). Return = cleanup. Empty deps [] = mount/unmount. No deps = every render. useContext(MyContext): consumes context value. Additional hooks: useReducer (complex state), useRef (mutable ref), useMemo (memoized value), useCallback (memoized fn), useLayoutEffect (sync after DOM), useImperativeHandle (expose methods).

---

### Q520: React Component Lifecycle?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Class components: constructor -> render -> componentDidMount (side effects, after mount) -> componentDidUpdate (prevProps) -> componentWillUnmount (cleanup). Hooks equivalent: constructor = useState + initializer. componentDidMount = useEffect([], fn). componentDidUpdate = useEffect(() => {}, [deps]) returns optional cleanup. componentWillUnmount = useEffect return function. getDerivedStateFromProps = not needed with hooks.

---

### Q521: Redux architecture?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
State management: Single immutable state tree. Actions: plain objects { type: 'INCREMENT', payload }. Reducers: pure functions (prevState, action) => newState. Store: holds state, dispatch(action), subscribe(listener). Middleware: intercepts dispatched actions (redux-thunk for async, redux-saga for generators, redux-observable for RxJS). React-redux: Provider provides store. connect(mapStateToProps, mapDispatchToProps) wraps components. useSelector, useDispatch hooks simplify.

---

### Q522: TypeScript: types and interfaces?
**Topic:** Frontend - TypeScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Types: union (string | number), intersection (A & B), literal ('active' | 'inactive'), tuple ([string, number]), enum, generic (T extends Constraint). Interface: object shape, extends multiple, declaration merging. Type vs Interface: type can do more (unions, mapped types, conditional types), interface is preferred for object types (better error messages, extends). Use interface for public API, type for computed/union/conditional types.

---

### Q523: TypeScript generics?
**Topic:** Frontend - TypeScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Generic functions: function identity<T>(arg: T): T { return arg; }. Generic constraints: <T extends HasLength>. Generic interface: interface Container<T> { value: T; }. Generic class: class Stack<T> { push(item: T) {} }. Built-in: Promise<T>, Array<T>. Utility types: Partial<T>, Required<T>, Pick<T,K>, Omit<T,K>, Record<K,V>, Exclude<T,U>, ReturnType<T>, Parameters<T>. Mapped types: { [K in keyof T]: T[K] }.

---

### Q524: CSS Preprocessors (SASS/LESS)?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CSS with superpowers: variables ($primary-color), nesting (parent selector &), mixins (@mixin flex-center), functions (lighten, darken), partials/import, inheritance (@extend), control directives (@if, @for, @each). SCSS (Sassy CSS): superset of CSS3 syntax. Reduces repetition, more maintainable. CSS-in-JS (styled-components, Emotion): component-scoped styles, dynamic styles via props, no class name conflicts.

---

### Q525: Web performance optimization?
**Topic:** Frontend - Performance
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Loading: lazy loading (images, routes), code splitting (dynamic import), preload/prefetch/preconnect, critical CSS inline, HTTP/2 multiplexing, CDN, compression (Brotli/gzip). Rendering: debounce/throttle, requestAnimationFrame for visual updates, avoid layout thrashing, CSS containment, virtualization (react-window for long lists). Images: WebP/AVIF format, responsive images (srcset/sizes), lazy loading (loading="lazy"), image CDN with transformations. Bundle size: tree shaking, minification, scope hoisting. Caching: service workers (PWA), localStorage/IndexedDB for API responses. Metrics: LCP, FID, CLS (Core Web Vitals).

---

### Q526: Browser rendering pipeline?
**Topic:** Frontend - Performance
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
1. HTML parsing -> DOM tree. 2. CSS parsing -> CSSOM (CSS Object Model). 3. DOM + CSSOM -> Render Tree (visible elements only, display:none excluded). 4. Layout (Reflow): calculate geometry (position, size). 5. Paint: fill pixels (text, colors, images). 6. Compositing: layers combined, GPU acceleration. Critical Rendering Path: minimize by inlining critical CSS, async JS (defer/async), optimizing image loading. Reflow triggers: DOM changes, style changes, resize, font load. Repaint: changes to color, visibility, background.

---

### Q527: Accessibility (a11y) best practices?
**Topic:** Frontend - HTML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Semantic HTML (landmarks, headings hierarchy). ARIA roles/attributes when HTML semantics insufficient: role="button", aria-label, aria-expanded, aria-live (dynamic content), aria-hidden. Keyboard navigation: tabindex, focus management, skip-to-content links. Color contrast: WCAG AA (4.5:1 normal text). Screen reader friendly: alt text on images, labels on form inputs, meaningful link text. Focus visible outlines. Test with: axe DevTools, Lighthouse, screen readers (JAWS, NVDA, VoiceOver).

---

### Q528: Web Security (XSS, CSRF)?
**Topic:** Frontend - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
XSS (Cross-Site Scripting): injecting malicious scripts. Stored (persistent in DB), Reflected (URL parameter), DOM-based (client-side). Prevention: escape output ({text} in React auto-escapes), Content-Security-Policy (CSP) header, HttpOnly cookies, input validation. CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery): attacker makes authenticated request on behalf of user. Prevention: CSRF tokens (anti-CSRF), SameSite cookies (Strict/Lax), Origin/Referer header check, re-authentication for sensitive actions.

---

### Q529: Progressive Web Apps (PWA)?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Web apps with native-like capabilities. Service Worker: JavaScript file acting as proxy between browser and network. Handles caching (Cache Storage API), offline support, background sync, push notifications. Web App Manifest: JSON file describing app (name, icons, theme_color, display: standalone). HTTPS required. Offline-first strategy: cache then network, service worker returns cached content when offline. Lighthouse PWA audit.

---

### Q530: JavaScript Module systems?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ES Modules (ESM): import/export. Static analysis (tree-shaking). Browser support (type="module"). Named exports (export const foo), default export (export default). Dynamic import() for code splitting. CommonJS (Node.js): require/module.exports. Synchronous, dynamic. Used by server-side. UMD: Universal, works with both. AMD: define/require (RequireJS). AMD is async browser-first (deprecated). SystemJS: dynamic module loader.

---

### Q531: State management in React: Context vs Redux?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React Context: built-in, no extra deps, good for low-frequency updates (theme, locale, auth). Provider wrapping can cause unnecessary re-renders (all consumers). Split contexts for unrelated concerns. Redux: global state store, devtools (time-travel debugging), middleware (async), predictable (reducers). Overkill for small apps. Alternatives: Zustand (simple), Jotai (atomic), Recoil (atom-based), MobX (observables). Consider: app size, update frequency, team familiarity.

---

### Q532: Testing in React?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Jest: test runner, assertions, mocking. React Testing Library: tests from user perspective (not implementation). fireEvent/userEvent for interactions. @testing-library/jest-dom for DOM assertions. Unit tests: individual functions/components. Integration tests: component interactions. E2E: Cypress/Playwright (full browser). getByRole, getByText, getByTestId. Avoid: testing internal state, implementation details. Test user-visible behavior.

---

### Q533: React keys and reconciliation?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Keys help React identify which items changed, added, removed. Use stable IDs (from data), never index (unless static list). Index as key: causes unnecessary re-renders, state bugs (input values). Reaction: React reconciles by comparing element type + key. Different type -> unmount/remount. Same type+key -> update in place (preserve state). Key outside component? Key on component instance, not DOM element.

---

### Q534: Debouncing and Throttling?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Debounce: executes function after specified delay since last call. Use: search autocomplete (wait until user stops typing), window resize end. Throttle: at most once per specified interval. Use: scroll handlers, infinite scroll. Implement: closure with setTimeout. Libraries: lodash.debounce, lodash.throttle. React: useCallback + useRef for stable debounced functions.

---

### Q535: CSS positioning?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
static: default, normal document flow. relative: positioned relative to normal position (still occupies space). absolute: relative to nearest positioned ancestor (or initial containing block). Removed from flow. fixed: relative to viewport, stays during scroll. sticky: hybrid (relative until scroll threshold, then fixed). z-index: stacking order (only works on positioned elements). Stacking context: root, positioned + z-index, opacity < 1, transform, filter.

---

### Q536: Responsive design?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Media queries: @media (max-width: 768px). Breakpoints: mobile (320-480), tablet (768-1024), desktop (1024+). Mobile-first: base styles for mobile, @media (min-width) for larger. Fluid grids: %, fr, auto. Responsive images: srcset + sizes, <picture> element. Viewport meta tag: <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1">. Container queries (future): @container for component-level responsiveness. REM/EM for scalable typography. CSS Grid/Flexbox for layout.

---

### Q537: JavaScript `this` keyword?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Determined by execution context (not lexical scope). 1. Default: window/global (undefined in strict mode). 2. Implicit: obj.method() -> obj. 3. Explicit: call, apply, bind specify this. 4. new: constructor instance. 5. Arrow function: lexical this (captures from enclosing scope). Event handlers: this = element. bind/arrow to fix. Context loss: const fn = obj.method; fn() -> undefined (lost implicit binding).

---

### Q538: Shadow DOM vs Virtual DOM?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Shadow DOM: browser API for DOM encapsulation (scoped styles, subtree isolation). Used by Web Components (<slot> for composition). Real DOM, part of browser rendering. Virtual DOM: JavaScript object representation of DOM (React). Diffing algorithm for efficient updates. Shadow DOM encapsulates (CSS, events), Virtual DOM optimizes (performance, state management). Can combine: React-in-Shadow for style isolation.

---

### Q539: Web Workers and Service Workers?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Web Worker: background thread for CPU-intensive tasks. No DOM access. Message passing (postMessage/onmessage). Terminate when done. SharedWorker: shared across multiple tabs. Service Worker: proxy between browser and network. Offline support, caching, push notifications, background sync. Lifecycle: install -> activate -> fetch events. Runs even when tab closed. Requires HTTPS. Different from Web Workers (design purpose, lifecycle, capabilities).

---

### Q540: Frontend build tools (Webpack, Vite)?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Webpack: bundler, configuration-heavy, code splitting, loaders (babel-loader, css-loader), plugins (HtmlWebpackPlugin, MiniCssExtractPlugin), dev server with HMR. Vite: next-gen (ES modules for dev, Rollup for production). Fast HMR (native ESM, no bundle needed). Slow bundling for production (Rollup). Why Vite faster: esbuild for pre-bundling (Go, 10-100x faster), native ES modules (no bundle during dev), instant HMR. Configuration simpler than Webpack.

---

### Q541: Next.js features?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React framework for production. SSR/SSG/ISR: Server-Side Rendering (getServerSideProps), Static Site Generation (getStaticProps + getStaticPaths), Incremental Static Regeneration (revalidate). File-based routing (/pages -> /about -> component). API routes (/pages/api/* -> serverless functions). Image optimization (next/image). Font optimization. Middleware (edge functions). Built-in CSS/SASS/CSS-in-JS support. TypeScript support. Automatic code splitting. Fast Refresh.

---

### Q542: Micro Frontends architecture?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Decompose frontend into independently deployable modules. Integration approaches: iframes (simple but UX issues), Web Components (standards-based, framework-agnostic), Module Federation (Webpack 5 - dynamically load remote modules at runtime), Single-SPA (router-based orchestrator). Shared: design system, auth state, routing conventions. Challenges: performance (duplicate deps), consistent UX, shared state, cross-team coordination, unified testing.

---

### Q543: Error Boundary in React?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React component that catches JavaScript errors in its child tree, logs error, and displays fallback UI. Class component with componentDidCatch(error, info) and getDerivedStateFromError(error). Hooks: no direct equivalent, use class wrapper. Does NOT catch: event handlers (use try-catch), async code (use .catch()), SSR, errors in error boundary itself. Error boundary per feature (not root). Good practice: graceful degradation.

---

### Q544: WebSockets in frontend?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
const ws = new WebSocket('wss://server.com'). Events: onopen, onmessage, onerror, onclose. ws.send(data) - string or binary. Reconnection logic needed (not built-in). Socket.IO: library with auto-reconnect, fallback (long-polling), rooms, namespaces. STOMP: messaging protocol over WebSocket (for RabbitMQ/ActiveMQ). Security: wss:// (TLS), validate origin header, authenticate on connect.

---

### Q545: CSS Animations and Transitions?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Transition: property change over time (hover, class toggle). transition: all 0.3s ease. Easing functions: ease, linear, ease-in, ease-out, cubic-bezier(). Animation: @keyframes for multi-step animations. animation: name 2s ease-in-out infinite. animation-fill-mode (backwards/forwards/both) maintains state before/after. Transform: rotate, scale, translate, skew (GPU-accelerated). Will-change property hints browser to optimize. Prefer transforms/opacity over layout-triggering properties.

---

### Q546: Lazy loading and code splitting?
**Topic:** Frontend - Performance
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React.lazy(() => import('./MyComponent')) dynamic import + code splitting. Suspense fallback while loading. React Router: lazy load routes. Webpack: import() automatically splits into separate chunk. Named chunks: webpackChunkName comment. Prefetch/preload: <link rel="prefetch"> for next-page resources. IntersectionObserver for lazy loading images (img loading="lazy"). Component-level vs route-level splitting. Balance between chunk count and size.

---

### Q547: Web vitals and monitoring?
**Topic:** Frontend - Performance
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Core Web Vitals: LCP (Largest Contentful Paint - loading, <2.5s), FID (First Input Delay - interactivity, <100ms, replaced by INP), CLS (Cumulative Layout Shift - visual stability, <0.1). Other: FCP (First Contentful Paint), TTFB (Time to First Byte), TBT (Total Blocking Time). Tools: Lighthouse, PageSpeed Insights, Chrome DevTools, Web Vitals library. Real User Monitoring (RUM): Performance API, web-vitals library, analytics (Google Analytics, Datadog RUM).

---

### Q548: React Context vs Prop Drilling?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prop Drilling: passing data through many layers of components (even those not needing it). Makes refactoring hard, components less reusable. Context API: provide value at higher level, consume anywhere below. Avoids prop drilling. Downside: all consumers re-render when context value changes (even if specific value unchanged). Mitigate: split contexts, useMemo for value, component memoization. Alternative: Jotai/Zustand (atomic state, targeted re-renders).

---

### Q549: Controlled vs Uncontrolled components?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Controlled: form state managed by React (value + onChange). Single source of truth, instant validation, complex UIs.
const [value, setValue] = useState(''); <input value={value} onChange={e => setValue(e.target.value)} />. Uncontrolled: DOM manages state, useRef to access value when needed. <input ref={inputRef} />. Simplified, more performant for simple forms. Prefer controlled for most cases (predictable, testable).

---

### Q550: Server-Side Rendering (SSR) vs Client-Side Rendering (CSR) vs Static Site Generation (SSG)?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CSR: HTML skeleton + JS bundle. Browser renders. Slower initial load (TTFB fast, FCP slow), but fast after. SEO challenges (Google handles JS, but not all crawlers). SSR: server renders full HTML (Node.js). Faster initial paint (FCP), good SEO. More server load (CPU, memory). SSG: pre-build HTML at build time. Fastest (CDN serving static HTML). Good for content sites, blogs. Rebuild on content change. ISR (Next.js): Incremental Static Regeneration (SSG + periodic revalidate). Best: SSG whenever possible, SSR when dynamic content needed, CSR for authenticated/dashboard apps.

---

### Q551: Stateful vs Stateless Components?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Stateless (Functional/Presentational): no internal state, only props. Pure function of props. Easier to test, reuse. Stateful (Class/Container): manages state, side effects, lifecycle. Hooks made functional components stateful. Prefer stateless components; extract state to parent. React.memo wraps component to skip re-render if props unchanged (shallow comparison). PureComponent does same for classes.

---

### Q552: TypeScript Utility Types?
**Topic:** Frontend - TypeScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Partial<T>: all props optional. Required<T>: all required. Readonly<T>: all readonly. Pick<T, K>: subset of keys. Omit<T, K>: all except keys. Record<K, V>: object with keys K, values V. Exclude<T, U>: types in T not in U. Extract<T, U>: types in both. NonNullable<T>: remove null/undefined. ReturnType<T>: inferred return type of function. Parameters<T>: tuple of parameter types. Awaited<T>: unwrapped Promise type.

---

### Q553: React Fiber?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Reconciliation algorithm rewrite in React 16+. Unit of work: Fiber node (virtual stack frame). Enables: incremental rendering (split work into chunks), priority-based scheduling (high priority: user input > animations > data fetch), pause/resume work, reuse completed work, abort work. Two phases: Render (reconcile - can interrupt) -> Commit (DOM update - synchronous). Fiber tree: linked list (child, sibling, return). Enables Concurrent Mode (React 18) with startTransition, useTransition, useDeferredValue.

---

### Q554: Web Components?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Browser-native component model: Custom Elements (define custom HTML tags), Shadow DOM (encapsulated DOM and styles), HTML Templates (<template> tag), HTML Imports (deprecated, use ES modules). class MyComponent extends HTMLElement { connectedCallback() { ... } }. customElements.define('my-component', MyComponent). Pros: framework-agnostic, native, future-proof. Cons: polyfills needed (older browsers), limited data binding, no built-in state management.

---

### Q555: CSS-in-JS (styled-components, Emotion)?
**Topic:** Frontend - CSS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Component-scoped CSS in JavaScript. styled-components: const Button = styled.button` color: blue; background: ${props => props.primary ? 'blue' : 'gray'}; `. Benefits: scoped styles (no class name collisions), dynamic styles based on props, co-located CSS (colocation with component), critical CSS extraction, no dead style elimination, theming. Downsides: runtime cost (CSS generation in JS), increased bundle size, no separate CSS caching. Alternatives: CSS Modules (compile-time scoping), Linaria (zero-runtime CSS-in-JS).

---

### Q556: Immutability in JavaScript/React?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Immutability: not modifying data directly, creating new copies with changes. Benefits: predictable state updates, optimized re-rendering (shallow comparison), time-travel debugging, easier reasoning. React: never mutate state directly. setState({...state, key: newValue}), setState(prev => {return {...prev, key: newValue}}). Array methods: map, filter, concat (not push, pop, splice). Spread operator (...), Object.assign, Immer library (produce for mutable syntax with immutable output).

---

### Q557: JavaScript Promises and async/await?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Promise: object representing eventual completion/failure of async operation. States: pending, fulfilled, rejected. Promise.then(onFulfilled, onRejected). Promise.catch(onRejected). Promise.finally(). Static: Promise.all (wait all, fail fast), Promise.allSettled (wait all, get all results), Promise.race (first settled), Promise.any (first fulfilled). async/await: syntactic sugar. async returns Promise. await pauses execution. Error handling: try/catch around awaits. Sequential vs concurrent: await Promise.all([p1, p2]) for concurrent.

---

### Q558: Axios vs Fetch API?
**Topic:** Frontend - JavaScript
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Axios: library, automatic JSON transformation, request cancellation (AbortController), request/response interceptors, timeout, base URL, progress events. Fetch: browser native, verbose (two-awaits for JSON), no timeout by default, no interceptors, no progress. Axios has better DX (developer experience). For simple requests, fetch suffices. For complex API interactions, Axios is better. Both support async/await.

---

### Q559: React Router?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
react-router-dom for web. Components: BrowserRouter (HTML5 history), Routes/Route (declarative routing), Link (navigation), NavLink (active styling), useParams (URL params), useNavigate (programmatic), useLocation (current URL), Outlet (nested layouts). Route config: <Route path="/users/:id" element={<UserPage />} />. Nested routes: parent renders <Outlet />. Lazy loading: React.lazy + Suspense. Protected routes: wrapper component checking auth. HashRouter for static file hosting.

---

### Q560: Frontend build optimization?
**Topic:** Frontend - Performance
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Bundle analysis: webpack-bundle-analyzer, source-map-explorer. Code splitting: dynamic import(), React.lazy. Tree shaking: ES modules, sideEffects: false in package.json. Image optimization: WebP/AVIF, responsive images, lazy loading, image CDN. Font optimization: subset, variable fonts, font-display: swap. CSS optimization: purge unused (PurgeCSS), minification, critical CSS inline. JS minification (Terser), CSS minification (cssnano). Compression: Brotli > Gzip. CDN for static assets. HTTP/2 multiplexing. Preload critical resources, prefetch next-page.

## Generative AI

### Q721: Generative AI overview?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
AI that generates new content (text, images, code, audio, video). Key models: LLMs (GPT, Claude, Llama), image generators (Stable Diffusion, DALL-E, Midjourney), code generators (GitHub Copilot, CodeLlama), audio (Whisper, ElevenLabs), video (Sora, Runway). Foundation models: large pretrained models adaptable to many tasks. Applications: content creation, chatbots, code completion, drug discovery, design, entertainment. Challenges: hallucination, bias, safety, cost, evaluation.

---

### Q722: Large Language Models (LLMs)?
**Topic:** Generative AI - LLMs
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Transformer-based models pretrained on massive text corpora (trillions of tokens). Next-token prediction (autoregressive): predict next token given previous tokens. Scale: from millions to trillions of parameters (GPT-3: 175B, Llama 3: 405B, GPT-4: ~1.8T estimated). Capabilities: text generation, translation, summarization, Q&A, code, reasoning, few-shot learning (in-context learning). Key models: GPT-4 (OpenAI), Claude (Anthropic), Gemini (Google), Llama 3 (Meta, open-weight), Mistral, DeepSeek. Prompt engineering: carefully designed input to get desired output. Temperature: controls randomness (0 = deterministic, 1 = creative).

---

### Q723: Transformer architecture in LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI - LLMs
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Decoder-only architecture (GPT style): masked self-attention + feedforward layers. Causal attention: each token can only attend to previous tokens (autoregressive generation). Key components: Token embedding + positional encoding. Multi-head causal self-attention. RMSNorm (instead of LayerNorm). SwiGLU activation (instead of ReLU). RoPE (Rotary Position Embedding) for position encoding. KV-cache: store K,V matrices during generation for efficiency (recompute only new tokens). Grouped Query Attention (GQA): multiple query heads share key/value heads (efficient inference). Vocabulary: tokenizer (BPE, SentencePiece, tiktoken). Context length: 4K tokens (GPT-3) to 1M+ (Gemini 1.5, Claude 3).

---

### Q724: Training LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI - LLMs
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Three stages: 1. Pretraining: next-token prediction on web-scale data (trillions of tokens). Massive compute (thousands of GPUs for months). Data pipeline: filtering, deduplication, quality filtering. Loss: cross-entropy. 2. Supervised Fine-Tuning (SFT): train on high-quality instruction-response pairs. 3. RLHF (Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback): learn reward model from human preferences, fine-tune LLM with PPO to maximize reward. DPO (Direct Preference Optimization): simpler alternative without explicit reward model. Scaling laws: Kaplan et al. (compute + data + params jointly determine loss). Chinchilla scaling: more data, smaller model better.

---

### Q725: RLHF (Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback)?
**Topic:** Generative AI - LLMs
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Align LLM outputs with human values. Steps: 1. SFT: fine-tune on high-quality demonstrations. 2. Reward modeling: collect human comparisons (output A vs output B), train reward model to predict human preference. 3. PPO: fine-tune LLM to maximize reward model score + KL penalty (prevent drifting too far). KL divergence constraint prevents reward hacking. Direct Preference Optimization (DPO): directly optimize from preferences without explicit reward model. Constitutional AI (Claude): train with self-critique against constitution principles. Helpfulness vs harmlessness trade-off.

---

### Q726: Prompt Engineering techniques?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Techniques to optimize LLM outputs. Zero-shot: "Translate to French: Hello". Few-shot: provide examples in prompt. Chain-of-Thought (CoT): "Let's think step by step" - improves reasoning. Tree-of-Thoughts (ToT): explore multiple reasoning paths. Self-Consistency: sample multiple CoT paths, majority vote. Role prompting: "You are an expert X". Structured prompts: clear format, delimiters (```, ---). Negative prompts: "Do not include..." Temperature: low for factual, high for creative. System prompt: define model behavior/persona. Output formatting: JSON mode, XML tags, markdown.

---

### Q727: Retrieval Augmented Generation (RAG)?
**Topic:** Generative AI - RAG
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Retrieve relevant documents, augment LLM context, generate grounded response. Pipeline: 1. Index documents (chunk + embed). 2. Query: embed user query. 3. Retrieve: similarity search (FAISS, Pinecone, Weaviate). 4. Augment: insert retrieved chunks + instruction into prompt. 5. Generate: LLM produces answer from context. Benefits: reduces hallucination (grounded in retrieved data), handles knowledge cutoff, domain-specific without fine-tuning. Chunking strategies: fixed size, semantic (sentence, paragraph), recursive (LangChain). RAPTOR: hierarchical chunking + summarization. Self-RAG: LLM decides when to retrieve. Advanced: HyDE (query expansion), ColBERT (late interaction), cross-encoder reranking.

---

### Q728: Vector Databases?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Store and search high-dimensional vectors (embeddings). Approximate Nearest Neighbor (ANN) search: trade accuracy for speed (vs exact kNN). Index types: IVF (inverted file), HNSW (Hierarchical Navigable Small Worlds - fast, memory-hungry), PQ (Product Quantization - memory efficient). Distance metrics: cosine similarity, L2, dot product. Popular: Pinecone (managed), Weaviate (self/managed), Qdrant (Rust), Milvus (scalable), Chroma (embedded), FAISS (library, not database). Use: semantic search, RAG, recommendation, similarity matching, clustering.

---

### Q729: Fine-tuning LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI - LLMs
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Adapt pretrained LLM to specific domain/task. Full fine-tuning: update all parameters (expensive: 175B * 16bit = 350GB GPU memory). PEFT (Parameter Efficient Fine-Tuning): fine-tune small number of parameters. LoRA (Low-Rank Adaptation): train low-rank matrices injected into attention layers (rank r=8-64). QLoRA: quantized LoRA (4-bit normal float, memory efficient: fine-tune 65B on single 48GB GPU). Adapters: small bottleneck layers between layers. Prefix Tuning: learn virtual tokens prepended to input. Prompt Tuning: learn soft prompts. Fine-tuning data: hundreds to thousands of examples. Use: domain-specific (legal, medical), instruction following, style adaptation, better performance than RAG alone.

---

### Q730: Evaluation of LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Standard benchmarks: MMLU (knowledge), HumanEval/Codex (code), GSM8K (math), HellaSwag (commonsense), TruthfulQA (truthfulness), BIG-bench. Automated evaluation: BLEU (translation), ROUGE (summarization), BERTScore, perplexity. LLM-as-judge: use strong LLM to evaluate outputs (GPT-4 evaluator). Human evaluation: preferences, ratings. Task-specific: answer accuracy, faithfulness (grounded in context), completeness, hallucination rate. RAG-specific: retrieval precision/recall, answer relevance, faithfulness. Guardrails: content safety evaluation. Toxicity detection. Evaluation frameworks: LangSmith, MLflow, Weights & Biases, DeepEval.

---

### Q731: Hallucination in LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
LLM generates factually incorrect or nonsensical content. Types: intrinsic (contradicts source), extrinsic (no source, unverifiable). Causes: language modeling objective (predict plausible tokens, not truth), training data memorization vs generalization, lack of knowledge, overconfidence. Mitigation: RAG (ground in retrieved documents), chain-of-verification, self-check, temperature reduction, constrained decoding, factual consistency checking. Prompting: "Only answer if confident", "Cite sources". Fine-tuning: train on high-quality data with rejection of incorrect answers. Cannot be fully eliminated (LLMs are not databases).

---

### Q732: Context Window and Length Extrapolation?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Context window: max tokens model can process. Limitations: quadratic attention O(n^2) memory/time. Solutions for longer contexts: Sparse attention (Longformer, BigBird), Sliding window (Mistral: 8K window), Flash Attention (tiled, IO-aware attention), ALiBi (relative position bias), YaRN (extend RoPE frequencies), NTK-aware scaling. Linear attention: RWKV, Mamba (state space models - linear in sequence length). Long context models: GPT-4 (128K), Claude 3 (200K), Gemini 1.5 (1M+), Llama 3.1 (128K). Long context still degrades (lost-in-the-middle). Retrieval augmentation often better than brute-force long context.

---

### Q733: LLM Safety and Alignment?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Safety: avoid harmful outputs (violence, hate, illegal, dangerous). Alignment: ensure model behaves according to human values and intent. Methods: RLHF, DPO, Constitutional AI, red-teaming (adversarial testing), safety guardrails (NeMo Guardrails, Guardrails AI), content filtering (classification-based). Challenges: jailbreaking (prompt injection circumventing safety), adversarial attacks, gradual erosion of alignment through fine-tuning. Techniques: input/output filtering, refusal training, RL from red-teaming. Evals: safety benchmarks (HarmBench, Safety-Prompts), bias testing. Continuous challenge (cat-and-mouse).

---

### Q734: Tokenization in LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Convert text -> tokens (subwords). BPE (Byte-Pair Encoding): GPT, Llama. SentencePiece: Llama (unigram). WordPiece: BERT. tiktoken: OpenAI's fast tokenizer. Tokenize by: whitespace -> subword merging. Vocabulary: 32K-200K tokens. Special tokens: [BOS], [EOS], [PAD], [SEP], [CLS]. Effects: tokenization affects model behavior. "hello" vs " hello" different tokens. Non-English text may be overfragmented. Multilingual tokenization challenging. Token count != character/word count (varies by language). Efficient tokenization reduces sequence length (saves compute).

---

### Q735: Beam Search vs Sampling?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Decoding strategies for text generation. Greedy: choose highest probability token each step (low diversity). Beam search: maintain k highest probability sequences, expand each step (better for translation, summarization). Top-k sampling: sample from top k tokens (k=40-50). Top-p (nucleus) sampling: sample from smallest set with cumulative probability p (p=0.9). Temperature: scale logits before softmax. Low temp (0.1): deterministic, factual. High temp (0.9): creative, diverse. Typical sampling: avoid tokens with low information (surprising tokens). Contrastive search: balance confidence and degeneration.

---

### Q736: Quantization of LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Reduce model precision to lower memory footprint and faster inference. FP16 (16-bit): standard training precision. INT8: 8-bit integer (2x memory reduction, minimal quality loss). INT4: 4-bit (4x reduction, slight quality loss). NF4 (NormalFloat4): QLoRA format, optimal for normally distributed weights. Quantization methods: Post-Training Quantization (PTQ), Quantization-Aware Training (QAT). GPTQ: weight quantization via optimal brain quantization. AWQ: activation-aware weight quantization (protect important channels). GGUF/GGML: llama.cpp format (CPU-friendly, K-quant). Bitsandbytes: 8-bit/4-bit inference in PyTorch. Quantization enables running large models on consumer hardware (7B in INT4 ~4GB).

---

### Q737: Speculative Decoding?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Accelerate LLM inference without quality loss. Use a small draft model to propose tokens (fast), large target model verifies (parallel). If draft matches target distribution: accept all tokens (multiple tokens per step). If mismatch: reject, fall back. Speedup: 2-3x. Requirements: draft model cheap, aligned with target. Tree verification: verify multiple draft sequences at once. Self-speculative: skip intermediate layers in same model for draft. Medusa: multiple parallel draft heads. Lookahead decoding. Staged speculative decoding.

---

### Q738: Mixture of Experts (MoE)?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Model architecture with multiple "expert" sub-networks. Router/gate: determines which experts process each token. Sparse activation: only top-k experts activated per token (e.g., top-2). More parameters (total expert count) but same inference cost (activation compute grows by k). Examples: Mixtral 8x7B (46B total, 12B active per token). Switch Transformer, DeepSeek-V2, GPT-4 (rumored MoE). Benefits: larger model capacity without proportional compute increase. Challenges: load balancing (routing collapse to few experts), communication overhead (distributed), expert capacity.

---

### Q739: Multimodal LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
LLMs that process multiple modalities: text + images + audio + video. Architecture: modality encoder (vision: ViT, CLIP), connector (Q-Former, linear projection) aligning embeddings to LLM space, LLM backbone, modality decoder (for generation). GPT-4V/Vision: images + text input. CLIP: joint image-text embedding. LLaVA: LMM using Vicuna + CLIP visual encoder. Llama 3.2: text + vision (11B, 90B). Gemini: native multimodal (trained on text, images, audio, video). ImageBind: cross-modal binding across 6 modalities. Applications: visual Q&A, image captioning, document understanding, multimodal search.

---

### Q740: Code Generation with LLMs?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
LLMs trained on code repositories (GitHub, Stack Overflow). Specialized models: GitHub Copilot (Codex, GPT-4), CodeLlama (Meta), StarCoder (BigCode), DeepSeek-Coder, Mistral Codestral. Capabilities: code completion, generation from description, bug fixing, refactoring, test generation, documentation. Fill-in-the-middle (FIM): context prefix + suffix, generate middle (hub for VS Code). Multi-file context: consider entire repo (repository-level code generation). Evaluation: HumanEval (function completion), MBPP (program synthesis), SWE-bench (real-world GitHub issues). Best practices: clear specification, provide context (imports, types), incremental generation, validate outputs.

---

### Q741: LLM Inference Optimization?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Optimizations for fast LLM inference. KV-cache: store past Key/Value tensors (trades memory for speed). Flash Attention: IO-aware attention (tiling, recomputation). Continuous batching: batch requests dynamically (vLLM, TensorRT-LLM). PagedAttention/vLLM: manage KV-cache like virtual memory (avoid fragmentation, share across sequences). Quantization: INT8, INT4, AWQ, GPTQ. Speculative decoding for latency. Prefix caching: reuse KV-cache for shared prefixes (prompt caching). Tensor parallelism: split across GPUs. Pipeline parallelism: split layers across GPUs. Serving frameworks: vLLM, TensorRT-LLM, TGI, SGLang, llama.cpp.

---

### Q742: Agents and Tool Use?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
LLMs using tools (APIs, databases, code execution) autonomously. Framework: ReAct (Reasoning + Acting): model reasons about task, selects tool, observes result, continues. Function calling: LLM outputs structured JSON to call functions. Tools: search, calculator, code interpreter, database query, API calls. Multi-agent: multiple specialized agents collaborate (AutoGPT, CrewAI). Memory: short-term (context) + long-term (vector store). Planning: decompose complex tasks into steps. Task-specific agents: coding agent (Devin, SWE-agent), data analysis agent, web agent. Frameworks: LangChain agents, AutoGen, CrewAI, Semantic Kernel.

---

### Q743: LangChain Framework?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Framework for building LLM applications. Core: LLM abstraction (OpenAI, Anthropic, local), prompt templates, chains (sequences of calls). RAG: document loaders, text splitters, vector stores, retrievers. Agents: LLM + tools + executor. Memory: conversation buffer, summary, vector store. LCEL (LangChain Expression Language): declarative chain composition (pipe operator |). Use: chatbots, Q&A systems, agents, summarization. Strengths: large ecosystem, integrations (all major LLM providers, vector stores, tools). Weaknesses: abstraction overhead, debugging complexity. Alternatives: LlamaIndex (focused on data indexing), Haystack, DSPy.

---

### Q744: LlamaIndex?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Framework focused on data indexing and RAG (LlamaIndex). Core: data connectors (load from 160+ sources), index structures (vector, summary, tree, keyword), query engines (retrieve + synthesize). Best for: complex RAG pipelines, structured/unstructured data mixing. Advanced: router query engine (route query to best index), sub-questions (decompose complex query), agent integration. LlamaParse: parse PDFs to markdown. LlamaHub: community collection of data connectors. Comparison: LangChain (general LLM apps) vs LlamaIndex (data-centric RAG). Can be used together.

---

### Q745: DSPy Framework?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Framework for algorithmically optimizing LLM prompts and weights. Key idea: treat prompt engineering as optimization problem. Program: module like ChainOfThought, ReAct, RAG. Teleprompter: optimizer that finds best prompt/demo examples. Compilation: system generates candidate prompts, evaluates on metrics, selects best. Bootstrap Few-Shot: generate demonstrations from program runs. Bayesian optimization or random search for prompt variants. Benefits: systematic, reproducible, no manual prompt tweaking. Trade-off: requires labeled evaluation data, more complex setup.

---

### Q746: LLM Memory and Long-term Memory?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Conversation memory: store chat history. Short-term: keep recent N turns in context (limited by context window). Summary memory: periodically summarize conversation, keep summary + recent. Vector store memory: embed conversation chunks, retrieve relevant past. Entity memory: extract and track entities (names, facts). Temporal memory: time-weighted recency. Composite memory: combine multiple types. MEMOW: memory for agents. MemGPT (LetMeDoIt): virtual context management (page in/out). For LLM agents, external memory (vector DB) is essential for long-running tasks.

---

### Q747: Reranking in RAG?
**Topic:** Generative AI
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
After initial retrieval (top-k chunks), rerank with more expensive but accurate model. Bi-encoder (initial retrieval): encode query + chunks independently, cosine similarity (fast, can precompute). Cross-encoder (rerank): encode query+chunk together (joint attention), more accurate, O(n) per query. Two-stage: retrieve 50-100 chunks with bi-encoder, rerank top-10 with cross-encoder. Models: Cohere rerank, BGE-reranker, BERT cross-encoder, MonoBERT. ColBERT: late interaction (token-level matching, more accurate than bi-encoder). Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF): combine multiple ranking signals. Reranking significantly improves RAG quality.

---

### Q748: Evaluation in RAG?
**Topic:** Generative AI - RAG
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Components to evaluate: retrieval (precision/recall@k, MRR, NDCG), generation (faithfulness, answer relevance, completeness, context precision/recall). Faithfulness: does answer align with retrieved context? (factual consistency). Answer relevance: does answer address query? Context relevance: are retrieved chunks relevant? Context recall: are all needed facts in retrieved chunks? Tools: RAGAS (framework for RAG evaluation), DeepEval, TruLens, LangSmith. Human evaluation: rating pairs of (query, response). Synthetic eval generation: use LLM to create test queries from document collection.

---

### Q749: Prompt Injection and Guardrails?
**Topic:** Generative AI - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prompt injection: attacker crafts input to override system prompt (e.g., "Ignore previous instructions..."). Types: direct, indirect (via retrieved content). Guardrails: protect LLM applications. Input guardrails: classify and filter malicious prompts. Output guardrails: check for sensitive data, toxicity, hallucinations. Frameworks: NeMo Guardrails, Guardrails AI, Prompt Guard (Meta), Llama Guard. Techniques: input/output classification, regex patterns, semantic similarity to known attacks, perplexity filter (unusual inputs). Instruction hierarchy (Anthropic): system > user > tool messages override each other. Defense-in-depth: multiple guard layers.

---

### Q750: Multimodal RAG?
**Topic:** Generative AI - RAG
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
RAG on documents containing images, tables, charts. Approaches: 1. Text-only: extract text content (ignoring images). 2. Multimodal embeddings: embed text + images together (CLIP). 3. Image description: use VLM to describe images, index descriptions (text). 4. Native multimodal: embed images directly, retrieve images + text. ColPali: vision-language model for document retrieval (page-level). LayoutLM: document layout understanding. Table understanding: text extraction, cell-level retrieval, semantic HTML. Chunking: preserve document structure (sections with images). Systems: Docling, Unstructured.io, LlamaParse for PDF parsing.

## General CS

### Q821: OOP Principles?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Encapsulation: bundling data + methods, hiding internal state (private fields, public methods). Inheritance: child class inherits from parent (extends, super). Polymorphism: same interface, different implementations (method overriding, overloading). Abstraction: hide complexity, expose only relevant (abstract classes, interfaces). SOLID: Single responsibility (class one reason to change), Open-closed (extend, don't modify), Liskov substitution (subtypes substitutable for base), Interface segregation (small, specific interfaces), Dependency inversion (depend on abstractions, not concretions). Composition over inheritance.

---

### Q822: Design Patterns basics?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Creational: Singleton (one instance), Factory Method (create objects), Abstract Factory (families), Builder (complex object construction), Prototype (clone). Structural: Adapter (incompatible interfaces), Decorator (add behavior dynamically), Proxy (control access), Facade (simplified interface), Composite (tree structures). Behavioral: Observer (publish/subscribe), Strategy (interchangeable algorithms), Command (encapsulate request), Iterator (sequential access), State (state-dependent behavior). Patterns are guidelines, not rules. Overuse leads to unnecessary complexity. Modern languages have simpler alternatives (functional interfaces, lambdas).

---

### Q823: Time Complexity?
**Topic:** General CS - DSA
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Measure how runtime grows with input size. Big O: upper bound (worst case). Common: O(1) - constant (array access), O(log n) - logarithmic (binary search), O(n) - linear (array iteration), O(n log n) - linearithmic (sort), O(n^2) - quadratic (nested loops), O(2^n) - exponential (recursive without DP), O(n!) - factorial (permutations). Asymptotic: drop constants and lower-order terms. Space complexity: memory usage. Amortized analysis: average cost over operations (ArrayList add O(1) amortized). Analyze algorithm complexity for interviews.

---

### Q824: RESTful API Design?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Resources identified by URLs (/users, /users/123). HTTP methods: GET (read), POST (create), PUT (full update), PATCH (partial update), DELETE (remove). Stateless: each request contains all information. Status codes: 200 OK, 201 Created, 204 No Content, 400 Bad Request, 401 Unauthorized, 403 Forbidden, 404 Not Found, 409 Conflict, 429 Too Many Requests, 500 Internal Server Error. HATEOAS: links in response (RESTful level 3). Versioning: /v1/users. Pagination: offset/limit or cursor-based. Filtering, sorting: query parameters. Idempotency: same request same effect (GET, PUT, DELETE), POST not idempotent. Richardson Maturity Model.

---

### Q825: GraphQL basics?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Query language for APIs. Client specifies exactly what data it needs. Single endpoint (/graphql). Types: Query (read), Mutation (write), Subscription (real-time). Schema: defined types, fields, relationships. Resolvers: functions that fetch data for each field. Benefits: no over-fetching/under-fetching, strong typing, self-documenting, client-driven. N+1 problem: separate resolver calls for related data (solve with DataLoader - batching + caching). Tools: Apollo (client + server), Relay (Meta), GraphQL Yoga. Vulnerable to: deeply nested queries (query cost analysis, depth limiting). Real-time via WebSocket subscriptions.

---

### Q826: Microservices vs Monolith?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Monolith: single application, simple development/deployment, easier testing, shared memory. Problems: scaling challenges, long CI/CD, tech lock-in, team coupling. Microservices: independent services, separate deployments, independent scaling, polyglot. Problems: distributed complexity (network, data consistency, service discovery, circuit breakers), operational overhead (Kubernetes, monitoring, tracing, logging). When to choose: start with monolith (or modular monolith), extract services when needed (team size, scaling bottlenecks). Strangler Fig pattern: incrementally migrate.

---

### Q827: ACID vs BASE?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ACID (relational databases): Atomicity (all or nothing transaction), Consistency (data follows rules), Isolation (concurrent transactions independent), Durability (committed persists). BASE (NoSQL): Basically Available (system always available), Soft state (state may change without input), Eventually consistent (system becomes consistent over time). CAP theorem: Consistency, Availability, Partition Tolerance - pick 2. MongoDB (CP or AP configurable), Cassandra (AP), HBase (CP). RDBMS: ACID compliant. NoSQL: BASE trade consistency for availability/performance.

---

### Q828: Caching strategies?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
