Cache-aside (lazy loading): app checks cache first, on miss loads from DB and updates cache. Read-through: cache layer handles DB read. Write-through: write to cache + DB synchronously. Write-around: write to DB, invalidate cache (lazy load next read). Write-behind (write-back): write to cache, async batch write to DB. Eviction policies: LRU (least recently used), LFU (least frequently used), FIFO, TTL, Random. Redis: most common cache (string, hash, list, set, sorted set, pub/sub). Memcached: simpler, only strings. Distributed caching: consistent hashing for key distribution.

---

### Q829: Database Indexing?
**Topic:** General CS - SQL
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Data structure for fast data retrieval. B-tree index: balanced tree, O(log n) lookup/insert/delete. Primary key: clustered (data stored in index order, one per table). Secondary index: non-clustered (points to row location). Composite index: multiple columns (order matters, leftmost prefix rule). Unique index: prevents duplicates. Full-text index: for text search. Bitmap index: low cardinality columns. Hash index: equality lookups only (no range). Trade-offs: faster reads, slower writes (maintain index), more storage. ANALYZE, EXPLAIN for query optimization. Covering index: index contains all needed columns (no table access). Avoid over-indexing.

---

### Q830: Event-Driven Architecture?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Components communicate via events. Producer emits event, consumer reacts. Decoupled: producers don't know consumers. Event broker: message queue or event stream. Patterns: Event Notification (simple messages), Event-Carried State Transfer (full data in event), Event Sourcing (events as source of truth), CQRS (separate read/write models). Technologies: Apache Kafka (distributed streaming, durable), RabbitMQ (message broker), AWS SQS/SNS (cloud), Azure Event Hubs, Google Pub/Sub. Benefits: scalability, loose coupling, fault isolation. Challenges: eventual consistency, debugging, exactly-once semantics.

---

### Q831: Distributed Systems CAP Theorem?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Consistency (all nodes see same data at same time), Availability (every request gets response), Partition Tolerance (system continues despite network failures). Choose 2: CP (consistency + partition tolerance - HBase, Zookeeper), AP (availability + partition tolerance - Cassandra, DynamoDB), CA (consistency + availability - single node systems, not distributed). In practice: networks partition, must choose CP or AP. PACELC extension: if partition E (else trade latency vs consistency). Eventual consistency: system converges over time. Strong consistency: linearizability (strict ordering). Tunable consistency (Cassandra: ONE, QUORUM, ALL).

---

### Q832: Consistent Hashing?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Distribution strategy for distributed caching/sharding. Hash servers onto a ring (0 to 2^32-1). Hash key to ring position, assign to nearest server clockwise. Benefits: minimal rehashing when adding/removing servers (only adjacent range affected). Virtual nodes: each server has multiple points on ring (load balancing, handles heterogeneity). Used in: DynamoDB, Cassandra, Discord, consistent hash rings for load balancers (Ketama). Avoids: traditional modulo hashing (key % N) where N changes causes massive remapping.

---

### Q833: Load Balancing algorithms?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Round Robin: sequential distribution (simple, doesn't account for load). Least Connections: send to server with fewest active connections. Least Response Time: send to fastest responding server. IP Hash: hash client IP to server (sticky sessions). Weighted variants: assign weights based on server capacity (Weighted RR, Weighted Least Connections). Random: simple, surprisingly effective. Layer 4 (transport): TCP/UDP based, faster, no content inspection. Layer 7 (application): HTTP based, content-aware routing, SSL termination, header inspection. Tools: NGINX, HAProxy, AWS ELB/ALB/NLB, Azure Load Balancer.

---

### Q834: Message Queues?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Async communication between services. Producer sends message, consumer processes. Decoupling: services don't need to be online simultaneously. Buffer: handle traffic spikes. Reliable: message persistence, retry, dead letter queues. Patterns: point-to-point (one consumer per message - queue), pub/sub (multiple consumers - topic). At-least-once: message may be delivered multiple times (idempotent consumers). At-most-once: may lose messages. Exactly-once: most complex (Kafka transactions). Kafka: distributed, partitioned, replicated log (stream). RabbitMQ: AMQP, flexible routing, exchange types. Message ordering: within partition (Kafka), per queue (RabbitMQ).

---

### Q835: ACID vs BASE in practice?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ACID: PostgreSQL, MySQL, SQL Server, Oracle. Good for financial transactions, inventory, strict consistency needed. BASE: MongoDB, Cassandra, Couchbase, DynamoDB. Good for high volume, global scale, flexible schema (user profiles, sessions, IoT). Many modern systems use hybrid: ACID for critical data (orders, payments), BASE for non-critical (analytics, logs). NewSQL: CockroachDB, Spanner (ACID at global scale, distributed SQL). Choose based on: consistency requirements, data volume, scalability needs, operational complexity.

---

### Q836: Sharding strategies?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Horizontal partitioning: split data across multiple databases. Key-based (hash): hash shard key -> assign shard (even distribution, but range queries across shards expensive). Range-based: partition by value range (e.g., date, ID) - simple range queries, but hot spots. Directory-based: lookup table maps key to shard (flexible, but lookup bottleneck). Vertical sharding: different tables in different databases. Consistent hashing: allows dynamic scaling. Challenges: cross-shard queries, distributed transactions (2PC), resharding (data migration), unique IDs (Snowflake, UUID). Geo-sharding: data near users.

---

### Q837: Idempotency in APIs?
**Topic:** General CS - API Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Same request multiple times produces same result (no side effects). HTTP methods: GET, PUT, DELETE are idempotent (by HTTP spec). POST is not idempotent (creates duplicate resource). Implementation: idempotency key (header), deduplication table (process if not exists), response caching. Use: payment processing (retry without double charge), event processing (once semantics). Idempotency-Key: client-generated UUID, server stores result on first request, returns same result on retry. Expiration: clean up old keys (GC). State machines: ensure transitions idempotent.

---

### Q838: Two-Phase Commit (2PC)?
**Topic:** General CS - Distributed Systems
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Distributed transaction protocol. Coordinator: Phase 1 (Prepare): ask all participants if ready to commit. Phase 2 (Commit): if all yes -> commit (broadcast commit), if any no -> abort. Problems: blocking (coordinator failure blocks participants), vulnerability to coordinator crash (recovery via log), slow (multiple round trips). Alternatives: Saga pattern (compensating transactions, eventual consistency), TCC (Try-Confirm/Cancel), Outbox pattern (local transaction + message), eventual consistency with reconciliation. Modern systems prefer Sagas over 2PC for microservices.

---

### Q839: Saga Pattern?
**Topic:** General CS - Distributed Systems
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Manage distributed transactions without 2PC. Chain of local transactions, each with compensating transaction on failure. Choreography: each service publishes event, next service reacts (simple, but logic spread across services). Orchestration: central orchestrator tells services what to do (better visibility, more complex). Saga flow: start -> local T1 -> if fail -> trigger C1 (compensate). If success -> event -> T2, etc. Eventually consistent: partial failure leaves system in intermediate state until compensation completes. Use for: multi-service workflows (order placement: create order -> reserve inventory -> process payment -> if payment fails, undo inventory).

---

### Q840: WebSocket vs SSE vs Polling?
**Topic:** General CS - Real-time
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Polling: client requests periodically (simple, wasteful if frequent). Long polling: hold request open until data available. Server-Sent Events (SSE): unidirectional (server -> client), HTTP-based, auto-reconnect, text-only. WebSocket: bidirectional, full-duplex, persistent connection, binary + text, no auto-reconnect (needs library). Use cases: polling (low frequency, simple), SSE (notifications, real-time feeds: logs, sports scores, stock tickers), WebSocket (chat, gaming, collaborative editing, real-time updates). SSE simpler than WebSocket for server-to-client only (uses standard HTTP). WebSocket needs upgrade handshake.

---

### Q841: Monorepo vs Polyrepo?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Monorepo: all code in one repository. Benefits: shared tooling, atomic commits, dependency management, code reuse. Challenges: git scale (large repo, history), CI/CD complexity (build only changed parts), access control (per-directory). Tools: Bazel, Nx, Turborepo, Lerna, Rush. Polyrepo: separate repos per service/team. Benefits: independent CI/CD, clear ownership, simpler git history. Challenges: cross-repo changes, dependency version drift, duplicated code. Choose: Google/Meta use monorepos (massive scale, custom tooling). Most teams: polyrepo initially, monorepo if tight coordination needed.

---

### Q842: Polyglot Persistence?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Use different database types for different data needs within same system. Example: PostgreSQL (relational data, transactions), Redis (caching, sessions), Elasticsearch (full-text search), MongoDB (product catalog, flexible schema), Neo4j (social graph), InfluxDB (time series metrics), Cassandra (high write throughput). Benefits: optimal storage/query for each data type. Challenges: operational complexity, data synchronization across stores, transaction spanning stores. Choose based on data access patterns, consistency needs, team expertise. Avoid over-engineering (start with fewer types).

---

### Q843: Back-of-the-envelope calculations?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Rough estimates for system design. Key numbers: 1 million seconds ~ 11.5 days. 1 billion seconds ~ 31.7 years. QPS (queries per second): 1M/day ~ 12 QPS, 1M/hour ~ 278 QPS, 1M/minute ~ 16.7K QPS. Storage: 1 character = 1 byte. 1 text page ~ 2-4KB. 1 photo ~ 100KB-5MB. 1 video (~5 min) ~ 30-100MB. Memory: server ~ 64-256GB RAM, disk ~ 1-10TB SSD. Network: 1 Gbps = 125 MB/s. CDN ~ 3x faster. Examples: Twitter: 500M tweets/day ~ 6K writes/sec, 200K reads/sec. Facebook: 2B users, 1PB photo storage. Important: make reasonable assumptions, show calculation.

---

### Q844: Git workflows?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Git Flow: master (production), develop (integration), feature/ (features), release/, hotfix/. Structured for releases. GitHub Flow: main (always deployable), feature branches -> PR -> merge. Simpler, CI/CD. GitLab Flow: environment branches (staging, production), feature branches, upstream. Trunk-based: short-lived feature branches, merge to main frequently (daily), feature flags for incomplete work. Choose: GitHub/GitLab Flow for continuous delivery, Git Flow for scheduled releases (enterprise). Conflict resolution: rebase feature branches on updated main. Merge vs squash merge vs rebase merge.

---

### Q845: Dependency Injection?
**Topic:** General CS - Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pass dependencies from outside (not create internally). Avoids hard coupling. Types: Constructor injection (most common, dependencies explicit, immutable), Setter injection (optional dependencies, mutable), Interface injection. Benefits: loose coupling, testability (inject mocks), flexibility (swap implementations). Frameworks: Spring (Java), Guice (Java), Dagger (Android), Unity (.NET), manual DI in small projects. Without DI: new Service() inside class (tight coupling). With DI: constructor(Service service), framework provides instance. Inversion of Control: framework controls lifecycle.

---

### Q846: SOLID Principles in practice?
**Topic:** General CS - Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
S (SRP): class/user module/service has one reason to change. UserService handles user CRUD, not email or auth. O (OCP): open for extension, closed for modification. Strategy pattern, plugin architecture. L (LSP): derived class must be substitutable for base. Square extends Rectangle problem (setWidth changes height). Violation: Bicycle inherits from Vehicle but has no engine. I (ISP): many specific interfaces, not one general-purpose. Don't force classes to implement unused methods. D (DIP): depend on abstractions, not concretions. High-level modules shouldn't depend on low-level modules.

---

### Q847: Immutable Infrastructure?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Server never modified after deployment. Replace (not update) for changes. New version = new server image -> deploy -> decommission old. Benefits: consistency (no configuration drift), reproducible, easy rollbacks (deploy previous image), cleaner deployments. Tools: Docker (immutable containers), Packer (machine images), Terraform (provision infrastructure), Kubernetes (immutable pods). Contrast: mutable (SSH into server, apt upgrade, config tweaks - leads to snowflake servers). Immutable is modern best practice. Blue-green deployment: old version kept for rollback.

---

### Q848: Service Mesh?
**Topic:** General CS - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Infrastructure layer for service-to-service communication (separate from application). Sidecar proxy (Envoy) injected alongside each service. Features: service discovery, load balancing, traffic management (canary, blue-green), encryption (mTLS), observability (metrics, tracing, logs), circuit breaking, retries, rate limiting. Istio: most popular (Envoy + control plane). Linkerd: lighter (Rust/Buoyant). Consul Connect (HashiCorp). Benefits: standardize networking across services without code changes. Complexity: adds latency, resource overhead (sidecars), operational burden.

---

### Q849: Functional Programming basics?
**Topic:** General CS - Programming
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Paradigm: computation as evaluation of mathematical functions, avoid state and mutation. Key concepts: Pure functions (same input -> same output, no side effects). Immutability (data never changed, new data created). First-class functions (pass as arguments, return from functions). Higher-order functions (map, filter, reduce). Function composition. Recursion (instead of loops). Lazy evaluation. Referential transparency (expression can be replaced with its value). Benefits: easier testing (no state), parallelization (no race conditions), predictable behavior. Languages: Haskell (pure), Scala, Clojure, F#. JS/Python/Java support functional features.

---

### Q850: Big Data Technologies?
**Topic:** General CS - Big Data
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hadoop ecosystem: HDFS (distributed storage), MapReduce (distributed processing), Hive (SQL on Hadoop), HBase (NoSQL on HDFS). Spark: in-memory distributed processing (faster than MapReduce), supports batch, streaming, ML, SQL. Data formats: Parquet (columnar, compressed), ORC, Avro (row-based, schema evolution). Streaming: Kafka (event streaming), Flink (real-time stream processing), Spark Streaming (micro-batches). Processing at rest (batch) vs in motion (streaming). Modern cloud-native: Snowflake, Databricks, BigQuery, Redshift, EMR. Lakehouse: combine data lake flexibility + warehouse reliability (Delta Lake, Iceberg).

---

### Q851: gRPC vs REST?
**Topic:** General CS - API
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
gRPC: high-performance RPC using Protocol Buffers (binary serialization). HTTP/2 (multiplexed, bidirectional streaming). Strong typing (.proto files), code generation (client/server stubs). 4 modes: Unary, Server streaming, Client streaming, Bidirectional streaming. Benefits: faster (binary, h2 multiplexing), typed, streaming, no REST verb confusion. Downsides: less browser support (needs gRPC-web), binary not human-readable, harder debugging, ecosystem less mature. gRPC-web: browser compatibility. REST: text (JSON/XML), HTTP/1.1, human-readable, ubiquitous. Choose: gRPC for internal microservices, REST for public APIs.

---

### Q852: Kubernetes basics?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Container orchestration platform. Pod: smallest deployable unit (one or more containers). Deployment: declarative updates for pods (replicas, rollback strategy). Service: stable IP/DNS for pods (ClusterIP, NodePort, LoadBalancer). ConfigMap/Secret: configuration. Ingress: HTTP routing to services. PersistentVolume: storage abstraction. Namespace: isolation. kubelet: node agent. kubectl: CLI. Control plane: API server, scheduler, controller-manager, etcd. Self-healing: restarts failed containers, reschedules nodes. Autoscaling: HPA (horizontal pod autoscaler). Kustomize/Helm: package management.

---

### Q853: Docker basics?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Container runtime. Dockerfile: blueprint for image (FROM, RUN, CMD, EXPOSE, WORKDIR, COPY, ENV, ENTRYPOINT). Image: read-only template. Container: running instance of image (isolated, ephemeral). Layer caching: each instruction creates layer (cache layers for faster builds). .dockerignore: exclude files. Docker Compose: multi-container app definition (YAML). Best practices: multi-stage builds (reduce image size), minimal base (alpine), non-root user, one process per container. Volumes: persistent data. Networking: bridge, host, overlay (Swarm). Registry: Docker Hub, ACR, ECR, GCR.

---

### Q854: CI/CD Pipeline design?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CI: build -> lint -> test (unit, integration) -> package -> artifact. CD: deploy to staging -> acceptance tests -> deploy to production (gradual). Tools: Jenkins, GitHub Actions, GitLab CI, CircleCI, Azure DevOps, ArgoCD (GitOps). Best practices: fast feedback (parallel stages), secure (secrets management, no passwords in config), idempotent, version control pipeline config, artifact storage (container registry, package repository), environment-specific configs, approval gates for production. GitOps: Git as source of truth (ArgoCD, Flux). Canary: gradual rollout with monitoring.

---

### Q855: Event Sourcing?
**Topic:** General CS - System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Store state changes as sequence of events (append-only log). Current state = fold/reduce over all events. Benefits: complete audit trail, time travel (reconstruct past state), event-driven (integration events), temporal queries. Challenges: event schema evolution, querying current state (need snapshots/projections), complex, storage growth. CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation): separate write model (event store) from read model (projections). Event store: Kafka (retain events), EventStoreDB, PostgreSQL (events table). Example: bank account events (Created, Deposited, Withdrawn). Snapshots: periodic state snapshots to avoid replaying all events.

---

### Q856: Data Lake vs Data Warehouse?
**Topic:** General CS - Data
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Data Warehouse: structured, schema-on-write (ETL), optimized for analytics queries (columnar storage), ACID or highly structured. Examples: Snowflake, Redshift, BigQuery, Azure Synapse. Data Lake: raw data (structured, semi-structured, unstructured), schema-on-read (ELT), cheaper storage (S3/ADLS/Blob), big data processing (Spark, Hive). Lakehouse: combines both (Delta Lake, Iceberg, Databricks). Use: warehouse for BI dashboards, reports; lake for data science, ML, exploration. Modern trend: lakehouse for unified analytics.

---

### Q857: Distributed Tracing?
**Topic:** General CS - Observability
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Track request through distributed system. Trace: end-to-end request flow. Span: individual unit of work (service call, DB query). Context propagation: trace ID passed via headers. OpenTelemetry: standard for instrumentation (traces, metrics, logs). Tools: Jaeger (open source), Zipkin, Datadog, New Relic, AWS X-Ray. Visualization: flame graphs (time per span), service graphs (dependency map). Sampling: head-based (decide at start), tail-based (sampled after completion). Helps: latency analysis, error attribution, dependency mapping.

---

### Q858: Feature Flags?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Toggle features on/off without deployment. Benefits: continuous deployment (release incomplete features), A/B testing, canary releases, kill switch (disable broken feature), operational control. Types: release toggle, experiment toggle, ops toggle, permission toggle. Tools: LaunchDarkly, Unleash, Flagsmith, Split. Best practices: keep flags short-lived (remove when feature stable), naming conventions, audit log of flag changes, flag evaluation should be fast (local cached). In code: if featureFlag.isEnabled('new-payment'): useNewPayment(). Use flags wisely (don't create flag hell). Avoid long-lived flags.

---

### Q859: Strangler Fig Pattern?
**Topic:** General CS - Migration
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Incremental migration from legacy to new system. Gradually replace specific functionality, route traffic from old to new, eventually decommission old. Steps: identify module to replace, build new implementation (API compatible), add routing layer (forward to old or new), switch traffic when ready, remove old code. Example: monolith to microservices migration. Add service for user management, route user-related requests to new service, continue for other modules. Benefits: low risk (can rollback), continuous delivery, no big bang migration. Martin Fowler's recommended approach.

---

### Q860: Database Connection Pooling?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Maintain pool of database connections for reuse (avoid creating connection per request). Expensive: TCP handshake, auth, memory. Pool: HikariCP (Java - fastest), pgBouncer (PostgreSQL connection pooler), SQLAlchemy pool (Python). Important settings: maximum pool size (typically ~10-50 per app instance, not 100+), minimum idle, connection timeout, idle timeout, max lifetime. Connection leak: not returning connection to pool (use try-with-resources, connection.close()). Validate connections: test query on borrow. Pool sizing: small pool often better (avoids DB overload). HikariCP formula: T*C / S (T=threads, C=roundtrips, S=avg time/request).

## Java

### Q1: What is the difference between JDK, JRE, and JVM?
**Topic:** Java
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
- **JVM:** Runtime engine that executes bytecode, provides memory management and garbage collection
- **JRE:** JVM + core libraries for running Java applications
- **JDK:** JRE + development tools (javac, jdb, jar)

**Relationship:** JDK contains JRE which contains JVM.

---

### Q2: Explain Java platform independence.
**Topic:** Java
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Java source code is compiled into bytecode (.class files) which is platform-neutral. Each platform has its own JVM that interprets bytecode into native instructions. "Write Once, Run Anywhere" - same bytecode runs on any platform with a compatible JVM.

---

### Q3: What are the four OOP principles?
**Topic:** Java - OOP
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
1. **Encapsulation:** Bundling data and methods, restricting access via access modifiers (private/public)
2. **Inheritance:** Creating child classes from parent using `extends`, promotes code reuse
3. **Polymorphism:** Compile-time (overloading) + Runtime (overriding, dynamic method dispatch)
4. **Abstraction:** Hiding implementation details via abstract classes and interfaces

---

### Q4: Method overloading vs overriding?
**Topic:** Java - OOP
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Overloading: same method name, different parameters, compile-time binding, within same class. Overriding: same signature, different implementation, runtime binding, between parent-child classes.

---

### Q5: Abstract class vs Interface?
**Topic:** Java - OOP
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Abstract class: can have instance variables, constructors, concrete + abstract methods, single inheritance ("is-a"). Interface: public static final constants, default/static methods (Java 8+), private methods (Java 9+), multiple inheritance ("can-do").

---

### Q6: String vs StringBuilder vs StringBuffer?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
String: immutable, thread-safe, slow for modifications (new object per operation). StringBuilder: mutable, not thread-safe, fastest. StringBuffer: mutable, thread-safe (synchronized methods).

---

### Q7: The final keyword?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
final variable: cannot be reassigned. final method: cannot be overridden. final class: cannot be extended. Provides immutability and security guarantees.

---

### Q8: Access modifiers in Java?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
private (same class) -> default/package-private (same package) -> protected (package + subclasses) -> public (everyone). Favor most restrictive access.

---

### Q9: What is garbage collection?
**Topic:** Java - Memory Management
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Automatic memory reclamation of unreachable objects. Generational: Young (Eden + Survivor spaces) -> Old (Tenured) -> Metaspace (class metadata). Algorithms: Serial, Parallel, G1 (default since Java 9), ZGC. Minor GC collects Young, Major GC collects Old, Full GC collects all.

---

### Q10: == vs equals()?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
== compares reference equality (same memory location). equals() compares value/logical equality (override for custom classes). Always override hashCode() when overriding equals().

---

### Q11: hashCode() and equals() contract?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. If objects are equal via equals(), they MUST have same hashCode()
2. If objects have same hashCode(), they MAY or MAY NOT be equal (hash collisions are allowed)
3. hashCode() must stay consistent during one execution if equals() fields don't change
4. Use same fields in both methods

---

### Q12: Collections Framework hierarchy?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Collection -> List (ArrayList, LinkedList), Set (HashSet, LinkedHashSet, TreeSet), Queue (PriorityQueue, ArrayDeque). Map is separate: HashMap, LinkedHashMap, TreeMap, ConcurrentHashMap. Collections is utility class with sort(), shuffle(), unmodifiableList(), etc.

---

### Q13: How does HashMap work internally?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Array of Node<K,V>[] buckets. put(): hash(key) via hashCode() XOR (hashCode >>> 16), bucket index = (n-1) & hash. Collisions stored as linked list, converted to red-black tree at threshold 8 (Java 8+). Load factor 0.75 triggers resize to double capacity. get(): same hash/index, traverse list/tree comparing keys via == then equals(). Java 8+ improvements: tree bins for O(log n) collision resolution.

---

### Q14: ArrayList vs LinkedList?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
ArrayList: O(1) get, O(n) insert/delete middle, O(1) amortized add at end, contiguous memory (cache-friendly). LinkedList: O(n) get, O(1) insert/delete at ends, more memory (prev/next pointers). Use ArrayList for most cases, LinkedList for frequent head/tail operations or when needing Deque.

---

### Q15: ConcurrentHashMap vs Hashtable vs synchronizedMap?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
ConcurrentHashMap: node-level locking + CAS operations, lock-free reads (volatile), weakly consistent iterators, high concurrency (multiple threads modify different buckets). Hashtable: single lock on entire map, poor concurrency, fail-fast iterators. synchronizedMap: single lock, poor concurrency. Always prefer ConcurrentHashMap for concurrent access.

---

### Q16: Comparable vs Comparator?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Comparable: compareTo(T o) in the class itself, natural ordering, single sort sequence. Comparator: compare(T o1, T o2) external class, multiple sort sequences, can be lambda. Use Comparator.comparing() for chaining.

---

### Q17: Ways to iterate a collection?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
for-index, enhanced for-each, Iterator (with remove()), ListIterator (bidirectional), forEach lambda, Stream API (filter/map/collect). Enumeration for legacy classes.

---

### Q18: Fail-fast vs fail-safe iterators?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Fail-fast: check modCount field, throw ConcurrentModificationException if collection structurally modified during iteration (ArrayList, HashMap). Fail-safe (weakly consistent): operate on snapshot/copy, no exception, may see stale data (ConcurrentHashMap, CopyOnWriteArrayList).

---

### Q19: Stream intermediate and terminal operations?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Intermediate (lazy, return Stream): filter, map, flatMap, distinct, sorted, peek, limit, skip. Terminal (produce result): forEach, collect, reduce, count, anyMatch, allMatch, noneMatch, findFirst, findAny, min, max, toList().

---

### Q20: map() vs flatMap()?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
map(): 1:1 transformation (each element -> one output element). flatMap(): 1:N transformation + flattening (each element -> Stream of elements, all flattened into single stream). flatMap is used for Optional unwrapping, nested collection flattening.

---

### Q21: What is Optional?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Container for nullable values (Java 8+). Methods: orElse(default), orElseGet(supplier), ifPresent(consumer), map(), filter(), orElseThrow(), ifPresentOrElse(). Best practice: use as return type only (NOT fields/parameters), prefer orElseGet over orElse for expensive defaults.

---

### Q22: Checked vs unchecked exceptions?
**Topic:** Java - Exception
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Checked: must handle via try-catch or declare throws (IOException, SQLException, ClassNotFoundException). Unchecked (RuntimeException): may handle but not required (NullPointerException, IllegalArgumentException, IndexOutOfBoundsException). Errors (Error class): unrecoverable, should not be caught (OutOfMemoryError, StackOverflowError).

---

### Q23: throw vs throws?
**Topic:** Java - Exception
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
throw: inside method body, actually throws an exception instance. throws: in method signature, declares what exceptions the method MAY throw.

---

### Q24: try-with-resources?
**Topic:** Java - Exception
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Java 7+ feature that automatically closes AutoCloseable resources. Resources declared in try header are closed in reverse order. Supports suppressed exceptions (when close() throws while another exception is active). Eliminates need for finally blocks for cleanup.

---

### Q25: Creating threads in Java?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Extend Thread class and override run()
2. Implement Runnable interface (preferred)
3. Implement Callable (returns value, throws checked exceptions) with FutureTask or ExecutorService
4. ExecutorService.submit() with lambda

---

### Q26: synchronized keyword?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensures mutual exclusion via intrinsic lock (monitor). synchronized method locks on this (instance) or Class (static). synchronized block locks on specified object. Reentrant: same thread can re-enter other synchronized blocks on same object. Lock released automatically when block exits (normally or via exception).

---

### Q27: volatile keyword?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensures visibility across threads: reads/writes directly to/from main memory (not CPU cache). Establishes happens-before relationship. Does NOT guarantee atomicity for compound actions (count++). Use AtomicInteger for atomic read-modify-write.

---

### Q28: Java Memory Model (JMM)?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
JMM defines how threads interact through memory. Happens-Before rules: program order, monitor lock (unlock happens-before subsequent lock on same monitor), volatile write-read, thread start (start happens-before thread action), thread join (thread actions happen-before join returns), transitivity. Memory barriers prevent instruction reordering by compiler/CPU.

---

### Q29: Thread pool types in Executors?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
newFixedThreadPool(n): fixed threads, unbounded LinkedBlockingQueue. newCachedThreadPool(): dynamic threads, SynchronousQueue, 60s idle timeout. newSingleThreadExecutor(): single thread, sequential execution. newScheduledThreadPool(n): delayed/periodic tasks. newWorkStealingPool() (Java 8+): ForkJoinPool with work-stealing.

---

### Q30: wait(), notify(), notifyAll()?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Object methods for inter-thread communication. MUST be called from synchronized context. wait() releases monitor lock, thread enters WAITING state. notify() wakes one waiting thread (random selection). notifyAll() wakes all waiting threads. Always call wait() in a while loop to guard against spurious wakeups.

---

### Q31: Callable and Future?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Callable<V>: functional interface with call() that returns V and throws Exception. Future<V>: represents async computation result. get() blocks until result available, get(timeout) with timeout, cancel(true) to interrupt, isDone() to check. CompletableFuture (Java 8+) extends Future with non-blocking callbacks and chaining.

---

### Q32: start() vs run()?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
start() creates new thread and calls run() on that thread asynchronously. run() executes on calling thread (synchronous, no new thread). Calling run() directly bypasses new thread creation - it becomes a regular method call.

---

### Q33: CountDownLatch vs CyclicBarrier?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
CountDownLatch: one-shot barrier, countDown() decrements, await() blocks until zero, NOT reusable. CyclicBarrier: reusable barrier, await() blocks until all parties arrive, optional barrier action (Runnable), can reset().

---

### Q34: What is Serialization?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Converting object state into byte stream for persistence/transmission. Class must implement Serializable (marker interface). transient fields are skipped. serialVersionUID for version control. readObject/writeObject for custom serialization. Static fields are not serialized.

---

### Q35: Externalizable vs Serializable?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Serializable: automatic serialization (reflection-based), no-arg constructor NOT required. Externalizable: writeExternal/readExternal (full control), public no-arg constructor REQUIRED, better performance as you control what/when to write.

---

### Q36: Custom annotations?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Defined with @interface. Meta-annotations: @Retention (SOURCE/CLASS/RUNTIME), @Target (METHOD, FIELD, TYPE, etc.). Elements: String value() default ""; RUNTIME retention allows reflection-based processing.

---

### Q37: Java modules (JPMS)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Project Jigsaw (Java 9+). module-info.java defines: requires (dependencies), exports (accessible packages), opens (for reflection), provides/uses (service loader). Benefits: strong encapsulation, reliable configuration, no classpath hell.

---

### Q38: Type erasure in generics?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Type parameters erased at compile time: T becomes Object (unbounded) or leftmost bound. Casts inserted automatically. Bridge methods generated for polymorphic type safety. Consequences: cannot instanceof parameterized types, cannot create arrays of parameterized types, cannot use new T(), overloaded methods with same erasure conflict.

---

### Q39: PECS (Producer Extends Consumer Super)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
? extends T (covariant): producer that provides T values (read only). ? super T (contravariant): consumer that accepts T values (write only). T (invariant): both read and write. Collections.copy(dest, src) uses List<? super T> dest (consumer) and List<? extends T> src (producer).

---

### Q40: Collection vs Collections?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Collection: root interface of collections framework (add, remove, size, iterator, isEmpty). Collections: utility class with static methods (sort, shuffle, reverse, binarySearch, unmodifiableList, synchronizedMap, max, min, frequency, disjoint).

---

### Q41: Arrays.asList() vs List.of()?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Arrays.asList(): fixed-size list backed by array, allows set() but not add/remove (UnsupportedOperationException), permits nulls. List.of() (Java 9+): fully immutable list, no nulls allowed, compact internal representation. Both prohibit structural modifications.

---

### Q42: Byte vs Character streams?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Byte streams (InputStream/OutputStream): read/write 8-bit bytes, for binary data (images, audio, zip). Character streams (Reader/Writer): read/write 16-bit Unicode characters, for text data, handle encoding/decoding via charset. Bridge classes: InputStreamReader, OutputStreamWriter convert between them.

---

### Q43: Lambda expressions?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Concise syntax for SAM (Single Abstract Method) interfaces. Syntax: (params) -> expression or (params) -> { statements }. Captures effectively final variables from enclosing scope. Used with functional interfaces: Predicate, Function, Consumer, Supplier.

---

### Q44: @FunctionalInterface?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Annotation indicating interface has exactly one abstract method. Compiler enforces this. Built-in: Runnable, Callable, Comparator, Predicate<T>, Function<T,R>, Consumer<T>, Supplier<T>, UnaryOperator<T>, BinaryOperator<T>, BiFunction<T,U,R>.

---

### Q45: java.util.concurrent package main classes?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Executors (thread pool management), Synchronizers (CountDownLatch, CyclicBarrier, Semaphore, Phaser, Exchanger), Concurrent Collections (ConcurrentHashMap, CopyOnWriteArrayList, BlockingQueue, ConcurrentLinkedQueue), Atomic classes (AtomicInteger, LongAdder, AtomicReference), Locks (ReentrantLock, ReentrantReadWriteLock, StampedLock), CompletableFuture.

---

### Q46: ReentrantLock vs synchronized?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
ReentrantLock: tryLock(timeout), lockInterruptibly(), fairness parameter, multiple Conditions via newCondition(), ReadWriteLock support. Must call unlock() in finally. synchronized: automatic lock release, simpler syntax, no timeout/cancel. Prefer synchronized for simple cases, ReentrantLock for advanced scenarios.

---

### Q47: ForkJoinPool?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Work-stealing thread pool (Java 7+) for divide-and-conquer parallelism. Each thread has a deque of tasks. fork() pushes subtask to local deque, join() waits for result. Idle threads steal tasks from busy threads' deque bottoms. Used by parallel streams. Extends RecursiveTask/RecursiveAction.

---

### Q48: CompletableFuture?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Extends Future and CompletionStage (Java 8+). Non-blocking: thenApply (map), thenCompose (flatMap), thenAccept, thenRun. Combining: thenCombine, allOf, anyOf. Error handling: exceptionally, handle, whenComplete. Manual completion: complete, completeExceptionally. Uses ForkJoinPool.commonPool by default.

---

### Q49: Stream reduce and collect?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
reduce(): immutable reduction with BinaryOperator. Three forms: Optional reduce(BinaryOperator), reduce(identity, BinaryOperator), reduce(identity, accumulator, combiner) for parallel. collect(): mutable reduction with Collector. Collectors: toList, toSet, toMap, groupingBy, partitioningBy, joining, summingInt, averagingDouble, summarizingInt, toCollection, teeing (Java 12+).

---

### Q50: parallelStream() vs stream().parallel()?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Both produce parallel streams using ForkJoinPool.commonPool(). No functional difference. collection.parallelStream() is direct, stream().parallel() converts sequential to parallel (can switch back via sequential()). Effective for large datasets, CPU-intensive operations, independent elements. Avoid for small data, I/O operations, or operations with shared mutable state.

---

### Q51: Heap vs Stack memory?
**Topic:** Java - Memory Management
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Stack: per-thread, stores local variables and method calls (frames), small size (~1MB default), StackOverflowError on deep recursion. Heap: shared across threads, stores objects and arrays, larger size (configurable via -Xms/-Xmx), OutOfMemoryError when full. Primitives and references live on stack, objects live on heap.

---

### Q52: ThreadLocal?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Per-thread variable: each thread has its own independent copy. Each Thread has a ThreadLocalMap keyed by ThreadLocal object. Use cases: request context (user, transaction ID), SimpleDateFormat (not thread-safe), per-thread DB connections. CRITICAL: always call remove() in finally block in thread pools to prevent memory leaks.

---

### Q53: sleep() vs wait()?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
sleep(): Thread static method, does NOT release monitor locks, no synchronization required. wait(): Object instance method, MUST be in synchronized context, RELEASES monitor lock, used for producer-consumer patterns. sleep is for timing, wait is for inter-thread communication.

---

### Q54: Future vs CompletableFuture?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Future: blocking get() API, no callbacks, no chaining, no exception handling, no manual completion. CompletableFuture: non-blocking with callbacks (thenApply, thenAccept), chaining (thenCompose), combining (thenCombine, allOf), exception handling (exceptionally), manual completion (complete, completeExceptionally).

---

### Q55: Error vs Exception?
**Topic:** Java - Exception
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Both extend Throwable. Error: serious unrecoverable JVM issues (OutOfMemoryError, StackOverflowError), should NOT be caught. Exception: recoverable conditions, SHOULD be caught/handled. Checked exceptions must be handled. Unchecked (RuntimeException) are programming bugs.

---

### Q56: try-catch-finally execution order?
**Topic:** Java - Exception
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Execution: try -> (if exception) matching catch -> finally -> method return/throw. NOTE: finally ALWAYS executes (even with return in try/catch). If finally has return, it overrides try/catch return. If finally throws exception, it replaces any exception from try/catch. Never return from finally.

---

### Q57: interrupt(), interrupted(), isInterrupted()?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
interrupt(): instance method, sets thread's interrupt flag. interrupted(): static method, returns current thread's flag AND clears it. isInterrupted(): instance method, returns flag without clearing. When InterruptedException is caught, the flag is cleared - always restore it: Thread.currentThread().interrupt().

---

### Q58: GC types?
**Topic:** Java - Memory Management
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Minor GC: collects Young Generation (Eden + Survivor), S-T-W pause, copying collector. Major GC: collects Old Generation. Full GC: Young + Old + Metaspace, most expensive. Algorithms: Serial (single-thread, small heaps), Parallel (throughput-oriented, multi-thread), G1 (region-based, default, predictable pauses), ZGC (concurrent, sub-millisecond, large heaps), Shenandoah (concurrent compaction).

---

### Q59: Diamond problem in Java?
**Topic:** Java - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Class implements two interfaces with same default method. The class must override the method to resolve ambiguity, using InterfaceName.super.methodName() syntax to call specific interface default.

---

### Q60: String pool and intern()?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
String literals are automatically interned (stored in String Constant Pool on heap, was PermGen pre-Java 7). new String("") creates separate heap object. intern() manually adds string to pool or returns existing pool reference. Useful for deduplication of frequently used strings.

---

### Q61: is-a vs has-a relationship?
**Topic:** Java - OOP
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
is-a: inheritance relationship (extends/implements). Dog IS-A Animal. has-a: composition/aggregation. Car HAS-A Engine. Prefer composition over inheritance (more flexible, looser coupling). Use inheritance for true IS-A relationships and polymorphic behavior.

---

### Q62: Method reference?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Shorthand for lambda calling existing method. Types: Class::staticMethod (Integer::parseInt), instance::method (System.out::println), Class::instanceMethod (String::toUpperCase), Class::new (ArrayList::new). Compiler infers functional interface type.

---

### Q63: Default method in interface?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Method with default implementation in interface (Java 8+). Enables adding methods to interfaces without breaking existing implementations. Classes can override. If conflict (same default method in two interfaces), class must override. Solves the interface evolution problem.

---

### Q64: Autoboxing/Unboxing?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Automatic conversion between primitives and wrapper classes. Integer i = 42; (int -> Integer via valueOf()). int j = i; (Integer -> int via intValue()). Caching: Integer, Short, Long (-128 to 127), Byte (all), Character (0-127), Boolean (both). Wrappers are objects (more memory, can be null). Performance overhead in tight loops.

---

### Q65: transient vs volatile?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
transient: exclude field from serialization (restored as default value on deserialization). volatile: ensure thread visibility (reads/writes directly from main memory). transient relates to serialization, volatile relates to threading.

---

### Q66: BigDecimal vs double?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
double: IEEE 754 binary floating-point, cannot represent decimal fractions exactly (0.1 + 0.2 != 0.3). BigDecimal: arbitrary-precision decimal, exact representation via unscaled integer x 10^(-scale). Use BigDecimal for financial/monetary calculations. Always use String constructor (new BigDecimal("0.1")), not double constructor. Specify scale and RoundingMode for division.

---

### Q67: Inner class types?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Member inner class: defined at class level, has access to outer class members, requires outer instance
2. Static nested class: static member, no access to outer instance fields (like top-level class)
3. Local inner class: defined in method, scope limited to method, access effectively final locals
4. Anonymous inner class: unnamed class created on the fly, typically for event handlers, thread creation

---

### Q68: Marker interface?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Interface with no methods or fields (Serializable, Cloneable, RandomAccess). Signals special behavior to JVM or frameworks. Modern alternative: annotations (@Serial). marker interfaces preserved for backward compatibility.

---

### Q69: ClassLoader hierarchy?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Three main classloaders: Bootstrap (rt.jar, core libs, written in native code), Extension (jre/lib/ext, Java 8-/deprecated in Java 9+), Application/System (classpath). Delegation model: classloader asks parent first, only tries to load if parent cannot find class. Prevents loading same class multiple times.

---

### Q70: Reflection?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Runtime inspection and modification of classes, methods, fields. API: Class.forName(), getMethod(), getDeclaredField(), setAccessible(true), invoke(). Used by: Spring (DI, AOP), Hibernate (JPA), JUnit, Jackson serialization. Performance overhead (caching can mitigate). Security restrictions (SecurityManager). Modern alternatives: method handles (java.lang.invoke), annotation processing.

---

### Q71: Record (Java 14+)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Transparent data carrier. Compiler auto-generates: canonical constructor, accessor methods (field() not getField()), equals(), hashCode(), toString(). Implicitly final, extends java.lang.Record, cannot extend other classes. Can add static methods and instance methods but fields are only the record components.

---

### Q72: Sealed class (Java 17+)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Restricts which classes/interfaces can extend/implement it. sealed class Shape permits Circle, Rectangle, Triangle {}. Permitted subclasses must be final, sealed, or non-sealed. Enables exhaustive pattern matching. Package-private permits by default.

---

### Q73: Switch expression (Java 14+)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Enhanced switch: can return value, no fall-through (arrow case), exhaustive (must cover all cases or have default). String result = switch(day) { case MON, FRI -> "Work"; case SAT, SUN -> "Rest"; default -> "Midweek"; }. Can be used as expression or statement.

---

### Q74: Text blocks (Java 15+)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Multi-line string literals delimited by triple quotes ("""). Preserves line breaks, automatic indentation stripping (based on leftmost non-whitespace character). Eliminates need for \n concatenation. Useful for JSON, SQL, HTML templates embedded in code.

---

### Q75: Pattern matching for instanceof (Java 16+)?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Combines type check with variable binding: if (obj instanceof String s) { s.length(); }. s is scoped to the if block (and else if negated). Reduces boilerplate of separate instanceof check + cast.

---

### Q76: PermGen vs Metaspace?
**Topic:** Java - Memory Management
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
PermGen (Java 7-): fixed-size heap memory for class metadata, string pool, static fields. Prone to OutOfMemoryError: PermGen space. Metaspace (Java 8+): native memory (outside heap), dynamically grows by default, uses OS memory, limited by available memory. -XX:MaxMetaspaceSize to cap.

---

### Q77: -Xmx and -Xms JVM flags?
**Topic:** Java - Memory Management
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
-Xms: initial heap size at JVM startup. -Xmx: maximum heap size. -Xss: thread stack size. -XX:MaxMetaspaceSize: Metaspace limit. -XX:+UseG1GC: use G1 garbage collector. -XX:MaxGCPauseMillis: target GC pause time.

---

### Q78: Race condition?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Occurs when multiple threads concurrently access shared data and result depends on thread scheduling/timing. Example: two threads incrementing count without synchronization (read one value, both write same result). Fix: synchronized, AtomicInteger, ReentrantLock, or other synchronization mechanisms.

---

### Q79: Deadlock? Prevention?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Thread A holds lock 1, waits for lock 2. Thread B holds lock 2, waits for lock 1. Prevention: consistent lock ordering (always acquire locks in same order), tryLock with timeout (back off and retry), use higher-level concurrency utilities (BlockingQueue, CompletableFuture), reduce lock scope, use lock-free data structures.

---

### Q80: Livelock?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Threads aren't blocked but keep responding to each other's actions without making progress. Example: two threads trying to acquire same locks, release when they detect conflict, retry - both keep releasing and retrying in sync. Fix: randomized wait times before retry, different lock acquisition order.

---

### Q81: CAS (Compare-And-Swap)?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Atomic CPU instruction: compares memory location value with expected value, if equal, swaps with new value atomically. Foundation of lock-free programming. Used by AtomicInteger, AtomicLong, etc. ABA problem: value changes A->B->A, CAS sees A and succeeds. Fix: AtomicStampedReference (version counter).

---

### Q82: EnumSet?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Specialized Set implementation for enum types. Backed by bit vector (64-bit long for enums up to 64 values, long[] for larger). Extremely compact and fast O(1) operations. Factory methods: allOf, noneOf, of, range, complementOf, copyOf. Null elements not allowed.

---

### Q83: EnumMap?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Specialized Map for enum keys. Backed by array indexed by enum ordinal. Faster (no hashing needed) and more memory-efficient than HashMap for enum keys. Maintains insertion order. Null keys not allowed. Factory: new EnumMap<>(EnumClass.class).

---

### Q84: WeakHashMap?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
HashMap with WeakReferences for keys. Key-value entry auto-removed when key is no longer referenced (GC clears WeakReference). Used for caches/mappings where keys are temporary. Complemented by ReferenceQueue: GC queues cleared references for cleanup. Not synchronized.

---

### Q85: IdentityHashMap?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Map that uses reference equality (==) instead of equals() for key comparison. Used in serialization (maintain object identity graph), debugging, deep-copy implementations. Linear-probing hash table (not chaining). Not synchronized.

---

### Q86: PriorityQueue?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Unbounded priority heap (min-heap by default). Orders elements by natural order or Comparator. O(log n) for offer/poll, O(1) for peek, O(n) for remove(Object). Not thread-safe (PriorityBlockingQueue for concurrent use). Does not permit null elements. Iterator does not guarantee priority order.

---

### Q87: Queue vs Deque?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Queue: FIFO single-ended - add/offer (tail), remove/poll/element/peek (head). Deque: double-ended - addFirst/Last, removeFirst/Last, getFirst/Last. Deque can be stack (push/pop - LIFO) or queue (FIFO). ArrayDeque is generally faster than LinkedList as Deque.

---

### Q88: retainAll() vs removeAll()?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
retainAll(Collection c): removes all elements NOT in c (intersection/set-and). removeAll(Collection c): removes all elements that ARE in c (difference/set-subtract). Both modify the collection.

---

### Q89: NavigableMap and NavigableSet?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Sorted navigation methods: lower(k) - strictly less, floor(k) - less or equal, ceiling(k) - greater or equal, higher(k) - strictly greater, pollFirst()/pollLast() - remove and return, descendingMap() - reverse order, subMap(from, to), headMap(to), tailMap(from). TreeMap implements NavigableMap.

---

### Q90: LinkedHashMap?
**Topic:** Java - Collections
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HashMap + doubly-linked list maintaining insertion order (or access order for LRU cache). accessOrder=true in constructor enables access-order iteration (least recently accessed first). Override removeEldestEntry() to implement LRU cache auto-eviction.

---

### Q91: Producer-Consumer with BlockingQueue?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
BlockingQueue handles all synchronization: put() blocks if full, take() blocks if empty. Implementations: ArrayBlockingQueue (bounded, fair/not-fair), LinkedBlockingQueue (optionally bounded), DelayQueue (delayed elements), PriorityBlockingQueue, SynchronousQueue (zero capacity handoff). Simplifies producer-consumer by eliminating explicit wait/notify.

---

### Q92: LockSupport park/unpark?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Thread parking mechanism (foundation for AQS). park(): suspends thread if permit unavailable (may return spuriously). unpark(thread): makes permit available. If unpark called before park, park returns immediately (permit consumed). Unlike wait/notify: no synchronized needed, thread-specific not object-specific.

---

### Q93: Phaser?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Reusable synchronization barrier (Java 7+) with dynamic party registration. More flexible than CyclicBarrier: parties can register/deregister between phases. Methods: register(), arriveAndAwaitAdvance(), arriveAndDeregister(), arrive(), awaitAdvance(). getPhase() returns current phase number. onAdvance() for phase-transition actions.

---

### Q94: Semaphore?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Counting semaphore controlling access to limited resource. acquire() decrements (blocks if zero), release() increments. Binary semaphore (1 permit) similar to mutex. Fairness parameter. Use for: connection pool, rate limiting, bounded resource access.

---

### Q95: Exchanger?
**Topic:** Java - Multi-threading
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Synchronization point where two threads exchange objects. exchange(V data) blocks until both threads call it, then swaps values. Useful for: two-thread pipeline, buffer swapping (producer fills buffer A, consumer empties buffer B, then swap).

---

### Q96: Stream parallel performance?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Use parallel when: large dataset, CPU-intensive operations per element, data structure splittable (ArrayList better than LinkedList), no shared mutable state, available CPU cores. Avoid parallel when: small dataset, I/O-bound operations, sequential dependencies, costly combining operations, operations with side effects.

---

### Q97: Custom Collector?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Collector.of(supplier, accumulator, combiner, finisher, characteristics). Supplier: creates mutable container (StringJoiner). Accumulator: adds element to container. Combiner: merges two containers (for parallel). Finisher: transforms container to final result. Characteristics: CONCURRENT, UNORDERED, IDENTITY_FINISH.

---

### Q98: Spliterator?
**Topic:** Java - Core
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Iterator for traversing and partitioning elements. tryAdvance() (single element) / forEachRemaining() (batch). trySplit() partitions elements for parallel processing. characteristics(): ORDERED, DISTINCT, SIZED, SUBSIZED, SORTED, NONNULL, IMMUTABLE, CONCURRENT. Used internally by parallel streams.

---

### Q99: Primitive streams (IntStream, LongStream, DoubleStream)?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Avoid autoboxing overhead. Creation: IntStream.range(a, b), rangeClosed(a, b), of(values). Operations: sum(), average(), min(), max(), summaryStatistics() (returns IntSummaryStatistics). map(), filter(), flatMap() work with primitive functions. boxed() converts to Stream<Integer>.

---

### Q100: Collectors.teeing() (Java 12+)?
**Topic:** Java - Streams
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Combines two collectors into one, processing stream once. Each element fed to both collectors, results merged with BiFunction. Example: Collectors.teeing(Collectors.counting(), Collectors.summingInt(Employee::getSalary), (count, sum) -> new Statistics(count, sum)).

## Machine Learning

### Q661: Supervised vs Unsupervised vs Reinforcement Learning?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Supervised: labeled data (features + target). Regression (continuous target) and Classification (categorical target). Examples: linear regression, logistic regression, random forest, SVM, neural networks. Unsupervised: no labels, finds hidden patterns. Clustering (K-means, DBSCAN, hierarchical), Dimensionality Reduction (PCA, t-SNE), Association (Apriori). Reinforcement Learning: agent learns by interacting with environment, receives rewards/penalties. Q-learning, Deep Q-Networks (DQN), Policy Gradients, PPO. Agent vs Environment vs Reward. Use: games, robotics, recommendation.

---

### Q662: Bias vs Variance tradeoff?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Bias: error from assuming model is too simple (underfitting). High bias = model misses relevant patterns. Variance: error from model being too complex (overfitting). High variance = model captures noise. Tradeoff: increasing model complexity reduces bias but increases variance. Goal: find sweet spot minimizing total error = bias + variance + irreducible error. Regularization increases bias, reduces variance. Ensemble methods (random forest) reduce variance while keeping bias low.

---

### Q663: Overfitting and prevention?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Overfitting: model performs well on training data but poorly on unseen data (memorizes noise). Symptoms: high train accuracy, low test accuracy. Prevention: 1) More training data. 2) Simplify model (fewer features, lower polynomial degree). 3) Regularization (L1/Lasso, L2/Ridge). 4) Cross-validation (detect when model starts overfitting). 5) Feature selection/reduction (PCA). 6) Early stopping (gradient boosting, neural nets). 7) Dropout (neural nets). 8) Ensemble (reduces variance). 9) Pruning (decision trees). 10) Data augmentation.

---

### Q664: Cross-validation techniques?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Metrics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
K-Fold: split data into K folds, train on K-1, test on 1, repeat K times. Stratified K-Fold: preserves class proportions (for imbalanced classification). Leave-One-Out (LOOCV): each sample is test set (n folds). Very expensive. Repeated K-Fold: repeat K-Fold multiple times with different shuffles. Time Series: temporal split (no future data leaks). Shuffle-Split: random train/test splits. Group K-Fold: no data from same group in both train/test (avoid leakage). Use cross_val_score() in sklearn.

---

### Q665: Precision, Recall, F1, AUC-ROC?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Metrics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Confusion Matrix: TP, TN, FP, FN. Accuracy = (TP+TN)/(total). Precision = TP/(TP+FP) - how many predicted positive are actually positive (no false alarms). Recall = TP/(TP+FN) - how many actual positives found (no misses). F1 = 2*P*R/(P+R) - harmonic mean of precision and recall (balanced metric). Specificity = TN/(TN+FP). ROC Curve: TPR vs FPR at various thresholds. AUC: area under ROC curve (0.5 = random, 1 = perfect). For imbalanced classes: prefer PR curve over ROC. Precision-Recall AUC.

---

### Q666: Linear Regression assumptions?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Regression
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Linearity: relationship between X and y is linear. 2. Independence: observations independent (no autocorrelation). 3. Homoscedasticity: constant variance of residuals (no increasing spread). 4. Normality: residuals normally distributed (for inference/p-values). 5. No multicollinearity: features not highly correlated (VIF < 5-10). 6. No outliers (high leverage). Violations: transform features, use robust regression, use polynomial features, use regularization. OLS estimator: minimize sum of squared residuals. R-squared: proportion of variance explained.

---

### Q667: Logistic Regression?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Classification algorithm (binary or multi-class). Predicts probability using sigmoid function: p = 1/(1 + e^-(b0 + b1*x)). Log-odds: log(p/(1-p)) = b0 + b1*x. Decision boundary: p > 0.5 -> class 1. Loss: Binary Cross-Entropy (Log Loss). Training: Maximum Likelihood Estimation (gradient descent). Regularization: L1/L2. Multi-class: Softmax (multinomial logistic regression). Fast, interpretable, probabilistically calibrated.

---

### Q668: Decision Trees?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tree model: internal nodes test feature, leaf nodes predict class/value. Training: recursive partitioning, choose best split at each node. Splitting criteria: Gini impurity (minimize), Information Gain/Entropy (maximize), MSE/MAE (regression). Handles non-linearity, mixed data types, missing values. Prone to overfitting (deep trees). Mitigate: max_depth, min_samples_split, min_samples_leaf, max_features. Unstable (small data changes -> different tree). Ensemble methods (RF, GBT) overcome limitations.

---

### Q669: Random Forest?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensemble of decision trees (bagging + random feature selection). Each tree trained on bootstrap sample of data + random subset of features at each split. Prediction: majority vote (classification) or average (regression). Advantages: high accuracy, handles high-dimensional data, feature importance (mean decrease impurity), no scaling needed, robust to outliers/imbalanced data. Hyperparameters: n_estimators, max_depth, max_features, min_samples_split. Reduced variance vs single tree. Out-of-bag (OOB) score: internal validation.

---

### Q670: Gradient Boosting (XGBoost, LightGBM)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Sequential ensemble: each tree corrects previous tree's errors. Gradient: uses gradient descent to minimize loss. Hyperparameters: learning_rate (shrinkage), n_estimators, max_depth, subsample, colsample_bytree. XGBoost: optimized (cache-aware, column block for parallel), handles missing values, regularization (L1/L2 in leaf weights), built-in cross-validation. LightGBM: leaf-wise tree growth (faster), GOSS (Gradient-based One-Side Sampling), EFB (Exclusive Feature Bundling), categorical feature support. CatBoost: handles categorical features natively, ordered boosting. Best for tabular data (structured).

---

### Q671: SVM (Support Vector Machines)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Finds hyperplane that maximizes margin between classes. Support vectors: closest points to margin. Kernel trick: map to higher dimension (RBF, polynomial, sigmoid) for non-linear separation. Soft margin (C parameter): allows misclassifications (tolerance). C high: hard margin (less tolerance). C low: soft margin (more tolerance, better generalization). Gamma (RBF): influence of single training point. Pros: effective high-dimensional, memory efficient. Cons: doesn't scale to large datasets, poor probability estimates.

---

### Q672: PCA (Principal Component Analysis)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Unsupervised dimensionality reduction. Finds directions of maximum variance (principal components). Steps: standardize data -> covariance matrix -> eigenvectors/eigenvalues -> sort by eigenvalue -> select top K components. Explained variance ratio: how much information preserved. Use: visualization (2D/3D), noise reduction, multicollinearity removal, feature compression. Limitations: linear, interpretability of components. t-SNE: non-linear, for visualization only (preserves local structure). UMAP: faster than t-SNE, better global structure.

---

### Q673: K-means clustering?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Clustering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Partitions data into K clusters. Initialize K centroids randomly. Iterate: assign each point to nearest centroid, recalculate centroids as mean of assigned points. Converges when centroids stabilize. Elbow method: WCSS vs K (choose elbow point). Silhouette score: measures cluster cohesion vs separation [-1, 1]. Limitations: need K, sensitive to initialization (K-means++), assumes spherical clusters, sensitive to outliers, fails with non-spherical clusters. Better: DBSCAN (density-based, finds arbitrary shapes, handles noise). Hierarchical clustering: dendrogram.

---

### Q674: Naive Bayes?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Probabilistic classifier based on Bayes theorem with "naive" assumption of feature independence (given class). P(class|features) = P(class) * P(feature1|class) * ... * P(featureN|class) / P(features). Types: Gaussian (continuous), Multinomial (count features - text), Bernoulli (binary features). Fast, scales well (linear in features), works well for high-dimensional data. Probability calibration good (compared to SVM). Independence assumption rarely holds but still works for text classification (spam detection, sentiment analysis).

---

### Q675: Feature scaling (Normalization vs Standardization)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Normalization (Min-Max): scale to [0,1] range. formula: (x - min)/(max - min). Sensitive to outliers. Use: neural networks, distance-based algorithms (KNN, K-means). Standardization (Z-score): mean=0, std=1. formula: (x - mean)/std. Handles outliers better. Use: SVM, linear regression, PCA. Robust scaling: uses median and IQR (handles outliers). When to scale: algorithms using distance, gradient descent, regularization, PCA. Not needed: tree-based models (RF, GBT, XGBoost).

---

### Q676: Handling imbalanced datasets?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Resampling: Oversample minority (SMOTE - Synthetic Minority Over-sampling Technique - creates synthetic samples, ADASYN). Undersample majority (RandomUnderSampler, TomekLinks, NearMiss). Algorithmic: class_weight parameter (penalize misclassifying minority more), balanced Random Forest, XGBoost scale_pos_weight. Metrics: use precision/recall/F1, PR curve (not accuracy). Anomaly detection: treat as anomaly detection (Isolation Forest). Cost-sensitive learning. Data augmentation (especially image). Ensemble: EasyEnsemble, BalanceCascade.

---

### Q677: Regularization (L1 vs L2)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
L2 (Ridge): adds squared magnitude of coefficients to loss: lambda * sum(w^2). Shrinks coefficients toward zero (never exactly zero). Multicollinearity advantage: distributes coefficients evenly. L1 (Lasso): adds absolute magnitude: lambda * |w|. Shrinks coefficients to EXACTLY zero (feature selection). Useful for high-dimensional data. ElasticNet: combines L1 + L2. lambda controls regularization strength (higher = more regularization). Alpha = L1 ratio. Bias-variance tradeoff: regularization increases bias, reduces variance.

---

### Q678: What is ROC curve?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Metrics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Receiver Operating Characteristic curve: plots TPR (True Positive Rate = Recall) vs FPR (False Positive Rate = 1 - Specificity) at various classification thresholds. AUC (Area Under Curve): aggregate measure (0.5 = random guessing, 1.0 = perfect). AUC threshold-independent. For imbalanced classes: PR (Precision-Recall) curve more informative. Use: comparing models, selecting threshold. Optimal threshold: Youden's J statistic (max TPR - FPR), cost-benefit analysis.

---

### Q679: Feature engineering techniques?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Handling missing values: impute (mean, median, mode, KNN, predictive model), indicator column for missing. Encoding categorical: one-hot encoding (nominal), label encoding (ordinal), target encoding, frequency encoding, ordinal encoding. Scaling: Min-Max, Standard, Robust. Binning: discretize continuous features (age groups). Feature crossing: combine features (product, interactions). Date features: day_of_week, month, hour, is_holiday, time since event. Text: TF-IDF, word embeddings (Word2Vec, BERT). Domain-specific: ratios, aggregates, rolling statistics. Feature selection: correlation, mutual information, feature importance, chi-squared, variance threshold, RFE (Recursive Feature Elimination).

---

### Q680: Ensemble methods (bagging vs boosting)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Bagging (Bootstrap Aggregating): parallel training of models on bootstrap samples. Reduces variance. Examples: Random Forest. Model averaging (voting). Boosting: sequential training, each model corrects previous errors. Reduces bias and variance. Examples: AdaBoost, Gradient Boosting, XGBoost, LightGBM, CatBoost. Stacking: meta-model trained on predictions of base models. Voting: hard (majority) or soft (weighted probabilities). Bagging: independent, parallelizable. Boosting: sequential, slower. Generally, boosting > bagging for accuracy (but more prone to overfitting).

---

### Q681: What is the Curse of Dimensionality?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
As number of features increases, data becomes sparse in high-dimensional space. Distances between points become similar (kNN fails). Model complexity increases (more parameters to fit). Overfitting risk increases. Performance degrades. Solutions: feature selection, dimensionality reduction (PCA, t-SNE), increasing training data, domain knowledge feature engineering. Rule of thumb: at least 10 samples per dimension for meaningful results.

---

### Q682: Confusion Matrix?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Metrics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
TP (True Positive): correctly predicted positive. TN (True Negative): correctly predicted negative. FP (False Positive): incorrectly predicted positive (Type I error). FN (False Negative): incorrectly predicted negative (Type II error). Accuracy = (TP+TN)/(TP+TN+FP+FN). Precision = TP/(TP+FP). Recall/Sensitivity = TP/(TP+FN). Specificity = TN/(TN+FP). F1 = 2*P*R/(P+R). MCC (Matthews Correlation Coefficient): balanced measure for imbalanced data.

---

### Q683: Handling missing values?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Feature Engineering
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Remove: drop rows/columns with missing values (if few). Impute: mean/median (numerical), mode (categorical), constant (fillna(-1) for tree models). Model-based: KNN imputer, MICE (Multivariate Imputation by Chained Equations). Prediction: treat missingness as predictive signal (add indicator column). Tree models handle missing values natively (XGBoost, LightGBM). Forward/backward fill (time series). Interpolation. Domain knowledge best. Understand MAR/MCAR/MNAR missingness mechanisms.

---

### Q684: What is A/B Testing?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Statistical experiment: randomly assign users to control (A) and treatment (B) groups. Hypothesis: H0 = no difference, H1 = treatment better. Metrics: conversion rate, revenue, click-through rate. Sample size calculation: power analysis (alpha=0.05, power=0.8, effect size). Duration: account for day-of-week effects, novelty effect. Statistical test: chi-squared (categorical), t-test (continuous). Guardrail metrics: ensure change doesn't harm other metrics (page load time, error rate). Multiple testing correction: Bonferroni, FDR. Practical significance vs statistical significance.

---

### Q685: Time Series Forecasting methods?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Statistical: ARIMA (AutoRegressive Integrated Moving Average). SARIMA (seasonal). Exponential Smoothing (Holt-Winters). Components: trend, seasonality, cycle, residual. Prophet (Facebook): decomposable, handles holidays, changepoints. Machine learning: XGBoost/LightGBM with lag features, rolling window features, calendar features. Deep learning: LSTM, TCN, Transformer (Informer, Autoformer). Evaluation: MAPE, MAE, RMSE, sMAPE. Walk-forward validation (time series split). Stationarity: differencing, transformations. Autocorrelation (ACF/PACF) for feature selection.

---

### Q686: What is K-Nearest Neighbors (KNN)?
**Topic:** Machine Learning - Classification
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Non-parametric lazy learner: stores all training data. Prediction: K closest training points (by distance: Euclidean, Manhattan, Minkowski). Classification: majority vote. Regression: average. K parameter: small K -> high variance (overfit), large K -> high bias (underfit). Feature scaling essential (distance-based). Curse of dimensionality: high-dim data distance not meaningful. Fast prediction. Decision boundary non-linear but rough. Use: recommendation, pattern recognition.

---

### Q687: ML Pipeline?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Business understanding (define problem, success metrics). 2. Data collection (sources, ETL). 3. Data cleaning (handling missing, outliers, inconsistencies). 4. EDA (exploratory analysis, visualization, hypotheses). 5. Feature engineering (create, transform, encode, scale). 6. Model selection (compare algorithms, baseline). 7. Training + hyperparameter tuning (cross-validation, grid search, random search, Bayesian). 8. Evaluation (holdout set, A/B test). 9. Deployment (API, batch, edge). 10. Monitoring (drift detection, retraining). MLOps: automate pipeline, version data/models.

---

### Q688: Saving and loading ML models?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Python pickle: pickle.dump(model, file), model = pickle.load(file). Joblib: joblib.dump(model, 'model.pkl'), joblib.load('model.pkl') - better for large NumPy arrays. ONNX: cross-platform format (PyTorch, TF -> ONNX -> any runtime). MLflow: model registry + serving. TensorFlow SavedModel: tf.saved_model.save, tf.keras.models.load_model. PyTorch: torch.save(model.state_dict()), torch.load. PMML: XML-based.

---

### Q689: Hyperparameter tuning?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Grid Search: exhaustive search over specified values (sklearn.model_selection.GridSearchCV). Expensive for many hyperparameters.
