Random Search: sample random combinations (often finds good params faster). Bayesian Optimization (Optuna, Hyperopt): builds probability model of performance, chooses promising params. Tree-structured Parzen Estimator (TPE). GPyOpt, skopt. Automated: AutoML (AutoGluon, H2O, Auto-sklearn). Successive Halving: early stopping poor configurations (Hyperband). Differential evolution, genetic algorithms.

---

### Q690: MLOps?
**Topic:** Machine Learning
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ML + DevOps: operationalizing ML models. Components: experiment tracking (MLflow, Weights & Biases, Neptune), model registry, feature store (Feast, Tecton), data versioning (DVC, LakeFS), pipeline (Kubeflow, Airflow, ZenML), monitoring (Evidently, WhyLabs, Sagemaker Model Monitor). Drift detection: data drift (feature distribution changes), concept drift (relationship X->y changes). Retraining: scheduled, performance-triggered. CI/CD for ML: testing data quality, model validation, infrastructure.

## Networking

### Q471: OSI Model layers?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
7 Layers: Physical (bits, cables, hubs), Data Link (frames, MAC, switches, ARP), Network (packets, IP, routers), Transport (segments, TCP/UDP), Session (session management, SSL), Presentation (encryption, encoding, compression), Application (HTTP, FTP, SMTP, DNS). Mnemonic: "Please Do Not Throw Sausage Pizza Away". Data encapsulation: each layer adds header to data from layer above.

---

### Q472: TCP/IP Model?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
4 Layers: Network Interface (physical + data link), Internet (IP, ICMP, ARP), Transport (TCP, UDP), Application (HTTP, FTP, DNS, DHCP, SMTP). More practical than OSI. Internet layer handles addressing (IP) and routing. Transport provides end-to-end communication. Application combines session, presentation, application layers.

---

### Q473: TCP vs UDP?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
TCP: connection-oriented (3-way handshake), reliable (ACK + retransmission), ordered (sequence numbers), flow control (sliding window), congestion control (AIMD), header 20-60 bytes, slower. Use: HTTP/HTTPS, FTP, SMTP, SSH. UDP: connectionless, no ACK, unordered, no flow/congestion control, header 8 bytes, faster. Use: DNS, VoIP, video streaming, gaming, DHCP, QUIC (Google).

---

### Q474: TCP 3-Way Handshake?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Client -> Server: SYN (seq=x). Server -> Client: SYN-ACK (seq=y, ack=x+1). Client -> Server: ACK (seq=x+1, ack=y+1). Purpose: synchronize sequence numbers, establish initial reliable connection. Connection termination: 4-way handshake (FIN, ACK, FIN, ACK). Time-Wait state ensures delayed packets don't corrupt new connections.

---

### Q475: TCP Flow Control vs Congestion Control?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Flow Control: prevents sender from overwhelming receiver. Uses sliding window: receiver advertises available buffer space (rwnd = receiver window). Sender can't send more than rwnd unacknowledged bytes. Congestion Control: prevents sender from overwhelming network. Uses congestion window (cwnd). Algorithms: Slow Start (exponential growth until ssthresh), Congestion Avoidance (linear growth), Fast Retransmit (3 duplicate ACKs trigger retransmit), Fast Recovery (reduce cwnd by half). Sender's effective window = min(cwnd, rwnd).

---

### Q476: HTTP/1.1 vs HTTP/2 vs HTTP/3?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HTTP/1.1: persistent connections (keep-alive), pipelining (theoretical but buggy), head-of-line blocking (one request blocks others), text-based. HTTP/2: binary protocol (frames), multiplexing (multiple streams over single connection), header compression (HPACK), server push, stream prioritization. Still has TCP-level HOL blocking. HTTP/3: QUIC (UDP-based), zero-RTT connection, no HOL blocking (because multiplexed over UDP), built-in encryption, connection migration (survives IP change). Faster than HTTP/2.

---

### Q477: DNS Resolution process?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Browser checks local DNS cache. 2. Check /etc/hosts file. 3. Query local DNS resolver (ISP/8.8.8.8). 4. Resolver queries Root DNS server (.) -> returns TLD server (e.g., .com). 5. Query TLD server -> returns Authoritative server (example.com). 6. Query Authoritative -> returns IP address for www.example.com. 7. Cache result. Recursive vs iterative queries (recursive: resolver does all work; iterative: server returns referral). DNS record types: A (IPv4), AAAA (IPv6), CNAME (alias), MX (mail server), TXT (text), NS (nameserver).

---

### Q478: What is HTTPS and TLS handshake?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HTTPS = HTTP over TLS (Transport Layer Security). TLS 1.3 handshake: (1) ClientHello (supported versions, cipher suites, key share). (2) ServerHello (chosen version/cipher, certificate, signature). (3) Client sends encrypted Finished (verify key exchange). (4) Server sends encrypted Finished. After handshake, symmetric encryption (AES-GCM/ChaCha20) for data. Provides: encryption (confidentiality), certificate (authentication), MAC (integrity). Earlier TLS versions: 1.2 (RTT 2), 1.3 (RTT 1, 0-RTT resumption).

---

### Q479: What are the HTTP methods and status codes?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Methods: GET (read), POST (create), PUT (replace), PATCH (partial update), DELETE (remove), HEAD (headers only), OPTIONS (capabilities), CONNECT (tunnel), TRACE (loopback). Status codes: 1xx (Informational - 101 Switching Protocols), 2xx (Success - 200 OK, 201 Created, 204 No Content), 3xx (Redirection - 301 Moved Permanently, 302 Found, 304 Not Modified), 4xx (Client Error - 400 Bad Request, 401 Unauthorized, 403 Forbidden, 404 Not Found, 429 Too Many Requests), 5xx (Server Error - 500 Internal Server Error, 502 Bad Gateway, 503 Service Unavailable).

---

### Q480: Load Balancer types and algorithms?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Types: L4 (Transport - IP:port, faster, NAT-based), L7 (Application - HTTP headers, cookies, content switching, SSL termination). Hardware: F5, Citrix ADC. Software: Nginx, HAProxy, Envoy. Cloud: AWS ALB/ELB, GCP HTTP LB. Algorithms: Round Robin, Least Connections, IP Hash (sticky sessions), Least Response Time, Random, Weighted. Health checks: passive (detect failures) and active (periodic probes). Sticky sessions via cookies or IP hash. Session persistence crucial for stateful apps.

---

### Q481: What is a Reverse Proxy?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Server that sits between client and backend servers. Accepts client request, forwards to backend, returns response. Functions: load balancing, caching (static content), SSL termination, security (hide backend, DDoS protection), compression, serving multiple sites from single IP, request filtering. Examples: Nginx, Apache, HAProxy, Caddy. Diff from Forward Proxy: forward proxy acts for clients (hiding them), reverse proxy acts for servers.

---

### Q482: Network Topologies?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Bus: single cable, all devices share, cheap but single point of failure, limited length. Star: central switch/hub, each device connected directly, easy management, single switch fails. Ring: each device connected to two others (closed loop), deterministic, single break affects all. Mesh: each device connected to many others, high redundancy, expensive. Tree: hierarchical star, root switch connecting sub-switches, scalable. Hybrid: combination.

---

### Q483: What is ARP (Address Resolution Protocol)?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Maps IP address to MAC address on local network. Host broadcasts ARP request "who has IP 192.168.1.5?". Target responds with ARP reply containing MAC. ARP cache stores mappings (avoid repeated broadcasts). Gratuitous ARP: host announces its MAC-IP mapping (new device, IP change). ARP spoofing/poisoning: attacker sends fake ARP replies to redirect traffic (man-in-the-middle). Defenses: dynamic ARP inspection (DAI), static ARP entries.

---

### Q484: Subnetting and CIDR?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Subnetting: dividing IP network into smaller subnets. CIDR (Classless Inter-Domain Routing): notation (192.168.1.0/24). /24 = 255.255.255.0 = 256 addresses (254 usable). Network address (first) = all host bits 0. Broadcast address (last) = all host bits 1. Subnet mask determines network vs host bits. Example: 10.0.0.0/8 -> 16M addresses. 192.168.1.0/28 -> 16 addresses (14 usable). VPC subnets: public, private, isolated.

---

### Q485: What is NAT (Network Address Translation)?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Translates private IP (LAN) to public IP (Internet). Types: SNAT (source NAT - outgoing traffic), DNAT (destination NAT - incoming forwarding). Implementations: Full Cone (any external can send to mapped port), Restricted Cone (only from IP that received from), Port Restricted Cone (only from IP+port), Symmetric (different mapping per destination IP+port). PAT (Port Address Translation): many private IPs share single public IP using different ports. Conserves IPv4 addresses, adds security (hides internal network).

---

### Q486: What is DHCP?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Dynamic Host Configuration Protocol: automatically assigns IP addresses, subnet mask, gateway, DNS server to devices. DORA: Discover (client broadcast), Offer (server offers IP), Request (client requests offered IP), Acknowledge (server confirms). Lease duration: how long IP valid. Renewal before expiry. Static reservation: bind IP to MAC for fixed assignment. DHCP relay forwards DHCP requests across subnets.

---

### Q487: Firewall types?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Packet Filter: inspect packets (source/dest IP, port, protocol). Stateless (each packet independent) or Stateful (track connection state). Application Gateway (Proxy): inspects application-layer data, terminates connection. Next-Gen Firewall (NGFW): IPS/IDS, application awareness, user identity, SSL inspection. Web Application Firewall (WAF): protect web apps from SQL injection, XSS, CSRF (OWASP Top 10). Network ACL: stateless, subnet-level. Security Group: stateful, instance-level (AWS). iptables/nftables (Linux). Windows Defender Firewall.

---

### Q488: VLAN and VPN?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
VLAN: virtual LAN - logically segment network devices on same physical switch. Tagged frames (802.1Q). Reduces broadcast domain, improves security, simplifies management. Trunk links carry multiple VLANs. VPN: Virtual Private Network - encrypted tunnel over public internet. Site-to-Site (IPsec between offices), Remote Access (OpenVPN, WireGuard). Protocols: IPsec (ESP/AH + IKE), OpenSSL (TLS-based), WireGuard (modern, simpler). Split vs full tunneling.

---

### Q489: What is CDN and Edge Computing?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CDN (Content Delivery Network): distributed servers at edge locations. Caches static content (HTML, CSS, JS, images, video) close to users. Reduces latency, offloads origin servers. Anycast routing. Providers: CloudFront, Akamai, Cloudflare, Fastly. Edge Computing: processing at edge (closer to user) rather than centralized cloud. CDNs + compute (Lambda@Edge, Cloudflare Workers). Use: real-time processing, personalization, IoT data processing.

---

### Q490: WebSocket protocol?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Full-duplex communication over single TCP connection. Initiated via HTTP Upgrade request (101 Switching Protocols). ws:// (unencrypted), wss:// (TLS). Frame types: text, binary, ping/pong (keep-alive), close. Persistent connection (no polling overhead). Use: real-time chat, live updates, gaming, collaborative editing. Server: Spring WebSocket, Socket.IO (Node.js), ws library. Auto-reconnect, heartbeats.

---

### Q491: gRPC?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
High-performance RPC framework by Google. HTTP/2 based, Protocol Buffers (binary, compact serialization). Service definition in .proto file. Unary (request-response), Server-Streaming, Client-Streaming, Bidirectional Streaming. Auto-generates client/server code (Java, Go, Python, etc.). Better than REST for internal microservices (faster, strongly typed). Use with: service mesh, real-time streaming. Limitations: browser support (needs gRPC-Web), complex debugging (binary).

---

### Q492: What is a Proxy vs VPN?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Proxy: application-level, forwards requests for specific protocols (HTTP, SOCKS), no encryption by default, only browser requests. VPN: OS-level, encrypts ALL traffic, creates virtual network interface, system-wide. Proxy is per-application, VPN is per-machine. VPN provides better privacy (encryption). Proxy is faster (less overhead). Reverse proxy is server-side (unrelated concept).

---

### Q493: What is ICMP?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Internet Control Message Protocol. Used by network devices to send error messages (host unreachable, network unreachable, port unreachable, TTL exceeded). ping uses ICMP Echo Request/Reply. traceroute uses ICMP TTL exceeded messages. Not for data transfer. No port concept (below TCP/UDP). DDoS: ICMP flood, Smurf attack (amplification via broadcast). Blocked by many firewalls.

---

### Q494: What is MTU and Fragmentation?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
MTU (Maximum Transmission Unit): max packet size a network layer can transmit. Ethernet: 1500 bytes. IPv4 routers can fragment large packets. IPv6: sends ICMPv6 "Packet Too Big" (no router fragmentation - end-to-end). Path MTU Discovery (PMTUD): find min MTU along path. Don't Fragment (DF) bit + ICMP. MSS (Maximum Segment Size) = MTU - 40 (TCP+IP headers). TCP negotiates MSS to avoid fragmentation. Fragmentation attacks (overlapping fragments evade firewalls).

---

### Q495: What is the difference between Hub, Switch, Router?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Hub: Layer 1, broadcasts to all ports, half-duplex, no intelligence. Switch: Layer 2, forwards based on MAC address, full-duplex, learning table, VLAN support. Router: Layer 3, forwards based on IP address, connects different networks, routing protocols (OSPF, BGP). Modern: Layer 3 switches (switch + router funcs), SDN (software-defined networking decouples control/data planes).

---

### Q496: BGP (Border Gateway Protocol)?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Path-vector routing protocol connecting autonomous systems (AS). Internet backbone protocol. Policy-based (not just shortest path). Attributes: AS_PATH (loop prevention), LOCAL_PREF (preferred exit), MED (exit metrics), NEXT_HOP, Communities. iBGP (within AS), eBGP (between ASes). Route reflectors for scalability. Convergence slower than OSPF. BGP hijacking: malicious AS advertises routes it doesn't own (IP prefix hijacking). RPKI (Resource Public Key Infrastructure) for validation.

---

### Q497: What is a Socket?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Endpoint for communication between processes. Identified by IP address + port number. Types: Stream sockets (TCP - reliable, connection-oriented), Datagram sockets (UDP - unreliable, connectionless), Raw sockets (direct IP, for custom protocols). Socket API: socket(), bind(), listen(), accept(), connect(), send(), recv(). Server socket (passive open): bind + listen + accept. Client socket (active open): connect.

---

### Q498: What is a MAC Address?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Media Access Control address: 48-bit unique identifier burned into NIC. First 24 bits: OUI (Organizationally Unique Identifier - manufacturer). Last 24 bits: unique per device. Written as 00:1A:2B:3C:4D:5E. Layer 2 addressing. ARP resolves IP -> MAC. Switch uses MAC table (CAM table) to forward frames. MAC address spoofing: changing MAC for privacy/impersonation. MAC flooding: attack on switch CAM table.

---

### Q499: Network Security: SSL/TLS, mTLS?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SSL/TLS: certificate-based authentication (server proves identity via CA-signed cert), encrypted connection. mTLS (Mutual TLS): both client and server present certificates, mutual authentication. Used in service mesh (Istio), gRPC, financial APIs. Certificate: X.509 format, contains public key, subject, issuer, validity, signature. Certificate Authority (CA) signs certificates. Let's Encrypt: free automated CA (ACME protocol). Certificate pinning vs certificate transparency.

---

### Q500: What are Network Sockets (Types)?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
DatagramSocket (UDP): send/receive datagrams, no connection needed. ServerSocket (TCP): listens for incoming TCP connections. Socket (TCP): connected endpoint for communication. Unix Domain Socket: same-host IPC (faster than TCP loopback). WebSocket: full-duplex over HTTP. Raw Socket: direct IP/ICMP access (for custom protocols, ping, traceroute). Secure Socket: SSL wrapping (SSLSocket).

---

### Q501: Connection Keep-Alive and Persistent Connections?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HTTP/1.0: new TCP connection per request (slow, high overhead). HTTP/1.1 Keep-Alive: reuse connection for multiple requests (default in HTTP/1.1). Reduces latency (no handshake), reduces server load (fewer connections). TCP keepalive: probe idle connections to detect dead peers. HTTP/2: multiplexing over single connection. Connection pooling: client maintains pool of reusable connections (Apache HttpClient, HikariCP). Tuning: max connections, idle timeout, TTL, validation.

---

### Q502: What is the difference between Symmetric and Asymmetric Encryption?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Symmetric: same key for encrypt/decrypt. Fast, simple. Key distribution problem. Algorithms: AES (Gold standard - 128/256), ChaCha20, DES (broken), 3DES (deprecated). Asymmetric: public/private key pair. Slower, solves key exchange. Algorithms: RSA, ECC (Elliptic Curve Cryptography - smaller keys, faster), Diffie-Hellman (key exchange). Typically hybrid: asymmetric for key exchange, symmetric for bulk data (like TLS: ECDHE for key agreement, AES-GCM for data).

---

### Q503: Content-Type vs Content-Encoding vs Transfer-Encoding?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Content-Type: format of body (application/json, text/html, multipart/form-data). Content-Encoding: compression applied to body (gzip, br/brotli, deflate). Transfer-Encoding: how body transported (chunked - for unknown size). Content-Type tells client how to parse. Content-Encoding tells client how to decompress. Transfer-Encoding is hop-by-hop (proxies may change). Accept-Encoding (client signals acceptable encodings).

---

### Q504: What is TLS 1.3 vs 1.2?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
TLS 1.2: 2-RTT handshake, many cipher suites, older algorithms (RC4, 3DES, CBC mode vulnerable). TLS 1.3: 1-RTT handshake (0-RTT resumption), simplified (only AEAD ciphers: AES-GCM, ChaCha20-Poly1305), forward secrecy required (no static RSA key exchange), removed insecure features (compression, renegotiation). Key exchange: ECDHE (Ephemeral Diffie-Hellman over Elliptic Curve). SNI (Server Name Indication) for multiple certificates on single IP. ECH (Encrypted Client Hello) for privacy.

---

### Q505: What is QUIC?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Quick UDP Internet Connections (Google -> IETF standard). HTTP/3 transport. Features: 0-RTT connection establishment (reduces latency for repeat connections), multiplexing without HOL blocking (lost packet only blocks single stream, not all), connection migration (survives IP/network changes - mobile), built-in TLS 1.3 encryption (not optional), forward error correction, faster than TCP+TLS. Adoption: Google services (YouTube, Chrome), Facebook, Cloudflare, Akamai.

---

### Q506: RESTful API design principles?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Resources as nouns (/users, /orders). HTTP methods as verbs: GET (read), POST (create), PUT (replace), PATCH (partial update), DELETE (remove). Stateless: each request contains all needed info. HATEOAS: responses include links to related resources. Versioning: /v1/users or Accept header. Pagination: offset/limit, cursor-based. Filtering: ?status=active. Sorting: ?sort=-created_at. Error responses: consistent format (Problem Details RFC 7807). Idempotency: same request same result. Caching: ETag, Cache-Control. Authentication: JWT/OAuth2.

---

### Q507: What is CORS?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Cross-Origin Resource Sharing: browser security mechanism restricting cross-origin HTTP requests. Same-Origin Policy: only requests to same origin (scheme + domain + port) allowed. CORS relaxes this. Preflight request (OPTIONS) for non-simple requests (non-standard headers, PUT/DELETE, content-type != form types). Server responds with: Access-Control-Allow-Origin, Allow-Methods, Allow-Headers, Allow-Credentials. Simple requests: GET/POST with certain content-types (no preflight). Credentials: cookies, Authorization header.

---

### Q508: What is a Webhook?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
HTTP callback: event notification from server to client (reverse of API polling). When event occurs, server sends POST request to registered URL. Use: Stripe (payment events), GitHub (push events), Slack (slash commands). Implementation: register URL + secret, validate via HMAC signature. Retry with backoff on failure. Logging for debugging. More efficient than polling (no periodic requests).

---

### Q509: Network Timeout types?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Connection Timeout: max time to establish TCP connection. Read Timeout: max time to receive data after connection established. Write Timeout: max time to send data. Request Timeout: total max time for complete request-response. Keep-Alive Timeout: idle time before closing persistent connection. DNS Timeout: max time for DNS resolution. Retry/backoff: exponential backoff with jitter on timeout. Timeout settings critical: too short -> false failures, too long -> resource exhaustion.

---

### Q510: What is Network Latency and Throughput?
**Topic:** Networking
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Latency: time for data to travel from source to destination. Propagation delay (speed of light), transmission delay (size/bandwidth), processing delay, queuing delay. Ping measures RTT. Throughput: actual data transfer rate (bits/second). Bandwidth: maximum theoretical rate. Latency matters for small requests (DNS, DB queries). Throughput matters for large data (file transfer, video). TCP window size affects throughput over high-latency links (Bandwidth-Delay Product). TCP tuning: window scaling, selective ACK.

## Operating Systems

### Q431: What is an Operating System?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
System software managing hardware resources and providing services for application programs. Key functions: process management (scheduling, synchronization), memory management (allocation, virtual memory), file system management, I/O management, security (user authentication, access control), networking. Types: batch, time-sharing, real-time, distributed, embedded.

---

### Q432: Process vs Thread?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Process: independent execution unit, own address space (code, data, heap, stack), inter-process communication via pipes/sockets/shared memory, context switch expensive (TLB flush). Thread: lightweight unit within process, shares address space (heap + code/data) with other threads, own stack, context switch cheaper (shared address space). Thread communication via shared memory (faster). Process is a program in execution; thread is a path of execution within a process.

---

### Q433: Process states?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
New (created) -> Ready (loaded in memory, waiting for CPU) -> Running (executing) -> Waiting/Blocked (waiting for I/O or event) -> Terminated (completed). Additional: Suspend Ready (moved to disk), Suspend Wait (waiting for I/O, moved to disk). Context switch: saving CPU state of current process, loading state of next process.

---

### Q434: CPU Scheduling algorithms?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
FCFS (First Come First Served): non-preemptive, simple, convoy effect (short jobs wait behind long). SJF (Shortest Job First): optimal avg waiting time, starvation risk (long jobs never scheduled). SRTF (Shortest Remaining Time First): preemptive SJF. Round Robin (RR): time quantum, fair, good response time, quantum size critical (too large -> FCFS, too small -> overhead). Priority Scheduling: preemptive/non-preemptive, starvation (aging fixes). Multilevel Queue: foreground (RR) + background (FCFS). Multilevel Feedback Queue: processes move between queues (lottery scheduling).

---

### Q435: What is a Deadlock? Conditions?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Permanent blocking of processes, each waiting for resource held by another. Four necessary conditions (Coffman): Mutual Exclusion (resource non-sharable), Hold and Wait (process holding resources waits for more), No Preemption (resources only released voluntarily), Circular Wait (cycle of processes each waiting for next). Deadlock prevention: break any condition. Deadlock avoidance: Banker's algorithm (safe state check). Deadlock detection: wait-for graph (cycle detection). Recovery: kill processes, preempt resources.

---

### Q436: Banker's Algorithm?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Deadlock avoidance algorithm. Process declares max resource claims. System checks if granting request leaves safe state (at least one sequence where all processes can complete). Data structures: Available (available resources), Max (max demand), Allocation (allocated), Need (Max - Allocation). Request: if Request <= Need and Request <= Available, simulate allocation and check if safe. Safe: there exists sequence of processes that can complete (Need <= Available + progressively freed resources).

---

### Q437: Memory Management: Paging vs Segmentation?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Paging: divides physical memory into fixed-size frames, logical memory into pages. Page table maps virtual page to physical frame. Eliminates external fragmentation. Internal fragmentation possible (last page). Segmentation: divides program into logical segments (code, data, stack). Segment table maps segment to base+limit. External fragmentation possible. Combined: segmented paging (segments divided into pages). Modern systems use paging.

---

### Q438: Virtual Memory and Page Replacement?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Virtual memory allows running programs larger than physical RAM. Pages loaded on demand (demand paging). Page fault: required page not in memory -> load from disk (expensive). Page replacement algorithms when memory full: FIFO (Belady's anomaly: more frames -> more faults possible), Optimal (replace page not used longest - theoretical), LRU (Least Recently Used - hardware counter/stack approx like Clock algorithm), Clock/Second Chance (circular list with reference bit), LFU (Least Frequently Used).

---

### Q439: What is Thrashing?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Excessive page faulting causing near-zero CPU utilization. Process spends more time swapping pages than executing. Causes: too many processes (insufficient frames per process), working set larger than allocated frames. Prevention: working set model (keep process pages in memory), page fault frequency control (if high, allocate more frames), degree of multiprogramming control.

---

### Q440: Inter-Process Communication (IPC)?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Mechanisms for processes to communicate: Shared Memory (fast, needs synchronization - semaphores/mutex), Message Passing (send/receive system calls, no shared memory race), Pipes (unnamed for parent-child, named FIFO for unrelated), Sockets (network IPC), Signals (asynchronous events), Semaphores (synchronization), Message Queues (structured messages), Shared Files, D-Bus (Linux desktop IPC). Message Passing is safer (OS manages), Shared Memory is faster.

---

### Q441: Semaphore vs Mutex?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Mutex: binary (0 or 1), ownership (must unlock by same thread), used for mutual exclusion. Semaphore: counting (0 to N), no ownership, any thread can signal/wait, used for signaling (producer-consumer). Mutex is for locking resources. Binary semaphore can be used like mutex (but no ownership). In Java: synchronized, ReentrantLock. In POSIX: pthread_mutex, sem_t.

---

### Q442: What is a System Call?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Programmatic way for user-space program to request service from OS kernel (privileged operation). Examples: process control (fork, exec, exit), file management (open, read, write, close), device management (ioctl), information maintenance (getpid), communication (pipe, socket). Interface between user mode and kernel mode. Implemented via software interrupt (trap) to switch to kernel mode.

---

### Q443: User Mode vs Kernel Mode?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
User Mode: restricted access to hardware, limited address space. Process isolation. If crash, only user process affected. Kernel Mode: full hardware access, executes OS code, privileged instructions (I/O, memory management). Mode bit (0 = kernel, 1 = user) in processor status register. Transition via system calls (trap/interrupt). Kernel code in kernel space, device drivers, file systems, network stack.

---

### Q444: What are the types of Operating Systems?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Batch: jobs grouped, no interaction (early computing). Time-Sharing: interactive, CPU time shared (Unix, Linux, Windows). Real-Time: deterministic response (RTOS - VxWorks, QNX). Hard RT: deadline misses catastrophic (airbag, medical). Soft RT: occasional miss tolerable (video streaming). Distributed: multiple interconnected computers (cluster). Embedded: specialized for devices (IoT, smartphone). Mobile: iOS, Android.

---

### Q445: What is a Kernel? Types?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Core of OS, manages resources, lowest-level abstraction layer. Monolithic Kernel: all OS services in kernel space (Linux - fast but unstable if driver crashes). Microkernel: minimal kernel (IPC, memory, scheduling), other services in user space (Minix, QNX - stable but slower due to IPC). Hybrid Kernel: combines both (Windows NT, macOS XNU). Exokernel: minimal abstraction, applications manage resources directly.

---

### Q446: What is RAID?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Redundant Array of Independent Disks. RAID 0 (Striping): data split across disks, no redundancy, max space, max performance. RAID 1 (Mirroring): exact copy, high reliability, half space. RAID 5 (Striping + Parity): parity distributed across disks, 1 disk recovery, min 3 disks. RAID 6 (Striping + Dual Parity): 2 disk recovery, min 4 disks. RAID 10 (1+0): mirroring + striping, high perf + reliability. Hot spare: standby disk for automatic rebuild.

---

### Q447: File Systems: NTFS vs ext4 vs FAT32?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
FAT32: legacy (Win95), max 4GB file, 2TB partition, no journaling. NTFS: Windows standard, journaling, security (ACLs), compression, encryption (EFS), max 256TB, 16EB with large files, quotas, hard links. ext4: Linux standard, journaling, extents (large contiguous blocks), delayed allocation, max 1EB, defragmentation, checksums. Journaling: metadata-only or full data + metadata. Log-structured file systems (ZFS, Btrfs): checksums, snapshots, compression.

---

### Q448: What is a Sparse File?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
File with "holes" (unwritten blocks) that are treated as zero bytes. Disk space allocated only for written blocks. Used for: virtual machine disk images (growing allocation), database snapshots, large files with sparse data. Linux: truncate, fallocate, cp --sparse. Windows: SetSparseFile. ls -ls shows actual vs apparent size.

---

### Q449: What is DMA (Direct Memory Access)?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hardware mechanism allowing I/O devices to transfer data directly to/from memory without CPU intervention. CPU initiates DMA transfer (specify source, dest, count), DMA controller handles data movement, interrupts CPU when done. Frees CPU for other tasks during large I/O operations. Speeds up disk/network transfers. Types: bus-mastering DMA (device controls bus), cycle stealing (DMA interleaves with CPU).

---

### Q450: Interrupts and Interrupt Handling?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Signal from hardware (I/O device, timer) or software (system call, exception) to CPU. CPU saves current state, jumps to Interrupt Service Routine (ISR) via interrupt vector table. After ISR, return to interrupted process. Interrupt priority levels (IPL). Maskable interrupts (can be disabled), non-maskable (NMI - hardware errors). Spurious interrupts (no source). IRQ lines (hardware interrupt request). Bottom half/tasklet for deferred work (handle minimal in ISR, rest later).

---

### Q451: What is a Zombie Process?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Process that has completed but still has entry in process table (waiting for parent to call wait() to read exit status). If parent doesn't call wait(), zombie remains (memory leak). If parent terminates, zombie adopted by init (PID 1), which reaps it. Orphan process: parent dies before child. init adopts orphan (harmless). Prevention: signal handler for SIGCHLD calls waitpid().

---

### Q452: What is Context Switch?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Switching CPU from one process/thread to another. Saves state (registers, program counter, stack pointer) of current, loads saved state of next. Overhead includes: saving/loading registers, TLB flush (new process address space), cache invalidation, scheduler decision time. Pure overhead (CPU doing no useful work). Minimize by: appropriate time quantum, lightweight threads, reducing TLB flushes, large page sizes.

---

### Q453: Scheduling: Preemptive vs Non-Preemptive?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Preemptive: OS can interrupt running process (via timer interrupt) to schedule another. Used in time-sharing systems. Better responsiveness, more complex (race conditions). Non-Preemptive: process runs until it voluntarily yields (I/O wait, block, exit) or terminates. Used in batch systems. Simpler implementation, no concurrency issues within kernel. Modern OS: preemptive kernel (preempt even kernel mode unless holding spinlock).

---

### Q454: Memory Allocation: First Fit, Best Fit, Worst Fit?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
First Fit: allocate first free block large enough. Fastest, moderate fragmentation. Best Fit: allocate smallest block that fits. Minimizes waste, but slow (search all free blocks). Worst Fit: allocate largest free block. Leaves large leftover (may be useful for future large request). All suffer from external fragmentation. Modern systems use paging (fixed-size pages).

---

### Q455: What are Translation Lookaside Buffers (TLB)?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Small hardware cache in CPU that stores recently used virtual-to-physical page mappings. Speeds up virtual address translation. TLB miss: walk page table in memory (or hardware page walker). TLB flush on context switch (new process has different page table). Reduce misses by: larger pages, TLB tagging (address space ID). TLB reach = TLB entries * page size. Need TLB reach > working set for good performance.

---

### Q456: What is the difference between Asymmetric and Symmetric Multiprocessing?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SMP (Symmetric): all processors equal, share memory, run OS independently. Each CPU can execute any process. Better load balancing, more complex synchronization. Common in multicore CPUs. AMP (Asymmetric): master processor runs OS, slaves run user tasks. Simplified OS design. Used in embedded systems, DSPs. Modern CPUs use SMP with cache coherency (MESI protocol) to maintain consistent memory views.

---

### Q457: What is the Dining Philosophers Problem?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Synchronization problem: 5 philosophers around table, 5 forks. Each needs 2 forks to eat. How to avoid deadlock and starvation? Solutions: (1) Lock mutex for both forks (atomic pick). (2) Odd philosophers pick left then right, even pick right then left. (3) At most 4 philosophers eating (N-1). (4) Waiter process (arbitrator). Represents resource allocation with circular wait.

---

### Q458: What is the Readers-Writers Problem?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Multiple readers read data, one writer writes. Readers don't conflict. Issues: Starvation (if continuous readers, writer never writes). First Readers-Writers Problem (reader priority): allow readers until writer waiting. Second Readers-Writers Problem (writer priority): once writer ready, no new readers start. Implement via reader count + semaphores or ReadWriteLock (Java ReentrantReadWriteLock).

---

### Q459: What is Cache Coherence?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Problem: multiple CPU caches containing copies of same memory location, writes must be visible to all. Protocols: snooping (bus-based - each cache monitors memory transactions). Directory-based (shared distributed memory). MESI protocol: Modified, Exclusive, Shared, Invalid states. Invalidates other caches when write occurs. MOESI, MESIF variants. Cache coherence is hardware-based.

---

### Q460: What is Belady's Anomaly?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
With FIFO page replacement, increasing number of page frames can increase page faults (contrary to expectation). Caused by FIFO's lack of temporal locality awareness. Other algorithms (LRU, Optimal) don't suffer this. Belady's anomaly only occurs with some reference strings, not all. Page faults per frame count is NOT monotonic for FIFO.

---

### Q461: What is Copy-on-Write (COW)?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
On fork(), child shares parent's pages (marked read-only). Physical copy only when either writes (page fault -> copy page). Saves memory (exec immediately after fork doesn't need copy) and time (no full process copy). Used by fork(), virtual machine snapshots, database snapshots (ZFS, btrfs). Also: COW strings in some languages.

---

### Q462: What is Memory-Mapped File?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Mapping file content directly into process virtual address space. Accessed via pointers (like memory array). Backed by page cache: reads cause page faults -> load from file to physical memory. Writes handled by OS (flushed back). Benefits: no read/write system calls, shared memory between processes (MAP_SHARED), lazy loading. Java: MappedByteBuffer, FileChannel.map(). Used for large file processing, inter-process communication.

---

### Q463: I/O Multiplexing (select, poll, epoll)?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Monitor multiple file descriptors for I/O readiness. select(): fixed max fd (1024), O(n) scanning, modifies fd sets (need to reset). poll(): no max fd, O(n) scanning. epoll (Linux): O(1) readiness notification, edge/level-triggered. epoll_create, epoll_ctl (add/modify fds), epoll_wait (blocking). IOCP (Windows I/O Completion Ports). More efficient than multi-threaded blocking I/O for many connections. Foundation for Node.js, Nginx, Netty, Redis.

---

### Q464: What is the difference between Hard and Soft Real-Time Systems?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hard Real-Time: deadline miss causes system failure (catastrophic). Airbag deployment, flight control, medical defibrillator. Guarantees using static scheduling (RMS, EDF). Soft Real-Time: deadline miss degrades quality but acceptable. Video streaming, online gaming, audio playback. Statistical guarantees. Priority-based scheduling with higher priority for real-time tasks.

---

### Q465: What is a Critical Section?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Code segment accessing shared resources (variables, files, devices) that must not be concurrently executed by multiple threads. Requirements: Mutual Exclusion (one thread at a time), Progress (no indefinite postponement of eligible threads), Bounded Waiting (bounded time to enter). Implemented via: mutex locks, semaphores, monitors, atomic operations (CAS).

---

### Q466: Race Condition in OS context?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two concurrent processes/threads access shared data and outcome depends on relative timing. Example: fork() + exec() -> if process table full between fork and exec, both may fail. Kernel race conditions: double fetch, TOCTOU (time-of-check time-of-use) on file system operations. Prevention: locks, atomic operations, proper ordering, copying to kernel space before validation.

---

### Q467: What is a Spinlock?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Busy-waiting lock: thread repeatedly checks (spins) until lock available. Used in kernel for short critical sections (interrupt handlers where sleeping not allowed). Overhead: CPU waste if long wait. Better on multi-processor (different thread runs on other CPU). Variants: ticket spinlock (FIFO fairness), queued spinlock (per-CPU queue). In Java: not common (higher-level locks use synchronized/park).

---

### Q468: What is the difference between External and Internal Fragmentation?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
External: free memory split into small blocks between allocated blocks. Total free enough but not contiguous. Problem for dynamic partitioning/segmentation. Compaction needed. Internal: allocated memory block larger than needed. Remaining space inside block wasted. Problem for paging (last page partially used), fixed-size allocation. Paging has only internal fragmentation (last page), no external.

---

### Q469: What is the Page Size tradeoff?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Small pages: less internal fragmentation, better locality (finer granularity), larger page tables (more levels, more TLB pressure). Large pages: more internal fragmentation, fewer page faults (spatial locality), smaller page tables, better TLB coverage. Typical: 4KB base page. Huge/Large pages: 2MB/1GB for high-memory workloads (databases, VMs). Transparent Huge Pages (THP) in Linux auto-converts.

---

### Q470: What is the Starvation problem?
**Topic:** Operating Systems
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Process/thread never gets scheduled because higher-priority processes always run. In scheduling: SJF can starve long jobs. Priority scheduling can starve low priority. Solution: aging (gradually increase priority of waiting processes). In deadlock: no deadlock detection (victim never chosen). In readers-writers: continuous readers starve writers. In dining philosophers: philosopher never eats.

## Python

### Q621: Python vs Java differences?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Python: dynamically typed, interpreted, indentation-based, duck typing, GIL (Global Interpreter Lock), slower runtime, faster development, scripting friendly. Java: statically typed, compiled+interpreted (JVM), explicit braces, interfaces, strong OOP, multi-threaded (no GIL). Python for: data science, ML, scripting, web (Django, FastAPI). Java for: enterprise, Android, large-scale systems, high-performance server apps.

---

### Q622: Mutable vs Immutable types?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Immutable: int, float, str, tuple, frozenset. Cannot be modified after creation (any change creates new object). Mutable: list, dict, set, bytearray. Can be modified in-place. Important: default function arguments are evaluated once at function definition (use None + check instead of mutable default). Tuples with mutable elements (tuple of lists) are overall mutable. str is immutable (concatenation creates new string).

---

### Q623: List vs Tuple vs Set vs Dict?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
List: ordered, mutable, duplicates allowed, []. Tuple: ordered, immutable, hashable (usable as dict key), (). Set: unordered, mutable, unique, {}. Frozenset: immutable set, hashable. Dict: key-value pairs, ordered (Python 3.7+), keys unique and hashable. List comprehension: [x*2 for x in range(10)]. Dict comprehension: {x: x**2 for x in range(5)}. Set comprehension: {x for x in range(10)}.

---

### Q624: Python generators and yield?
**Topic:** Python - Generators
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Generator: function with yield (instead of return). Pauses execution, remembers state, resumes on next iteration. Lazy evaluation (yield one at a time). def gen(): yield 1; yield 2. gen() -> generator object. next(gen) -> 1. Memory efficient for large sequences. send() for bidirectional communication. throw() and close(). Generator expression: (x*2 for x in range(10)) - similar to list comprehension but lazy. Use: streaming data, infinite sequences, processing large files.

---

### Q625: Python decorators?
**Topic:** Python - Decorators
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Function that takes function as argument, extends behavior, returns function. @decorator syntax sugar: @my_decorator def func(): pass is same as my_decorator(func). def my_decorator(f): def wrapper(*args, **kwargs): print('before'); result = f(*args, **kwargs); print('after'); return result; return wrapper. Preserve function metadata with @functools.wraps. Decorators with arguments: @decorator(arg). Class-based decorator: __call__. Use: logging, timing, auth, caching.

---

### Q626: GIL (Global Interpreter Lock)?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Mutex that allows only one thread to execute Python bytecode at a time. Simplifies CPython memory management (no multi-thread memory corruption). Consequence: CPU-bound Python threads don't benefit from multi-core (only one runs at a time). I/O-bound threads still benefit (GIL released during I/O wait). Workarounds: multiprocessing (separate processes, each with own GIL), using C extensions (NumPy releases GIL), asyncio (cooperative multitasking). Python 3.12+: nogil experimental, per-interpreter GIL.

---

### Q627: List comprehension vs generator expression?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
List comprehension: [x*2 for x in range(10)] - creates full list in memory. Generator expression: (x*2 for x in range(10)) - lazy, yields values on demand. Difference: list comp uses brackets, creates all elements; gen expr uses parens, creates iterator. Memory: list comp O(n), gen expr O(1). Use gen expr for: large sequences, streaming, single-use iteration. Use list comp for: small data, random access, repeated iteration. Both faster than manual for-loop (Python-level optimizations).

---

### Q628: Python typing (type hints)?
**Topic:** Python - Typing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Optional static typing. Basic: name: str = "Alice". Function: def add(x: int, y: int) -> int: return x + y. Collections: List[int], Dict[str, int], Tuple[int, str], Set[float]. Optional: Optional[str] = str | None. Union: Union[str, int] = str | int (Python 3.10+). Any: any type. TypeVar for generics. Callable[[int], str] - function type. Protocol for structural typing (duck typing at type level). @dataclass for auto-generated __init__/__repr__/__eq__. Type checkers: mypy, pyright, pyre. Not enforced at runtime (only tooling).

---

### Q629: Python OOP concepts?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Class: class MyClass(Parent):. Magic methods: __init__, __str__, __repr__, __len__, __getitem__, __eq__, __hash__, __call__. @property: getter/setter without method call syntax. @classmethod: method receiving class (not instance). @staticmethod: method with no cls/self. Method Resolution Order (MRO): C3 linearization for diamond inheritance. super() follows MRO. Abstract base class: from abc import ABC, abstractmethod. Multiple inheritance. __slots__ for memory optimization.

---

### Q630: Python context managers (with statement)?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
with statement ensures setup/teardown (open/close, acquire/release). with open('file.txt') as f: content = f.read(). __enter__ (setup, return object assigned to as variable). __exit__ (teardown, suppress exception by returning True). contextlib.contextmanager: @contextmanager def my_context(): yield resource. from contextlib import contextmanager. Use: file I/O, DB connections, locks (threading.Lock), redirect stdout, temporary directory.

---

### Q631: Python pickle and JSON serialization?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
JSON: text-based, cross-language, limited types (dict, list, str, int, float, bool, None). json.dumps(obj), json.loads(str). Custom serialization: default parameter, object_hook. Pickle: Python-specific binary format (protocol 5). Supports all Python objects (functions, classes, custom objects). WARNING: unpickling untrusted data executes arbitrary code (security risk). marshal: internal use only (code objects). YAML: human-readable, broader types than JSON, PyYAML. msgpack: binary JSON alternative.

---

### Q632: Lambda functions in Python?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Anonymous function: lambda x: x * 2. Single expression only. Use with: map(lambda x: x*2, list), filter(lambda x: x > 0, list), sorted(list, key=lambda x: x.name). Avoid complex lambdas (define function for readability). Limitations: no statements (return, print, assignment). Use operator module for common ops (operator.add, operator.itemgetter). functools.partial for partial application.

---

### Q633: Dunder methods?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
__init__: constructor. __str__: human-readable (str(), print()). __repr__: unambiguous (repr(), debugging). __len__: len(). __getitem__: indexing (obj[key]). __setitem__: assignment (obj[key]=val). __iter__/__next__: iteration. __contains__: in operator. __call__: callable instance. __enter__/__exit__: context manager. __eq__/__hash__: equality/hashing. __add__/__sub__: operators. __bool__: truthiness. __new__: object creation (before __init__, metaclasses). __del__: destructor (unreliable). __slots__: restrict attributes, memory savings.

---

### Q634: with statement and contextlib?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@contextlib.contextmanager decorator creates context manager from generator function. try: yield value finally: cleanup. contextlib.suppress: suppress specific exceptions. with suppress(FileNotFoundError): os.remove('file'). contextlib.redirect_stdout: capture print output. contextlib.ExitStack: dynamically manage multiple context managers. contextlib.closing: ensure close called. contextlib.nullcontext: no-op context.

---

### Q635: Python testing (pytest)?
**Topic:** Python - Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
pytest: no boilerplate, auto-discovery (test_ prefix), fixtures, parameterized tests, plugins. assert raises: with pytest.raises(ValueError): func(). Fixtures: @pytest.fixture def db(): setup; yield conn; teardown. conftest.py: shared fixtures. parameterize: @pytest.mark.parametrize('input,expected', [(1,2),(3,4)]). Mocking: unittest.mock, pytest-mock (mocker fixture). Coverage: pytest-cov.

---

### Q636: Async/await in Python?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
asyncio: async def fetch(): await async_request(). async def: coroutine function. await: pauses until coroutine completes. Event loop: asyncio.run(main()). Tasks: asyncio.create_task(coro()) for concurrent execution. asyncio.gather(*tasks): run concurrently. Async context manager: async with. Async iterator: async for. asyncio.sleep() not time.sleep() (non-blocking). Libraries: aiohttp (HTTP), asyncpg (PostgreSQL), aioredis, aiofiles. Use: I/O-bound, high-concurrency apps (not CPU-bound). Python 3.12+: improved error messages.

---

### Q637: Python data science stack?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
NumPy: ndarray, vectorized operations, linear algebra, broadcasting. Pandas: DataFrame, Series, groupby, merge/join, time series. Matplotlib: plotting (pyplot), customization. Seaborn: statistical visualizations (heatmap, pairplot). SciPy: scientific computing (optimization, signal, stats). Scikit-learn: ML algorithms. Jupyter Notebook/Lab: interactive computing. Streamlit: data app framework. Polars: faster DataFrame alternative (Rust-based). Dask: parallel computing for larger-than-memory datasets.

---

### Q638: Python list vs array?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
list: dynamic, heterogeneous (any type), built-in, methods (append, sort, pop). array.array: typed (single type C), memory efficient (like C array). from array import array; arr = array('i', [1,2,3]). numpy.ndarray: multi-dimensional, vectorized operations, broadcasting, contiguous memory. For numeric computation: NumPy array (fast). For general mixed data: list.

---

### Q639: Python memory management?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Reference counting: each object has ref count, freed when count reaches 0. Circular references handled by garbage collector (gc module). gc.get_objects(). gc.collect(). Generational GC: young (0), middle (1), old (2). Memory pools: CPython uses arenas (256KB), pools (4KB), blocks. Small objects (<512 bytes) from pools. PyPy: JIT-compiled, more efficient memory. Memory profiling: tracemalloc, memory_profiler, objgraph.

---

### Q640: Python dataclasses?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@dataclass decorator auto-generates __init__, __repr__, __eq__, __hash__. from dataclasses import dataclass. @dataclass class Point: x: int; y: int. field(default=0, repr=False, compare=False). dataclasses.asdict(obj). frozen=True: immutable (like namedtuple but more flexible). slots=True (Python 3.10+): __slots__ from fields. KW_ONLY: keyword-only fields. InitVar: parameter for __post_init__. dataclasses.field for custom field config.

---

### Q641: Python property decorator?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@property: method accessed as attribute. @x.setter: called on assignment (obj.x = val). @x.deleter: called on delete (del obj.x). Allows validation, computed attributes, backward compatibility. class Circle: def __init__(self, r): self._r = r; @property def area(self): return 3.14 * self._r ** 2. Cached property: @functools.cached_property. Property vs plain attribute: property gives control without breaking API.

---

### Q642: Python map, filter, reduce?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
map(func, iterable): apply func to each element, return iterator. map(str.upper, ['a','b']). filter(pred, iterable): keep elements where pred True. filter(lambda x: x > 0, [-1,0,1]). functools.reduce(func, iterable): cumulatively apply (sum product). reduce(lambda a,b: a*b, [1,2,3,4]) -> 24. Modern Python prefers: list comprehensions, generator expressions. map/filter vs comprehension: readability preference, map slightly faster for simple built-in functions.

---

### Q643: Python's functools module?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@functools.lru_cache: memoization with LRU eviction. @functools.cache (Python 3.9+): unbounded memoization. functools.partial: fix function arguments. functools.reduce: cumulative application. functools.singledispatch: single-dispatch generic function (type-based overloading). @functools.wraps: preserve wrapped function metadata (in decorators). functools.cmp_to_key: convert comparison function to key function. functools.total_ordering: fill in __gt__/__ge__/__lt__/__le__ from __eq__ + one other.

---

### Q644: Python threads vs processes?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
threading: GIL limits CPU-bound tasks (one thread runs at a time). Good for I/O (file, network, DB) - GIL released during blocking calls. Shared memory (easy data sharing). Lighter weight (one process). multiprocessing: separate processes, each with own GIL, true parallelism for CPU-bound. Higher memory overhead. IPC needed (Queue, Pipe, shared memory). concurrent.futures: ThreadPoolExecutor vs ProcessPoolExecutor (unified API). asyncio: cooperative multitasking for I/O-bound (single thread, no GIL issues). Choose: CPU-bound -> multiprocessing, I/O-bound with many concurrent connections -> asyncio, I/O-bound with blocking libraries -> threading.

---

### Q645: Python file I/O best practices?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Use with open (auto-close). Specify encoding (encoding='utf-8'). Read large files line by line (for line in file:). Buffering. Pathlib for path operations (pathlib.Path). tempfile for temporary files. mmap for memory-mapped file (large file access). shutil for file operations (copy, move, delete). Context manager for custom file-like objects. IOError handling.

---

### Q646: Python *args and **kwargs?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
*args: non-keyword variable arguments (tuple). **kwargs: keyword variable arguments (dict). def func(*args, **kwargs): print(args, kwargs). func(1,2,3, x=4, y=5). Unpacking: *list, **dict. Use in decorators, function wrappers, redirecting calls. Order: positional, *args, keyword-only (after *), **kwargs. Keyword-only arguments: def func(a, b, *, option=True):. Positional-only (Python 3.8+): def func(a, b, /, c):.

---

### Q647: Python logging?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
import logging. logging.basicConfig(level=logging.DEBUG, format='%(asctime)s - %(name)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s'). logger = logging.getLogger(__name__). Levels: DEBUG, INFO, WARNING, ERROR, CRITICAL. Handlers: FileHandler, RotatingFileHandler, StreamHandler, HTTPHandler. Formatters. Logger hierarchy (name '.' separated). Best practice: getLogger(__name__) in each module, configure root logger in app entry point. Structured logging: python-json-logger for JSON output (log aggregation). Avoid: print() for logging.

---

### Q648: Python virtual environments?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
venv: built-in (Python 3.3+), python -m venv myenv, source myenv/bin/activate. Isolates dependencies per project. pip freeze > requirements.txt. pip install -r requirements.txt. Poetry: modern dependency management (pyproject.toml). Pipenv: pip + virtualenv combined. Conda: language-agnostic (Python, R, C++), handles non-Python dependencies (NumPy). Best practice: always use virtual environments, pin versions.

---

### Q649: Python type hints advanced?
**Topic:** Python - Typing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
TypeAliias: Vector = list[float]. Generics: TypeVar('T'), List[T] = list[T]. Generic classes: class Stack[T]: def push(self, item: T): pass. TypeVar bounds/constraints. Callable: Callable[[int, str], bool]. Literal: Literal['red', 'blue']. Final: Final[int] = 42. ClassVar: for class variables. TypedDict: dict with fixed keys and types. Protocol: structural subtyping. NotRequired, ReadOnly (Python 3.11+). Self type (Python 3.11+): return Self for fluent interfaces.

---

### Q650: Python metaclasses?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Metaclass = class of a class. type is the default metaclass. Custom metaclass: class Meta(type): def __new__(mcs, name, bases, namespace): return super().__new__(mcs, name, bases, namespace). class MyClass(metaclass=Meta):. Metaclass methods: __new__ (before class creation), __init__ (after __new__), __call__ (class instantiation). Use: ORMs (SQLAlchemy declarative), validators, singletons, register all subclasses, modify class creation. Alternatives: class decorators, __init_subclass__. "Metaclasses are deeper magic than 99% of users should ever worry about" - Tim Peters.

---

### Q651: Python slotted classes?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
__slots__ = ('x', 'y') reduces memory by avoiding __dict__ per instance. Faster attribute access. Cannot add new attributes not in __slots__. Inheritance: child must define __slots__ or use __dict__. Use: millions of instances (data classes, ORM models), performance-critical code. Python 3.10+: @dataclass(slots=True). Namedtuple: immutable, __slots__-like, but less flexible than dataclasses with slots.

---

### Q652: Python descriptor protocol?
**Topic:** Python - OOP
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Object defining __get__(obj, objtype=None) -> value, __set__(obj, value), __delete__(obj). property is implemented as descriptor. class Typed: def __get__(self, obj, objtype=None): return obj.__dict__[self.name]; def __set__(self, obj, val): if not isinstance(val, self.expected_type): raise TypeError; obj.__dict__[self.name] = val. __set_name__ descriptor (Python 3.6+): self.name = name. Used for: type validation, ORM fields, computed properties, lazy loading. Functions are also descriptors (methods binding via __get__).

---

### Q653: Python collections module?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
deque: double-ended queue, O(1) append/pop both ends, maxlen for bounded deque. Counter: dict subclass for counting (Counter('abracadabra').most_common(3)). defaultdict: dict with default factory (defaultdict(list) for auto-creating list values). OrderedDict (before Python 3.7 dicts were unordered): preserves insertion order, move_to_end(). namedtuple: immutable tuple with named fields (Point = namedtuple('Point', ['x', 'y'])). ChainMap: multiple dicts as single mapping. UserList/Dict/String: subclassable list/dict/str.

---

### Q654: Python iterators and iterables?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Iterable: object implementing __iter__ (returns iterator) or __getitem__ (for indexing). Can be used in for loop. Iterator: object implementing __next__ (returns next element, raises StopIteration) and __iter__ (returns self). iter() converts iterable to iterator. next() advances iterator. All iterators are iterables (not vice versa). Generator functions produce iterators. itertools: chain, cycle, repeat, combinations, permutations, product, groupby.

---

### Q655: Python's global/nonlocal?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
global: declare variable in global scope (module level). def func(): global x; x = 5. Without global, assignment creates local variable. nonlocal (Python 3): for nested functions, bind to outer function scope (not global). def outer(): x = 0; def inner(): nonlocal x; x += 1. Use: closures, decorators, counters. Avoid excessive globals (use class/module instead). SCSS: LEGB (Local, Enclosing, Global, Built-in).

---

### Q656: Python pip and package management?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
pip install package, pip install -r requirements.txt. pip freeze > requirements.txt. pyproject.toml (PEP 517/518): modern build system config. Poetry: pyproject.toml with dependencies, lock file. pipenv: Pipfile + Pipfile.lock. Conda: handles non-Python deps. uv: fast Rust-based pip alternative. Twine: upload to PyPI. Virtual environments isolate. Best practice: use pyproject.toml, specify dependencies ranges, use virtual environments.

---

### Q657: Python performance optimization?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Profile first: cProfile, py-spy, profiling-guided optimization. Use built-in functions (C-optimized): map, filter, sum, list comprehension > manual loops. Local variable lookup faster than global (put in local). Use __slots__ for memory. Use array/NumPy for numeric operations. Use @lru_cache for memoization. Generator lazy evaluation for large data. Avoid string concatenation in loops (use ''.join(list)). Use collections.deque for frequent insert/pop ends. multiprocessing for CPU-bound. C-extensions: Cython, CFFI, PyPy (JIT compiler). Numba: JIT for numerical code.

---

### Q658: Python module vs package?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Module: single .py file. Named via import. import math uses math.py. Package: directory with __init__.py. Use: from package import module. Namespace package: directory without __init__.py (PEP 420). __init__.py runs when package imported. Can define __all__ (list of public names). Relative imports: from . import sibling_package (within package). Avoid circular imports (restructure). Third-party: installed site-packages.

---

### Q659: Python's walrus operator (:=)?
**Topic:** Python - Basics
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Assignment expression: assign and return value in expression. if (n := len(a)) > 10: print(f"List has {n} items"). while (line := file.readline()): process(line). Avoids redundant expressions. Not valid in some contexts (left-hand side of augmented assignment). Use sparingly for readability. Python 3.8+.

---

### Q660: Python for ML/AI?
**Topic:** Python - ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Python is dominant for ML/AI: Scikit-learn (classic ML: regression, classification, clustering, dimensionality reduction), TensorFlow/PyTorch (deep learning), XGBoost/LightGBM (gradient boosting), Hugging Face Transformers (NLP: BERT, GPT), NumPy/Pandas (data manipulation), Matplotlib/Seaborn (visualization), Jupyter (interactive development), MLflow (experiment tracking), Ray (distributed training). Python's ecosystem, readability, and community make it the standard.

## Security

### Q751: OWASP Top 10?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Most critical web security risks (2021). 1. Broken Access Control, 2. Cryptographic Failures, 3. Injection (SQL, NoSQL, OS, LDAP), 4. Insecure Design, 5. Security Misconfiguration, 6. Vulnerable and Outdated Components, 7. Identification and Authentication Failures, 8. Software and Data Integrity Failures, 9. Security Logging and Monitoring Failures, 10. SSRF (Server-Side Request Forgery). Input validation, parameterized queries, proper authentication/authorization, regular updates, security headers minimize risks.

---

### Q752: SQL Injection? Prevention?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Attacker inserts malicious SQL into query. Example: "SELECT * FROM users WHERE id = " + userId. If userId = "1 OR 1=1", gets all users. Types: in-band (response reflects data), out-of-band (data exfiltrated to attacker), blind (inference). Prevention: parameterized queries (PreparedStatement), ORM (automatic escaping), stored procedures (safe if parameterized), input validation, least privilege (read-only DB user). Never concatenate user input into SQL strings.

---

### Q753: XSS (Cross-Site Scripting)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Attacker injects client-side scripts into web pages viewed by others. Types: Stored (script saved on server - comments, profiles), Reflected (script in URL/request - phishing), DOM-based (client-side manipulation). Impact: session theft, redirects, keylogging, defacement. Prevention: output encoding (HTML entity encode), Content-Security-Policy header (restrict script sources), input validation, HttpOnly cookies (prevent JS access), XSS sanitization libraries (DOMPurify).

---

### Q754: CSRF (Cross-Site Request Forgery)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Attacker tricks authenticated user into executing unintended actions. Example: user clicks link -> sends request to bank.com/transfer?amount=1000&to=attacker. User's cookies sent automatically. Prevention: CSRF tokens (random per-request token validated server-side), SameSite cookie attribute (Strict/Lax), custom request headers (X-Requested-By), re-authentication for sensitive actions. Modern SPAs with SameSite=Strict mitigate most CSRF.

---

### Q755: Authentication vs Authorization?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Authentication: verifying identity (who you are). Methods: password, OTP, biometrics, OAuth, SAML. Authorization: verifying permissions (what you can access). Methods: RBAC (Role-Based Access Control), ABAC (Attribute-Based), ACL. Typically: authn -> authz. JWT: signed token containing user claims (authentication). Permissions checked separately (authorization). Common mistakes: relying only on authentication for authorization, not checking permissions for each resource.

---

### Q756: JWT (JSON Web Tokens)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compact, URL-safe token for transmitting claims. Structure: header.payload.signature. Header: algorithm (HS256, RS256). Payload: claims (sub, iat, exp, custom). Signature: HMAC (symmetric - HS256) or RSA (asymmetric - RS256). Stateless: server doesn't need session storage. Storage: httpOnly cookie (prevent XSS) vs localStorage (XSS vulnerable). Refresh token: short-lived access token (15min) + long-lived refresh token (7 days). Security risks: token theft, algorithm confusion (change alg to none), weak secret. Best practices: short expiry, secure flag, rotate signing keys.

---

### Q757: OAuth 2.0 and OpenID Connect?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
OAuth 2.0: authorization framework (delegated access). Roles: Resource Owner (user), Client (app), Authorization Server, Resource Server. Flows: Authorization Code (most secure, for web apps), PKCE (for mobile/SPA), Client Credentials (server-to-server), Implicit (deprecated). OpenID Connect (OIDC): authentication layer on OAuth 2.0. Adds ID Token (JWT with user identity). /authorize -> /token -> /userinfo. Scopes: requested permissions. Grant types: authorization_code, client_credentials, refresh_token. Security: use state parameter (CSRF), PKCE for public clients, validate redirect URIs.

---

### Q758: HTTPS and SSL/TLS?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
TLS (Transport Layer Security): encrypts HTTP traffic. Handshake: client hello -> server cert + key exchange -> client verifies cert -> session keys established. Certificate: X.509, issued by Certificate Authority (CA). Certificate validation: verify signature chain, check expiration, check hostname, check revocation (CRL/OCSP). HTTPS provides: confidentiality (encryption), integrity (tamper detection), authentication (server identity). Cipher suites: key exchange (ECDHE), authentication (RSA/ECDSA), encryption (AES-GCM), MAC (SHA-256). TLS 1.3: faster handshake, removed weak algorithms. HTTP/2 over TLS.

---

### Q759: Password Security?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Never store plain text passwords. Hashing: one-way function. Bcrypt (adaptive, cost factor), Argon2 (memory-hard - OWASP recommended), PBKDF2, scrypt. Salt: unique per-password random value (prevents rainbow tables). Pepper: application-wide secret (not needed with strong hashing). Password policies: minimum length 8-12, no arbitrary complexity rules (NIST SP 800-63). MFA: TOTP, SMS, hardware keys (FIDO2/WebAuthn). Account lockout after failed attempts. Breach detection: check HaveIBeenPwned. Rate limiting login attempts.

---

### Q760: API Security best practices?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Authentication: API keys, JWT, OAuth 2.0. Rate limiting: prevent abuse (per-user, per-IP). Input validation: whitelist parameters, reject malformed input. Output filtering: never expose internal details. HTTPS required. CORS: restrict allowed origins. Request validation: Content-Type, Accept headers, schema validation. Logging and monitoring: audit trail, anomaly detection. Versioning: /v1/, /v2/. Least privilege: scoped API keys. Secrets management: environment variables, vaults (HashiCorp Vault, AWS Secrets Manager). API gateway: request throttling, authentication, logging centralization.

---

### Q761: CORS (Cross-Origin Resource Sharing)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Browser security mechanism: controls cross-origin HTTP requests. Same-Origin Policy default: only same origin (protocol+domain+port) can read responses. CORS headers: Access-Control-Allow-Origin (which origins), Access-Control-Allow-Methods (GET, POST...), Access-Control-Allow-Headers. Preflight: OPTIONS request for non-simple requests (custom headers, PUT/DELETE). Credentials: Access-Control-Allow-Credentials: true (cookies, auth headers). Wildcard (*) cannot be used with credentials. CORS is browser-enforced; APIs should still implement authentication.

---

### Q762: Security Headers?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HTTP response headers for security. Content-Security-Policy: restrict resource sources (scripts, styles, images). X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff (prevent MIME sniffing). Strict-Transport-Security: force HTTPS (max-age, includeSubDomains). X-Frame-Options: DENY/SAMEORIGIN (prevent clickjacking). X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block (legacy XSS filter). Referrer-Policy: control Referer header. Permissions-Policy: restrict browser APIs (camera, microphone). Cache-Control: no-store for sensitive data.

---

### Q763: Cryptography basics?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Symmetric encryption: same key for encrypt/decrypt. AES (128/256 bit, modes: GCM - authenticated, CBC - needs padding, CTR). Asymmetric: public/private key pair. RSA (slow), ECC (Elliptic Curve - smaller keys, faster). Use: exchange symmetric keys, digital signatures. Hashing: SHA-256, SHA-3 (one-way). HMAC: keyed hash (message authentication). Digital signature: sign with private key, verify with public (non-repudiation). Perfect forward secrecy: ephemeral session keys (ECDHE). TLS uses hybrid: ECDHE for key exchange, AES-GCM for encryption.

---

### Q764: Rate Limiting and Throttling?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Prevent abuse by limiting requests. Types: per-user (API key, IP), per-endpoint, global. Algorithms: Token Bucket (burst + sustained rate), Leaky Bucket (smooth), Fixed Window (simple but edge bursts), Sliding Window Log, Sliding Window Counter. Headers: X-RateLimit-Limit, X-RateLimit-Remaining, X-RateLimit-Reset. Backend: Redis (INCR + EXPIRE), NGINX (limit_req), API Gateway. Response: 429 Too Many Requests. Retry-After header. Strategies: queue (async), degrade gracefully, prioritize premium users.

---

### Q765: Dependency and Supply Chain Security?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Risks: malicious packages (typosquatting, dependency confusion), compromised maintainers, vulnerable transitive dependencies. Prevention: software bill of materials (SBOM), lock files (package-lock.json, requirements.txt), dependency scanning (Snyk, Dependabot, OWASP Dependency-Check), regular updates, pin versions (semver), private registries for internal packages. Verify signatures (npm audit signatures). Least privilege for CI/CD pipeline. No install scripts from untrusted sources.

---

### Q766: Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Attacker makes server-side application send requests to internal resources. Bypasses firewalls (requests from trusted server). Exploit: provide internal URL (http://169.254.169.254/metadata - AWS metadata), file:// protocol, internal services. Impact: access cloud metadata, internal services, port scanning. Prevention: URL allowlist (no blocklist), disable unnecessary URL schemes, validate/restrict redirects, network segmentation, deny by default outbound traffic, use dedicated tools with URL parsing. Modern cloud: IMDSv2 (requires token, PutResponseHopLimit=1).

---

### Q767: Content Security Policy (CSP)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HTTP header preventing XSS and data injection. Directives: default-src, script-src, style-src, img-src, connect-src, font-src, frame-src, object-src, media-src. Values: 'self', 'none', *.domain.com, 'unsafe-inline' (avoid), 'unsafe-eval' (avoid), nonce-{random}, {hash}. Report-URI/report-to: violation reporting. Level 2: nonces/hashes for inline scripts. Level 3: strict-dynamic (trust propagated from nonce/hash scripts). Implementation: start with report-only (Content-Security-Policy-Report-Only), then enforce. Hard to implement on existing apps with many inline scripts.

---

### Q768: Secure Session Management?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Session ID generation: cryptographically random (CSPRNG), sufficient entropy (128+ bits). Transmission: only over HTTPS, httpOnly (prevent XSS read), secure (only HTTPS), SameSite (prevent CSRF). Storage: server-side (in-memory, Redis) or client-side (JWT). Expiration: idle timeout (15-30min), absolute timeout (8h). Regenerate session ID after login (prevent session fixation). Logout: invalidate session server-side. No session ID in URL. Multi-device: session management UI (view/revoke sessions). Rotation: refresh tokens auto-rotate.

---

### Q769: Input Validation and Sanitization?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Validate: check input meets expected format/type/range. Server-side validation (client-side can be bypassed). Whitelist approach (allow known good) - stronger than blacklist. Sanitize: remove/encode dangerous characters. Examples: SQL (parameterized queries), XSS (HTML entity encode), command injection (validate against shell metacharacters), path traversal (resolve and check prefix). Libraries: validator.js, OWASP Java HTML Sanitizer. Defense in depth: validate at multiple layers (frontend, API, backend). Never trust user input.

---

### Q770: Logging and Monitoring for Security?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Log all: authentication events (login, logout, failures), access control failures, input validation failures, data changes, privilege escalation. Protect logs: append-only, immutable storage, access controls. Sensitive data: never log passwords, tokens, PII (mask/redact). Monitoring: SIEM (Splunk, ELK, Azure Sentinel), alerts for anomalies (multiple failures, unusual times/locations), automated response (rate limiting, account lock). OWASP Top 10 #9: Security Logging and Monitoring Failures. Mean Time to Detect (MTTD) and Respond (MTTR). Audit trails for compliance.

## Spring Boot

### Q101: What is Spring Framework?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Spring is a comprehensive enterprise Java framework.
