Core features: IoC/DI (Inversion of Control via Dependency Injection), AOP (Aspect-Oriented Programming for cross-cutting concerns), Spring MVC (web framework), Spring Data (data access abstraction), Spring Security (auth/authz), Spring Boot (auto-configuration + embedded servers + starters).

---

### Q102: Spring Boot vs Spring?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Spring Boot extends Spring with: (1) Auto-configuration - automatically configures beans based on classpath dependencies, (2) Starters - pre-packaged dependency groups, (3) Embedded servers (Tomcat, Jetty, Undertow) - no WAR deployment, (4) Actuator - production monitoring, (5) Externalized configuration via application.properties/yml. Spring Boot is convention-over-configuration on top of Spring.

---

### Q103: IoC and DI?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
IoC (Inversion of Control): framework controls object lifecycle and flow, not application code. DI (Dependency Injection): objects receive dependencies from external source (IoC container) rather than creating them internally. Constructor injection is preferred for immutability, required dependencies, and easier testing.

---

### Q104: Types of DI in Spring?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
1. Constructor injection (preferred): dependencies via constructor parameters, enables final fields. 2. Setter injection: dependencies via @Autowired on setter methods. 3. Field injection: @Autowired directly on fields (discouraged - hard to test, no immutability). Since Spring 4.3+, single-constructor classes have implicit @Autowired.

---

### Q105: ApplicationContext vs BeanFactory?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
BeanFactory: foundational IoC container, lazy initialization (beans created on demand), lightweight. ApplicationContext: extends BeanFactory with eager initialization, AOP support, message i18n (MessageSource), event publishing (ApplicationEvent), Environment abstraction, WebApplicationContext. ApplicationContext is used in most applications.

---

### Q106: Spring bean scopes?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
singleton (default): one instance per IoC container. prototype: new instance per injection/getBean. request: one instance per HTTP request (web). session: one instance per HTTP session. application: one instance per ServletContext. websocket: one instance per WebSocket. Configure via @Scope annotation.

---

### Q107: @Component, @Service, @Repository, @Controller?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
All are stereotype annotations for Spring-managed beans. @Component is generic. @Service: service layer (business logic). @Repository: DAO layer (adds persistence exception translation via PersistenceExceptionTranslationPostProcessor). @Controller: MVC controller (returns view). @RestController: @Controller + @ResponseBody (returns JSON).

---

### Q108: @Autowired vs constructor injection?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Autowired (field/setter): uses reflection to inject after object creation, no final fields, harder to test in isolation. Constructor injection: dependencies in constructor call, enables final/immutable fields, no reflection needed, easier unit testing (just pass dependencies). Spring team recommends constructor injection.

---

### Q109: @Primary and @Qualifier?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
When multiple beans of same type exist, @Primary marks one as default candidate. @Qualifier specifies exact bean by name: @Qualifier("mongoRepo") or @Qualifier("mysqlRepo"). @Primary is global, @Qualifier is specific to injection point.

---

### Q110: Spring Boot auto-configuration?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@EnableAutoConfiguration (included in @SpringBootApplication) triggers auto-configuration. Spring Boot scans classpath for spring.factories files (META-INF/spring/org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.AutoConfiguration.imports). @ConditionalOnClass, @ConditionalOnMissingBean, @ConditionalOnProperty determine which configurations apply. Users can override by defining their own beans.

---

### Q111: @SpringBootApplication?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Convenience annotation combining @Configuration (marks class as config), @EnableAutoConfiguration (enables auto-config), @ComponentScan (scans current package and subpackages). Typically placed on main class containing SpringApplication.run().

---

### Q112: Spring Boot starters?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Pre-packaged dependency descriptors. Naming: spring-boot-starter-*. Examples: spring-boot-starter-web (REST + Tomcat), spring-boot-starter-data-jpa (JPA + Hibernate), spring-boot-starter-security, spring-boot-starter-test (JUnit, Mockito), spring-boot-starter-actuator (monitoring). Include in pom.xml, transitive dependencies resolved automatically.

---

### Q113: Spring Boot Actuator?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Production-ready HTTP endpoints for monitoring/managing application. Common endpoints: /actuator/health (liveness/readiness), /actuator/info (custom app info), /actuator/metrics (JVM, system, custom metrics), /actuator/env (environment properties), /actuator/beans (all beans), /actuator/mappings (request mappings), /actuator/loggers (log level management), /actuator/threaddump (thread dump).

---

### Q114: Spring Data JPA?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Spring Data JPA reduces data access boilerplate. Extends JpaRepository<T, ID> interface, Spring implements at runtime. Derived query methods: method names parsed to generate JPQL (findByLastName, countByAgeGreaterThan, deleteByExpiredBefore). @Query for custom JPQL/native queries. @Modifying for UPDATE/DELETE. Specification/Example for dynamic queries.

---

### Q115: Derived query methods?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Spring Data JPA parses method names: findBy[Property][Operator]. Supported: And, Or, Between, LessThan, GreaterThan, Like, Containing, OrderBy, Not, In, IsNull, True, False, IgnoreCase. Return types: Entity, Optional, List, Page (with Pageable parameter). Example: findDistinctByLastNameIgnoreCase(String name).

---

### Q116: @Entity, @Table, @Id, @GeneratedValue?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
@Entity: marks class as JPA entity (mapped to DB table). @Table(name="users"): specifies table name (optional, defaults to class name). @Id: marks primary key field. @GeneratedValue(strategy=GenerationType.IDENTITY): auto-generates PK. GenerationType strategies: IDENTITY (auto-increment), SEQUENCE (database sequence), TABLE (simulated sequence), AUTO (JPA chooses).

---

### Q117: @OneToMany, @ManyToOne, @ManyToMany?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@OneToMany(mappedBy="user") + @ManyToOne: bidirectional one-to-many. Use Set/HashSet for collections. CascadeType: ALL, PERSIST, MERGE, REMOVE, REFRESH, DETACH. FetchType.LAZY (default for collections) vs EAGER (default for *ToOne). @ManyToMany needs @JoinTable with joinColumns and inverseJoinColumns. Avoid EAGER fetching for performance.

---

### Q118: JPA vs Hibernate?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
JPA: Java Persistence API - standard specification (jakarta.persistence interfaces/annotations). Hibernate: JPA implementation plus proprietary features (caching, batch, filters). Spring Data JPA builds on JPA. Using JPA standard: can switch providers (Hibernate, EclipseLink, OpenJPA). Hibernate-specific features accessed via native API.

---

### Q119: Pagination and Sorting?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pageable: findAll(PageRequest.of(page, size, sort)). Page<T> response: getContent(), getTotalPages(), getTotalElements(), getNumber(), isFirst(), isLast(), getSort(). Sort by: Sort.by("name").ascending().and(Sort.by("age").descending()). Custom queries accept Pageable parameter and return Page<T>.

---

### Q120: @Transactional?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Declarative transaction management. Ensures ACID atomicity: all DB operations succeed or all roll back. Propagation types: REQUIRED (default - join existing or create new), REQUIRES_NEW (suspend existing, create new), NESTED (savepoint within existing), MANDATORY (require existing), NEVER (error if exists), SUPPORTS, NOT_SUPPORTED. Isolation levels: READ_UNCOMMITTED, READ_COMMITTED, REPEATABLE_READ, SERIALIZABLE. readonly=true optimizes for read-only operations. rollbackFor specifies exceptions that trigger rollback.

---

### Q121: @Component vs @Bean?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Component: class-level, auto-detected via component scanning, Spring creates bean instance. @Bean: method-level in @Configuration class, explicit bean creation, used for third-party classes you cannot annotate (RestTemplate, DataSource). Both register beans in container.

---

### Q122: Spring AOP?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Aspect-Oriented Programming modularizes cross-cutting concerns (logging, transactions, security, caching). Key terms: Aspect (module), Join Point (method execution), Advice (action at join point: @Before, @After, @Around, @AfterReturning, @AfterThrowing), Pointcut (expression matching join points), Weaving (linking aspects with code). Spring AOP uses runtime proxy-based AOP (JDK dynamic proxy for interfaces, CGLIB for classes).

---

### Q123: Advice types?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Before: runs before join point. @After: runs after join point (regardless of outcome). @AfterReturning: runs after successful return. @AfterThrowing: runs after exception thrown. @Around: wraps join point (most powerful - can modify arguments, return value, handle exceptions, skip execution). Around advice uses ProceedingJoinPoint.proceed().

---

### Q124: Spring Security architecture?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Security
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
SecurityFilterChain: chain of filters intercepting HTTP requests. AuthenticationManager: authenticates credentials (supports multiple providers). UserDetailsService: loads user details from DB. SecurityContextHolder: stores current Authentication (ThreadLocal). GrantedAuthority: user roles/permissions. PasswordEncoder: encodes and verifies passwords (BCryptPasswordEncoder recommended). Authorization: method security (@PreAuthorize, @Secured) and URL security (authorizeHttpRequests).

---

### Q125: JWT with Spring Security?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Security
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
JWT stateless token: header.payload.signature. Flow: (1) POST /auth/login with credentials, (2) Server authenticates, generates JWT with claims (sub, roles, exp, iat), (3) Client stores JWT in localStorage/HttpOnly cookie, (4) Client sends Authorization: Bearer <token> header, (5) JwtAuthenticationFilter extends OncePerRequestFilter, extracts token, validates signature/expiry, sets SecurityContextHolder. Use JJWT or nimbus-jose-jwt library. Spring Security OAuth2 Resource Server supports JWT natively.

---

### Q126: Spring MVC architecture?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Front Controller pattern: DispatcherServlet receives all requests. HandlerMapping maps request to controller method. Controller (@Controller) processes request, returns ModelAndView or @ResponseBody. ViewResolver resolves logical view name to actual view (JSP, Thymeleaf, Freemarker). For REST: @RestController returns JSON directly (HttpMessageConverter handles serialization, typically Jackson).

---

### Q127: @RestController vs @Controller?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
@Controller: returns view name (HTML), used with @ResponseBody on methods for JSON. @RestController: @Controller + @ResponseBody on all methods, returns JSON/XML directly. For REST APIs, always use @RestController.

---

### Q128: @RequestMapping, @GetMapping, @PostMapping?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
@RequestMapping(path="/users", method=RequestMethod.GET) - generic (any HTTP method) @GetMapping (GET), @PostMapping (POST), @PutMapping (PUT), @DeleteMapping (DELETE), @PatchMapping (PATCH) are composed annotations combining @RequestMapping with specific HTTP method.

---

### Q129: @PathVariable and @RequestParam?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
@PathVariable: extracts value from URI template. @PathVariable Long id from /users/{id}. @RequestParam: extracts query parameter. @RequestParam(defaultValue="1") int page from /users?page=1. @RequestParam supports required, defaultValue, and multi-value (List<String>).

---

### Q130: @RequestBody and @ResponseBody?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
@RequestBody: deserializes HTTP request body to Java object (JSON via Jackson HttpMessageConverter). @ResponseBody: serializes Java object to HTTP response body. Both use HttpMessageConverter (configured via Content-Type/Accept headers). @RestController adds @ResponseBody to all methods.

---

### Q131: ResponseEntity?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Full control over HTTP response: status code (ResponseEntity.status(HttpStatus.CREATED)), headers (ResponseEntity.ok().header("X-Custom", "value")), body. Factory methods: ok(), badRequest(), notFound(), created(URI), accepted(), noContent(). Use @ResponseStatus for simple status codes, ResponseEntity for dynamic responses.

---

### Q132: Exception handling in REST?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@ExceptionHandler in controller: handles exceptions locally. @ControllerAdvice: global handler across all controllers. @RestControllerAdvice: @ControllerAdvice + @ResponseBody. @ExceptionHandler methods return ResponseEntity<ErrorResponse>. Custom exception classes with @ResponseStatus. @ResponseStatus on exceptions for automatic HTTP status mapping.

---

### Q133: Bean validation with @Valid?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Jakarta Bean Validation annotations on DTO fields: @NotBlank, @Email, @Min/@Max, @Size, @Pattern, @NotNull. @Valid triggers validation on @RequestBody. MethodArgumentNotValidException handling returns field-level errors. @Validated for group validation. Custom validators via @Constraint(validatedBy=...).

---

### Q134: Spring profiles?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Profile-specific configuration files: application-dev.properties, application-prod.properties. Activate via spring.profiles.active=dev or --spring.profiles.active=prod. @Profile("dev") on beans configures them for specific profiles. @Profile("!dev") excludes from profile. spring.profiles.include to include additional profiles.

---

### Q135: @ConfigurationProperties?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Type-safe external configuration binding. @ConfigurationProperties(prefix="app") maps properties to Java object fields. @EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProps.class) enables registration. Supports nested properties, lists, maps, relaxed binding (kebab-case, camelCase). Validation via @Validated. IDE has auto-completion with spring-boot-configuration-processor.

---

### Q136: Spring Boot DevTools?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Development tools: automatic restart (two-classloader architecture - base unchanged, restart loads app classes), LiveReload (auto-refresh browser), remote debugging, template cache disabling (Thymeleaf, Freemarker), H2 console. Disable for production: exclude spring-boot-devtools or set -Dspring.devtools.restart.enabled=false.

---

### Q137: Custom Spring Boot Starter?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
1. Create auto-configuration module with @Configuration + @ConditionalOnClass/@ConditionalOnMissingBean. 2. @EnableConfigurationProperties(MyProperties.class) for property binding. 3. Register in META-INF/spring/org.springframework.boot.autoconfigure.AutoConfiguration.imports (or spring.factories for Boot 2.x). 4. Provide spring-boot-starter POM with dependencies. Naming: custom-spring-boot-starter.

---

### Q138: CORS configuration?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Global: WebMvcConfigurer.addCorsMappings(). Config: allowedOrigins, allowedMethods (GET,POST,PUT,DELETE), allowedHeaders, allowCredentials (true for cookies/Authorization), maxAge (preflight cache duration). Controller-level: @CrossOrigin(origins="http://localhost:3000"). Security: http.cors() in SecurityFilterChain.

---

### Q139: Spring Cloud microservices?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Spring Cloud provides tools for distributed systems: Config Server (external config), Eureka (service discovery), Gateway (API gateway), Resilience4j (circuit breaker, retry, rate limiter), Sleuth/Micrometer (distributed tracing), Cloud Stream (event-driven messaging), Feign/WebClient (HTTP clients). Works with Spring Boot via auto-configuration.

---

### Q140: What are microservices? Pros/cons?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Independent, loosely coupled services each handling specific business capability. Pros: independent deployability and scaling, technology diversity, team autonomy, fault isolation, faster releases. Cons: network latency, distributed data management/consistency, testing complexity, operational overhead (monitoring, logging, deployment), DevOps maturity required.

---

### Q141: Microservice communication?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Synchronous: HTTP/REST (RestTemplate, WebClient, Feign client), gRPC (Protocol Buffers, HTTP/2, streaming). Asynchronous: message brokers (RabbitMQ AMQP, Apache Kafka), event-driven (Event Sourcing, CDC - Change Data Capture). Service Mesh: sidecar proxies (Istio, Linkerd) handle communication, security, observability at infrastructure layer.

---

### Q142: Circuit Breaker pattern?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prevents cascading failures when downstream service fails. Three states: CLOSED (normal - requests pass), OPEN (failure threshold exceeded - requests fail fast immediately), HALF_OPEN (test if recovered - limited probe requests, success -> CLOSED, failure -> OPEN). Resilience4j provides @CircuitBreaker with configurable failure rate threshold, wait duration, sliding window size. Fallback method when circuit open.

---

### Q143: API Gateway?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Single entry point for all clients. Responsibilities: routing (forward requests to appropriate services), load balancing, authentication (validate JWT centrally), rate limiting, request/response transformation, caching, logging/monitoring, API versioning, cross-cutting concerns. Spring Cloud Gateway provides RouteLocator with predicates and filters.

---

### Q144: Service Discovery (Eureka)?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Eureka Server: registry where services register their network addresses. Eureka Client: registers itself on startup, sends heartbeats (30s interval), discovers other services by name. Client-side load balancing via Spring Cloud LoadBalancer (replacement for Netflix Ribbon). @EnableEurekaServer / @EnableEurekaClient (or @EnableDiscoveryClient). Self-preservation mode prevents false removals during network issues.

---

### Q145: Distributed tracing?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tracks request across microservices. Unique traceId (propagated across service calls via HTTP headers). spanId (individual service operation). Parent-child span relationships. OpenTelemetry (replacement for Sleuth + Zipkin): automatic instrumentation, exports to Zipkin/Jaeger/OtLP. Visualizes request flow, identifies latency bottlenecks and error sources.

---

### Q146: @Async and @EnableAsync?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@EnableAsync on configuration enables async method execution. @Async on method executes in separate thread. Returns void or CompletableFuture. Configure via AsyncConfigurer: custom ThreadPoolTaskExecutor (corePoolSize, maxPoolSize, queueCapacity). Exception handling via AsyncUncaughtExceptionHandler.

---

### Q147: @Scheduled?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@EnableScheduling enables scheduled task execution. @Scheduled options: fixedRate (milliseconds between starts regardless of duration), fixedDelay (milliseconds after last completion), cron (expression - second minute hour day-of-month month day-of-week), initialDelay (delay before first execution). Configure via TaskScheduler: ThreadPoolTaskScheduler for multi-threaded execution.

---

### Q148: RestTemplate vs WebClient?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
RestTemplate (deprecated in favor of WebClient): blocking (synchronous), thread-per-request model, error handling via try-catch/ResponseErrorHandler. WebClient (reactive): non-blocking, event-loop model, fluent API, supports both reactive (Mono/Flux) and blocking (block()) usage, error handling via .onStatus(), .onErrorResume(). WebClient is the future direction.

---

### Q149: HATEOAS?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hypermedia as the Engine of Application State: API responses include links to related resources. EntityModel<T> wraps entity with links. CollectionModel<T> wraps collection. linkTo(methodOn(Controller.class).method()).withSelfRel() generates links. Clients navigate API via hyperlinks rather than hardcoded URLs.

---

### Q150: Spring Data REST?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Exposes JPA repositories as REST endpoints automatically. @RepositoryRestResource(path="users"). Generated: GET /users (list, pagination, sort), GET /users/{id}, POST /users, PUT /users/{id}, PATCH /users/{id}, DELETE /users/{id}. Integrates with HATEOAS. @RestResource(exported=false) to hide specific methods. Projections and Excerpts for custom views.

---

### Q151: Spring Boot caching?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@EnableCaching enables cache support. @Cacheable("cacheName"): checks cache before method execution, returns cached if present. @CachePut: always executes method, updates cache. @CacheEvict: removes entries (beforeInvocation, allEntries). @Caching: group multiple annotations. Supported providers: JCache (JSR-107), EhCache, Redis, Caffeine, Hazelcast, Simple (ConcurrentHashMap).

---

### Q152: @Cacheable vs @CachePut vs @CacheEvict?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Cacheable: skip execution if cache hit, cache result on miss. @CachePut: always execute method, update cache with result (never skips). @CacheEvict: remove cache entries (clear stale data). @Caching: combine multiple annotations for complex scenarios (e.g., update one cache, evict another).

---

### Q153: Logging configuration?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Default: Logback + SLF4J. Configure in application.properties: logging.level.root=INFO, logging.level.com.example=DEBUG. logging.file.name=app.log. logging.pattern.console=%d{...} - %msg%n. Custom logback-spring.xml for advanced config (appenders, rolling policy, logstash encoder). Logging system auto-detected (Logback, Log4j2 via exclusion + starter).

---

### Q154: @PropertySource?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Loads properties file into Spring Environment. @PropertySource("classpath:custom.properties"). @PropertySource("file:${app.home}/config.properties"). Multiple @PropertySource. Spring Boot automatically loads application.properties/yml from classpath, config/location, environment variables, command-line args.

---

### Q155: SpEL (Spring Expression Language)?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Expression language for runtime object manipulation. @Value("#{systemProperties['user.home']}"). @Cacheable(key="#user.id"). @PreAuthorize("hasRole('ADMIN')"). @EventListener(condition="#event.success"). @Scheduled(cron="#{@cronConfig.getCron()}"). Accessed via ExpressionParser: SpelExpressionParser.

---

### Q156: @SpringBootTest?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Creates full application context for integration tests. Properties: webEnvironment (MOCK, RANDOM_PORT, DEFINED_PORT, NONE). @TestRestTemplate or TestWebClient for HTTP calls. @AutoConfigureMockMvc for MockMvc. Slice tests for focused testing: @WebMvcTest (web layer only), @DataJpaTest (JPA only), @JsonTest (JSON serialization), @RestClientTest (REST clients).

---

### Q157: Mockito with Spring?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Mock: creates mock of class/interface. @InjectMocks: injects mocks into tested object. @Spy: partial mock (real object with some methods mocked). @MockBean: replaces bean in Spring context (for integration tests). BDDMockito: given/willReturn style. ArgumentMatchers: any(), eq(), anyString(), anyLong(). verify() checks method invocation count.

---

### Q158: Spring Data MongoDB?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Spring Data for MongoDB: @Document(collection="users") maps Java object to collection. MongoRepository<T, String> provides CRUD + derived query methods. @DBRef for references. Aggregation operations via MongoTemplate. @Indexed for secondary indexes. GeoJSON support for geospatial queries.

---

### Q159: Spring Batch?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Framework for batch processing. Job -> Step -> ItemReader/ItemProcessor/ItemWriter. @EnableBatchProcessing. Chunk-oriented processing: read items in bulk (chunk size), process, write. Readers: FlatFileItemReader (CSV), JdbcCursorItemReader (database), JmsItemReader (queue). Processors: transform/validate/filter. Writers: FlatFileItemWriter, JdbcBatchItemWriter. JobLauncher triggers jobs. JobRepository stores metadata.

---

### Q160: Spring Cloud Config?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
External configuration management. Config Server serves configuration from Git repository (supports versioning, labeling). @EnableConfigServer. Config Client (bootstrap.properties/yml): spring.cloud.config.uri=http://config-server:8888, spring.application.name=my-service, spring.cloud.config.profile=prod. /actuator/refresh triggers runtime reload. Spring Cloud Bus propagates refresh events across all instances.

---

### Q161: Resilience4j?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Fault tolerance library. Modules: CircuitBreaker (fail fast on threshold reached), Retry (configurable attempts and backoff), RateLimiter (limit requests per period), TimeLimiter (timeout), Bulkhead (semaphore or thread-pool isolation), Cache (result caching). Configuration via annotation (@CircuitBreaker, @Retry) or code. Metrics integration with Micrometer. Fallback methods for degraded response.

---

### Q162: Health indicators?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Actuator
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Health endpoint shows status (UP, DOWN, OUT_OF_SERVICE, UNKNOWN). Built-in: DataSourceHealthIndicator, MongoHealthIndicator, RedisHealthIndicator, DiskSpaceHealthIndicator. Custom: implement HealthIndicator interface, return Health.up()/Health.down(ex). Composite health via CompositeHealthContributor for multi-component resources.

---

### Q163: @Value?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Injects property value from Environment. @Value("${app.name:DefaultApp}") sets appName with fallback. @Value("#{systemProperties['user.home']}") uses SpEL. @Value("${java.home}") for system properties. Supports type conversion (int, boolean, URI, Duration, etc.). Injected at field/method/constructor parameter level.

---

### Q164: @Conditional?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Conditionally register beans. Built-in: @ConditionalOnClass (class present), @ConditionalOnMissingBean (bean not defined), @ConditionalOnProperty (property has value), @ConditionalOnExpression (SpEL), @ConditionalOnResource (resource exists), @ConditionalOnWebApplication, @ConditionalOnNotWebApplication. Can create custom condition class implementing Condition.

---

### Q165: Spring Data Redis?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
RedisTemplate for operations: opsForValue(), opsForList(), opsForSet(), opsForHash(), opsForZSet(). Serializers: StringRedisSerializer, Jackson2JsonRedisSerializer, JdkSerializationRedisSerializer (default). @RedisHash for repository support. RedisCacheManager for @Cacheable with Redis. Spring Session Redis for distributed sessions. Lettuce (default) or Jedis client.

---

### Q166: @ControllerAdvice vs @RestControllerAdvice?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@ControllerAdvice: global exception handling for @Controller classes, returns view or @ResponseBody. @RestControllerAdvice: @ControllerAdvice + @ResponseBody, returns JSON for REST APIs. Both intercept exceptions across all controllers and apply to multiple controllers. Can be selective with annotations, basePackages, assignableTypes.

---

### Q167: @ExceptionHandler?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Handles specific exception types from controller methods. Method parameters: exception instance. Return types: ResponseEntity, @ResponseBody, ModelAndView. @ExceptionHandler(ResourceNotFoundException.class) maps to NOT_FOUND response. Can access request via HttpServletRequest parameter. Can combine with @ResponseStatus.

---

### Q168: @JsonIgnore, @JsonManagedReference, @JsonBackReference?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prevent infinite JSON recursion in bidirectional relationships. @JsonIgnore: excludes field from serialization (breaks one direction). @JsonManagedReference: parent side (serialized normally). @JsonBackReference: child side (excluded). Better approach: use DTOs (Data Transfer Objects) separate from entities. @JsonView for selective serialization based on context.

---

### Q169: DataSource configuration?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
spring.datasource.url (JDBC URL), username, password, driver-class-name. HikariCP is default connection pool (fast, lightweight). Config: spring.datasource.hikari.maximum-pool-size, minimum-idle, connection-timeout, idle-timeout, max-lifetime. Multiple datasources: @Primary + @ConfigurationProperties on each. JNDI datasource: spring.datasource.jndi-name.

---

### Q170: Flyway/Liquibase?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Data JPA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Database migration version control. Flyway: SQL files named V1__description.sql, V2__add_column.sql. Checksum verification, undo support (Pro). Liquibase: XML/YAML/JSON changelogs. Both integrate with Spring Boot: spring.flyway.enabled=true, spring.liquibase.enabled=true. Auto-detected on classpath. Can be disabled for tests.

---

### Q171: Spring WebFlux?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Reactive
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Reactive web framework (Project Reactor). Non-blocking, backpressure-aware. Mono<T> (0-1 element), Flux<T> (0-N elements). @RestController same as MVC but returns Mono/Flux. Functional endpoints: RouterFunction -> HandlerFunction. Netty (default server) is event-loop based. R2DBC for reactive database access (non-blocking SQL). WebClient for reactive HTTP calls.

---

### Q172: Spring MVC vs WebFlux?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Reactive
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
MVC: Servlet API, blocking (thread-per-request), thread pool limited, Tomcat/Jetty/JBoss. WebFlux: reactive streams, non-blocking (event-loop), fewer threads handle more requests, Netty undertow/Jetty. Use MVC for standard apps with JPA/JDBC (blocking DB). Use WebFlux for high-concurrency streaming apps (real-time, SSE, WebSockets). Can coexist using @EnableWebFlux annotation.

---

### Q173: Spring Cloud Stream?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Event-driven microservices framework. Functional programming model (since 3.x): java.util.function.Supplier/Function/Consumer as message sources/processors/sinks. Binder abstraction: Kafka, RabbitMQ. Binding: input/output channels via spring.cloud.stream.bindings. @StreamListener (legacy). DLQ (dead letter queue) support for failed messages.

---

### Q174: @Configuration class?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - DI/IoC
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Class annotated with @Configuration containing @Bean methods. Replaces XML configuration. Proxied via CGLIB to ensure singleton bean semantics (calling @Bean method returns same instance). Can use @Profile and @Conditional on methods. Can @Import other configuration classes. @Configuration is meta-annotated with @Component.

---

### Q175: @Import and @ImportResource?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
@Import(ConfigClass.class): imports other @Configuration classes (bypasses component scanning). @ImportResource("classpath:legacy-config.xml"): imports XML configuration files (for migrating legacy Spring XML to Java config). @Import also imports components directly (not just @Configuration).

---

### Q176: Spring Boot Banner?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
ASCII banner shown at startup. Custom banner.txt in src/main/resources. spring.banner.location=classpath:custom-banner.txt. spring.banner.image.location=classpath:banner.png (image to ASCII). Disable: spring.banner.mode=off. Programmatic banner via Banner interface.

---

### Q177: Embedded Server config?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
server.port=8080, server.servlet.context-path=/api. SSL: server.ssl.enabled=true, server.ssl.key-store, key-store-password, key-store-type (PKCS12). Tomcat: server.tomcat.max-threads, max-connections, connection-timeout, accept-count, min-spare-threads. Switch server: exclude Tomcat starter, include Jetty/Undertow starter. Compression: server.compression.enabled=true.

---

### Q178: Spring Session?
**Topic:** Spring Boot
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Distributed session management. @EnableRedisHttpSession stores sessions in Redis. @EnableJdbcHttpSession for database. Eliminates sticky sessions for load-balanced apps. SessionRepositoryFilter intercepts and replaces HttpSession with Spring-managed session. Serialization via JdkSerializationRedisSerializer or Jackson.

---

### Q179: Spring OAuth2?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - Security
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
OAuth2 authorization framework: client (app), resource owner (user), authorization server, resource server. Authorization Code flow (recommended for web apps): (1) User -> login, (2) Redirect to auth server, (3) User approves, callback with code, (4) Server exchanges code for access + refresh tokens, (5) Server uses token to access resources. Spring Security OAuth2 Login (social login) @EnableOAuth2Sso (deprecated, use Spring Security OAuth2 Client module).

---

### Q180: PUT vs PATCH?
**Topic:** Spring Boot - REST
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
PUT: complete resource replacement. Omitted fields set to null/defaults (full update). Idempotent. PATCH: partial update. Only specified fields changed. Not necessarily idempotent. HTTP spec: PUT replaces document, PATCH applies partial modifications described in request body (JSON Patch RFC 6902 or JSON Merge Patch RFC 7396).

## SQL & Databases

### Q181: What is SQL and its types?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
SQL (Structured Query Language) manages relational databases. Types: DDL (CREATE, ALTER, DROP, TRUNCATE) - schema definition. DML (SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE) - data manipulation. DCL (GRANT, REVOKE) - permissions. TCL (COMMIT, ROLLBACK, SAVEPOINT) - transaction control. DQL (SELECT) - data querying.

---

### Q182: Primary Key vs Foreign Key?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Primary Key: uniquely identifies each row. NOT NULL + UNIQUE. One per table. Clustered index by default. Foreign Key: references Primary Key of another table. Enforces referential integrity. Prevents orphan records. ON DELETE CASCADE/SET NULL/RESTRICT actions.

---

### Q183: What are the types of JOINs?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
INNER JOIN: matching rows in both tables. LEFT JOIN: all rows from left + matches from right (NULL for non-matches). RIGHT JOIN: all rows from right + matches from left. FULL OUTER JOIN: all rows from both (NULL for non-matches). CROSS JOIN: Cartesian product. SELF JOIN: table joined with itself (alias required). NATURAL JOIN: auto-joins on same-named columns.

---

### Q184: Normalization forms (1NF, 2NF, 3NF, BCNF)?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1NF: atomic columns (no repeating groups), each cell single value. 2NF: 1NF + all non-key attributes fully functionally dependent on entire primary key (no partial dependency). 3NF: 2NF + no transitive dependency (non-key attribute depends only on PK). BCNF: 3NF + every determinant must be candidate key (stricter). Higher forms: 4NF (multi-valued dependency), 5NF (join dependency). Denormalization for read performance.

---

### Q185: ACID properties?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Atomicity: transaction fully completes or fully rolls back (all or nothing). Consistency: transaction brings database from valid state to valid state (constraints preserved). Isolation: concurrent transactions appear serial (not interfere). Durability: committed transaction persists (survives crashes). RDBMS guarantees ACID (vs NoSQL's BASE - Basically Available, Soft state, Eventually consistent).

---

### Q186: Indexes? Types and when to use?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Clustered index: determines physical order of data rows. One per table. Fastest for range queries. Non-clustered index: separate structure, points to data rows. Multiple allowed. Composite index: multiple columns. Column order matters (leftmost prefix rule). Unique index: ensures uniqueness. Full-text index: text search. Bitmap index: low-cardinality columns. Covering index: includes all needed columns (no table access). B-Tree index: default for most databases.

---

### Q187: EXPLAIN and query execution plan?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
EXPLAIN (or EXPLAIN ANALYZE) shows query execution plan: access method (table scan vs index scan), join algorithm (NLJ, Hash Join, Merge Join), row estimates, actual rows, execution time, sorting method. Use to identify: full table scans (missing indexes), sort operations, temporary tables, table spools. Optimize: add indexes, rewrite queries, use covering indexes.

---

### Q188: Transaction isolation levels?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
READ UNCOMMITTED (level 0): can see uncommitted changes (dirty reads). READ COMMITTED (level 1, default for most): only committed changes (prevents dirty reads, but non-repeatable reads possible). REPEATABLE READ (level 2): same row read twice gives same data (prevents dirty + non-repeatable reads, but phantom reads possible). SERIALIZABLE (level 3): complete isolation, prevents all anomalies. ANSI anomalies: dirty read, non-repeatable read, phantom read, lost update.

---

### Q189: What are database transactions?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Transaction: group of SQL operations executed as single unit. BEGIN TRANSACTION/COMMIT/ROLLBACK. Automatic commit for single statements. Savepoints allow partial rollback within transaction. Benefits: ACID guarantees, error recovery, concurrency control. Use explicit transactions when multiple operations must succeed or fail together.

---

### Q190: N+1 query problem?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1 query to fetch entities + N queries for each entity's relationships. Common with ORMs (Hibernate lazy loading). Example: SELECT * FROM Users (1 query) + SELECT * FROM Orders WHERE user_id=? (N queries for N users). Solutions: JOIN FETCH in JPQL/HQL, EntityGraph (@EntityGraph(attributePaths="orders")), batch fetching (@BatchSize), eager loading (careful).

---

### Q191: Views in SQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Virtual table based on SELECT query. Stores query definition, not data (unless materialized). Uses: security (hide columns), simplify complex queries, data abstraction. CREATE VIEW view_name AS SELECT... Materialized view: stores result physically, better performance for expensive queries, requires refresh.

---

### Q192: Stored Procedures vs Functions?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stored Procedure: can perform transactions, use DML, return multiple result sets, have input/output parameters, cannot be used in SELECT. Function: must return single value/table, can be used in SELECT/WHERE clauses, no transactions, only input parameters. Use procedures for complex business logic, functions for computed columns.

---

### Q193: Subqueries vs CTE vs Temporary Tables?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Subquery: nested query in SELECT/FROM/WHERE. Can be correlated (references outer query) or non-correlated. CTE (WITH clause): named temporary result set within single query. Readable, recursive (WITH RECURSIVE for hierarchies). Temporary table (#temp in SQL Server): physical temp storage, survives across queries in session, can have indexes.

---

### Q194: OLTP vs OLAP?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
OLTP (Online Transaction Processing): many small transactions, normalized schema, row-oriented storage, low latency, high concurrency (INSERT/UPDATE heavy). OLAP (Online Analytical Processing): complex analytical queries, denormalized/snowflake schema, column-oriented storage (compression), aggregations, historical data. OLTP is operational, OLAP is analytical/BI.

---

### Q195: Denormalization?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Intentional redundancy in schema for read performance. Adds duplicate columns to avoid joins. Trade-offs: faster reads, slower writes (update anomalies), more storage, data consistency maintenance complexity. Use when: read-heavy workloads, caching insufficient, complex joins frequent. Often combined with materialized views/summary tables.

---

### Q196: SQL injection and prevention?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SQL injection: attacker inserts malicious SQL via input fields. Example: ' OR 1=1; -- bypasses authentication. Prevention: parameterized queries (PreparedStatement in Java - ? placeholders), stored procedures, input validation/whitelisting, ORM frameworks (JPA/Hibernate handle escaping), least privilege DB user, WAF. NEVER concatenate user input directly into SQL.

---

### Q197: CAP Theorem?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CAP: Consistency (every read gets most recent write), Availability (every request gets non-error response), Partition Tolerance (system works despite network partitions). Can achieve at most 2 of 3. RDBMS: CA (sacrifices partition tolerance). NoSQL: AP (Cassandra, DynamoDB) or CP (HBase, MongoDB). In distributed systems, P is mandatory (partitions happen), so tradeoff is C vs A.

---

### Q198: NoSQL database types?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Document stores (MongoDB, Couchbase): JSON-like documents, schema-less, flexible queries. Key-Value stores (Redis, DynamoDB): simple GET/SET by key, extremely fast, value opaque. Column-family stores (Cassandra, HBase): wide columns, high write throughput, time-series data. Graph databases (Neo4j, Amazon Neptune): nodes + edges, relationships traversals (social networks, recommendations).

---

### Q199: What is Sharding?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Horizontal partitioning of data across multiple database instances. Each shard holds subset of rows based on shard key. Advantages: read/write scaling beyond single server, geo-distribution. Challenges: cross-shard queries (complex), distributed transactions (2PC), resharding/rebalancing, shard key selection crucial (hot spots). Common strategies: hash-based, range-based, directory-based.

---

### Q200: What is Replication?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Copying data from one database server to another. Master-Slave (Primary-Replica): writes to master, reads from slaves. Asynchronous replication (master doesn't wait for slaves - eventual consistency). Synchronous replication (master waits - strong consistency, slower). Multi-master: writes to any node, conflict resolution needed. Use cases: read scaling, high availability, disaster recovery, geographic distribution.

---

### Q201: What is a Deadlock in databases?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Two transactions wait for each other's locks. Transaction A locks row 1, waits for row 2. Transaction B locks row 2, waits for row 1. DB detects via wait-for graph, kills one (deadlock victim). Prevention: consistent lock ordering (always access tables/rows in same order), keep transactions short, use lower isolation levels, index (row vs table locks).

---

### Q202: Window Functions?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Perform calculations across set of rows related to current row (without collapsing rows). Functions: ROW_NUMBER(), RANK(), DENSE_RANK(), NTILE(n) - ranking. LAG(), LEAD() - access previous/next rows. FIRST_VALUE(), LAST_VALUE(), NTH_VALUE() - window frame positions. SUM/AVG/COUNT OVER - moving aggregates. PARTITION BY divides rows into groups. ORDER BY defines order within partition. ROWS/RANGE BETWEEN specifies frame boundaries.

---

### Q203: Query optimization techniques?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Use indexes appropriately (covering indexes for common queries). Avoid SELECT * (fetch only needed columns). Avoid functions in WHERE clauses on indexed columns (WHERE YEAR(date)=2020 prevents index use -> WHERE date >= '2020-01-01'). Use EXISTS instead of IN for subqueries (short-circuits). USE JOIN instead of subqueries where possible. Use UNION ALL instead of UNION (no distinct sort). Use pagination with keyset (WHERE id > last_id) not OFFSET. Monitor slow query log. Analyze execution plans.

---

### Q204: SQL vs NoSQL differences?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SQL (RDBMS): fixed schema, ACID, strong consistency, joins, normalized, vertical scaling, suited for complex transactions. NoSQL: flexible/schema-less, BASE (eventual consistency), horizontal scaling, no joins (denormalized), suited for high volume, unstructured data, real-time web apps. Convergence: NewSQL (CockroachDB, Spanner) offers SQL + horizontal scaling. Polyglot persistence: use both for different needs.

---

### Q205: Database connection pooling?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pool of pre-established DB connections reused by multiple clients. Avoids connection setup overhead (TCP handshake, auth). HikariCP (default Spring Boot): fast, lightweight. Configuration: maximumPoolSize, minimumIdle, connectionTimeout, idleTimeout, maxLifetime, poolName. Pool tuning: monitor active/inactive connections, adjust based on concurrent requests. Too few: request queuing. Too many: resource waste.

---

### Q206: TRUNCATE vs DELETE?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
DELETE: DML, removes rows one by one (row locks), can use WHERE, triggers fire, slower, can rollback, transaction log grows, auto-increment counter NOT reset. TRUNCATE: DDL, deallocates data pages, no WHERE, no triggers, faster, minimally logged (partial rollback), auto-increment counter RESET. TRUNCATE is DDL (can't rollback in some databases).

---

### Q207: What is a Unique Constraint?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Ensures all values in column(s) are distinct. Differs from PRIMARY KEY: allows NULL (single NULL in most DBs), one table can have multiple unique constraints. Creates unique index (for performance). Enforced with unique index.

---

### Q208: What is a Check Constraint?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Ensures column values satisfy boolean expression. CREATE TABLE Employee (Salary DECIMAL CHECK (Salary > 0)). Can reference multiple columns: CHECK (EndDate > StartDate). Maintains data integrity at database level (regardless of application). Not supported by MySQL (ignored in parsing).

---

### Q209: What is UNION vs UNION ALL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
UNION: combines result sets, removes duplicates (uses DISTINCT sort - expensive). UNION ALL: combines all rows (duplicates included, faster). Use UNION ALL unless duplicates must be removed. Column count and data types must match.

---

### Q210: Different BETWEEN and IN?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
BETWEEN: inclusive range check (col BETWEEN 10 AND 20 includes 10 and 20). IN: set membership check (col IN (1,3,5)). BETWEEN is equivalent to col >= 10 AND col <= 20.

---

### Q211: GROUP BY and HAVING?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
GROUP BY: groups rows with same values into summary rows. Used with aggregate functions (COUNT, SUM, AVG, MIN, MAX). HAVING: filter groups (like WHERE for groups). WHERE filters before grouping, HAVING filters after. HAVING can reference aggregate results. ORDER BY after GROUP BY.

---

### Q212: Correlated subquery?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Subquery that references outer query's columns. Executed once for each outer row (can be slow). SELECT e.name, (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM Orders o WHERE o.emp_id = e.id) AS order_count FROM Employees e. EXISTS proven to be efficient (short-circuits). Often rewrite as JOIN for better performance.

---

### Q213: What are Common Table Expressions (CTE)?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
WITH clause creates temporary named result set. Readable, modular, supports recursion. WITH RegionalSales AS (SELECT region, SUM(amount) AS total FROM Sales GROUP BY region) SELECT * FROM RegionalSales WHERE total > 1000. Recursive CTE: WITH RECURSIVE OrgHierarchy AS (base case UNION ALL recursive step). Used for tree/graph traversal (org chart, bill of materials).

---

### Q214: What is a covering index?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Index that contains ALL columns needed by query - query can be satisfied entirely from index without accessing table data (no key lookup/row lookup). Add INCLUDE columns to non-clustered index for covering. CREATE INDEX idx_covering ON Employees (DepartmentID) INCLUDE (Name, Salary). Dramatically improves read query performance. Adds write overhead (index maintenance).

---

### Q215: NULL handling in SQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
NULL = unknown/missing value. IS NULL / IS NOT NULL (not = NULL). Three-valued logic: NULL AND TRUE = NULL, NULL OR TRUE = TRUE. COALESCE(val1, val2, default) returns first non-null. NULLIF(a,b) returns NULL if a=b else a. ISNULL() (SQL Server) / IFNULL() (MySQL). Aggregate functions ignore NULLs (except COUNT(*)). DISTINCT treats NULLs as equal (single NULL in result).

---

### Q216: What is a Composite Key?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Primary key consisting of multiple columns. CREATE TABLE OrderItem (order_id INT, product_id INT, quantity INT, PRIMARY KEY (order_id, product_id)). Column order matters for index performance (leading columns more selective). JPA: @IdClass or @EmbeddedId for composite key mapping.

---

### Q217: What is a Junction/Bridge Table?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Intermediate table for many-to-many relationships. Contains foreign keys to both related tables. student_course(student_id FK, course_id FK). Can have additional columns (enrollment_date, grade). Composite primary key on both FKs.

---

### Q218: Explain Locking in databases?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Shared (S) lock: read lock, multiple transactions can hold simultaneously, no exclusive locks allowed. Exclusive (X) lock: write lock, only one transaction holds, no other locks allowed. Update (U) lock: prevents deadlocks (upgradable shared lock). Intent locks: table-level locks indicating intention to lock at row level (IS, IX, SIX). Row-level vs page-level vs table-level locking. Lock escalation: many row locks -> table lock. Deadlock: detect via wait-for graph, victim chosen for rollback.

---

### Q219: String functions in SQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
UPPER/LOWER (case conversion). LEN/LENGTH (string length). SUBSTRING/SUBSTR (extract portion). TRIM/LTRIM/RTRIM (remove spaces). REPLACE (search and replace). CONCAT (join strings, handles NULL as empty). CHARINDEX/INSTR (find position). LEFT/RIGHT (extract from start/end). REVERSE (reverse string). FORMAT (SQL Server) / TO_CHAR (Oracle/PostgreSQL).

---

### Q220: Date functions?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
GETDATE()/NOW()/CURRENT_TIMESTAMP (current date-time). DATEADD/INTERVAL (add to date). DATEDIFF (difference between dates). DATEPART/EXTRACT (year, month, day). FORMAT/TO_CHAR (format date as string). EOMONTH (last day of month). SYSDATETIME() (higher precision). CAST/CONVERT (date format conversion).

---

### Q221: Optimistic vs Pessimistic locking?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pessimistic: lock data when reading (SELECT FOR UPDATE). Prevents conflicts but reduces concurrency. Best for high contention, frequent updates. Optimistic: no locks, check version/timestamp on update (UPDATE WHERE version = old_version). If version mismatch, retry. Higher concurrency, best for low contention. JPA: @Version annotation for optimistic locking.

---

### Q222: What is a Materialized View?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
View that stores result physically (not just query definition). Improves query performance for expensive aggregations. Requires refresh (ON COMMIT, ON DEMAND, or scheduled). Trade-off: faster reads, stale data (if not refreshed), storage overhead, refresh cost. CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW mv_name AS SELECT ... REFRESH COMPLETE ON DEMAND.

---

### Q223: Partitioning vs Sharding?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Partitioning: splitting table within same database instance. Range (date-range), List (category values), Hash (hash function). Improves query performance (partition elimination), manageability (archive old partitions). Sharding: distributing data across multiple database instances/servers. Horizontal scaling, no single point of failure. Shard key determines distribution. Cross-shard queries need scatter-gather. Partitioning is intra-DB, sharding is inter-DB.

---

### Q224: What are triggers?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stored procedures that automatically execute on INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE. Row-level triggers (FOR EACH ROW) fire once per affected row. Statement-level triggers (FOR EACH STATEMENT) fire once per SQL. BEFORE triggers validate/modify data before write. AFTER triggers for auditing, cascading operations. INSTEAD OF triggers on views. Use cases: auditing, validation, derived columns, integrity enforcement. Caution: hidden logic, performance impact, debugging difficulty.

---

### Q225: What are Cursors in SQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Iterate over query result set row by row. DECLARE CURSOR, OPEN, FETCH NEXT, CLOSE, DEALLOCATE. Types: FORWARD_ONLY (default), SCROLL (backward, random access), STATIC (snapshot), DYNAMIC (reflects changes), KEYSET (unique key based). Performance: slow (row-by-row), use SET-based operations when possible. Alternatives: window functions, recursive CTEs, temp tables.

---

### Q226: Full-Text Search?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Specialized indexing for text content. Supports: word stemming (run -> running), thesaurus, stop words removal, ranking by relevance. CREATE FULLTEXT INDEX ON Articles(Content). Query: CONTAINS(Content, 'database OR "SQL Server"'), FREETEXT (fuzzy). Better than LIKE '%term%' (which can't use indexes, full table scan). Alternatives: Elasticsearch, Solr for advanced search.

---

### Q227: Recursive Queries?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
WITH RECURSIVE CTE for hierarchical data. Structure: anchor member (base case) UNION ALL recursive member (joins CTE). WITH RECURSIVE OrgTree AS (SELECT id, name, manager_id, 0 AS level FROM Employees WHERE manager_id IS NULL UNION ALL SELECT e.id, e.name, e.manager_id, o.level + 1 FROM Employees e JOIN OrgTree o ON e.manager_id = o.id) SELECT * FROM OrgTree.

---

### Q228: Database Security best practices?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Principle of least privilege (read-only accounts for reporting). Parameterized queries (prevent SQL injection). Encrypt sensitive data at rest (TDE) and in transit (SSL/TLS). Regular backups + recovery testing. Audit logging for schema/data changes. Network security: private subnets, security groups, firewalls. Password policies. Encryption: column-level for PII (SSN, credit cards). Data masking for non-production.

---

### Q229: What is ACID compliance in NoSQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Most NoSQL databases sacrifice ACID for scalability/performance. MongoDB: document-level atomicity (multi-document transactions in 4.0+). Cassandra: row-level atomicity (no cross-row transactions). DynamoDB: transaction API (limited, 25 items). BASE (Basically Available, Soft state, Eventual consistency). NewSQL (CockroachDB, YugabyteDB) offers ACID + horizontal scaling via distributed consensus (Raft).

---

### Q230: Database Monitoring?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Metrics to monitor: connection count (idle vs active), query latency (P95/P99), throughput (QPS/TPS), cache hit ratio, disk I/O (read/write latency, IOPS), replication lag, lock waits/deadlocks, buffer pool hit ratio, tempdb usage, long-running queries. Tools: pg_stat_statements (PostgreSQL), sys.dm_exec_query_stats (SQL Server), Performance Schema (MySQL), CloudWatch (RDS), Datadog, New Relic, Prometheus.

---

### Q231: Sequence vs Identity?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Identity: column property (auto-increment). Tied to table. Gaps allowed (rollback consumes identity). Cannot be shared across tables. Sequence (SQL Server 2012+, Oracle, PostgreSQL): database object generating sequential numbers. Not tied to table. Can be shared across tables. More flexible: CACHE, CYCLE, MINVALUE, MAXVALUE, ORDER. Used with DEFAULT NEXT VALUE FOR.

---

### Q232: MongoDB Aggregation Pipeline?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Data processing pipeline similar to Unix pipes. Stages: $match (filter), $group (aggregate), $sort, $project (reshape), $lookup (left outer join), $unwind (deconstruct array), $bucket (histogram), $facet (multiple pipelines), $addFields (new computed fields). db.orders.aggregate([{$match: {status: "completed"}}, {$group: {_id: "$customerId", total: {$sum: "$amount"}}}, {$sort: {total: -1}}]).

---

### Q233: Redis data structures?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
String: simple key-value (SET, GET). List: ordered, duplicates (LPUSH, RPUSH, LPOP, LRANGE). Set: unordered, unique (SADD, SMEMBERS, SINTER, SUNION). Sorted Set: ordered by score (ZADD, ZRANGEBYSCORE, ZRANK). Hash: field-value pairs (HSET, HGET, HGETALL). Bitmap: bit operations (SETBIT, BITCOUNT). HyperLogLog: cardinality estimation (PFADD, PFCOUNT). Geospatial: (GEOADD, GEORADIUS). Stream: log/timeline (XADD, XREAD). Expiration: TTL, EXPIRE.

---

### Q234: Cassandra data model?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Wide-column store. Keyspace (like database). Table: columns with clustering order. Primary key = Partition key (determines node, single or composite) + Clustering columns (within-partition sort order). Denormalized, query-driven design (write tables for specific queries, not normalized like RDBMS). CQL (Cassandra Query Language) similar to SQL. Consistency level: ONE, QUORUM, ALL, LOCAL_QUORUM. Tunable consistency per query.

---

### Q235: Elasticsearch?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Distributed search and analytics engine. Document-oriented (JSON). Inverted index for full-text search. REST API. Index (like database), Type (deprecated), Document (like row). Sharding (horizontal scaling), Replication (HA). Near real-time search. Analyzer: tokenizer + filters (lowercase, stop words, stemmer). Aggregations: bucketing (term, date histogram), metrics (avg, sum). Use cases: log analytics (ELK stack), full-text search, application monitoring.

---

### Q236: HBase architecture?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Column-family NoSQL (on HDFS/Hadoop). HMaster: manages region assignment, DDL operations. RegionServer: serves read/write for regions. Region: contiguous range of rows (sorted by row key). MemStore: in-memory write buffer (sorted by column family). HFile: on-disk sorted file (immutable). Write-Ahead Log (WAL): for durability. Bloom filters: skip files without row key. Row key design crucial for performance (hotspot avoidance via salting, hashing).

---

### Q237: DynamoDB concepts?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
AWS managed NoSQL (key-value + document). Tables, Items, Attributes. Primary key: Partition key (simple) or Partition + Sort key (composite). LSI (Local Secondary Index): same partition key, different sort key. GSI (Global Secondary Index): different partition key. RCU (Read Capacity Units): eventually consistent (1 RCU = 8KB/s), strongly consistent (1 RCU = 4KB/s). WCU (Write Capacity Units): 1 WCU = 1KB/s. DAX (DynamoDB Accelerator): in-memory cache. Auto scaling. On-demand vs provisioned capacity.

---

### Q238: Database Backup strategies?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Full backup: complete database (slow, large). Differential backup: changes since last full backup. Transaction log backup: point-in-time recovery (frequent). Recovery Point Objective (RPO): acceptable data loss. Recovery Time Objective (RTO): acceptable downtime. Strategy: weekly full + daily differential + hourly log. Test restores regularly. Off-site backup (geographic redundancy). Immutable backups (ransomware protection).

---

### Q239: What is Connection Leak?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Application fails to close database connections. Connection pool connections become active indefinitely. Eventually pool exhausted -> no new connections -> application hangs/crashes. Causes: unclosed ResultSet/Statement in try-catch, exception without finally cleanup, connection returned but not closed. Prevention: always use try-with-resources (Java), connection pool with leak detection (HikariCP leakDetectionThreshold), monitoring active connections.

---

### Q240: Query Plan Analysis?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Execution plan operations: Table Scan (full table - bad, missing index), Index Seek (efficient, O(log n)), Index Scan (scans entire index - okay for covering queries), Key Lookup (non-clustered to clustered index - expensive), RID Lookup (heap lookup), Sort (expensive, consider index ordering), Hash Match (large joins), Nested Loops (small tables/joins), Merge Join (sorted inputs). STATISTICS IO (logical/physical reads). Missing index suggestions. Actual vs estimated rows. Parameter sniffing issues.

---

### Q241: PostgreSQL vs MySQL?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
PostgreSQL: advanced features (CTE, window functions, full-text search, GiST/GIN indexes, JSONB, array types, table inheritance, partial indexes, exclusion constraints), ACID compliant (MVCC), extensible (custom functions, data types), licensing (open, no vendor lock). MySQL: simpler, faster replication, more intuitive (for basic use), wider hosting support, InnoDB (default engine, ACID compliant). PostgreSQL stronger for complex queries, GIS (PostGIS), analytical workloads. MySQL for simpler CRUD, high-read workloads.

---

### Q242: Database migration strategies?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Phased (Strangler Fig): gradually migrate functionality, both old and new systems run in parallel. Blue-Green: two identical environments, switch traffic. Rolling: migrate shards/partitions one by one. Zero-downtime: create replica, sync, cutover. ETL: extract-transform-load in batches. CDC (Change Data Capture): streaming changes. Schema migration tools: Flyway, Liquibase (version-controlled). Rollback planning always required. Data validation post-migration.

---

### Q243: What is Connection String?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
String specifying database connection parameters: Server=myServer;Database=myDB;User Id=myUser;Password=myPass;. Contains: server host/port, database name, credentials, additional options (SSL, timeout, pooling, encryption). Best practice: store in config files/environment variables (not in code). Use managed identities/connection strings in production (Azure SQL, RDS).

---

### Q244: What is Connection Pool starvation?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
All connections in pool are in use, new requests wait for connection release. Causes: long-running queries without proper timeout, connection leaks, higher concurrency than pool size. Symptoms: increased response times, timeouts, thread starvation (Tomcat threads blocked waiting). Solutions: optimize pool size (monitor active/idle), optimize queries, use async DB access, set query timeouts, monitor pool metrics.

---

### Q245: SQL vs ORM (JPA/Hibernate)?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SQL: direct DB access, full control, optimized queries, DB-specific features, lower abstraction. ORM: object-relational mapping, reduces boilerplate (CRUD), caching, lazy loading, database portability, less error-prone (type safety). Trade-offs: ORM can generate inefficient queries (N+1, cartesian product), learning curve (cache, flush modes, session management), complex queries better in SQL. Best practice: ORM for CRUD, native SQL/JPA @Query for complex queries.

---

### Q246: Polyglot Persistence?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Using multiple database types within same application based on data requirements. Examples: PostgreSQL (relational/transactions), Redis (cache/sessions), MongoDB (documents/flexible schema), Elasticsearch (full-text search), Neo4j (graph/relationships), Cassandra (time-series/high write). Each database optimized for specific workload. Complexity: more operational overhead, data synchronization, distributed transactions.

---

### Q247: Functional Dependency?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Attribute Y is functionally dependent on X if each X value determines exactly one Y value. X -> Y. Full functional dependency: Y depends on entire composite X (not subset). Partial dependency: Y depends on subset of composite X (violates 2NF). Transitive dependency: X -> Y -> Z, so X -> Z indirectly (violates 3NF). Trivial dependency: X -> X (always true).

---

### Q248: Temporal Tables?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
System-versioned temporal tables: automatically track data history (SQL Server 2016+, PostgreSQL with extensions). Period columns: SysStartTime, SysEndTime. All changes create new version row in history table. Query: SELECT * FROM Employee FOR SYSTEM_TIME BETWEEN '2020-01-01' AND '2020-12-31'. Use cases: auditing, point-in-time analysis, compliance.

---

### Q249: Graph Databases?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Data as nodes (entities) and edges (relationships). Native graph: Neo4j (Cypher query language). SQL Server: graph tables (NODE, EDGE). Use cases: social networks (friendship), recommendation engines (users-purchased-products), fraud detection (transaction patterns), knowledge graphs, IT networks, logistics/routing (shortest path). Property graph model: nodes with labels and properties, edges with type and direction.

---

### Q250: Database-as-a-Service (DBaaS)?
**Topic:** SQL & Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Managed cloud database services: AWS RDS (MySQL, PostgreSQL, SQL Server, Oracle, MariaDB), Azure SQL Database, Google Cloud SQL, MongoDB Atlas, DynamoDB. Benefits: automated backups, patching, replication, scaling, monitoring, HA (multi-AZ), DR (cross-region). Trade-offs: limited DB configuration, vendor lock-in, cost at scale. Serverless options: Aurora Serverless, Azure SQL Serverless.

## System Design

### Q371: What is System Design?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Process of defining architecture, components, modules, interfaces, and data for a system to satisfy specified requirements. Two levels: LLD (Low-Level Design) - class diagrams, method signatures, algorithms. HLD (High-Level Design) - system architecture, components, data flow, technology choices. Covers: scalability, reliability, availability, performance, security, maintainability.

---

### Q372: Design a URL Shortener (like TinyURL)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** shorten long URLs, redirect, analytics (clicks, referrers), expiration. **HLD:** API: POST /shorten (returns short URL), GET /{shortCode} (redirect 301). **Encoding:** Base62 (a-zA-Z0-9) for 6-7 char codes. **Storage:** Key-Value store (DynamoDB/Cassandra) for <shortCode, longURL>. **Cache:** Redis for hot URLs. **Generation:** counter (distributed sequence like Snowflake) or hash (MD5/SHA1 first N chars + collision check). **Redirection:** 301 Moved Permanently (permanent, cached by browsers). **Scaling:** consistent hashing for DB sharding, CDN for geodistribution.

---

### Q373: Design a Rate Limiter?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Algorithms:** Token Bucket (tokens refill at rate), Leaky Bucket (queue with rate), Sliding Window Log (timestamp log per user), Sliding Window Counter (counters per time window). **Distributed:** Redis sorted sets (ZREMRANGEBYSCORE for window, ZCARD for count) or Lua scripts for atomicity. **Response:** 429 Too Many Requests, Retry-After header. **Rules:** per user, per API, per endpoint. Rate limiting in API Gateway (Kong, Envoy) or middleware.

---

### Q374: Design a Chat System (WhatsApp)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** 1-on-1 chat, group chat, online status, delivery/read receipts, media sharing, E2E encryption. **Architecture:** WebSocket for real-time bidirectional communication. **Connection Handler:** maintains user <-> WebSocket mapping. **Message Service:** receives, persists, routes messages. **Group Service:** fanout (send to all group members). **Storage:** Messages - Cassandra (time-series, high write). Media - Blob store (S3). Metadata - MySQL (user profiles, groups). **Delivery:** offline messages stored, push notification (APNs/FCM) sent when user comes online. **E2E Encryption:** Signal Protocol (X3DH for key agreement, Double Ratchet for message keys). Each message encrypted per-device.

---

### Q375: Design a News Feed (Facebook)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** Infinite scroll, personalized ranking, low latency. **Approaches:** Push (fanout on write): when user posts, pre-compute feed for each follower. Pull (fanout on read): fetch and merge posts from friends on request. Hybrid: push for active users (lots of followers), pull for celebrities. **Ranking:** ML model scores posts based on recency, affinity (closeness to poster), engagement (likes/comments from friends), content type (photo > text). **Storage:** Feed pre-computed in Redis lists (per user). Posts in Cassandra (sharded by author_id). Social graph in Neo4j/MySQL. **Caching:** Feed cache in Redis, post cache in Memcached.

---

### Q376: Design a Distributed Cache?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Data Distribution:** Consistent Hashing (minimize rehashing on node add/remove). Virtual nodes for load balancing. **Replication:** Each key stored on N nodes (quorum-based replication). **Consistency:** Read-Repair, Hinted Handoff for eventual consistency. **Eviction:** LRU, LFU, TTL-based. **Operations:** GET(key), SET(key, value, ttl). **Cluster:** Gossip protocol for node discovery. Failure detection via Phi Accrual (adaptive heartbeat). **Wire protocol:** RESP (Redis). **Use:** cache-aside (check cache, if miss read DB, write cache). Cache-through.

---

### Q377: Design a Database (Distributed Key-Value)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Inspired by DynamoDB/Cassandra. **Partitioning:** Consistent hashing with virtual nodes. **Replication:** N copies per key (replication factor). W = write quorum (need W acks), R = read quorum (need R responses). **Conflict Resolution:** Last-Write-Wins (LWW) based on timestamp/vector clock. **Gossip:** Peer-to-peer, each node exchanges state periodically (heartbeats, partition info). **Hinted Handoff:** if replica unreachable, temp store data on another node. **Read Repair:** on read, update stale replicas. **Anti-Entropy:** Merkle tree-based sync for consistency.

---

### Q378: Design a File Storage System (Google Drive)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Client:** desktop/mobile/web app. **API:** upload, download, delete, share, list, search. **Upload:** chunked upload (parallel, resumable). **Storage:** Object storage (S3/Azure Blob). **Metadata:** SQL database for file metadata, user data, sharing permissions. **Transactions:** for rename/move operations. **File versioning:** delta sync (upload only changed chunks), deduplication (hash-based - same content stored once). **CDN:** for file download (thumbnails, previews). **Search:** Elasticsearch for full-text search (OCR on images, text extraction). **Caching:** CDN for reads, Redis for directory listings.

---

### Q379: Design a Messaging Queue (Kafka-like)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Components:** Producer (publishes messages), Broker (stores), Consumer (reads), Topic (category), Partition (ordered immutable log). **Data Model:** Log (append-only, sequential writes). Each message has offset (unique position). **Partitioning:** messages hashed to partition by key. Enables parallelism (one consumer per partition). **Replication:** each partition replicated to N brokers (leader-follower). Leader handles reads/writes. ISR (In-Sync Replicas) set. **Storage:** Segment files on disk, rolled by time/size. Index files for efficient offset lookup. PageCache used for read buffering (zero-copy sendfile). **Consumer Groups:** each partition consumed by one consumer in group. Exactly-once semantics via transactions and idempotent producers. **Use:** event sourcing, log aggregation, stream processing.

---

### Q380: Design a CDN (Content Delivery Network)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Purpose:** serve static/dynamic content from edge locations close to users (reduce latency, offload origin). **Components:** Origin server (source), Edge/PoP servers (cached copies), DNS routing to nearest edge. **Caching strategies:** Push CDN (manually upload content), Pull CDN (cache on first request). **Cache invalidation:** TTL-based, purge API, versioned URLs (immutable content). **Routing:** GeoDNS (different A records by geography), Anycast (same IP, routed to nearest PoP via BGP). **Dynamic content:** Edge computing (Lambda@Edge, Cloudflare Workers) for personalization. **Security:** DDoS protection, WAF, HTTPS termination.

---

### Q381: Design a Web Crawler?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**URL Frontier:** queue of URLs to crawl. Prioritize (news sites first). Politely crawl (respect robots.txt, crawl delay). **Fetch:** HTTP client with headless browser (for JS-rendered pages). **Parse:** extract links, metadata, content. **Deduplication:** Bloom filter/BitSet for visited URLs (efficient, small false positive). **Storage:** Raw HTML (compressed, S3), extracted text (Elasticsearch for indexing), links graph (HDFS for analysis). **Scaling:** workers partitioned by URL hash. Message queue (Kafka) between stages. **Politeness:** per-domain crawl delay, parallel requests to different domains.

---

### Q382: Design a Recommendation System?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Approaches:** Collaborative Filtering (users with similar taste), Content-Based (similar items), Matrix Factorization (SVD, ALS), Deep Learning (NCF, Two-Tower). **Pipeline:** Data collection (user actions, item features) -> Feature engineering -> Model training -> Serving. **Offline:** batch compute recommendations nightly (MapReduce/Spark). **Online:** real-time scoring of candidate items (50->1000 candidates) -> ranking ML model (GBDT/DNN) -> prune -> serve. **Storage:** item features (Redis), user embeddings (KV store), user history (Cassandra). **Cold Start:** popularity-based for new users, content-based for new items.

---

### Q383: What is CAP Theorem?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
In a distributed system, you can only achieve 2 of 3 guarantees: Consistency (every read returns most recent write), Availability (every request receives a response), Partition Tolerance (system continues despite network partitions). Since network partitions are inevitable in distributed systems (P must be chosen), the tradeoff is between C and A. CA systems (RDBMS) give up P (single node). CP systems (HBase, MongoDB) give up A (reject writes during partition). AP systems (Cassandra, DynamoDB) give up C (eventual consistency).

---

### Q384: What is ACID vs BASE?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**ACID:** Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, Durability. Traditional RDBMS property. Strong consistency. **BASE:** Basically Available, Soft state, Eventually consistent. NoSQL property. Availability and Partition tolerance prioritized over consistency. Trade-off: sacrifice immediate consistency for scalability and availability. BASE systems relax consistency constraints, allowing temporary inconsistency that resolves over time.

---

### Q385: Design Patterns - Singleton?
