**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Ensures class has only one instance globally. Java: private constructor + static getInstance(). Thread-safe: double-checked locking (volatile) or static inner class (Bill Pugh). Enum singleton (best for serialization safety). Use: logging, configuration, connection pools, caches.

---

### Q386: Factory Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Creates objects without exposing instantiation logic. Factory Method: subclass decides which class to instantiate. Abstract Factory: factory of factories, creates families of related objects. Use: DB connection (JDBC driver manager), UI component creation parsers.

---

### Q387: Builder Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Separates complex object construction from representation. Fluent API: builder.withName("x").withAge(25).build(). Used when an object has many optional parameters (instead of telescoping constructors). Immutable objects with Builder pattern.

---

### Q388: Observer Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
One-to-many dependency: when subject changes state, all observers notified. Java: Observable (deprecated), PropertyChangeListener. Event-driven programming: GUI events, message queues, pub-sub systems. Loose coupling: subject doesn't know observer details.

---

### Q389: Strategy Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Defines family of algorithms, encapsulates each, makes them interchangeable. Client chooses strategy at runtime. Example: Payment processing (CreditCard, PayPal, Crypto strategies). Sorting (merge vs quick vs heap). Avoids if-else chains.

---

### Q390: Decorator Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Design Patterns
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Adds behavior to objects dynamically without modifying class. Wraps object with decorator class having same interface. Example: Java IO (BufferedReader wraps FileReader). Coffee shop: Base coffee + milk decorator + sugar decorator.

---

### Q391: What is Sharding / Horizontal Partitioning?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Splitting database across multiple servers. Shard key determines which server stores each row. Strategies: Range-based (by ID range), Hash-based (hash(shard_key) % N), Directory-based (lookup table). Challenges: cross-shard queries, joins, transactions, resharding, hotspotting (uneven load). Consistent hashing minimizes reshuffling on rebalancing.

---

### Q392: What is Consistent Hashing?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hash ring: nodes and keys placed on same ring. Key assigned to nearest clockwise node. When node added/removed, only keys in that range move (not all keys). Virtual nodes (multiple positions per physical node) improve load balancing. Used in DynamoDB, Cassandra, Discord.

---

### Q393: Caching Strategies?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Cache-Aside: app checks cache, on miss loads from DB and sets cache. Read-Through: cache layer is authoritative, loads on miss. Write-Through: write to cache first, then to DB. Write-Behind (Write-Back): write to cache, async write to DB. Refresh-Ahead: cache proactively refreshes before TTL expiry. Cache eviction: LRU, LFU, FIFO, TTL.

---

### Q394: Load Balancing algorithms?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Round Robin: sequential distribution (simple, ignores load). Least Connections: route to server with fewest active connections. IP Hash: hash of client IP to specific server (session stickiness). Weighted Round Robin: different weights per server. Least Response Time: fastest responding server. Random: simple, statistically even. Application-aware: based on request characteristics.

---

### Q395: Database Indexing strategies for performance?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Clustered index on primary key (data sorted physically). Covering index (include all needed columns). Composite index (column order matters - leftmost prefix rule). Partial index (WHERE clause conditions). Index on foreign keys (join performance). Expression/function-based indexes. Avoid: too many indexes (write slowdown), unused indexes, wide indexes. Monitor index usage. Use covering indexes for frequent queries.

---

### Q396: Microservices vs Monolith?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Monolith:** single deployable unit. Pros: simple, fast communication (in-process), ACID transactions, easy testing, minimal overhead. Cons: scaling (scale all or nothing), tech lock-in, deployment coupling, onboarding complexity. **Microservices:** independent services. Pros: independent scaling/deployment, technology diversity, team autonomy, fault isolation. Cons: network overhead, distributed transactions (Saga, 2PC), operational complexity, eventual consistency, testing difficulty (contract testing).

---

### Q397: What is Event Sourcing?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Store changes as sequence of events (not current state). Event store is append-only log. Current state = replay all events. Benefits: complete audit trail, temporal queries (state at any point), event-driven architecture, debugging. Challenges: event schema evolution, replay performance, eventual consistency, CQRS required (separate read model). Used in financial systems, version control, collaboration tools.

---

### Q398: CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Separate read and write models. Commands (writes): validate, process, store in event store. Queries (reads): pre-computed projections/denormalized views. Benefits: independent scaling (read replicas, write masters), optimized read models (different storage for reads), security separation. Challenges: eventual consistency (write-to-read lag), complexity. Often combined with Event Sourcing.

---

### Q399: SQL vs NoSQL design considerations?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Choose SQL when:** strong consistency required, ACID transactions, complex joins/analytical queries, well-defined schema, relationships critical, reporting needs. **Choose NoSQL when:** high scalability/horizontal scaling, flexible schema, high write throughput, massive data volumes, simple key-based access, eventual consistency acceptable, time-series/messaging. Polyglot persistence: use multiple DB types within same system.

---

### Q400: What is Idempotency?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Operation produces same result regardless of how many times executed. Important for payment (charging twice). Implementation: idempotency keys (client sends unique key, server deduplicates), idempotent APIs (PUT instead of POST, conditional updates). Use unique request IDs, check DUP before processing.

---

### Q401: What is a Blob (Binary Large Object) Store?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Storage for unstructured binary data: images, videos, documents, backups. Examples: S3 (AWS), Azure Blob Storage, Google Cloud Storage. Features: unlimited scale, durability (99.999999999%), lifecycle management, versioning, encryption at rest/in transit, access control (IAM, signed URLs), CDN integration. Keys: bucket + object key + version ID.

---

### Q402: Design a Notification Service?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Types:** Email, SMS, Push (APNs for iOS, FCM for Android), In-app. **Architecture:** Notification API receives request (type, recipient, content). Message queue (Kafka/RabbitMQ) buffers notifications. Workers process each type: Email (SendGrid/Mailgun), SMS (Twilio/Amazon SNS), Push (FCM/APNs). **Template Service:** manages notification templates (with variables). **Preference Service:** user notification preferences (what/where/when). **Rate Limiter:** per-user, per-type throttle. **Delivery tracking:** open rates, click rates. **Multi-channel:** if email fails, try SMS.

---

### Q403: Design a Payment System?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Components:** Payment Gateway (authorizes/n captures), Payment Processor (routes to bank), Payment Service Provider (Stripe/Square - full stack). **Flow:** User initiates payment -> Payment Service creates transaction -> redirect to gateway -> user enters card details -> gateway sends to processor -> processor routes to issuing bank -> auth/n approved -> response sent back -> confirmation. **Key concerns:** idempotency (prevent double charge), reconciliation, refunds, chargebacks, fraud detection. **Storage:** transaction log (append-only, immutable), ledger (double-entry accounting). **Security:** PCI-DSS compliance, tokenization (replacing card PANs with tokens), encryption.

---

### Q404: What is a Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Queue that stores messages that couldn't be processed (max retries exceeded, processing error, TTL expired). Allows analysis of failed messages without losing them. Monitoring DLQ size alerts on systemic failures. Can reprocess after fixes. Used in message queues (SQS, RabbitMQ, Kafka) and workflow systems.

---

### Q405: What is SLA, SLO, SLI?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SLI (Service Level Indicator): actual measured metric (latency P99, error rate, uptime). SLO (Service Level Objective): target value for SLI (99.9% uptime, P99 < 200ms). SLA (Service Level Agreement): contractual commitment with consequences (credits, penalties) if SLO not met. Error budget: allowable downtime (1 - SLO). Burn rate: how fast error budget consumed.

---

### Q406: Design a Search Autocomplete System?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** fast (sub-100ms), relevant, support partial matches, handle typos. **Data Structure:** Trie (prefix tree) with frequency counters. Compressed Trie (Radix Tree) for memory. **Backend:** batch compute top N queries per prefix from logs (MapReduce). Store in distributed Trie (sharded by prefix). **Caching:** Redis for hot prefixes. Browser-side caching (localStorage for recent). **Ranking:** by frequency, recency, user personalization. **Fallback:** if no results, fuzzy matching (Levenshtein distance, Soundex).

---

### Q407: Design a Video Streaming Platform (YouTube)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Upload:** chunked upload to blob storage. **Transcoding:** video processing pipeline (FFmpeg) to generate multiple resolutions (360p, 720p, 1080p, 4K), formats (H.264, H.265, VP9), segments (DASH/HLS for adaptive bitrate). **CDN:** edge caching for popular videos. **MetaData:** MySQL for video metadata, Cassandra for views. **Recommendation:** ML model based on viewing history, collaborative filtering. **Comments:** real-time service with moderation. **Search:** Elasticsearch. **Thumbnails:** generated at various timestamps. **Live streaming:** RTMP/WebRTC ingest, HLS output via media server.

---

### Q408: Design a Distributed ID Generator (Snowflake)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Twitter Snowflake ID: 64-bit long. 1 bit (sign, always 0) + 41 bits (millisecond timestamp, 69 years) + 10 bits (worker ID, 1024 nodes) + 12 bits (sequence per ms, 4096 IDs). Generates ~4M IDs/sec per worker. No coordination needed (worker ID assigned at startup). ID monotonically increasing. Alternative: database sequence (bottleneck), UUID (128-bit, not sortable), Redis INCR.

---

### Q409: What is a Service Mesh?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Infrastructure layer for service-to-service communication. Sidecar proxy (Envoy, Linkerd) alongside each service handles: service discovery, load balancing, traffic routing, circuit breaking, retries, metrics, tracing, mTLS encryption. Control plane (Istio, Consul) manages proxy configuration. Decouples communication logic from application code. Kubernetes-native deployment.

---

### Q410: WebSockets vs Server-Sent Events (SSE) vs Polling?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Polling: client repeatedly requests server. Simple but inefficient (many empty responses). SSE: server pushes to client over HTTP. Unidirectional server->client. Simpler than WebSockets. Auto-reconnect. WebSockets: full-duplex bidirectional over single TCP connection. Low latency. Use WebSockets for real-time chat/games. Use SSE for notifications/streams. Use polling for simple periodic updates.

---

### Q411: What is a Write-Ahead Log (WAL)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Before applying changes to data pages, write them to append-only log. Enables crash recovery: after crash, replay WAL to restore consistent state. Used in PostgreSQL, MySQL (InnoDB), Cassandra, Kafka. Atomicity: all changes from transaction present or none. Durability: WAL on stable storage means committed data survives crash.

---

### Q412: Two-Phase Commit (2PC)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Distributed transaction protocol across multiple nodes. Phase 1 (Prepare): coordinator asks all participants to prepare (vote Yes or No). Phase 2 (Commit): if all Yes, coordinator sends commit; if any No, sends abort. Blocking protocol: if coordinator crashes after prepare, participants wait (hold locks). Alternatives: Saga (compensating transactions), Three-Phase Commit (3PC), TCC (Try-Confirm/Cancel).

---

### Q413: Saga Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Managing distributed transactions in microservices. Each transaction has compensating action for rollback. Choreography: services emit events, each service processes and emits next event (no coordinator). Orchestration: coordinator (SagaExecutionCoordinator) tells each service what to do, handles failures. Example: Order saga - CreateOrder, ReserveCredit (compensate: ReleaseCredit), ShipOrder (compensate: CancelShipment). Eventual consistency.

---

### Q414: Design a Ticket Booking System (BookMyShow)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Concurrency:** multiple users booking same seats. Use row-level locking (SELECT FOR UPDATE), optimistic locking with version, or Redis distributed lock (Redlock). **Service:** Show (movie + theater + time), Seat layout (seat types, availability), Booking (reserve, hold, expire), Payment. **Seat hold:** temporary reservation (10 min TTL) while user pays. Timeout -> seats released. **Optimistic:** blocked seat visualization in near-real-time via WebSocket/SSE. **Database:** partition by city/theater. Read replicas for browsing. Redis for seat availability (fast reads).

---

### Q415: Scalability: Vertical vs Horizontal?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Vertical (Scale Up): bigger server (more CPU, RAM, SSD). Limited by hardware max. Simple, no architectural changes. Expensive at high end. Horizontal (Scale Out): more servers. Virtually unlimited. Requires load balancer, distributed data, eventual consistency. More cost-effective. Modern systems designed for horizontal scaling. Stateless services for easy horizontal scaling.

---

### Q416: What is a Bloom Filter?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Probabilistic data structure for set membership. Uses bit array + multiple hash functions. add(x): hash x with k functions, set k bits. contains(x): check k bits - if any 0 -> definitely NOT. If all 1 -> MAYBE (false positive possible, false negative impossible). Space-efficient (1% false positive rate at ~10 bits per element). Use: cache filtering (prevent cache miss storms), URL deduplication in crawlers, spell checkers, early termination of expensive DB queries.

---

### Q417: What is a Merkle Tree (Hash Tree)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Binary tree where leaf nodes are data hashes, internal nodes are hashes of children. Root hash represents entire dataset. Efficient comparison: compare root hash (O(1)). For difference, walk down tree to find differing leaves (O(log n)). Used in: Git (content verification), Bitcoin (transaction integrity), Cassandra/DynamoDB (anti-entropy), Certificate Transparency. Efficient for large dataset comparison.

---

### Q418: Distributed Consensus (Raft/Paxos)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Algorithms for agreeing on values in distributed systems. **Raft:** leader election (terms, heartbeats), log replication (leader sends entries to followers, majority commit), safety (election restriction prevents outdated leaders). More understandable than Paxos. **Paxos:** quorum-based, roles (proposer, acceptor, learner). Multiple phases (prepare/promise, propose/accept). Used in: etcd (Raft), Consul (Raft), ZooKeeper (Zab), Google Chubby (Paxos), Spanner (Paxos).

---

### Q419: What is Chaos Engineering?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Practice of experimenting on system to build confidence in its ability to withstand turbulent conditions. Intentionally inject failures (kill services, network latency, resource exhaustion) in controlled production-like environment. Principles: Define steady state, hypothesize will sustain, vary real-world events, run experiments in production, automate continuously. Tools: Chaos Monkey (Netflix), Gremlin, Litmus.

---

### Q420: Design a Ride-Sharing System (Uber)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Components:** Rider App, Driver App, Location Service, Ride Matching, Pricing, Payment, Trip Management. **Location:** Driver sends GPS coordinates every 3-4 seconds. Geohashing (Z-order curve) indexed in Redis for efficient nearby driver queries. **Matching:** rider's pickup location -> query nearby drivers (geohash prefix) -> filter (availability, rating, direction) -> find best (closest ETA, surge pricing). **Pricing:** dynamic (surge) based on demand/supply ratio, traffic, events. **Routing:** OSRM/GrapHopper for route calculation and ETA. **Trip:** real-time tracking via WebSocket. **Fare calculation:** base + distance + time + surge. **Payments:** prepaid/wallet, split, payment gateway.

---

### Q421: What is Multi-Tenancy?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Single software instance serving multiple tenants (customers). Isolation levels: Database per tenant (strong isolation, more cost), Schema per tenant (shared DB, separate schemas), Table per tenant (shared schema, tenant_id column - simplest, least isolation). Considerations: tenant isolation, per-tenant customization, tenant-specific scaling, data migration. Row-level security (RLS) policies.

---

### Q422: What is the difference between REST and GraphQL?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**REST:** multiple endpoints (GET/users, GET/users/:id), server-defined response shape, over-fetching/under-fetching. **GraphQL:** single endpoint (/graphql), client specifies exactly what data needed (query { user(id: 1) { name email } }), type system (schema), resolver for each field, batch loading (DataLoader to solve N+1). Trade-offs: GraphQL complexity (resolver performance, caching complexity), REST simplicity (HTTP caching, stateless). Use REST for simple CRUD APIs, GraphQL for complex data requirements (feeds, dashboards).

---

### Q423: Data Consistency Models?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Strong Consistency: after write completes, all subsequent reads see it. Linearizability (single-copy). Use in financial systems. Use Paxos/Raft. Eventual Consistency: if no new writes, all replicas converge to same state eventually. Use in DNS, CDN. Causal Consistency: related events seen in order, unrelated events may not. Read-Your-Writes: user always sees own writes. Monotonic Reads: after reading value, subsequent reads return same or newer.

---

### Q424: What is Back-of-the-Envelope Calculation?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Approximate capacity estimation for system design. Key numbers: 1M requests/sec on modern server. Memory: hashmap 1M entries ~ 50MB. CPU: SSD ~ 100K IOPS, HDD ~ 100 IOPS. Network: 1 Gbps ~ 125 MB/s. Storage: 1TB HDD ~ $50, 1TB SSD ~ $100. Latency: L1 cache 0.5ns, L2 7ns, RAM 100ns, SSD 10-100us, HDD 5-10ms, network within DC 0.5ms, cross-continent 50-100ms. Daily active users: estimate 10M DAU. Reads per user: 100/day. Total read QPS: 10M * 100 / (24*3600) = ~11,574 QPS.

---

### Q425: Design a Proximity Service (Nearby Places)?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** find nearby places (restaurants, gas stations) within radius. **Approaches:** Geohash (grid-based Z-order index), QuadTree (spatial index), Google S2/HLI (Hilbert curve). **Geohash:** encode lat/lng into base32 string. Prefix match for nearby. Geohash precision: 5 chars ~ 5km, 6 chars ~ 1km. Inefficient at boundaries (grid cells). **Redis Geo:** GEOADD, GEORADIUS (geohash-based, efficient). **DB:** PostgreSQL + PostGIS (GiST index on geography column). Geospatial queries: near (ORDER BY distance LIMIT 20), within (ST_DWithin). **Caching:** reverse geocode (lat/lng -> place list) results cached.

---

### Q426: Design a Leaderboard System?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Requirements:** real-time ranking, top N, user rank, tie-breaking. **Simple (small scale):** sorted set (Redis ZADD/ZREVRANGE/ZRANK). O(log n) per update. **Large scale:** approximate leaderboard (count-min sketch, t-digest for quantiles). Batch update (hourly). Multiple leaderboards: global, friends, regional, time periods (daily/weekly/all-time). Periodic reset: rename sorted set, keep old for reference. **Ranking:** score + timestamp (for ties: earlier timestamp higher rank).

---

### Q427: What are Micro Frontends?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Extending microservices principles to frontend. Each team owns a vertical slice (frontend + backend). Integration approaches: iframes (simple but limited), Web Components (standards-based), Module Federation (Webpack 5 - share modules at runtime), Single SPA (router-based composition). Benefits: independent deployment, team autonomy, gradual migration. Challenges: common UI consistency, performance (duplicate dependencies), shared state between micro frontends.

---

### Q428: Design a Distributed Lock?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
**Redis:** SET key value NX EX 30 (atomic create + TTL). Redlock: acquire lock on majority (5/3) of Redis nodes. **ZooKeeper:** ephemeral sequential nodes, watch events for lock release. **Database:** SELECT FOR UPDATE (pessimistic). **Considerations:** deadlock detection (lock timeout), reentrancy, lease renewal, fencing tokens (increment token on each lock, reject stale writes). For most cases, Redis lock with TTL sufficient.

---

### Q429: What is a Sidecar Pattern?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Co-located helper container sharing same pod/host with main application. Extends functionality without modifying main code. Examples: Envoy sidecar (service mesh), logging agent (Filebeat), config reloader, secrets provider. Benefits: language-agnostic, independent lifecycle, reuse across services. Drawbacks: added latency (proxy overhead), resource consumption.

---

### Q430: Design a Logging and Monitoring System?
**Topic:** System Design - HLD
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
**Logging:** agents (Filebeat/Fluentd) collect logs -> Kafka (buffering) -> Logstash (parse/transform) -> Elasticsearch (index) -> Kibana (visualize). ELK stack. Structured logging (JSON) for searchability. **Metrics:** Prometheus scrapes metrics endpoints (pull model). VictoriaDB/Thanos for long-term storage. Grafana for dashboards. Counters, gauges, histograms, summaries. **Tracing:** OpenTelemetry -> Jaeger/Zipkin. TraceId propagation. Sampling strategies (head-based, tail-based). **Alerting:** Alertmanager evaluates rules, routes to PagerDuty/Slack/email. **Synthetic Monitoring:** external probes checking API health.

## Testing

### Q771: Testing pyramid?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Test pyramid (Cohn): Unit tests (fast, many) -> Integration tests (medium, fewer) -> E2E tests (slow, few). Unit: individual functions/classes (isolated). Integration: module interactions, database, API. E2E: complete user flows (UI + backend). Trophy (Kent C. Dodds): static analysis (TypeScript, ESLint) + unit + integration + E2E (critical paths). Testing strategy: 70% unit, 20% integration, 10% E2E (approximate). Focus on testing behavior, not implementation.

---

### Q772: Unit Testing best practices?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
FIRST: Fast, Isolated, Repeatable, Self-validating, Timely. One assertion per test (concept, not literal line). Arrange-Act-Assert pattern. Mock external dependencies. Test behavior, not implementation. Descriptive test names (functionUnderTest_scenario_expectedBehavior). Avoid testing private methods (test through public interface). Coverage: 80%+ is good (focus on critical paths, not 100%). Mutation testing: verify tests catch bugs (Stryker). TDD: write tests first -> implement -> refactor.

---

### Q773: Mocking vs Stubbing vs Faking?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Mock: object with expectations (verify behavior: was method called with args?). Stub: provides predefined responses (return value for test). Fake: working lightweight implementation (in-memory DB instead of real DB). Spy: wraps real object, records interactions (verify calls + real behavior). Dummy: object passed around but never used (fills parameters). Libraries: Mockito (Java), unittest.mock (Python), jest.fn() (JS), Moq (.NET). Principle: mock owned dependencies, stub external services.

---

### Q774: Integration Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Test interactions between components (DB, API, services). Approaches: embedded/real DB (Testcontainers for Docker), in-memory DB (H2 - but not production DB). API testing: REST/GraphQL endpoints (full request-response). Contract testing: test API contracts between services (Pact, Spring Cloud Contract). Database testing: test queries, migrations, transactions. Testcontainers: Java/Python/Go library for disposable Docker containers (PostgreSQL, Redis, Kafka). Spring Boot: @SpringBootTest, @DataJpaTest, @WebMvcTest. Clean test data between runs.

---

### Q775: E2E Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Test full user workflows from UI to backend. Frameworks: Selenium (browser automation, slow), Cypress (fast, developer-friendly, JS), Playwright (cross-browser, reliable, Microsoft), Puppeteer (Chrome/Chromium). Page Object Model: create page classes encapsulating selectors and interactions. Best practices: test critical user journeys (login, purchase, checkout), not every edge case. Data management: separate test environment with test data. Retry flaky tests (but investigate root cause). CI integration: headless mode. Visual regression testing: Percy, Chromatic.

---

### Q776: Test-Driven Development (TDD)?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Red-Green-Refactor cycle: write failing test (red) -> write minimal code to pass (green) -> refactor. Benefits: cleaner design, better test coverage, regression safety, documentation via tests. Types: outside-in (acceptance test drives unit tests), inside-out (unit tests first). When TDD works well: well-understood requirements, algorithmic code. When less suitable: exploratory/prototype code, UI-heavy applications. Pair with BDD (behavior-driven tests) for stakeholder communication.

---

### Q777: Code Coverage?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Metrics: Line coverage (lines executed), Branch coverage (branches true/false), Function coverage (functions called), Path coverage (all possible paths - exponential). Tools: JaCoCo (Java), coverage.py (Python), Istanbul/nyc (JS), Gcov (C++). Target: 70-80% line coverage recommended. 100% coverage possible but diminishing returns (some code untestable: error handlers, rare conditions). Coverage != quality: tests might pass with wrong assertions. Use mutation testing for quality. Focus coverage on critical business logic.

---

### Q778: Mutation Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Evaluate test quality by introducing code mutations (bugs) and checking if tests catch them. Mutations: change operators (> to <), reverse conditionals, delete method calls, modify return values. Mutation score: % of mutants killed (caught by tests). High score (<90%) means tests effectively catch bugs. Tools: Stryker (JS, Java, C#, Scala), PIT (Java), Cosmic Ray (Python). Slower than coverage but gives confidence. Run mutation tests on critical modules. Better metric than coverage alone.

---

### Q779: API Testing (REST/GraphQL)?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
REST: verify HTTP methods, status codes, request/response schemas, headers, authentication. Tools: Postman/Newman (collections, test scripts), REST Assured (Java), Supertest (JS), pytest + requests (Python). Contract testing: Pact, Spring Cloud Contract. GraphQL: test queries, mutations, subscriptions; validate response against schema; test error handling. Tools: Apollo testing tools, graphql-request. Load testing: k6, Gatling, JMeter. Security: OWASP ZAP for automated security testing.

---

### Q780: Performance / Load Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Types: Load (expected users), Stress (beyond breaking point), Spike (sudden increase), Soak (long duration for resource leaks), Endurance. Metrics: response time (p50, p95, p99), throughput (RPS/TPS), error rate, resource utilization (CPU, memory, I/O). Tools: k6 (modern, scriptable), JMeter (Java, extensive), Gatling (Scala, high performance), Locust (Python), Artillery (Node.js). Test in production-like environment. Warmup period. Gradual ramp-up. Bottlenecks: DB queries, external API calls, thread pool exhaustion, memory leaks. Measure before and after optimizations.

---

### Q781: Contract Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Test that services adhere to agreed-upon interface contracts. Producer (provider): publishes contract with API expectations. Consumer: tests against contract. Tools: Pact (consumer-driven), Spring Cloud Contract. Consumer-Driven Contracts: consumer writes test defining expected provider behavior -> generates contract -> CI validates provider against contract. Benefits: early detection of breaking changes, independent deployments, API compatibility verification. Microservices pattern: verify contracts without E2E tests for all combinations.

---

### Q782: Testing in CI/CD Pipeline?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pipeline stages: Commit -> Lint + Static Analysis -> Unit Tests (fast) -> Build -> Integration Tests -> Contract Tests -> E2E Tests (parallel) -> Performance Tests (nightly) -> Deploy. Parallel test execution: split tests across multiple CI runners. Test reporting: JUnit XML, coverage reports, HTML reports. Quality gates: fail pipeline if coverage drops below threshold, performance degrades, tests fail. Flaky test handling: automatic retry + flaky test detection + tracking. Test isolation: clean Docker containers per run. Parallel stages for different module tests.

---

### Q783: Flaky Tests?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tests that pass/fail intermittently without code changes. Causes: race conditions, timing issues (thread.sleep), order-dependent tests, network flakiness, test environment interference, random data, external service availability. Detection: run tests multiple times (CI retry), statistical flaky detection. Mitigation: remove shared mutable state, use deterministic data, proper test isolation, avoid Thread.sleep (use awaitility), mock external services, clean environment. Quarantine flaky tests (separate suite). Track flaky rate over time.

---

### Q784: Testing Microservices?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Challenges: distributed transactions, eventual consistency, external dependencies, network failures. Strategies: unit test each service in isolation. Integration: test with real dependencies (Testcontainers). Contract tests between services. Consumer-driven contracts (Pact). Component tests: test service with stubbed external dependencies (WireMock). End-to-end: limited subset of critical flows. Chaos engineering: test behavior under failures (service down, latency). Monitoring: alerts based on SLA violations in production. Testing in production: feature flags, canary releases, shadow traffic.

---

### Q785: Smoke vs Sanity vs Regression Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Smoke (build verification): basic check that application runs (critical paths). Quick, automated, run after deployment. Sanity: focused check after minor changes (specific feature area). Regression: verify recent code changes didn't break existing functionality. Full test suite. Smoke is subset of regression (quickest). Sanity is narrow, exploratory. Automated: regression suite runs in CI/CD. Risk-based: focus regression on changed areas. Benefits: catches regressions early. Automated regression is essential for CI/CD.

---

### Q786: Behavior-Driven Development (BDD)?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Extension of TDD: tests written in natural language (Given-When-Then). Gherkin syntax: Feature -> Scenario -> Steps. Given (preconditions), When (action), Then (expected outcome). Tools: Cucumber (Java, Ruby, JS), SpecFlow (.NET), Behave (Python). Benefits: non-technical stakeholders can read/contribute to tests, living documentation, shared understanding. Challenges: maintaining Gherkin files as code, test step definitions become large, Gherkin-to-code overhead. Modern alternatives: Serenity BDD, JBehave.

---

### Q787: Test Automation Frameworks?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Web: Selenium (grid, WebDriver), Cypress (developer-friendly, .then()), Playwright (modern, cross-browser, auto-wait). Mobile: Appium (cross-platform), Detox (React Native). API: REST Assured, Supertest, pytest. Unit: JUnit 5 (Java), pytest (Python), Jest (JS), NUnit (.NET). Performance: k6, Gatling, JMeter. Reporting: Allure (beautiful reports), ExtentReports. Data-driven: parameterized tests (JUnit 5 @ParameterizedTest). Select framework based on: team skills, ecosystem, CI compatibility, required features (parallel execution, video recording).

---

### Q788: Testing Database Code?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Test queries, stored procedures, ORM mappings, migrations. Use in-memory DB (H2) vs real DB (Testcontainers). In-memory faster but has SQL dialect differences (produces false positives/negatives). Testcontainers: Docker PostgreSQL/MySQL for realistic tests. Transaction management: rollback after test (@Transactional in Spring). Seed test data: SQL scripts, ObjectMother pattern, factory_boy (Python). Flyway/Liquibase: test migrations (rollback + forward). Test query performance: explain plan, query count assertions (assertQueryCount). ORM-specific: test N+1 queries (Hibernate Stats). Test data cleanup between runs.

---

### Q789: A/B Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compare two versions (A=control, B=variant) to determine which performs better. Random assignment of users to groups. Statistical significance: p-value < 0.05, confidence intervals. Metrics: conversion rate, click-through rate, revenue, retention. Duration: minimum 1-2 weeks (weekend effects, novelty). Run one test at a time (interaction effects). Segment analysis: does effect vary by user type? Challenges: multiple testing corrections (Bonferroni), Simpson's paradox, peeking (don't check results daily). Infrastructure: feature flags (LaunchDarkly, Unleash), experiment platforms (Google Optimize, Azure Experimentation). Full Stack: server-side experiments for consistency.

---

### Q790: Chaos Engineering?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Test system resilience by intentionally injecting failures. Principles: build hypothesis about steady state, introduce real-world failures (Kill a server, network delay, resource exhaustion), observe. Tools: Chaos Monkey (Netflix - randomly terminate instances), Litmus (K8s), Gremlin (SaaS), Chaos Mesh. Types: infrastructure (kill pods, network partitions), application (slow queries, OOM errors), dependencies (DB down, Redis unavailable). Run in staging first, then production (limited blast radius, rollback). GameDays: scheduled chaos exercises. Benefits: uncover hidden failure modes, improve monitoring and automation.

---

### Q791: Snapshot Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compare rendered output against stored reference snapshot. UI: React component render output (Jest snapshot testing). API responses: match against saved JSON. Image diffing: visual regression (Percy, Chromatic). Benefits: catches unintended changes quickly. Problems: large snapshots hard to review, false positives (minor formatting), encourages accepting bad snapshots, brittle. Best practices: keep snapshots small, review changes in PR, commit snapshots, use in combination with other tests. Prefer explicit assertions over snapshots for critical logic.

---

### Q792: Testing State Management (React/Vue)?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Redux: test reducers (pure functions, given state+action -> new state), test action creators (return expected action), test selectors, test async thunks (mock API). React Testing Library: test behavior, not implementation. Query elements by role/label/text (not CSS class). Fire events, assert rendered output. MSW (Mock Service Worker): mock API at network level (realistic, no mocking library). Vue: Vue Test Utils, @vue/test-utils. Pinia: test stores directly. Best practice: test state changes through component interaction (user clicks button -> state updates -> UI changes).

---

### Q793: Testing Async Code?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Challenges: callbacks, Promises, timeout races. Solutions: async/await in tests (Jest test async fn), done callback (for older patterns), fake timers (jest.useFakeTimers - control setTimeout/setInterval), race condition testing (await yield + advance timers). Async event testing: waitFor (RTL - retry until assertion passes), findBy queries (async). Network requests: mock at different levels (intercept at network layer with MSW, mock fetch/interceptors). Test both success and failure paths. Timeout: set test timeout (jest.setTimeout, @Test(timeout). Handle unhandled promise rejections.

---

### Q794: Testing React Components?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React Testing Library (RTL) - preferred over Enzyme. RTL principle: test as user interacts (no internal state access). Queries: getByRole (preferred), getByText, getByLabelText, getByPlaceholderText, getByTestId (last resort). Events: fireEvent (old), userEvent (user-like interactions: click, type, hover - async). Async: waitFor, findBy, findAllBy. Mocking: jest.mock for modules, jest.spyOn for methods. MSW for API. Testing hooks: renderHook (RTL). Test user workflows: render -> locate element -> interact -> assert output. Avoid testing implementation (internal state, component instances).

---

### Q795: Testing Micro Frontends?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Each micro frontend tested independently (unit, integration). Integration: test shell/composition layer (integration of MFs). Cross-MF communication: events (window.postMessage, custom events). Shared dependencies: version compatibility, API contracts. E2E: critical user flows spanning multiple MFs. Integration testing: import MF directly (if module federation), stub/container components. Challenges: testing Webpack Module Federation, testing cross-origin communication, maintaining test data across MFs. Composition layer: test routing, shell UI, error boundaries for failed MFs.

---

### Q796: Visual Regression Testing?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Detect visual UI changes by comparing screenshots. Process: baseline screenshot -> code change -> new screenshot -> diff comparison. Pixel comparison: percentage difference. Tools: Percy (SaaS, cross-browser), Chromatic (Storybook integration), Applitools (AI-powered), backstopjs (open source). Integration with CI: fail build if visual diff > threshold. Best practices: test responsive designs (multiple viewports), component-level (Storybook) vs page-level. Challenges: flakiness (animations, dynamic content, fonts), false positives (anti-aliasing differences). Stabilize: disable animations, freeze date/time.

---

### Q797: Testing Accessibility (a11y)?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Automated: axe-core (Jest-axe, Cypress-axe, Playwright), WAVE, Lighthouse. Check: ARIA attributes, color contrast, keyboard navigation, focus management, screen reader output. Manual: screen readers (NVDA, VoiceOver), keyboard-only navigation. Integration: automated a11y checks in CI pipeline (jest-axe, cypress-axe). Checklist: images have alt text, form fields have labels, buttons have accessible names, proper heading hierarchy, error messages announced. Automation catches ~30% of issues; manual testing required for complete coverage. WCAG 2.1 AA standard.

---

### Q798: Testing GraphQL?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Query/Mutation tests: test resolvers in isolation (unit). Schema tests: validate schema evolution (breaking changes). Integration: run queries against test server (Apollo Server testing, graphql-request). Data source tests: mock REST/database, test resolver data fetching. Walkthrough testing: complete user flows through Apollo Client. Apollo-specific: MockedProvider for testing React components (mock GraphQL responses). Schema registry: check schema diff for breaking changes (Apollo Studio). Performance: n+1 queries via DataLoader, query complexity analysis. Security: test authorization (user scopes per field/resolver).

---

### Q799: Testing Database Migrations?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Test migrations in CI with real database (Testcontainers). Verify: migration up, migration down (rollback), data preservation, schema correctness. Sequence: migration V1 -> insert data -> migration V2 -> verify data integrity -> rollback to V1 -> verify V1 state. Check: NOT NULL constraints, foreign keys, indexes, default values. Performance: large dataset migration speed. idempotent: running migration twice same result. Automated: Flyway/Liquibase testing utilities. Version control: migration scripts in SCM alongside tests. Contract: migration output matches expected schema (hibernate ddl validation).

---

### Q800: Testing Strategy for AI/ML?
**Topic:** Testing
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Data testing: schema validation, distribution checks, data drift detection, missing value rates, label correctness. Model testing: accuracy, precision, recall, F1, fairness metrics (disparate impact), robustness (adversarial examples). Integration: model API endpoint testing, model + business logic. Pipeline testing: feature computation correctness (test features against golden dataset), retraining pipeline, model registry. Model monitoring: prediction drift, feature drift, performance degradation. Shadow testing: compare new model vs old in production (no user-facing). A/B testing: compare models online. Explainability tests: SHAP/LIME consistency.

## Additional Topics

### Q861: Event-Driven Architecture patterns?
**Topic:** Software Architecture
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Event Notification: simple publish-subscribe (something happened -> notify consumers). Event-Carried State Transfer: event includes full data (reduces queries). Event Sourcing: events as source of truth. CQRS: separate read/write. Saga: distributed transaction via events. Transactional Outbox: write to DB + publish event atomically. Change Data Capture (CDC): capture DB changes as events (Debezium). Reliable: exactly-once semantics, idempotent consumers. Use: real-time updates, decoupling, scalability.

---

### Q862: CQRS (Command Query Responsibility Segregation)?
**Topic:** Software Architecture
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Separate read and write models. Commands (writes): change state, return void. Queries (reads): return data, no side effects. Benefits: optimized read model (denormalized, different DB), optimized write model (validated, normalized), separate scaling (read replicas). Implementations: Event Sourcing + CQRS (events -> write store, projections -> read store). Simple: separate service classes (CommandService, QueryService). When useful: complex domain (event sourcing), read-heavy vs write-heavy workloads, performance optimization. Overhead: eventual consistency (read may be stale), more code.

---

### Q863: Domain-Driven Design (DDD)?
**Topic:** Software Architecture
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Model software around business domain. Ubiquitous Language: shared language between devs and domain experts. Bounded Context: explicit boundary where domain model applies (microservice boundary). Entities: objects with identity (User, Order). Value Objects: immutable, no identity (Money, Address). Aggregates: cluster of entities treated as unit (Order + OrderItems). Domain Events: something meaningful happened. Repositories: persistence abstraction. Application Services: orchestrate domain logic. Strategic Design: context mapping, shared kernel, anti-corruption layer. DDD for complex domains, overkill for CRUD.

---

### Q864: Hexagonal Architecture (Ports & Adapters)?
**Topic:** Software Architecture
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Core business logic isolated from external concerns (DB, UI, API). Ports: interfaces defining interactions (inbound port, outbound port). Adapters: implementations of ports (PostgreSQL adapter, REST adapter, CLI adapter). Core: pure business logic, no framework dependencies. Benefits: testable (swap adapters), technology-agnostic, maintainable. Onion Architecture: similar layering (domain -> application -> infrastructure). Clean Architecture: concentric circles (entities -> use cases -> interface adapters -> external). All focus on dependency inversion: outer layers depend on inner.

---

### Q865: Rate Limiting Algorithms in detail?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Token Bucket: tokens refill at fixed rate, consume per request (allow bursts). Leaky Bucket: requests process at fixed rate (queue-like, smooths bursts). Fixed Window: count requests in time window (edge burst problem - reset at boundary). Sliding Window Log: track timestamps of all requests (accurate but memory heavy). Sliding Window Counter: approximate sliding window (combines fixed window + rolling). Redis implementation: INCR + EXPIRE for fixed window, sorted sets for sliding log. Distributed: local counters (eventually consistent) or central Redis (consistency cost).

---

### Q866: AWS Core Services overview?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compute: EC2 (VMs), Lambda (serverless), ECS/EKS (containers), Beanstalk (PaaS). Storage: S3 (object), EBS (block), EFS (NFS), Glacier (archive). Database: RDS (relational), DynamoDB (NoSQL), ElastiCache (Redis/Memcached), Redshift (warehouse), Neptune (graph). Networking: VPC, Route53 (DNS), CloudFront (CDN), ELB/ALB (load balancer), API Gateway. Messaging: SQS (queue), SNS (pub/sub), EventBridge (event bus), Kinesis (streaming). Security: IAM, KMS, Cognito, WAF, Shield. ML: SageMaker, Bedrock, Rekognition. Monitoring: CloudWatch, X-Ray, CloudTrail.

---

### Q867: Azure Core Services overview?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compute: VMs, App Service (PaaS), Azure Functions (serverless), AKS (Kubernetes), Container Instances. Storage: Blob (object), Disk, Files (SMB), Archive. Database: SQL Database, Cosmos DB (NoSQL), Azure Database for PostgreSQL/MySQL, Redis Cache, Synapse (analytics). Networking: VNet, Azure DNS, CDN, Load Balancer, Application Gateway, Traffic Manager, Front Door. Messaging: Queue Storage, Service Bus, Event Grid, Event Hubs, Notification Hubs. Security: Entra ID (Azure AD), Key Vault, RBAC, Defender, Sentinel. AI: OpenAI Service, AI Search, Machine Learning, Cognitive Services. Monitoring: Monitor, Log Analytics, Application Insights.

---

### Q868: Google Cloud Core Services overview?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compute: Compute Engine (VMs), GKE (Kubernetes), Cloud Functions, App Engine (PaaS), Cloud Run (serverless containers). Storage: Cloud Storage (object), Filestore (NAS), Persistent Disk. Database: Cloud SQL (relational), Cloud Spanner (globally distributed SQL), Firestore (NoSQL), Bigtable (wide-column), Memorystore (Redis), BigQuery (serverless warehouse). Networking: VPC, Cloud DNS, Cloud CDN, Cloud Load Balancing, Cloud NAT. Data/Analytics: BigQuery, Dataflow (streaming), Pub/Sub (messaging), Dataproc (Spark/Hadoop). AI/ML: Vertex AI, AutoML, AI Platform, Gemini API. Security: Cloud IAM, KMS, Cloud Armor, Security Command Center.

---

### Q869: Infrastructure as Code (IaC)?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Manage infrastructure through code (declarative or imperative). Terraform: declarative, multi-cloud (HashiCorp HCL), state management, resources as code. AWS CDK: imperative (TypeScript/Python), AWS-resources as code. CloudFormation: AWS-native, JSON/YAML. Pulumi: multi-cloud, real programming languages. Ansible: configuration management, agentless, push-based. Benefits: repeatable, version-controlled, reviewable, self-documenting, automated. State: Terraform state (remote backend: S3, Azure Storage). Best practices: modules, remote state, workspaces, DRY. Plan before apply.

---

### Q870: Serverless Architecture?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Serverless: no server management, auto-scaling, pay-per-execution. FaaS: AWS Lambda, Azure Functions, Google Cloud Functions. BaaS: Auth0, Firebase, Supabase. Pros: no infrastructure management, auto-scaling (zero to infinite), pay for what you use, fast deployment. Cons: cold starts (latency), state management (external), limited execution time (15min Lambda), vendor lock-in, debugging harder. Cold start: function invocation after idle (container spin-up). Mitigation: provisioned concurrency, keep-warm, Lambda SnapStart. Best for: event-driven (S3 upload, webhook), API backends, scheduled tasks. Not for: long-running compute, low-latency.

---

### Q871: API Gateway pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Single entry point for microservices. Responsibilities: routing (to appropriate service), authentication (validate tokens), rate limiting, caching, request/response transformation, logging, monitoring, cross-cutting concerns. Backend for Frontend (BFF): separate API gateway per client type (mobile, web, IoT). BFF advantages: customized response per client, reduced payload size, client-specific logic. Tools: AWS API Gateway, Azure API Management, Kong, NGINX, Traefik, Envoy. Edge gateway: at CDN layer (Cloudflare, Fastly). Gateway vs service mesh: different concerns (gateway: north-south, mesh: east-west).

---

### Q872: Blue-Green vs Canary Deployment?
**Topic:** DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Blue-Green: two identical environments. Blue: current production. Green: new version. Switch traffic (load balancer) from blue to green. Instant switch, easy rollback (switch back). Downside: double infrastructure cost during deployment. Canary: gradually shift traffic (5% -> 25% -> 50% -> 100%). Monitor metrics (errors, latency) at each step. Rollback if issues. Slower but lower risk. Tools: Kubernetes (Istio, Flagger, Argo Rollouts), AWS (CodeDeploy), Spinnaker. Traffic routing: DNS (weighted RR), load balancer, service mesh (Istio). Feature flags can also control rollout.

---

### Q873: Observability (Three Pillars)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Logs: event recordings (structured, searchable, grepable). Metrics: aggregated measurements (latency p50/p99, error rate, CPU, memory). Traces: request flow across services (distributed tracing). OpenTelemetry: standard for telemetry (logs, metrics, traces unified). Observability vs Monitoring: monitoring (known unknowns), observability (unknown unknowns). Tools: Grafana, Prometheus, Loki, Tempo, ELK, Datadog, New Relic. Cardinality: high cardinality dimensions in metrics (user_id in Prometheus = bad).

---

### Q874: Chaos Engineering in practice?
**Topic:** System Design - Resilience
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Netflix Chaos Monkey: random instance termination in production. Principles: steady state hypothesis, vary real-world events (server crash, latency, DNS failure), run experiments in production (limited blast radius), automate. Types: infrastructure (kill pod, network partition), application (inject latency, exceptions, OOM), dependencies (DB down, cache miss). Blast radius: start small, expand. Automated rollback. Tools: Litmus (K8s), Gremlin, Chaos Mesh. Culture: blameless postmortems, learning from failures.

---

### Q875: Web Security - OWASP top mitigations?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SQL Injection: parameterized queries. Broken Access Control: role-based checks. Cryptographic Failures: HTTPS, AES-GCM, Argon2. XSS: output encoding, CSP. Insecure Design: threat modeling. Security Misconfiguration: CIS benchmarks. Vulnerable Components: Snyk, Dependabot. Auth Failures: MFA, rate limiting. Integrity Failures: code signing. SSRF: URL allowlists, network segmentation.

---

### Q876: Competitive Programming tips?
**Topic:** General CS - DSA
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Strategy: understand problem -> examples -> brute force -> optimize -> edge cases -> code. Hashmap: O(1) lookups. Two pointers: sorted arrays, sliding window. Binary search: O(log n). DFS/BFS: graphs and trees. DP: memoization, tabulation. Practice: LeetCode Top Interview 150, Blind 75. Prioritize easier problems first (build confidence). Focus on patterns not memorization. Review solved problems periodically.

---

### Q877: NoSQL Database types?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Key-Value: Redis, DynamoDB, Memcached (simple, fast, schema-less). Document: MongoDB, Couchbase, Firestore (JSON documents, flexible schema). Column-Family: Cassandra, HBase, ScyllaDB (wide-column, high write throughput). Graph: Neo4j, Amazon Neptune (nodes + edges). Time Series: InfluxDB, TimescaleDB, Prometheus. Search: Elasticsearch, Meilisearch (full-text, inverted index). Choose based on: data model, access patterns, consistency needs, scalability.

---

### Q878: SQL vs NoSQL?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
SQL: structured schema, ACID, JOINs, complex queries, strict consistency. Best for: financial systems, inventory, relationships. NoSQL: flexible schema, BASE, horizontal scaling, high write throughput. Best for: user profiles, sessions, IoT, content management. Many systems use both (polyglot persistence). NewSQL (CockroachDB, Spanner) combines SQL with horizontal scaling.

---

### Q879: Cache Invalidation strategies?
**Topic:** System Design - Caching
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
TTL: expire after fixed time (simplest). Write-through: update cache immediately on write (consistent but write latency). Write-around: write to DB, cache miss on next read. Write-behind: write to cache, async write to DB (fast writes, risk of data loss). Read-through: on cache miss, load from DB into cache. Cache aside: application manages cache (check -> miss -> load -> update). Pattern: cache-aside + TTL is most common. Redis expiration: lazy (check on access) + periodic (sampling).

---

### Q880: Bloom Filter?
**Topic:** System Design - Data Structures
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Probabilistic set membership. No false negatives, configurable false positives. Bit array + k hash functions. Add: hash element through k functions, set bits. Check: hash through k functions, if any bit 0 -> not present. Parameters: n (elements), m (bits), k (hashes). False positive rate: (1 - e^(-kn/m))^k. Uses: cache (avoid miss for non-existent keys), web crawler, spell checker. Cassandra uses Bloom filters.

---

### Q881: Merkle Tree (Hash Tree)?
**Topic:** System Design - Data Structures
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Tree where leaf = data hash, internal = hash of children. Root hash represents entire data set. Efficiently verify integrity: compare root hashes, binary search down tree to find differences. Used in: Git (commits), blockchain, Cassandra (repair), DynamoDB (replication). Merkle proof: path from leaf to root to prove inclusion. O(log n) to locate differences.

---

### Q882: Consistent Hashing in detail?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Hash keys and servers onto ring (0..2^m-1). Assign key to nearest server clockwise. Server addition: only affected range moves. Server removal: only that server's keys reassigned. Virtual nodes: multiple points per server (load balance, heterogeneous capacity). Data replication: replicate to next k servers. Applications: DynamoDB, Cassandra, Discord, Akamai CDN. Jump consistent hash: O(log n), no ring.

---

### Q883: Gossip Protocol?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Decentralized: each node exchanges info with random peers periodically. Information spreads exponentially. Uses: failure detection, membership, state dissemination. Cassandra: gossip for node discovery. Convergence: O(log N) rounds. Anti-entropy: periodic comparison + repair. Pros: decentralized, fault-tolerant, eventually consistent. Cons: bandwidth, probabilistic convergence.

---

### Q884: Leader Election algorithms?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Select one node as leader for coordination. Paxos: consensus protocol (complex). Raft: understandable consensus (leader election, log replication). Terms: time divided into terms with one leader. Heartbeats: leader sends to prevent election. Majority wins. ZooKeeper: Zab protocol. etcd: Raft (Kubernetes). Ensures: at most one leader, leader has latest data.

---

### Q885: Distributed ID Generation?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Requirements: globally unique, time-ordered, monotonically increasing. UUID v4: 128-bit random (not ordered). Snowflake (Twitter): 64-bit (timestamp + worker + sequence). 41-bit timestamp = ~69 years. 4096 IDs per ms per worker. Database sequence: bottleneck. Redis INCR: atomic. MongoDB ObjectId: timestamp + machine + pid + counter. ULID: sortable, 26 chars. Snowflake variants widely used.

---

### Q886: Geohashing and Spatial Indexing?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Geohash: encode lat/lng into base32 string. Longer = more precision. Nearby locations share prefix. Z-order curve. QuadTree: recursive subdivision into quadrants. R-Tree: bounding boxes (PostgreSQL GiST). Google S2: cell hierarchy on sphere. Uber H3: hexagonal grid. Applications: Uber pricing zones, maps, food delivery.

---

### Q887: CAP Theorem nuances?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
CAP: Consistency (linearizability), Availability, Partition Tolerance. PACELC: if Partition trade C/A, else trade Latency/Consistency. Linearizability: strongest consistency. Eventual consistency: converges over time. Causal consistency: causally related ops seen in order. Read-after-write: read your writes. DynamoDB: eventually consistent reads default, consistent optional.

---

### Q888: Replication strategies?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Leader-based: one leader writes, replicates to followers. Multi-leader: multiple leaders (conflicts: LWW, CRDT). Leaderless: any replica accepts writes (Dynamo). Read repair: update stale replicas on read. Hinted handoff: store writes for down nodes. Quorum: R+W > N. Synchronous: durable, slower. Async: faster, potential data loss.

---

### Q889: Consensus Algorithms (Paxos, Raft)?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Paxos: Prepare/Accept phases, majority quorum. Complex. Raft: leader election, log replication. Randomized timeouts prevent split votes. Log: leader sends AppendEntries to followers, majority commits. Safety: elected leader has all committed entries. Configuration changes: joint consensus. etcd, Consul use Raft.

---

### Q890: CRDT (Conflict-free Replicated Data Types)?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Update concurrently without conflicts, always converge. G-Counter (merge=max), PN-Counter, G-Set, OR-Set. Merge: commutative, associative, idempotent. Applications: collaborative editing (Yjs), Redis CRDTs, offline-first apps. State-based vs operation-based. Automerge: JS CRDT library.

---

### Q891: Thundering Herd problem?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Many processes hit same resource simultaneously (cache miss). Solutions: Mutex/lock (one loads, others wait). Probabilistic early expiration. Random TTL stagger. Single flight: only one request computes. Redis SET NX lock. Exponential backoff. Pre-compute popular items.

---

### Q892: Sliding Window vs Fixed Window Rate Limiting?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Fixed Window: O(1) memory, edge burst problem (double traffic at boundary). Sliding Window Log: O(n) memory, precise but memory heavy. Sliding Window Counter: approximate, O(1) memory, weighted previous+current. Token Bucket: fixed rate + burst. Leaky Bucket: fixed drain rate. Sliding Window Counter is best balance of accuracy and memory.

---

### Q893: Database Sharding approaches?
**Topic:** System Design - Databases
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Horizontal: split rows across shards. Key-based (hash): even distribution. Range-based: by value range. Directory-based: lookup table. Challenges: cross-shard queries, distributed joins (denormalize), distributed transactions (Saga), resharding. Consistent hashing helps resharding. Shard key: high cardinality, even distribution. Re-balancing: virtual nodes.

---

### Q894: Backpressure?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Receiver overloaded signals sender to slow down. Prevents OOM, latency degradation. Bounded queue (block when full). Drop messages. Throttle sender (HTTP 429). Reactive Streams backpressure (Subscriber requests n). Kafka: consumer lag indicates backpressure need. SQS: visibility timeout, DLQ.

---

### Q895: Service Mesh (Istio, Linkerd)?
**Topic:** System Design - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Infrastructure layer for service-to-service communication. Sidecar proxy (Envoy) per service instance. Features: service discovery, traffic management (canary, blue-green), mTLS, observability, circuit breaking, retries. Istio: Envoy + control plane (Pilot, Mixer, Citadel). Linkerd: lighter (Rust/Buoyant). Benefits: standardize networking without code changes. Cons: latency overhead, resource usage (sidecars), operational complexity.

---

### Q896: Database Connection Pooling detail?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Maintain pool of connections for reuse. Avoid expensive TCP handshake per request. HikariCP (Java - fastest): maxPoolSize typically 10-50 per instance (not 100+). pgBouncer: PostgreSQL pooler. Connection leak: not returning connection (use try-with-resources). Pool sizing: small pool often better (avoids DB overload). Hikari formula: T*C/S.

---

### Q897: Indexing Strategies beyond B-tree?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Hash Index: O(1) equality lookups, no range queries. Bitmap Index: low cardinality, efficient AND/OR operations (data warehousing). GiST (Generalized Search Tree): spatial, full-text. GIN (Generalized Inverted Index): composite values (JSONB, arrays). BRIN (Block Range Index): large tables with natural ordering (time series). Covering Index: includes all needed columns (index-only scan). Partial Index: WHERE condition (smaller index). Expression Index: index on function result.

---

### Q898: Advanced SQL (Window Functions, CTEs)?
**Topic:** SQL
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Window Functions: aggregate over partition without grouping. ROW_NUMBER(), RANK(), DENSE_RANK(), LEAD(), LAG(), SUM() OVER (PARTITION BY dept ORDER BY salary). CTE (WITH clause): name subquery for readability, recursive queries (hierarchical data). Examples: running total (SUM OVER), pagination (ROW_NUMBER), hierarchical org chart (RECURSIVE CTE). Performance: window functions often faster than self-joins.

---

### Q899: OLTP vs OLAP?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
OLTP (Online Transaction Processing): many short transactions, real-time, normalized schema. Examples: order processing, banking. High concurrency, ACID. OLAP (Online Analytical Processing): complex analytical queries, historical data, denormalized (star/snowflake schema). Examples: BI dashboards, reporting. Columnar storage (Parquet, ORC) for OLAP. HTAP (Hybrid): both in one system (SingleStore, TiDB).

---

### Q900: Compiler vs Interpreter?
**Topic:** General CS - Programming
**Difficulty:** Easy

**Answer:**
Compiler: translates entire source to machine code (binary), then execute. Faster execution, slower startup. Examples: C, C++, Rust, Go. Interpreter: executes source line by line. Faster startup, slower execution (can optimize with JIT). Examples: Python, JavaScript, Ruby. JIT Compiler: compile at runtime (Java JVM, V8 JS). Hybrid: compile to bytecode, interpret/compile at runtime (Java, C#). AOT: ahead-of-time compilation (Go, C++).

### Q901: Memory Management (Stack vs Heap)?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stack: fixed size, function call frames (local variables, return address). LIFO, fast allocation (move stack pointer). Heap: dynamic allocation (malloc/new), manual or GC managed. Slower, fragmentation risk. Stack overflow: deep recursion. Heap overflow: memory leaks. Values on stack (primitives), references on heap (objects). Garbage collection: mark-sweep, reference counting, generational. Memory pools: pre-allocate for performance.

---

### Q902: Concurrency vs Parallelism?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Concurrency: multiple tasks in progress (interleaved execution on single core). Structure: deal with many things at once. Parallelism: multiple tasks executing simultaneously (multiple cores). Execution: run many things at once. Concurrency is about design, parallelism about hardware. Go goroutines: concurrency with channels. Async/await: concurrent I/O. Data parallelism: SIMD, GPU. Task parallelism: different tasks on different cores. Amdahl's law: speedup limited by sequential portion.

---

### Q903: Virtual Memory and Paging?
**Topic:** General CS - OS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Virtual memory: each process has own virtual address space. Pages: fixed-size blocks (4KB typical). Page table: maps virtual to physical pages. TLB (Translation Lookaside Buffer): cache for page table (fast address translation). Page fault: accessed page not in memory (load from disk). Demand paging: load pages on demand. Swapping: move pages between memory and disk. MMU: hardware for address translation. Huge pages: reduce TLB misses (2MB/1GB pages).

---

### Q904: Interrupts and System Calls?
**Topic:** General CS - OS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Interrupt: hardware signal to CPU (I/O completion, timer). CPU saves context, jumps to interrupt handler. Return from interrupt. System call: user process requests kernel service (read file, create process). Context switch: save user state, switch to kernel mode, execute, restore. syscall instruction (vs old int 0x80). Costly: ~1-2 microseconds. Avoid: batch system calls, use mmap, use VDSO (virtual dynamic shared object) for time/clock syscalls.

---

### Q905: Locking and Deadlock?
**Topic:** General CS - OS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Lock (mutex): mutual exclusion - one thread at a time. Semaphore: counter for resource access. Read-write lock: multiple readers, exclusive writer. Deadlock: mutual blocking (circular wait). Conditions: mutual exclusion, hold and wait, no preemption, circular wait. Prevention: lock ordering, timeout, trylock. Avoidance: banker's algorithm. Detection: wait-for graph. Starvation: thread never gets resource (fair locks). Livelock: threads keep changing state without progress.

---

### Q906: Threading Models?
**Topic:** General CS - OS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1:1 (kernel thread per user thread): Java threads, pthreads (Linux). Pros: true parallelism. Cons: expensive threads. N:1 (all user threads on one kernel thread): green threads, fibers. Pros: lightweight. Cons: no parallelism, blocking syscall blocks all. M:N (many user threads on many kernel threads): Go goroutines, Erlang processes. Pros: lightweight + parallelism. Cons: complex scheduler. Modern: async/await is concurrency without threads (event loop). Coroutines: cooperatively scheduled lightweight threads.

---

### Q907: REST vs GraphQL vs gRPC?
**Topic:** General CS - API
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
REST: endpoints per resource, HTTP methods, JSON. Simple, cacheable, ubiquitous. Over-fetching/under-fetching. GraphQL: single endpoint, client specifies fields, strongly typed. Flexible, no over-fetching. Complex queries, caching harder. gRPC: binary (protobuf), HTTP/2, strong typing, streaming. Fastest, code generation. Browser support limited (gRPC-web). Choose: REST for simple/public APIs, GraphQL for complex client needs, gRPC for high-performance internal services.

---

### Q908: Streaming (Kafka) vs Messaging (RabbitMQ)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Kafka: distributed event log. High throughput, persistence, replay, partitioning. Pull-based consumers. Use: event streaming, data pipelines, log aggregation. RabbitMQ: AMQP broker, exchange types (direct, topic, fanout). Push-based, immediate delivery, complex routing. Use: task queues, RPC, transient messages. Kafka excels at long-term storage and replay. RabbitMQ excels at complex routing and immediate delivery. Kafka partitions > RabbitMQ queues for parallelism.

---

### Q909: CAP Theorem - Dynamo vs Bigtable?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Dynamo (Amazon, 2007): AP system - eventual consistency, always writable. Vector clocks for conflict resolution. Gossip-based membership. Consistent hashing. Quorum: R+W>N. Influence: Cassandra, DynamoDB, Riak. Bigtable (Google, 2006): CP system - strong consistency, columnar storage, tablets + Chubby (Paxos). Influence: HBase, Spanner. Modern systems: Spanner (CP + high availability via TrueTime). DynamoDB: configurable consistency (eventually or strongly consistent).

---

### Q910: Real-time data processing?
**Topic:** System Design - Data
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Stream processing: process data as it arrives. Tools: Apache Flink (true streaming, exactly-once), Kafka Streams (embeddable, exactly-once), Spark Streaming (micro-batches), Beam (unified batch/streaming). Stateful processing: windowing (tumbling, sliding, session). Exactly-once semantics: Kafka transactions, idempotent producers. Watermarks: handle late data. Use: real-time analytics, fraud detection, monitoring, personalization. Lambda architecture: batch + streaming layers. Kappa architecture: streaming only (replay for batch).

---

### Q911: Idempotent Consumer pattern?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Process same message multiple times without side effects. Use: at-least-once delivery (Kafka, SQS) must be idempotent. Implementation: dedup table (process_message_id unique key), idempotency key in message, state machine (check current state before transition). Kafka: enable.idempotence=true for producer. Consumer: track processed offsets. Use transactional outbox: write event + mark sent in same DB transaction. Design: operations naturally idempotent (SET status = 'paid' not increment counter).

---

### Q912: Distributed Locking?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Coordinate access to shared resources across machines. Redis: SET key uuid NX EX 10 (acquire lock), DEL if uuid matches (release atomically with Lua script). Redlock: distributed lock across multiple Redis nodes. ZooKeeper: ephemeral sequential znodes for lock. etcd: lease + key for lock. Problems: lock expiry before completion, split-brain, clock drift. Best practice: keep critical section short, use fencing tokens (sequential token to prevent stale lock usage). Modern: use database row-level locks or leases.

---

### Q913: Time Series Databases?
**Topic:** System Design - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Optimized for timestamped data (metrics, IoT, logs). InfluxDB: columnar storage, continuous queries, retention policies. Prometheus: pull-based, built-in alerting, TSDB, integrates with Grafana. TimescaleDB: PostgreSQL extension (hypertables, automatic partitioning). QuestDB: high-performance, columnar, SQL. Features: downsampling, data retention, continuous aggregates, gap filling. Use: monitoring, IoT sensor data, financial tick data, application metrics.

---

### Q914: Full-Text Search and Elasticsearch?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Inverted index: token -> documents. Elasticsearch: distributed, RESTful, based on Apache Lucene. Index -> types (deprecated) -> documents. Shard: Lucene instance (primary + replica). Query DSL: match, term, bool, range, fuzzy. Aggregations: bucketing, metrics, pipeline. Analyzer: tokenizer + filters (lowercase, stopwords, stemming). Relevance scoring: TF-IDF, BM25. N-grams for partial matching. Use: full-text search, log analytics (ELK stack), product search.

---

### Q915: WebSockets in depth?
**Topic:** General CS - Real-time
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Full-duplex persistent connection over TCP. Initiated as HTTP upgrade (101 Switching Protocols). ws:// (unencrypted), wss:// (encrypted over TLS). Frames: text, binary, ping/pong, close. Binary format: small header (opcode, payload length, masking). Auto-reconnect: not built-in (implement with exponential backoff). Server scaling: sticky sessions (no), external pub/sub (Redis), broadcasting. Libraries: Socket.IO (JS, fallback), ws (Node.js), Spring WebSocket, Netty. Use: chat, live updates, multiplayer games, collaborative editing.

---

### Q916: Rate Limiting at Scale?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Distributed rate limiting challenges: consistency, performance, accuracy. Centralized: Redis (atomic counters) - single point of failure, latency. Local counters: no coordination, eventual consistency, approximate. Global: Redis Cluster with consistent hashing. GCRA (Generic Cell Rate Algorithm): rate limiting with jitter. Adaptive rate limiting: dynamically adjust based on system load (circuit breaker style). Need: minimize Redis per-request overhead (pipelines, Lua scripts). Edge rate limiting: CDN layer (Cloudflare, Fastly).

---

### Q917: Circuit Breaker pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Resilience
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Prevent cascading failures. States: Closed (normal, pass requests), Open (fail fast), Half-Open (test one request). Threshold: error rate > 50%, or consecutive failures > N. Transition: closed -> open when threshold exceeded. Open -> half-open after timeout. Half-open -> closed if request succeeds, open if fails. Implementation: Resilience4j (Java), Hystrix (Netflix, deprecated), Polly (.NET). Configure: failure threshold, timeout, half-open max requests. Use: wrapping external API calls, DB queries, downstream services.

---

### Q918: Bulkhead pattern?
**Topic:** System Design - Resilience
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Isolate resources into pools (ship compartments). Prevents failure in one pool from affecting others. Thread pools: separate thread pool per downstream service (one service slow doesn't exhaust all threads). Semaphore isolation: limit concurrent calls per service. Bulkhead + Circuit Breaker: complementary. Example: checkout service has its own thread pool (10 threads), search has its own (20 threads). If search is slow, checkout thread pool is unaffected.

---

### Q919: Retry with Exponential Backoff?
**Topic:** System Design - Resilience
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Retry failed operations with increasing delay. Backoff: delay = base * multiplier^attempt (e.g., 1s, 2s, 4s, 8s). Jitter: add randomness to prevent thundering herd (delay * random(0.5, 1.5)). Max retries: stop after N attempts (avoid infinite retry). Circuit breaker + retry: retry in closed/half-open, fail fast in open. Retryable errors: 429 (too many requests), 503 (service unavailable). Non-retryable: 400 (bad request), 401 (unauthorized). Retry respect Retry-After header.

---

### Q920: Database Migration strategies?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Manually versioned scripts: Flyway, Liquibase. Version: sequential (V1, V2) or timestamp. Checksum: detect changed scripts. Rollback: separate undo script (Flyway undo, Liquibase rollback). Repeatable: execute if checksum changed (views, functions). Migration types: schema changes (add column, create table), data migration (backfill), reference data. Zero-downtime: expand-migrate-contract pattern. Expand: add new column (nullable). Migrate: backfill data. Contract: remove old column. Test: Testcontainers + CI to verify migrations.

---

### Q921: Git internals (blobs, trees, commits)?
**Topic:** General CS - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Objects: Blob (file content), Tree (directory listing: blobs + subtrees), Commit (snapshot: root tree + parent + message + author). HEAD: pointer to current commit/branch. Branch: moving pointer to commit. Refs: branches (refs/heads/), tags (refs/tags/). Object store: .git/objects (content-addressable, SHA-1 hash). Pack files: compressed, delta-encoded for efficient storage. Merge: three-way merge (base + ours + theirs). Rebase: replay commits on new base (rewrites history). GC: prune unreachable objects.

---

### Q922: Microservices - Service Discovery?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Services find each other without hardcoded addresses. Client-side: service registry (Consul, Eureka, ZooKeeper), client queries and caches. Server-side: load balancer (NGINX, AWS ALB) forwards to instances. Kubernetes: built-in DNS (service name resolves to cluster IP), endpoints controller tracks pods.
