Consul: DNS + HTTP API + health checks. Service mesh (Istio): sidecar handles discovery transparently. Health checks: periodic (heartbeat, TCP, HTTP health endpoint). Deregister on failure.

---

### Q923: API Versioning strategies?
**Topic:** General CS - API Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
URL path: /v1/users vs /v2/users (most common, simple). Query parameter: /users?version=1. Header: Accept: application/vnd.myapi.v1+json. Breaking vs non-breaking: adding fields (non-breaking), removing/renaming (breaking). Sunset: deprecation notice, sunset date in response headers. Support period: maintain old version for reasonable time. Avoid: internal services can use consumer-driven contracts instead of versioning (coordinate upgrades). GraphQL: no versioning needed (evolve schema, deprecate fields).

---

### Q924: HATEOAS (Hypermedia as Engine of App State)?
**Topic:** General CS - API Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
REST level 3: API responses include links to related actions. Example: {"orderId": 123, "status": "pending", "links": [{"rel": "pay", "href": "/orders/123/pay", "method": "POST"}, {"rel": "cancel", "href": "/orders/123", "method": "DELETE"}]}. Benefits: self-documenting, discoverable, server-driven navigation. Disadvantages: clients more complex, harder to consume, not widely adopted. Most APIs stay at level 2 (resource + HTTP verbs). Spring HATEOAS, JSON:API support.

---

### Q925: Twelve-Factor App?
**Topic:** DevOps - Cloud
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Methodology for cloud-native apps. 1. Codebase: one codebase tracked in VCS, many deploys. 2. Dependencies: explicitly declare and isolate. 3. Config: store in environment variables. 4. Backing services: treat as attached resources. 5. Build, release, run: strictly separate stages. 6. Processes: stateless (no sticky sessions). 7. Port binding: export services via port. 8. Concurrency: scale out via process model. 9. Disposability: fast startup and graceful shutdown. 10. Dev/prod parity: keep environments similar. 11. Logs: treat as event streams. 12. Admin processes: run as one-off processes.

---

### Q926: Secure Coding Practices?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Input validation: whitelist, not blacklist. Output encoding: context-aware (HTML, URL, JS, SQL). Principle of least privilege: minimal permissions. Defense in depth: multiple security layers. Fail securely: default deny. Secure defaults: safe configuration out-of-box. Never trust user input. Validate all data (length, type, range, format). Use parameterized queries (SQL injection). Escape all output (XSS). Cryptography: use standard libraries (don't roll your own). Session management: secure, httpOnly, sameSite cookies. Disable debug/info in production.

---

### Q927: Browser Security features?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Same-Origin Policy: restrict cross-origin reads. CORS: opt-in cross-origin access. CSP: restrict resource sources. X-Frame-Options: prevent clickjacking. Subresource Integrity (SRI): verify loaded scripts (hash). Trusted Types: prevent DOM XSS. COOP/COEP: cross-origin isolation (SharedArrayBuffer). Sandbox: iframe restrictions. Fetch metadata headers: Sec-Fetch-*, Sec-GPC. Referrer-Policy: control Referer header. Feature Policy: restrict browser features (camera, mic). Origin isolation: prevent side-channel attacks.

---

### Q928: Web Authentication (WebAuthn / Passkeys)?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
WebAuthn: W3C standard for passwordless authentication using public key cryptography. FIDO2: WebAuthn + CTAP (Client to Authenticator Protocol). How: user registers with device (TPM, Secure Enclave) generating key pair. Private key stays on device. Login: challenge signed by private key, server verifies with public key. Passkeys: WebAuthn credentials sync'd across devices via cloud keychain (iCloud, Google Password Manager). Benefits: phishing-resistant (bound to origin), no passwords, biometric/PIN unlock. Resident key: stored on authenticator (discoverable credential). Platform vs cross-platform authenticators.

---

### Q929: Zero Trust Architecture?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Never trust, always verify. No implicit trust based on network location. Every request authenticated, authorized, encrypted. Principles: verify explicitly (always authenticate + authorize), least privilege access, assume breach. Microsegmentation: network segmentation per workload. BeyondCorp (Google): access based on identity + device state, not VPN. SASE (Secure Access Service Edge): network + security convergence (Zscaler, Cloudflare). Zero Trust Network Access (ZTNA): per-application access tunnels (Cloudflare Access, Zscaler ZPA). Identity-centric: strong auth, device posture checks.

---

### Q930: Data Classification and Protection?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Classification tiers: Public, Internal, Confidential, Restricted. Protection by classification: Public: no controls. Internal: basic access control. Confidential: encryption at rest/in transit, access logging. Restricted: encryption + DLP + audit. Data discovery: classify data (automated scanning). Encryption: AES-256 at rest, TLS 1.3 in transit. Key management: HSM, KMS. Data Loss Prevention (DLP): detect/prevent unauthorized data transfer. Masking: dynamic data masking for non-privileged users. Tokenization: replace sensitive data with tokens. Retention: defined retention policy. Destruction: secure deletion/crypto-shredding.

### Q931: Machine Learning Pipeline?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
End-to-end ML workflow: data ingestion -> validation -> preprocessing -> feature engineering -> model training -> evaluation -> deployment -> monitoring. Feature store: centralized features (Feast, Tecton). Model registry: version models (MLflow, DVC). Training pipeline: orchestrated (Kubeflow, Airflow, TFX). Feature engineering: transformations, encoding, scaling. Hyperparameter tuning: Optuna, Hyperopt. Evaluation: holdout, cross-validation, A/B testing. Deployment: batch (scheduled) or real-time (REST/gRPC). Monitoring: data drift, concept drift, performance degradation. CI/CD for ML (MLOps).

---

### Q932: Model Versioning and Registry?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Model registry: centralized system to store, version, and manage models. MLflow Model Registry: stage transitions (staging -> production -> archived), model lineage, annotations. DVC: data + model versioning (Git for data). S3/Blob Storage: store model artifacts (pickle, ONNX, TorchScript). Versioning: semantic version (1.0.0), tags, hash. Metadata: training code, hyperparameters, dataset version, metrics, evaluation results. Compare: experiment tracking (MLflow, W&B, Neptune). Deployment: deploy specific version, rollback. Audit trail: who deployed what when.

---

### Q933: Feature Stores?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Centralized feature management for ML. Online store: low-latency feature serving (Redis, DynamoDB). Offline store: batch feature computation + storage (S3, Parquet). Feature registry: metadata (name, type, source, transformation). Point-in-time correctness: join features at correct timestamp (avoid data leakage). Feast: open source feature store (Spark, BigQuery, Redis). Tecton: enterprise (Databricks). Benefits: feature reuse across models, consistency between train/serve, feature discovery, time travel.

---

### Q934: A/B Testing for ML Models?
**Topic:** ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Compare model performance in production. Setup: split traffic (control = existing model, treatment = new model). Metrics: business metrics (conversion, CTR, revenue), model metrics (accuracy, latency). Statistical significance: t-test, z-test, sequential testing. Sample size: power analysis to detect minimum effect. Duration: minimum 1-2 full business cycles. Challenges: network effects (users interact), carryover effects (multi-session experiments), interference (user A in treatment affects user B). ML-specific: model staleness, prediction caching. Multi-armed bandit: adaptively allocate traffic.

---

### Q935: Shadow Deployment for ML?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Deploy new model alongside production. New model receives traffic copy (shadow) but responses not served to users. Compare: predictions, latency, resource usage. Benefits: test with production traffic without risk, compare model behavior, detect drift. Implement: sidecar proxy, API gateway mirroring, async prediction comparison. Automate: evaluate performance, approve/reject promotion. Challenges: double compute cost, logging all predictions, storage for comparison results. Canary: next step after shadow (serve small % of real traffic).

---

### Q936: Data Drift vs Concept Drift?
**Topic:** ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Data (covariate) drift: input distribution changes (P(X) changes). Example: user demographics shift. Concept drift: relationship between input and target changes (P(Y|X) changes). Example: user preferences change over time. Detection: statistical tests (KS test, chi-square, population stability index), monitoring prediction distribution vs training, monitoring feature distributions. Virtual drift: model sees same distribution as training but sampling changes. Real drift: actual data distribution changes. Remediation: retrain, adaptive model (online learning), feature re-engineering.

---

### Q937: ML Model Monitoring?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Monitor: prediction drift, feature drift, model performance (accuracy, precision, recall), data quality (missing values, outliers), latency, throughput, resource usage. Alerts: performance degradation, drift threshold exceeded, service down. Tools: Evidently AI (drift detection, data quality), WhyLabs (AI observability), Arize, MLflow. Dashboards: Grafana, custom. Logging: store predictions + features + model version for analysis. Retraining triggers: scheduled (weekly), drift-based (automatic), performance-based (degradation). Golden dataset: maintain curated test set for evaluation.

---

### Q938: Gradient Boosting (XGBoost, LightGBM, CatBoost)?
**Topic:** ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensemble of decision trees built sequentially. Each new tree corrects errors of previous. Gradient Boosting: gradient descent in function space. XGBoost: regularized, column subsampling, weighted quantile sketch (fast), handles missing values. LightGBM: histogram-based, leaf-wise growth (faster), GOSS (Gradient-based One-Side Sampling), EFB (Exclusive Feature Bundling). CatBoost: categorical features natively, ordered boosting (unbiased), symmetric trees. XGBoost: most widely used, robust. LightGBM: fastest, very large datasets. CatBoost: categorical-heavy data.

---

### Q939: Ensemble Methods (Bagging, Boosting, Stacking)?
**Topic:** ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Combine multiple models for better performance. Bagging (Bootstrap Aggregating): train models on bootstrap samples, average predictions. Reduces variance. Random Forest: bagging + random feature subset. Boosting: sequential models correcting errors. Reduces bias + variance. AdaBoost, Gradient Boosting, XGBoost. Stacking (Stacked Generalization): train meta-model on base model predictions. Uses different algorithms as base models (Random Forest + XGBoost + Neural Net -> Logistic Regression meta-model). Voting: majority (classification) or average (regression). Ensembles reduce overfitting, improve generalization.

---

### Q940: Clustering Algorithms (K-Means, DBSCAN, Hierarchical)?
**Topic:** ML - Unsupervised
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
K-Means: partition into K clusters, minimize within-cluster variance. Fast, requires K specified, spherical clusters only. Elbow method for K. DBSCAN: density-based, clusters based on point density. Handles arbitrary shapes, detects outliers (noise). Parameters: epsilon (neighborhood radius), minPts. Hierarchical: agglomerative (bottom-up) or divisive (top-down). Dendrogram visualization. Ward linkage: minimize variance. BIRCH: scalable to large datasets. Gaussian Mixture Models: probabilistic clusters (soft assignment). Evaluation: silhouette score, Davies-Bouldin index.

---

### Q941: Dimensionality Reduction (PCA, t-SNE, UMAP)?
**Topic:** ML
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
PCA: linear, project onto principal components (max variance directions). Used for: feature reduction, noise reduction, visualization (2D/3D). Eigenvalue = variance explained. t-SNE: non-linear, preserves local structure, excellent visualization. Perplexity parameter. Problems: non-deterministic, global structure not preserved, expensive O(n^2). UMAP: newer, faster, preserves more global structure. Used for: visualization of high-dimensional data (single-cell RNAseq, embeddings). Feature selection vs extraction: select subset vs transform features. Autoencoders: non-linear dimensionality reduction.

---

### Q942: Reinforcement Learning in depth?
**Topic:** ML - RL
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Agent learns from environment via reward. Markov Decision Process (MDP): S, A, P, R, gamma. Value-based: Q-learning, DQN. Policy-based: REINFORCE, PPO. Actor-Critic: A2C, A3C, SAC. Exploration: epsilon-greedy, Boltzmann exploration, UCB. Off-policy: learn from other policy's experience (Q-learning, DQN). On-policy: learn from current policy (SARSA, PPO). Model-based: learn environment model, plan. Model-free: no model (most common). Deep RL: DQN (experience replay, target network), PPO (clipped objective, stable), SAC (maximum entropy).

---

### Q943: Hardware for ML (GPU, TPU)?
**Topic:** ML - Hardware
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
GPU: many parallel cores (CUDA), optimized for matrix operations (neural networks). NVIDIA: A100 (40/80GB), H100 (80GB, Transformer Engine), V100, RTX series. AMD: MI250, MI300X. TPU (Tensor Processing Unit): Google custom ASIC for TensorFlow/JAX. Matrix multiply unit (MXU). Bottleneck: GPU memory (model too large), memory bandwidth, compute utilization. Mixed precision training: FP16/FP32 for speed + memory. Tensor Cores: NVIDIA specialized for matrix multiply-accumulate. NPU: Neural Processing Unit (Apple Neural Engine, Qualcomm Hexagon) for mobile inference.

---

### Q944: Distributed Training (Data Parallel, Model Parallel)?
**Topic:** ML - Deep Learning
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Data Parallel: replicate model on each GPU, split batch. All-reduce gradients. DDP (PyTorch DistributedDataParallel): efficient gradient sync. FSDP (Fully Sharded Data Parallel): shard model parameters + gradients + optimizer states across GPUs. Model Parallel: split model layers across GPUs. Pipeline Parallel: layers = stages, micro-batches flow through pipeline. Tensor Parallel: split individual operations across GPUs (Megatron-LM). Sequence Parallel: split sequence dimension (Ring Attention). ZeRO: memory optimization (ZeRO-1: optimizer states, ZeRO-2: +gradients, ZeRO-3: +parameters). 3D Parallelism: data + pipeline + tensor parallel combined (Megatron-DeepSpeed).

---

### Q945: ONNX and Model Export?
**Topic:** ML - MLOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ONNX (Open Neural Network Exchange): open standard for model representation. Export from PyTorch (torch.onnx.export), TensorFlow (tf2onnx), scikit-learn (skl2onnx). Benefits: interoperability (train in PyTorch, inference in TensorRT), hardware acceleration (ONNX Runtime, TensorRT, OpenVINO). Quantization: ONNX Runtime supports INT8/FP16. Model optimization: constant folding, node fusion. Dynamic vs static axes. Verify: onnxruntime inference + compare outputs. ONNX Runtime: cross-platform, high-performance inference engine. Use: production deployment of ML models.

---

### Q946: Edge AI and On-Device ML?
**Topic:** ML - Deployment
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Run ML models on edge devices (mobile, IoT, embedded). Benefits: low latency, offline, privacy (no data to cloud), reduced bandwidth. Challenges: limited compute, memory, power. Frameworks: TensorFlow Lite (mobile, micro), Core ML (iOS), ML Kit (Google), PyTorch Mobile (Android/iOS), ONNX Runtime (cross-platform). Optimization: quantization (INT8), pruning, knowledge distillation (smaller model), model compression. Hardware acceleration: GPU, NPU, DSP. Federated learning: train across devices without centralizing data (Google Gboard). Secure: on-device processing.

---

### Q947: GraphQL Subscriptions (Real-time)?
**Topic:** General CS - API
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Real-time updates via GraphQL. WebSocket-based transport. Subscription: client subscribes to event, server pushes updates. Schema: type Subscription { newMessage(roomId: ID!): Message }. Resolver: async iterator (pubsub.asyncIterator). PubSub: in-memory (development), Redis (production for multi-instance), MQTT. Frameworks: Apollo (useSubscription, subscribeToMore), Relay. Event filters: client sends variables, server filters events. Lifecycle: connect, subscribe, unsubscribe, disconnect. Security: authenticate subscription connection. Backpressure: handle slow consumers (buffer, drop).

---

### Q948: WebRTC?
**Topic:** General CS - Real-time
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Real-time peer-to-peer communication (audio, video, data). APIs: getUserMedia (capture), RTCPeerConnection (p2p), RTCDataChannel (data). Signaling: exchange SDP (offer/answer) and ICE candidates. STUN: discover public IP/port. TURN: relay if P2P fails (firewall, NAT). ICE: interactive connectivity establishment (candidates = IP:port pairs). Simulcast: send multiple qualities. SFU (Selective Forwarding Unit): server routes streams (MediaSoup, Jitsi Videobridge). MCU (Multipoint Control Unit): server mixes streams (older). Applications: video calls (Zoom, Google Meet), live streaming, file sharing, gaming.

---

### Q949: WebAssembly (WASM)?
**Topic:** General CS
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Binary instruction format for stack-based VM. Run languages (C, C++, Rust, Go, Java) in browser at near-native speed. Compilation target: compile to .wasm. Runtime: browser WASM engine (V8, SpiderMonkey, JavaScriptCore). Features: deterministic execution, sandboxed, memory-safe. WASI: WebAssembly System Interface (system calls for non-browser). Use: computationally intensive tasks (gaming, video editing, 3D, ML inference), code portability (write once run anywhere). Limitations: no direct DOM access (need JS glue), large binary sizes. Tools: Emscripten (C++), wasm-pack (Rust), Blazor (.NET).

---

### Q950: Rust programming basics?
**Topic:** General CS - Programming
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Systems programming language: memory-safe (ownership, borrowing, lifetimes), zero-cost abstractions, no garbage collector. Ownership: each value has one owner. Borrowing: reference without ownership (& = immutable, &mut = mutable). Lifetimes: ensure references valid. Traits: interfaces with default implementations. Enums: algebraic data types (Option, Result). Pattern matching: exhaustive, expressive. Unsafe: for FFI, raw pointers, interior mutability. Concurrency: Send + Sync traits, message passing (channels). Use: systems programming, WASM, CLI tools, network services (servers, proxies). Performance: comparable to C++.

---

### Q951: System Design - Designing URL Shortener?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Requirements: short URL (6-8 chars), high availability, low latency, analytics, custom slugs. Estimation: 100M URLs/month, 10:1 read/write ratio. ~40 writes/sec, ~400 reads/sec. Storage: 100M * 1KB = 100GB/year. API: POST /shorten (longUrl -> shortId), GET /{shortId} (redirect 301). ID generation: Base62 (a-z, A-Z, 0-9) from auto-increment or Snowflake ID. Database: key-value store (DynamoDB, Redis) for fast lookups. Cache: Redis (hot URLs). Redirect: 301 (permanent, browser cached). Rate limiting: per user. Analytics: async logging to Kafka -> analytics DB.

---

### Q952: System Design - Designing Chat System?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
1:1 and group chat, online status, message history, media. WebSocket for real-time. Message: id, sender, chat_id, content, timestamp, type. Store: messages (Cassandra for write-heavy, time-based ordering), chat metadata (PostgreSQL). Message ordering: server-assigned timestamp + sequence ID (within chat). Presence: heartbeat every few seconds, publish to Redis pub/sub. Push notifications: Firebase/APNs for offline users. Chat service: handles WebSocket connections, fan-out (group chat: write to each user's inbox). Inbox model: each user has message timeline (Cassandra). Group chat: write once, read many (fan-out on read). Media: CDN + presigned URLs.

---

### Q953: System Design - Designing Social Media Feed?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Feed generation: pull (user requests -> query friends' posts -> rank) vs push (fan-out on publish). Hybrid: active users get push, celebrities get pull. Pre-compute feed: fan-out on post creation to followers' timelines (Redis sorted sets). Ranking: recency + relevance + affinity. Storage: post content (Blob/S3), feed (Redis sorted set, TTL), relationships (graph DB). Newsfeed API: GET /feed?limit=20&cursor=. Pagination: cursor-based (offset for large data). Comments: nested (tree structure). Notifications: push on like/comment. Caching: CDN for media, Redis for top feeds.

---

### Q954: System Design - Designing a CDN?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Content Delivery Network: cache content at edge locations (POPs) near users. Pull CDN: cache on first request (push origin). Push CDN: pre-populate cache. Origin shield: intermediate cache layer to reduce origin load. Caching: TTL per content type, cache invalidation API. Routing: Anycast (same IP from different locations, BGP routes to nearest POP), DNS-based (geographic DNS). Request routing: latency-based, geo-based, weight-based. Dynamic content acceleration: optimized TCP, TLS termination at edge, route optimization. Purge: invalidate cached content. Security: DDoS protection, WAF at edge. CloudFront, Cloudflare, Akamai.

### Q955: Design Patterns - Visitor?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Separate algorithms from objects. Visitor defines new operation without changing element classes. Element: accept(visitor). Visitor: visit(ConcreteElement). Double dispatch: which method called depends on both element and visitor types. Use: when many unrelated operations on object structure (AST traversal, document export). Alternative: pattern matching (modern languages). Example: ShoppingCartVisitor (visitBook, visitFruit calculate price). Trade-off: adding new element requires updating all visitors.

---

### Q956: Design Patterns - Strategy?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Define family of algorithms, make interchangeable. Context uses strategy interface. Example: PaymentStrategy (CreditCard, PayPal, Crypto). SortingStrategy (QuickSort, MergeSort, BubbleSort). Benefits: open-closed principle, avoid conditional logic, runtime algorithm switching. Implementation: interface/abstract class, concrete implementations, context holds reference. Modern alternative: function pointers, lambdas (pass behavior as parameter). Spring: inject different strategy implementations.

---

### Q957: Design Patterns - Observer (Pub-Sub)?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Subject maintains list of observers, notifies them of state changes. One-to-many dependency. Push: subject pushes data to observers. Pull: observers pull from subject. Benefits: loose coupling, broadcast communication. Examples: event listeners (UI), messaging systems (Kafka, RabbitMQ). Java: Observer/Observable (deprecated). React: Flux/Redux (store notifies components). Modern: event emitters (EventEmitter in Node), RxJS observables. Distributed: message queue (Kafka).

---

### Q958: Design Patterns - Factory vs Abstract Factory?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Factory Method: single method creating objects. Subclass decides which class to instantiate. Abstract Factory: interface for creating families of related objects. Example: GUIFactory -> WinFactory, MacFactory. Button + Checkbox created together. Factory Method: one product type. Abstract Factory: multiple related product types. Spring: @Bean methods are factory methods. Java: Calendar.getInstance() is factory. Abstract Factory used when product families need consistency.

---

### Q959: Design Patterns - Proxy vs Decorator?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Proxy: controls access to another object (same interface). Types: Virtual (lazy loading), Protection (access control), Remote (local proxy for remote object), Logging. Decorator: adds behavior to object dynamically. Wraps original object. Decorator adds new functionality (open-closed). Proxy controls access. Both are structural patterns wrapping objects. Similar implementation (same interface, delegation). Intent differs: decorator enhances, proxy controls. Java: InputStream wrapped by BufferedInputStream (Decorator). Spring AOP: Proxy for aspects.

---

### Q960: Design Patterns - Singleton pattern?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Ensures class has only one instance. Global access point. Implementation: private constructor, static instance, public static getInstance(). Thread-safe: eager initialization (JVM guarantees), double-checked locking (volatile + synchronized), Bill Pugh holder pattern (inner static class). Problems: hard to test (global state), breaks SRP, hidden dependencies. Alternatives: dependency injection (Spring beans - singleton by default), enum singleton (Java). Modern: avoid singletons, use DI containers.

---

### Q961: Design Patterns - Builder pattern?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Separate object construction from representation. Especially useful for objects with many parameters. Fluent interface: builder.named("foo").age(30).city("NYC").build(). Immutable: builder creates object at end (final fields, no setters). Lombok: @Builder annotation. Kotlin: named arguments + default values (no builder needed). Step builder: enforce parameter order (compile-time validation). Use: complex object creation (SQL query builder, HTTP request builder).

---

### Q962: Design Patterns - Adapter pattern?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Convert one interface to another (compatible). Client expects Target interface. Adapter implements Target, wraps Adaptee. Object adapter: composition (wrap adaptee). Class adapter: inheritance (multiple inheritance needed). Use: integrate third-party library with different interface, legacy code integration. Example: NewPaymentGateway interface, legacy OldPaymentGateway. Adapter wraps OldPaymentGateway to implement NewPaymentGateway. Spring: various adapters (HandlerAdapter for controllers).

---

### Q963: Design Patterns - Command pattern?
**Topic:** Software Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Encapsulate request as object. Parameters: receiver, action, arguments. Invoker: executes command. Benefits: parameterize clients, queue/log requests, undo/redo, transactional behavior. Example: text editor (commands: InsertChar, DeleteChar, Paste). Each command has execute() and undo(). Macro: composite command (sequence of commands). Java: Runnable, Callable are command pattern. CQRS: Command pattern at architectural level. GUI: menu items, buttons as commands.

---

### Q964: Distributed Transactions - Two-Phase Commit in practice?
**Topic:** System Design - Distributed
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Prepare phase: coordinator asks all participants to prepare (vote yes/no). Commit phase: if all yes, commit; if any no, abort. Problems: blocking (coordinator failure blocks participants), coordinator SPOF, slow (multiple round trips). Alternatives: Saga pattern (compensating transactions), TCC (Try-Confirm/Cancel), Transactional Outbox (local transaction + reliable message). XA transactions: Java JTA (Java Transaction API) for 2PC across resources. Most microservices avoid 2PC (prefer eventual consistency + Sagas).

---

### Q965: Distributed Tracing in Microservices?
**Topic:** System Design - Observability
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
End-to-end request tracking across services. Trace ID: propagated via headers (HTTP headers: x-request-id, traceparent, W3C Trace Context). Span: unit of work (service call, DB query). OpenTelemetry: standard for instrumentation (SDKs, exporters, collectors). Sampling: head-based (consistent), tail-based (focus on interesting traces). Storage: Jaeger, Zipkin, Tempo (Grafana). Visualization: flame graphs, service dependency graphs. Integration: logs + metrics + traces correlation. Ad-hoc: logs include trace ID for cross-service log correlation.

---

### Q966: Health Checks (Liveness vs Readiness)?
**Topic:** DevOps - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Kubernetes probes: Liveness: is app alive? (restart container if fails). Readiness: is app ready to serve? (remove from service if fails). Startup: delayed start (avoid premature failure for slow-start apps). Liveness: simple (check process is up). Readiness: thorough (check DB connection, cache warm). Startup: for apps needing initialization (model loading, connection pool). Endpoints: /healthz (liveness), /readyz (readiness). Graceful shutdown: SIGTERM, wait for in-flight requests, exit. PreStop hook: execute before container terminates.

---

### Q967: Container Security?
**Topic:** Security - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Image security: scan for vulnerabilities (Trivy, Snyk, Docker Scout), use minimal base images (distroless, alpine), sign images (Cosign). Runtime: run as non-root user (USER directive), read-only root filesystem, drop capabilities (--cap-drop=ALL), seccomp profiles, AppArmor/SELinux. Network: least privilege (no host networking), network policies (K8s NetworkPolicy). Registry: private, authenticated, scan on push. Supply chain: SBOM, verify signatures, trusted registry only. Secrets: never in images (use K8s Secrets, Vault). Admission controllers: enforce policies (OPA/Gatekeeper, Kyverno).

---

### Q968: Kubernetes Security (Pod Security, RBAC)?
**Topic:** Security - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
RBAC: Role (permissions in namespace), ClusterRole (cluster-wide), RoleBinding/ClusterRoleBinding. Principle of least privilege. Pod Security: Pod Security Standards (Privileged, Baseline, Restricted). Pod Security Admission: enforce at namespace level (enforce, audit, warn). Network Policies: control pod-to-pod traffic (ingress/egress rules). ServiceAccount: identity for pods, never use default SA. Secrets: encrypted at rest (KMS), etcd encryption. Admission Controllers: OPA/Gatekeeper, Kyverno for policy enforcement. Container runtime: containerd, CRI-O (no Docker daemon). Audit logging: API server audit.

---

### Q969: Secret Management (Vault, KMS)?
**Topic:** Security - DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HashiCorp Vault: dynamic secrets (DB credentials, API keys), encryption as a service, leasing (auto-renew), audit logging. Kubernetes: External Secrets Operator (sync from Vault/AWS Secrets Manager), Sealed Secrets (encrypted Git-backed secrets), CSI Secrets Store (mount as volumes). AWS KMS: managed key creation/rotation. Azure Key Vault: secrets + keys + certificates + HSM. Best practices: never in env vars (env inspected by processes), never in code, short-lived credentials (dynamic secrets), rotation, audit access. Sidecar pattern: Vault agent sidecar provides secrets.

---

### Q970: OWASP Top 10 2021 detail?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Broken Access Control: 94% of apps tested. 2. Cryptographic Failures: weak crypto, data exposure. 3. Injection: SQL, NoSQL, OS command. 4. Insecure Design: missing threat modeling. 5. Security Misconfiguration: default creds, unpatched. 6. Vulnerable Components: CVEs in dependencies. 7. Auth Failures: weak passwords, session issues. 8. Integrity Failures: software supply chain. 9. Logging/Monitoring: insufficient detection. 10. SSRF: server-side request forgery. New entries: Insecure Design (#4), Software Integrity (#8). Removed: CSRF (detected by frameworks), XXE (rare).

---

### Q971: CVE and Vulnerability Management?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
CVE (Common Vulnerabilities and Exposures): standardized identifier for vulnerabilities. CVSS (Common Vulnerability Scoring System): severity score (0-10). NVD (National Vulnerability Database). Vulnerability management: discover (scan), prioritize (CVSS, exploitability, asset criticality), remediate (patch, workaround, accept), verify. Scanning: Snyk, Trivy, Qualys, Nessus, OWASP ZAP. SBOM (Software Bill of Materials): inventory of components. Remediation SLAs: Critical (24h), High (7d), Medium (30d). Patch management: automated patching, canary deployments.

---

### Q972: Privacy by Design?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Privacy embedded into system design proactively. Principles: proactive not reactive, privacy as default, privacy embedded, full functionality (positive-sum), end-to-end security, visibility and transparency, user-centric (respect user privacy). GDPR compliance: data minimization, purpose limitation, storage limitation, accuracy, integrity, accountability. Data Protection Impact Assessment (DPIA). Consent management: explicit, granular, revocable. Right to be forgotten: data deletion. Data portability. Privacy engineering: anonymization, pseudonymization, differential privacy, federated learning.

---

### Q973: Differential Privacy?
**Topic:** Security - Privacy
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Add controlled noise to query results to protect individual privacy. Epsilon: privacy budget (lower = more privacy, less accuracy). Laplace mechanism: add noise from Laplace distribution with scale = sensitivity / epsilon. Exponential mechanism: for non-numeric outputs. Sensitivity: maximum change from adding/removing one individual. Use: census data (US Census Bureau), Apple (device data collection), Google (RAPPOR). Local DP: add noise on device before sending (RAPPOR). Central DP: add noise after aggregation. Challenges: privacy budget management (composition), utility loss.

---

### Q974: Multi-tenancy in SaaS?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Multiple customers (tenants) share same application instance. Isolation models: Database per tenant (strongest isolation, more resources). Schema per tenant (shared DB, separate schemas). Shared table (tenant_id column - simplest, least isolation). Hybrid: critical tenants get separate DB, small tenants share. Tenant identification: domain (tenant.example.com), subdomain (tenant.example.com), path, header. Row-level security: PostgreSQL RLS (policy per tenant). Cross-tenant data leak prevention: strict filtering, NoSQL: DynamoDB partition key = tenant_id. Backup/restore per tenant.

---

### Q975: GraphQL - N+1 problem and Dataloader?
**Topic:** General CS - API
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
N+1: resolver fetches parent list (1 query), then per item fetches child (N queries). Solution: Dataloader (Facebook library). Batch + cache: collect individual load() calls in event loop tick, batch into single query. Dataloader per request (clear cache between requests). Function: keys -> values (return array same length as keys). Caches: per-request (implicit dedup). Example: { posts { author { name } } } -> Dataloader batches all author queries: WHERE id IN (1,2,3). Prisma, Apollo, Hasura have built-in batching.

---

### Q976: Database Normalization (1NF, 2NF, 3NF)?
**Topic:** General CS - SQL
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1NF: atomic columns (no arrays/nested), each row unique. 2NF: 1NF + no partial dependencies (all non-key columns depend on full primary key). 3NF: 2NF + no transitive dependencies (non-key depends only on key). BCNF: stronger 3NF, every determinant is candidate key. Denormalization: intentionally violate for performance (reduce joins). OLTP: normalized (avoid redundancy, ensure consistency). OLAP/DW: denormalized (star schema) for query efficiency. In practice: 3NF is good balance, denormalize selectively for performance.

---

### Q977: Stored Procedures vs ORM?
**Topic:** General CS - SQL
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Stored Procedures: SQL in database (precompiled, fast). Pros: performance (no round trips), security (direct table access hidden), encapsulation. Cons: language-specific (PL/pgSQL), harder to version/test, logic split across app + DB. ORM (Hibernate, Sequelize, SQLAlchemy): objects to tables. Pros: productivity, portability, caching, migration tools. Cons: N+1 queries, complex SQL generation, performance overhead. Hybrid: ORM for CRUD, stored procedures for complex operations, raw SQL for performance-critical queries.

---

### Q978: Database Locking (Pessimistic vs Optimistic)?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Pessimistic: lock row on read (SELECT ... FOR UPDATE). Prevents concurrent modifications. Use: high contention, conflicts expected. Implementation: DB row locks, application-level locks. Optimistic: version column (integer or timestamp). On update: check version unchanged, if changed -> retry. Use: low contention, conflicts rare. Implementation: @Version (JPA), CAS (compare-and-swap). Advantage: no locks, better performance. Disadvantage: retry logic for conflicts. Which to choose: pessimistic for high contention (financial), optimistic for read-heavy.

---

### Q979: Connection Pool Sizing formula?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Core formula: pool_size = (core_count * 2) + effective_spindle_count (old HikariCP recommendation). Modern: pool_size = T * (C - 1) / S + 1 where T = thread count, C = DB round trips per request, S = avg DB time. Rule of thumb: start with 10-20 per app instance. Too small = request queuing. Too large = DB overload (context switches, connection management). Postgres max_connections: set to pool size * instances + buffer. Monitor: active connections, wait time, CPU. HikariCP: maxPoolSize default 10.

---

### Q980: ACID vs BASE - which one for your use case?
**Topic:** General CS - Databases
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
ACID: financial systems, order management, inventory (must be accurate), billing. Transactions guarantee consistency. BASE: social feeds, analytics, IoT sensor data, user sessions (can tolerate stale data). Performance and availability prioritized. Many systems do both: ACID for core business data, BASE for supporting data (activity logs, analytics). Example e-commerce: orders (ACID - PostgreSQL), product recommendations (BASE - Cassandra), search (BASE - Elasticsearch). NewSQL (CockroachDB, Spanner) tries to give best of both.

---

### Q981: Queue vs Topic vs Event Bus?
**Topic:** System Design - Messaging
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Queue (SQS, RabbitMQ queue): point-to-point (one consumer per message). Good for: task distribution, load leveling. Topic (SNS, RabbitMQ topic): pub/sub (multiple consumers receive each message). Good for: notifications, fan-out. Event Bus (EventBridge, Azure Event Grid): schema registry, routing rules, transformations. Good for: event-driven architecture. Stream (Kafka): ordered, replayable, partitioned log. Good for: event sourcing, data pipelines. Choose based on: consumption pattern (competing vs broadcast), ordering requirements, replay needs.

---

### Q982: API Gateway vs Service Mesh?
**Topic:** System Design - Microservices
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
API Gateway: north-south traffic (external -> internal). Request-level: auth, rate limiting, routing, transformation, caching. Aggregates responses. Service Mesh: east-west traffic (internal service <-> internal service). Connection-level: mTLS, retry, circuit breaker, observability, traffic splitting. Sidecar proxy (Envoy) per pod. They complement each other: Gateway handles edge concerns, Mesh handles inter-service concerns. Both can overlapping (routing, retries). Istio Gateway: extends service mesh to edge. Modern: both in same stack (Istio Ingress Gateway + sidecars).

---

### Q983: Web Security - SameSite Cookie attribute?
**Topic:** Security
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
SameSite attribute controls when cookies sent with cross-site requests. Strict: cookie only sent for same-site requests (not even for top-level navigation). Best for security but breaks third-party links. Lax: sent for top-level navigations (GET) from other sites. Good balance. None: cookie sent for all cross-site requests (must also set Secure). Default: Lax in modern browsers. CSRF protection: Strict/Lax prevents most CSRF attacks. Sets were SameSite is not a replacement for CSRF tokens but reduces risk. Chrome defaults: Lax for new cookies.

---

### Q984: Performance - Database Query Optimization?
**Topic:** General CS - SQL
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
1. Identify slow queries: slow query log, pg_stat_statements, EXPLAIN ANALYZE. 2. Indexing: create indexes on WHERE columns, JOIN columns, ORDER BY (covered if possible). 3. Rewrite queries: avoid SELECT *, use EXISTS instead of IN for large subqueries, avoid functions in WHERE (index can't be used). 4. Denormalize: reduce joins for read-heavy. 5. Partition: for large tables (time-based, list). 6. Connection pooling. 7. Caching: Redis for hot data. 8. Read replicas: offload reads. 9. Vacuum/ANALYZE: update statistics, reclaim space. 10. Query hints: force index, join order.

---

### Q985: Performance - Frontend Optimization?
**Topic:** Frontend
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Critical rendering path: minimize blocking resources, inline critical CSS. Lazy loading: images (loading=lazy), components, routes. Bundle size: code splitting (dynamic import()), tree shaking, minification. Images: WebP/AVIF, responsive srcset, CDN, compress. Caching: service worker, HTTP caching (Cache-Control, ETag). Preload/prefetch: critical resources. Resource hints: dns-prefetch, preconnect. SSR/SSG: faster initial render. Lighthouse: measure and optimize. Core Web Vitals: LCP (<2.5s), FID (<100ms), CLS (<0.1). Fonts: font-display: swap, subset fonts.

---

### Q986: TypeScript - Utility Types?
**Topic:** Frontend - TypeScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Built-in: Partial<T> (all optional), Required<T> (all required), Readonly<T>, Pick<T, K>, Omit<T, K>, Record<K, V> (object with keys K, values V), Exclude<T, U> (union difference), Extract<T, U> (union intersection), NonNullable<T> (remove null/undefined), ReturnType<T> (function return type), Parameters<T> (function parameter tuple), Awaited<T> (unwrap Promise). Mapped types: {[K in keyof T]: T[K]}. Conditional types: T extends U ? X : Y. Template literal types: `${K}Id`. Use: create type-safe APIs, form state, API responses.

---

### Q987: TypeScript - Generics and Conditional Types?
**Topic:** Frontend - TypeScript
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Generics: type parameters (T, K, V). Function: function identity<T>(arg: T): T. Interface: interface Box<T> { value: T }. Constraints: <T extends HasLength>. Conditional types: T extends string ? 'string' : 'other'. Infer: type Return<T> = T extends (...args: any[]) => infer R ? R : never. Distributive conditional: union type distributes over conditional. keyof: keys of type. typeof: get type from value. Use: type-safe builders, API response types, discriminated unions.

---

### Q988: React - Server Components?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
React Server Components (RSC): components that run on server, send serialized result to client. Zero client JavaScript (lighter bundle). Direct database access (no API calls). Automatic code splitting. Client Components: 'use client' directive. Interleaving: server components can render client components. Benefits: faster initial load, smaller bundles, better SEO. Data fetching: server components fetch directly (async component). Limitations: no hooks, no event handlers, no browser APIs. Next.js App Router: server components by default. RSC + Server Actions: form handling.

---

### Q989: React - Concurrent Features?
**Topic:** Frontend - React
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Concurrent React: interruptible rendering, prioritize urgent updates. useTransition: mark state update as non-urgent (isPending + startTransition). useDeferredValue: defer re-rendering for slow parts (debounce-like). Suspense: loading states for async operations (code splitting, data fetching). Automatic batching: multiple setState in same event batched. startTransition: UI stays responsive during expensive re-render. Benefits: smoother UI, prioritize user input, better perceived performance. Patterns: useTransition for expensive filtering, useDeferredValue for search results.

---

### Q990: State Management in 2024?
**Topic:** Frontend - State Management
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Local: useState, useReducer (within component). Context + useReducer: simple global state (no external lib). Server state: React Query/TanStack Query (caching, sync, invalidation), SWR, RTK Query. Client state: Zustand (minimal, no boilerplate), Jotai (atomic), Recoil (experimental), Redux Toolkit (mature). URL state: next/navigation (useSearchParams), react-router (useSearchParams). Form state: React Hook Form + Zod. Modal/toast: custom context or library (Sonner). Trend: less Redux, more TanStack Query + Zustand. Server Components reduce need for client state libraries.

---

### Q991: Edge Computing and CDN?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Edge computing: process data near user (edge node), not centralized data center. Low latency, reduced bandwidth. CDN: static content caching at edge. Edge Functions: code running at edge (Cloudflare Workers, Vercel Edge Functions, AWS Lambda@Edge). Use: personalization, A/B testing, API gateway, authentication, rewrite/redirect. V8 isolates (Cloudflare): fast cold start (~5ms). Benefits: no regional server, reduced origin load. Limitations: limited runtime (no Node.js APIs), CPU time limits, storage. Edge DB: D1 (Cloudflare SQL), PlanetScale (edge-read replicas). Edge config: KV stores.

---

### Q992: Serverless vs Containers comparison?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Serverless (AWS Lambda, Azure Functions, Cloud Functions): auto-scale from 0, pay per invocation, max execution time (15min Lambda), limited memory (10GB), cold start. Containers (ECS, AKS, GKE): always running, scale from min (no cold start), pay for provisioned resources, longer execution, larger memory options. Cold start mitigation: provisioned concurrency, SnapStart (Lambda), keep-warm. When serverless: event-driven, variable traffic, lightweight tasks. Containers: steady traffic, complex apps, long-running, GPU workloads. Typical: serverless for background tasks + API, containers for main app. Fargate: serverless containers (no cluster management).

---

### Q993: Dapr (Distributed Application Runtime)?
**Topic:** System Design
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Microsoft Dapr: sidecar pattern for microservices (similar to service mesh but for application logic). Building blocks: Service Invocation, State Management, Pub/Sub, Bindings, Actors, Secrets, Configuration, Distributed Lock, Workflow. Sidecar: runs alongside app (HTTP/gRPC API). Pluggable components: Redis for state, Kafka for pub/sub. Benefits: simplifies distributed systems development (no SDK dependency), polyglot (any language), portable. Example: state store (save state via Dapr API, backed by Redis/CosmosDB). Actor model: virtual actors (stateful, timers, reminders). Placement: actor placement service.

---

### Q994: Apache Beam / Dataflow?
**Topic:** Big Data
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Unified programming model for batch + streaming. Write once, run on any runner (Apache Flink, Google Dataflow, Spark, Samza). Pipeline: PCollection (data) -> PTransform (computation). Windowing: fixed, sliding, session. Watermarks: handle late data. Triggers: when to emit results (early, on-time, late). Exactly-once: by default. Runner v2: portable (any language). Use: ETL pipelines, real-time analytics, event processing. Dataflow: managed Beam runner on GCP (auto-scaling, exactly-once). Beam Portability Framework: run pipelines written in Java/Python/Go on any runner.

---

### Q995: GitOps?
**Topic:** DevOps
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Git is single source of truth for declarative infrastructure and applications. Desired state in Git. Operator (ArgoCD, Flux) syncs cluster to desired state. Benefits: audit trail (Git history), rollback (git revert), approval via PR, consistency. ArgoCD: app definition in Git, auto-sync, sync strategies (manual, automated), Health checks, Diff preview, SSO integration. Flux: lighter, Kustomize + Helm support, image automation (update manifests on new image). Git + PR: review all changes. Drift detection: operator detects and corrects manual changes. Reconciliation: periodic sync.

---

### Q996: FinOps (Cloud Cost Optimization)?
**Topic:** Cloud Computing
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
Financial operations: manage cloud spend. Principles: visibility (cost allocation tags), optimization (right-sizing, reserved instances, spot instances), accountability (team budgets), governance (policies, limits). Right-sizing: match instance type to workload (don't over-provision). Reserved Instances: 1-3 year commitment (up to 72% savings). Spot/Preemptible Instances: 60-90% discount, can be reclaimed. Autoscaling: scale down when idle. Storage lifecycle: move cold data to cheaper tiers. Waste elimination: stale resources, orphaned volumes, idle load balancers. Tools: AWS Cost Explorer, Azure Cost Management + Billing, CloudHealth, Kubecost.

---

### Q997: Kubernetes - Operators and CRDs?
**Topic:** DevOps - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Operator: automated operational knowledge (human operator in code). Extends Kubernetes API via CRDs (Custom Resource Definitions). CRD: custom API resource (kind, spec, status). Controller: watches CRD + reconciles to desired state. Pattern: Observe -> Diff -> Act (reconciliation loop). Examples: Prometheus Operator (manage Prometheus instances), Postgres Operator (create/backup/restore PostgreSQL), Strimzi (Kafka), Cert-Manager (TLS certificates), Crossplane (infrastructure provisioning). Operator SDK: framework for building operators (Go, Helm, Ansible). RBAC: controllers need permissions to manage resources.

---

### Q998: Kubernetes - Autoscaling (HPA, VPA, KEDA)?
**Topic:** DevOps - Kubernetes
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
HPA (Horizontal Pod Autoscaler): scale number of pods based on CPU/memory or custom metrics (QPS, request latency). Target: average utilization. Metrics Server: required. VPA (Vertical Pod Autoscaler): adjust pod resource requests/limits based on usage. Recommender, Updater, Admission Controller. KEDA: event-driven autoscaling (scale based on Kafka lag, queue depth, cron, Prometheus). Works with HPA. Cluster Autoscaler: scale number of nodes (add/remove VMs). Combination: HPA for pods + Cluster Autoscaler for nodes. Custom metrics: Prometheus adapter, KEDA.

---

### Q999: Hexagonal Architecture vs Clean Architecture vs Onion?
**Topic:** Software Architecture
**Difficulty:** Medium

**Answer:**
All aim for separation of concerns, dependency inversion. Hexagonal (Ports & Adapters): core domain with ports (interfaces), adapters implement ports. Symmetrical: driving adapters (REST, CLI) and driven adapters (DB, API). Onion: layers from core outward (Domain -> Application -> Infrastructure). Each layer depends inward. Clean Architecture: concentric circles (Entities -> Use Cases -> Interface Adapters -> External). Each circle isolated. Differences: Hexagonal focuses on ports/adapters (symmetry). Clean emphasizes use cases as outer entry. Onion has application services layer. All achieve: testable core, technology independence, changeable infrastructure.

---

### Q1000: Capstone - Full Stack AI System Design?
**Topic:** System Design - AI
**Difficulty:** Hard

**Answer:**
Design AI-powered document Q&A system (like ChatGPT for company docs). Requirements: users ask questions about documents, get answers with citations. Scale: 10M docs, 10K QPS. Pipeline: Document ingestion (PDF, Word, HTML) -> chunking -> embedding (text-embedding-3-small) -> vector DB (Pinecone/Weaviate). Query: user question -> embed -> retrieve top-10 chunks -> rerank (cross-encoder) -> LLM (GPT-4) generate answer with citations. Architecture: Web (React) -> API Gateway -> Query Service (LLM) + Ingestion Service (async queue). Cache: Redis for frequent queries. CDN: static assets. Observability: OpenTelemetry. Security: auth (OAuth2), guardrails, PII redaction. Infrastructure: Kubernetes, auto-scale based on queue depth. Data: blob storage (S3), PostgreSQL for metadata, vector DB for embeddings. Cost: embedding (GPU batch), LLM (token cost), storage (S3). Backup: daily DB snapshots.
